# 太上大道玉清经

*The Supreme Dao and Jade Purity Scripture*

**Scripture Title:** *The Supreme Dao and Jade Purity Scripture* (abbreviated as *Jade Purity Scripture*). Author unknown, approximately composed during the Tang dynasty. Ten fascicles.

**Source Text:** *Daoist Canon of the Orthodox Tradition*, First Section of the Zhengtong Era.
**Collated Manuscripts:** Dunhuang manuscripts P.2257 (Fascicle 2); S.5507 (Fascicle 4); P.2405, P.2341 (Fascicle 7); P.2385 (Fascicle 10), among others.

**Table of Contents**

**Fascicle One**
1. The Origin of the Dao (Chapter One)
2. Causes and Conditions (Chapter Two)
3. The World (Chapter Three)
4. Preface to the Compassionate Precepts (Chapter Four)
5. The Structure of Precept Exposition (Chapter Five)

**Fascicle Two**
6. The Skillful Means of Compassion (Chapter Six)
7. The Teaching of the Middle Kalpa: Liberating Beings in the Dragon Realm (Chapter Seven)

**Fascicle Three**
8. Universal Salvation of the Netherworld (Chapter Eight)

**Fascicle Four**
9. The Upper Primordial (Chapter Nine)
10. The Middle Primordial (Chapter Ten)
11. The Lower Primordial (Chapter Eleven)
12. The Circulation of the Three Primordials’ Treasure Scripture (Chapter Twelve)

**Fascicle Five**
13. The Eight Solar Terms (Chapter Thirteen)

**Fascicle Six**
14. The Rites of Fasting and Abstinence (Chapter Fourteen)
15. The Manifestation of the Numinous (Chapter Fifteen)
16. The Subjugation of Demons (Chapter Sixteen)

**Fascicle Seven**
17. The Dao’s Transformation of the Four Barbarians (Chapter Seventeen)

**Fascicle Eight**
18. The Secluded Dwelling (Chapter Eighteen)

**Fascicle Nine**
19. The Perfected of Luminous Might Subduing Evil (Chapter Nineteen)

**Fascicle Ten**
20. The Dharma Seal (Chapter Twenty)

**The Supreme Great Dao Jade Clarity Scripture, Fascicle One**
**1. The Origin of the Dao (Chapter One)**

The Dao spoke: In former times, the Most High Primordial Heavenly Worthy, together with countless sages and worthies in the billions, roamed throughout the realms. Finally, he gazed down upon the Abandoned-Worthy World.

At that time, the people of the Four Continents had exhausted their merit and virtue, and before long, the great kalpa would shift its course. The people withered and perished, the world lost its stability, the Great Dao ceased to circulate, and all favored warfare. Punishments and killings knew no bounds; armies arose everywhere, and mutual harm was plotted. Neighboring states severed righteousness and ceased friendly exchange. The strong plundered the weak, seizing from the orphaned and widowed. Bandits and thieves arose on all sides, and Heaven sent forth omens of calamity. The sun and moon were eclipsed, stars fell from their lodgings, the Seven Luminaries moved in reverse, and thunder and rain came without clouds. At times, blood rained down along with other strange portents. Drought and flood were unbalanced, the hundred grains withered and dried, the great earth quaked and split open everywhere, mountains and peaks collapsed, gold and jade melted away, ferocious beasts devoured people, and malevolent spirits revealed their forms, spreading poison and pestilence. The earth sprouted hair, the six livestock spoke in human voices, and the countless people of the world were unsettled in heart. Rulers and ministers grew suspicious of one another, fathers and sons punished each other, and none cultivated the good Dao, favoring only evil. Over five hundred years, this grew ever more severe, and none could find life. Some, unable to bear the suffering and distress, threw themselves into abysses or fire, or hanged themselves to die. Hunger and hardship drove people to consume one another. The great earth grew parched, and springs ceased to flow.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy and the assembly of sages, moved by compassion for the short-lived beings who had no refuge, saw them flee in terror, wailing in sorrow, their pain as if scorched by fire and poison. Thereupon, by the power of the Heavenly Worthy’s great compassion, he and the assembly of sages sat together in the mysterious void, a hundred *zhang* above the earth. Then the heavens and earth trembled greatly for seven days and seven nights without ceasing. The empty sky announced auspicious signs: the sun and moon bore double wheels, their radiance resplendent; the stars shone brightly; wind and rain dispersed; clouds and mist spread forth; the sequence of *qi* was harmonious. Fragrant smoke coiled through the void, Brahmanic chants rang in unison, golden bells chimed clearly, jade chimes and bells resounded, the thunderous tones carried far and wide, and myriad celestial melodies played of themselves in the sky. Dragon thrones were arrayed, feathered canopies stretched high, numinous standards cast shadows in the heavens, long banners draped from the sky, immortal blossoms carpeted the earth, and cloudy curtains veiled the void. Lions raised their voices, divine deer bowed their cries, golden phoenixes sang in harmony, horned dragons intoned, jade chimes kept rhythm, and the ten thousand sounds hummed in unison.

The Heavenly Worthy and the assembly of sages together emitted the light of their bodies, illuminating the ten directions, leaving no darkness unlit. Their light was of a thousand kinds, shifting in myriad ways in an instant. Within each light appeared Perfected Ones, and each Perfected One had their own retinue. Clear voices rang out, expounding the wondrous Dharma.

All the kings, ministers, and people of the Four Continents, both human and non-human, each saw the Heavenly Worthy, the Great Sage, seated in the void, conferring with the Great Creator Perfected Lord and the Mighty Numinous Immortals to determine the kalpa’s reckoning, rescue and deliver the myriad beings, re-examine the great register of the Azure Origin, and extend the appointed course. On golden tablets, they inscribed the true writs of the Five Thearchs and the cloudy, radiant chapters to pacify the five directions. He then commanded the Five Thearchs, the spirits of the rivers, and the Dragon Kings of the Four Seas to unblock the flow of springs. Heaven showered sweet dew to moisten the great earth. He ordered the Earl of Wind and the Master of Rain to harmonize *yin* and *yang*, making cold and heat appropriate. He commanded the Five Thearchs and the earth spirits to harmonize the hundred grains and cause medicinal herbs to grow. He dispatched the envoys of the Five Thearchs to slay and subdue demonic forces. He ordered the Heavenly Dragons and Thunder Gods to startle and discipline the treacherous and rebellious, striking fear into the *yin* evil. He commanded the Arrayed Immortals of the Gathering Winds to harmonize the *qi*, refine human conduct, and cause rulers and ministers to live in harmony, fathers to be kind and children filial. The murderous turned to goodness, the hidden and manifest returned to unity, poison and pestilence hid away, and evil demons concealed their forms. Fragrant blossoms and medicinal herbs flourished everywhere; the five grains bore fruit and ripened in winter and summer.

The sweet waters of flowing springs overflowed and spread in abundance. He further commanded the Five Dipper Immortals to align the celestial pivot, demarcate the sun’s path, and arrange the constellations. He dispatched the Four Heavenly Benevolent Spirits to assist the Son of Heaven. He assigned immortal officials to successively oversee state governance, causing the world to be transformed by virtue, the myriad people to live in peace and joy, neighboring states to engage in exchange, and resentments to dissolve. People upheld great righteousness, all walked the true Dao, and each kept to their proper place.

Thereupon, the Most High Lord of the Great Dao, pitying the teeming masses in their perilous fragility, fanned the mysterious wind to guide all living beings. They feasted on harmonious *qi* and bathed in the transformative power of the Dao, returning from decay to flourishing, turning failure into success.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy, together with the great sages and countless multitudes, each descended upon the various lands in jeweled celestial terraces. In those lands, the Son of Heaven, the kings, ministers, and all the people—men and women, young and old—everywhere made offerings with incense, flowers, banners, and music, singing praises as they listened to the Dharma.

At that time, the Dao Lord of the Southern Eight Barbarians, accompanied by sixty-four billion holy multitudes, descended from the Southern Prosperity Palace in crimson cloud chariots. From the Dark Heavens of the North, the True Lords of the Five Northern Tribes, with twenty-five million billion immortal officials, descended in black cloud chariots. In the void, they assessed the cycles of water and fire, the kalpas and their appointed times.

At that time, the Dao Lord of the Western Six Tribes, with thirty-six million billion perfected immortals, descended from the Luminous Origin Heaven in chariots of threefold radiant mist. At that time, the Dao Lord of the Eastern Nine Yi Tribes, with eighty-one billion multitudes, descended from the Primordial Azure Heaven in chariots of jade-green flying wheels. Together with the Dao Lord of the Six Tribes, they assessed the disasters of war and illness, recording the registers of good and evil deeds and their consequences.

Thereafter, the Central Void Sovereign, the Most Mysterious Ancient Lord, received the jade tallies from his left and right attendants and was entreated to expound the wondrous principles of creation, the profound and secret methods, to correctly determine the celestial origins, reverse the turning of the cosmic cycles, harmonize the four *qi*, and bring forth the myriad existences.

At that time, in the world of Abandoned Worthiness, there was a king named Virtue-Righteous, intelligent and upright, sharp-witted and discerning. He was a being of karmic fortune and virtuous power, descended in response to the times to serve as a guide for all living beings. He addressed all the ministers and people, men and women, within his domain, saying: “Now we have attained great peace, the world is at rest, fires and disasters have ceased, wars and illnesses do not arise, and the hundred grains ripen—all through the grace of the Dao, not by natural occurrence. How shall we repay this boundless grace? We must devote our hearts and minds, reverently make offerings, establish palaces and temples, present incense, flowers, lamps, and candles, and morning and evening perform rituals, recitations, fasts, and repentance to seek blessings and protection. Now is the very moment when the Heavenly Worthy is assessing fortune and misfortune, the appointed times of the kalpas. I shall act on my own behalf and on yours, prostrating myself to take refuge in the Most High and True, specially beseeching compassion and deliverance, that the supreme Dharma be bestowed upon us. May the lives of all men and women within my domain be prolonged, each completing their allotted span. Moreover, I wish to invite the Most High and True to descend upon my land, to express my humble devotion and the sincerity of my offerings. Do you, my people, share this wish?”

Thereupon, sixty thousand elders—including the Elder of Spiritual Mind, the Elder of Five Penetrations, the Elder of Literary Brilliance, and the Elder of Mystic Understanding—came from the four directions to pay their respects to the king. Hearing the king’s decree, they dared not fully believe. There were also eighty great ministers, with the Minister of Treasure Brilliance as their chief. The remaining ministers and elders harbored doubts, turning to one another and saying: “Since our birth into this world, from our ancestors and fathers, we have heard of the true Dao, yet our eyes have never beheld it. The great void is vast and empty—where is the proof? Now we enjoy peace and freedom from heaven; what has this to do with the power of the Dao?”

At that time, the Minister of Treasure Brilliance, wise and eloquent, upright in speech, whose words were always verified and trusted throughout the land, perceived the people’s skepticism and lack of pure faith. Before the king, he raised his voice and proclaimed: “I have heard that the Supreme Ultimate Heavenly Worthy established heaven and earth, covering and supporting the myriad things, opening the sun and moon, arranging the stars, circulating the true *qi*, and nurturing all living beings. Though dwelling in the upper realms, he responds and transforms the lower lands. The present great peace and the prolongation of the kalpa’s destiny are all through the power of the Dao. Yet living beings, dull and ignorant, know only their daily affairs, their hearts devoid of shame or reverence. They forget their origins and say that this peace and freedom come from heaven alone, unrelated to the power of the Dao. How can you deceive yourselves thus? I have heard that the Great Dao gives birth to heaven and earth.”

Heaven and earth honor the Dao, thus attaining tranquility; the myriad things value virtue, thus achieving full generation. If you do not believe in the Dao, this is your gravest fault—just as the foolish and deluded in the world, their hearts devoid of compassion, turn against their parents, abandon their siblings, and yet dwell complacently, claiming their well-being is self-derived, not owing to their parents. Your ignorance is no different.

As Baoming spoke these words, his virtue shook heaven and earth, the empty sky rained blossoms, and fragrant clouds enveloped the four directions. Then a voice from the heavens above resounded: *"The Dao does not proclaim itself; the true person does not boast of merit. Within the profound and obscure, there is faith—through kindness and benevolence, all may be united."*

The voice from the void had scarcely faded when, in an instant, from the northwest arose sudden winds, thunder, and lightning, clouds and mist obscuring the sky. Only the Heavenly King and Baoming remained bathed in light, each surrounded by a radiance spanning a *zhang*. From afar, the people witnessed these auspicious signs, their hearts stirred with remorse. They kowtowed, begging for mercy, surrendering to the great king, their faith now aligned with the unseen covenant.

In a moment, the winds and thunder vanished, the clouds and mist dispersed, and the entire kingdom’s ministers and people prostrated before the king: *"We do not yet understand the teachings Your Majesty has imparted. We beseech the descent of the Heavenly Perfected to your presence, that you may instruct us—what is required?"* They pleaded, *"May the great king take pity on living beings and awaken those who have not yet heard."*

The king replied: *"The Dao resides in the human heart. You must only offer reverent devotion, establish palaces and temples, provide for their needs, and morning and evening perform rites and prayers, repenting of transgressions and seeking blessings."*

Hearing this, the people rejoiced in their hearts, bowing in gratitude for the gift of rebirth. The king further instructed: *"Each of you may now return home, retreat in fasting to reflect on your faults, purify body and mind, and inform those who have not yet heard, as I have commanded."*

The people, having heard, took their leave at once and returned to their homes. The king then ordered the minister Baoming to announce throughout the city and its outskirts that all should prepare the palace halls, sweep and purify the streets, burn incense everywhere, and offer reverent devotion, arranging all worldly possessions—beds and seats—with utmost care.

When the day of retreat concluded, the people from the four directions gathered like clouds. The king, together with his inner and outer ministers and their families, sprinkled the ground with fragrant water, set out beds and canopies, and made all necessary preparations. The entire kingdom, great and small, bowed in reverence to the ten directions, performing rites and prayers for seven days and seven nights, beseeching the descent of the Supreme Perfected to the earth below. *"How pitiable are the dull and ignorant beings!"*

Then, at noon on the fifteenth day of the third month, from the northwest of the heavens suddenly appeared nine-colored streaming clouds, their radiance resplendent, fragrant winds pure and refreshing, celestial chants harmonious and refined, heavenly music flowing and bright. Sweet dew rained from the sky, the great earth trembled, and a shower of jeweled celestial blossoms fell, startling the land.

Cloud chariots and feathered canopies floated through the void, arriving in splendor. The multitude of perfected sages and great saints each rode upon celestial jewel platforms, within which shone a light that illumined the night. Five-colored divine radiance illuminated the empty sky, its brilliance surpassing sun and moon, descending upon the royal city and lingering for seven days and seven nights.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy, through the power of compassion, accomplished great mercy, rescuing and protecting living beings, taking pity on them, opening the ears of the deaf and the eyes of the blind, healing all ailments, serving as their guide and ferry, safeguarding the kalpa’s destiny, and renewing the myriad things.

Thereupon, the king, his ministers, and all the people bowed again, earnestly entreating the Heavenly Worthy to unfold the great transformation, to compassionately instruct the multitude, to clarify their senses, and to guide them to the true Dao, that they might receive the secret essentials.

Then the Heavenly Worthy commanded the Immortal of Vast Spirit to address the king: *"You, as ruler of a kingdom, are esteemed by all under heaven, having attained the highest earthly rank, a position of unparalleled honor. Yet if you govern with upright law and do not oppress the people, this alone is enough to move heaven with merit—why trouble yourself with the secret essentials? The secret essentials of the Dao are not easily heard in haste."*

The king and his ministers, being beings of accumulated virtue, sought through expedient means to open the eyes and ears of living beings. The Heavenly Worthy declared: *"The gateway to the secret essentials lies in nothing other than kindness and goodness; the method of kindness and goodness does not transgress the precepts and prohibitions. Through the power of great compassion, I perfect the realm."*

Hearing this, all rejoiced exceedingly, their hearts filled with the desire to uphold the precepts. The Heavenly Worthy continued: *"Precepts are of many kinds, and people are of many grades. The highest grade of person commits no transgressions in body. Having no transgressions, they have nothing to uphold. The middle grade of person has a heart that wavers between high and low; upon encountering circumstances, their nature changes. They restrain themselves with precepts, preventing recklessness. Such persons may receive the Ten Precepts or the Five Precepts to guard themselves. The lowest grade of person harbors myriad evil intentions, difficult to restrain. Among the lowest, there are two types: the higher of these desires to uphold precepts and may receive the One Hundred Ninety-Nine Precepts, or the Three Hundred Great Precepts of Observing the Body, or the One Thousand Two Hundred Precepts of Dignified Conduct, to protect themselves and prevent transgression. The lowest of the low are like beasts in body; though they possess human form, they lack a human heart. Even if they receive precepts, it will be of no benefit."*

*"For now, I shall bestow the second, middle-grade precepts—the Ten Prohibitions as the initial gateway to the Dao."*

Hearing this, the people rejoiced beyond measure, all prostrating themselves to receive the precepts. The Heavenly Worthy declared:

*"The first precept: Do not defy or disobey parents or teachers, nor commit the sin of filial impiety.*
*The second precept: Do not kill living beings, nor slaughter, harm, or sever the lives of creatures.*
*The third precept: Do not rebel against the sovereign or plot to harm the state or family. This precept is the weightiest. Why? Because all kings are those who govern through the turning of the kalpa’s destiny, ruling over all under heaven. They are the pivot upon which all people depend. Without a ruler, none would meet a proper end. For this reason, you must understand."*

The fourth precept: Do not engage in lewdness or disorder with kin—mothers, aunts, sisters, or other women.
The fifth precept: Do not slander the Daoist teachings or recklessly disclose scriptural texts.
The sixth precept: Do not defile or profane the sacred altar, nor expose yourself while wearing only a single garment.
The seventh precept: Do not bully the orphaned or impoverished, nor seize others’ property.
The eighth precept: Do not expose the Three Luminaries to contempt, nor mistreat the elderly or infirm.
The ninth precept: Do not indulge in wine to the point of recklessness, nor engage in duplicity or vicious cursing.
The tenth precept: Do not act with wolfish cruelty, nor wrongfully impose harsh punishments.

These Ten Precepts must be upheld throughout one’s life.

The Heavenly Worthy declared:
*"Those who are unfilial to parents or teachers will, upon death, fall into hell and remain there for ten thousand kalpas. Even if reborn among humans, they will be orphaned and destitute, subjected to others’ scorn, and forever dwell in lowliness.
Those who delight in killing will, for five hundred lifetimes, endure being cut and sliced, suffering myriad torments.
Those who rebel against their sovereign will, upon death, enter hell and endure ten thousand kalpas of agony. Upon rebirth, they will dwell in borderlands without a ruler, constantly besieged and living in perpetual terror.
The precept against lewdness is the gravest. If any man or woman, even for a single thought-moment, harbors lustful desires toward parents, aunts, uncles, brothers, sisters, or any kin of the six relations, they will suffer hell’s retribution for eighty thousand great kalpas—pierced by iron nails, burned and boiled in countless ways. Emerging from hell, they will take the forms of the six livestock. After another eighty thousand kalpas, they will become worms in filth, and after yet another eighty thousand kalpas, their suffering shall continue.
Good men, you must now understand: even a single thought-moment of lust toward kin brings such retribution. How much greater, then, is the sin of those who commit such acts with their own flesh and blood? Their crimes are beyond description.
Such people must not share the same path, dwelling, seat, or bed. They must not live in the same village. I name them the Ten Evils. Though their bodies may appear strong, their souls are seized by malevolent spirits, and no benevolent deities will protect them. Their presence defiles the Dao; they must be swiftly expelled and barred from instruction. Those who would teach them would become their kind—doomed to rise and fall together.
Nine generations of their ancestors will be punished. I name them the Corrupters of Humanity.
Good men and women, you must now understand: lewdness, killing, plunder, theft, bullying the orphaned and weak, neglecting the poor and sick, slandering the true Dao, harming those of virtuous conduct, and profaning sacred texts—these sins are of the utmost gravity. I need not enumerate them all.
You must only guard the precepts with utmost sincerity, and the Dao will naturally descend upon you."*

Thereupon, the king, ministers, and all good men rejoiced and vowed to uphold them, daring not to transgress. The Dao Lord then commanded the Mighty Spirit True Lord to bestow upon the king the *Cloud-Script Heavenly Writ*—a thousand esoteric methods comprising the upper, middle, and lower chapters—inscribed on tablets of supple jade with characters of purple gold. The king received and recited them diligently.

The scripture was declared a celestial treasure: *"Those who recite it with devotion will gain the power of flight, never perish, and master the Six Penetrations, their will made manifest."*

The Dao Lord then addressed the king: *"You must understand: beneath the Four Heavens, all ages share the same fortune as this day. The majestic power of the Great Dao follows all beings, guiding and transforming them in ways beyond imagination. After a thousand days, you may transmit this dharma to the upright and worthy within your realm, that together you may govern the world, widely open the gates of the Mysterious, and let the Dao’s transformation flow freely. Let all men and women in the kingdom guard the precepts as they would a luminous pearl. Let the king and his ministers govern with righteousness and recite the true writ with single-minded devotion. Instruct the entire kingdom to establish temples, dedicating themselves solely to the Dao, seeking nothing else."*

The people of the kingdom bowed in reverence and departed. The king recited the true writ for a thousand days, then abdicated his throne to enter meditation, entrusting governance to his eldest son, named Good Cultivation, who followed his father’s example. After more than ninety years, the throne was passed to his younger brother, named Goodness, who likewise governed in his father’s manner. Over six thousand descendants of the royal line succeeded one another for thirty-six thousand years, and the world knew perfect peace.

The former king and Good Cultivation upheld the most wondrous practices for over forty years, attaining the Six Penetrations. Though they managed state affairs by day, their spiritual progress remained unobstructed. The Dao Lord had previously granted them the rank of Middle Immortals to oversee governance, though they had not yet ascended to the Great Ultimate. From this day forward, the Most High Dao Lord, recognizing their immense merit, bestowed upon them the secret essentials and appointed the king and his sons as Supreme Perfected Ones, commanding them to attend the Heavenly Perfected, teach the kingdoms, manifest in various forms to relieve suffering, expound the dharma, and deliver beings.

Thereupon, the Supreme Perfected and the assembly of sages alternately revealed their teachings, serving as masters and disciples to one another. In the first year of the Kai Guang era, on the fifteenth day of the seventh month, they crossed the Dark Valley to the north and ascended the Terrace of Lofty Wind. There, they paid homage to the Supreme True Lord and entreated entry into the Great Luo Heaven to pay respects to the Ancestor of Primordial Qi and the Origin of the Lofty Mysterious.

The True Lord said: *"Though you have attained the Six Penetrations, your Daoist cultivation remains incomplete. Why? You are not self-so; you have become perfected through study. Yet the Origin of Primordial Qi is a being of true qi, spontaneously transformed—a natural body. The Ancestor of Primordial Qi is uniquely revered among the ten thousand Dao, the Great Sage who entrusts qi, the True One of Emptiness and Non-Being. To behold him is nearly impossible, for his transformations are as countless as one, vast and boundless, serene and tranquil, empty and still, expansive and profound, utterly beyond words and forms. The myriad Dao of the ten directions—thirty-six thousand kinds in all—trace their origin to the True One of Emptiness and Non-Being. Since my own attainment of the Dao, countless kalpas have passed, and I have met him but twice. Now, the Heavenly Emperor has reviewed the turning of the kalpa and issued a decree: you are to descend to the Four Heavens, teach the kingdoms, disseminate the Dao’s qi, and attend the Heavenly Worthy in guiding all beings."*

Why is this so? To prolong the calamity of this kalpa’s fire and qi, the Dao’s teachings must be practiced to suppress the misfortune of the Nine Yangs and extinguish the essence of fire. Yet when the kalpa’s end arrives and heaven and earth collapse, when the people’s fortune is exhausted, the Dharma will no longer save them. The extremity of fate’s reckoning is thus by nature. At the beginning of the water kalpa, my Dao flourished greatly, and for three hundred seventy thousand years, the people remained pure and simple. Thereafter, the Great Dao gradually waned, yin qi grew dominant, and the people turned to reckless fortune-seeking. They built empty tombs and erected temples across the world. Men and women, their hearts perverse, practiced destructive rites, disregarding proper forms. They wailed and begged for death, leapt into fire pits or plunged into deep abysses, slashed themselves or severed their own limbs. They gathered in crowds to perform the Dao, singing hymns and weeping bitterly. Some entered empty tombs to sit in silence; others embraced corpses or revered dry bones. They made altars of filth or smeared the ground with incense and ashes, disrespected their parents, and engaged in every manner of ascetic suffering. They consumed foul and vile things, committing every conceivable transgression—yet still could not attain the true and orthodox Dao. Their hearts grew crooked, and father and son abandoned righteousness, while factions thrived in false teachings.

Before the great water kalpa, there came a lesser water kalpa, lasting ten years before subsiding. Thereafter, for four thousand years, within the false teachings, wars arose, and men schemed against one another. Some proclaimed themselves kings, ruling for ten or a hundred days before perishing by their own hands. Father and son cast aside propriety, the strong oppressed the weak, and even those of the same bloodline debauched one another. Though they bore human form, they lacked human hearts—ruthless and reckless, trusting no one. When this time arrives, false ways will flourish, yin qi will reach its peak, and before long, floods will surge, drowning all, transforming men into fish, devoured by dragons and serpents. At this juncture, the Dharma demands the selection of the seed-people, to be placed in lands of blessing. You must toil diligently, never slackening from dawn to dusk. This is what it means for the Great Dao to be magnified through humanity: my destiny lies in my own hands, shaped by my conduct. A heart aligned with the Dao invokes its response; following perversity invites calamity. Those who delight in killing will be felled by their own violence—thus, one must practice great compassion.

**Chapter Two: Corresponding Retributions**

At that time, the Supreme Perfected, accompanied by thirty-six thousand newly attained Daoists from the Great Clarity Heaven, attended the Heavenly Worthy in teaching the farthest reaches of the celestial realms. They descended to the lower worlds, journeying among the barbarian lands, the kingdoms of birds and beasts, and all manner of beings. Adapting to their inclinations, they manifested diverse teachings, instructing and benefiting them through expedient miracles, subduing their hearts with majestic transformations.

They arrived at the western edge of the Blackwater, where there lay a world spanning eight thousand *li*. Its myriad beings, of every kind, dwelled in caves and devoured one another. The land bore thorny brambles, poisonous grasses, and toxic trees, while its springs ran black and foul, unfit for washing or drinking. On the western border of this land flowed a great river, square in shape and over five thousand *li* wide. Its waters were turbid and filthy, teeming with venomous dragons. The river’s winds and waves raged violently, making crossing by boat impossible.

Along the river’s eastern bank stretched a plain of three thousand *li*, rising five hundred *zhang* above the water’s edge. Half the people in this world were eyeless, groping their way forward, devouring one another when hungry and drinking blood when thirsty. Those with eyes suffered from loathsome diseases—brows and hair falling out, bodies festering with sores, oozing pus and filth. Serpents abounded, swallowing people whole. There was no order of ruler and subject, no bond of father and son; instead, they fought ceaselessly. The eyeless, hearing the clash of weapons, fled in terror, some tumbling into the river to be devoured by dragons. Those who avoided the river were eaten by marauding bands, their cries of terror and agony echoing in despair.

Foul ditches overflowed with putrid sludge, their stench unbearable. Within these pits writhed countless maggots, their heads resembling men’s, their bodies a *zhang* long, writhing on their bellies and wailing. Vultures and monstrous birds pecked at them, leaving the ground strewn with rotting flesh. Malevolent ghosts, their fur like needles, exhaled scorching breath that burned like fire.

To the north of this plain lay six great hells, their gates each a *zhang* square. Descending into them, the space widened endlessly, their depths unfathomable. Within, only the sounds of wind, thunder, fire chariots, wailing, and torment could be heard—the clamor of blades, saws, hammers, and cudgels. Voices cried out for rescue, for life. Smoke and flames raged, their fire and fumes billowing skyward.

In the first hell to the west, the roar of wind and water resounded, its air so bitterly cold it could not be approached. From the darkness came faint, mournful cries. The winds from all six hells carried an indescribable stench of burning and decay.

A *li* and a half north of the hells’ gates bubbled a scalding spring, six *li* wide. Its boiling waters churned with yellow fat, grease, rotting skin, bones, and flesh. From within came faint, pitiful wails, the spring’s vapors searing all they touched.

North of the spring rose mountains of blades and forests of swords, strewn with fresh and old corpses, severed limbs, and flesh hanging from the weapons’ edges. The sight of such suffering was unbearable to behold.

There was also a hell of flaying alive, where those who had slaughtered sheep in life fell after death. For five hundred years, they endured torment before being reborn as sheep, then spent another five hundred lives repaying their debt in kind, trapped in an endless cycle of retribution.

East of the boiling spring lay the Wind-Blade Hell, a *li* wide, where those who had corrupted the true teachings—violating precepts, leaking sacred texts, transmitting them to the unworthy, or peddling the Dao for personal gain—were cast after death. For a kalpa, they suffered as fierce winds hurled them against razor-sharp blades, dying and reviving a thousand times in a single day.

Having emerged from hell, they are reborn among humans, their bodies afflicted with perverse maladies, their faculties dull and benighted, forever dwelling in the lowest strata, never to hear the Dharma again. When the sinful souls of hell at last escape, they are mostly born in borderlands or godforsaken realms, constantly beset by raids and pillage, living in terror day and night, their bodies stunted and misshapen, their breath foul and rank, never to hear the Dharma.

Moved by the unceasing anguish of these sinners, the Dao Lord, together with the Supreme Perfected and the host of sages, came to the deliverance of the damned and the deaf-and-blind of this world, that they might awaken to life and death. Thereupon, in the void above this world, a hundred *zhang* from the earth, they bowed from afar to the primordial qi.

The Most High and Lofty Heavenly Worthy, through the divine power of the Dao, entered the Great Samādhi of the Six Voids. Splitting into a hundred million bodies, each body in turn radiated a thousand kinds of light, and within each light sat a perfected immortal upon a flying-dragon throne, expounding the wondrous Dharma. The jade-like voices resounded like thunder; to the left, golden bells tolled, to the right, jade chimes rang. A canopy of nine-colored radiant mist enveloped this realm, and within each mist sat a host of sages, preaching the Dharma. The great earth trembled, sweet dew rained from heaven, fragrant springs overflowed, all sounds stilled into emptiness, the Three Luminaries shone as one. The earth brought forth a hundred grains, waters turned cool and clear, human hearts grew pure and guileless, free from mutual harm. Venomous dragons sheathed their poison, plague demons hid their forms, hell’s sorrows ceased, the blades of sword-trees snapped, sinful souls were reborn, chronic ailments healed, the deaf and blind regained their senses, the maimed and crippled were restored to wholeness.

So vast was this transformation that no name could encompass it. Among the assembly, those newly attained to the Dao, not yet ascended to the highest mystery, beheld this divine marvel yet knew not its source. Then arose from the multitude a youth of the Five Penetrations, named Good Accumulation, together with Golden-Tressed Youth, Flower-Wisdom Youth, and Treasured Light Youth—eighty-four thousand in all—who rose from their seats, knelt with hands clasped, and addressed the Heavenly Worthy:

“Since attaining the Dao, we have traversed eighty thousand great kalpas, journeying through the eight directions, reaching every place, yet never have we witnessed the majestic, divine, and sovereign power of the Great Dao as we do today. We rejoice in this assembly, having encountered this vast transformation. We only pray that the True and Perfected One take pity on the unenlightened, awaken the dull-rooted, and resolve all doubts.”

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy remained silent. The youths entreated thrice without cease, until at last the Heavenly Worthy gathered his thoughts into profound stillness, his divine radiance serene and luminous. He snapped his fingers, cleared his throat, and after a long while, spoke:

“Excellent, excellent! Your question is profound and subtle indeed. The Great Dao is vast and silent, its principle beyond perception or hearing, abstruse and recondite, obscure and deeply trustworthy. Though you have traversed kalpas and preserved the Dao and its virtue, the realm you inhabit lies close to the Supreme Clarity, yet remains utterly cut off from the Profound Mystery. How could you merge with the transformation, scattered among thirty-six thousand kinds, yet remain ignorant of the origin of the Highest Mystery of the Great Luo? Bound by what you see and hear, how can you fathom this wondrous truth? To wander freely without hindrance and attain enduring existence—this you may achieve. But to forget the Lord of Primordial Qi and the calamity of premature demise—from this, you have yet to be delivered.”

Then, upon hearing the Heavenly Worthy’s discourse, Shanji’s mind opened and his understanding deepened. Together with the multitude of youths, he reflected inwardly: “By virtue of profound blessings accumulated in past lives, I have encountered this auspicious gathering—joy beyond all previous experience. Now that I have attained awakening, I vow to ascend to the Great Luo, to pay homage before the Primordial Qi’s Ancestor, the Highest Mystery Dao Lord, and to receive the secret teachings and the path of cultivation.”

Thereupon, Shanji and his retinue of eighty-four thousand advanced together and made obeisance, saying: “Most High Dao Lord, we have been graciously enlightened in matters never before heard. We now wish to lead this assembly in ascending to the Great Luo, to pay reverence before the Highest Mystery’s august presence. We beseech the Dao Lord to show compassion and grant permission.”

The Dao Lord replied: “If you wish to depart, you must relinquish all that is seen and heard. Though you lead a great multitude, let your mind remain without companions; devote yourself single-mindedly to stillness and resolve. Let cloud and mud be as one; withdraw your gaze and reverse your hearing—thus shall the Dao spontaneously unite with the Profound. ”

Shanji and his retinue, obeying the teaching, first paid homage to the upper realms, took leave of the Dao Lord, and ascended into the Great Void of the Great Luo Heaven, where they beheld the Lord of Primordial Qi, the Highest Mystery’s Ancestor.

At that time, the people of this realm all found respite and rejoiced, leaping with joy. They raised their hands toward the heavens, snapped their fingers, and exclaimed: “We, burdened by sins from past lives, were born in this wretched land, having forgotten the true mind and clung only to evil, passing it down through generations without awakening. Our sins and habitual defilements cast us into hell, where we cycled through suffering without self-awareness, bound by unyielding karmic bonds. Yet in a single moment, these bonds have dissolved—without the grace of the Dao, what could have saved us? We long to repay this debt, yet know not how. We beseech the Heavenly Worthy to descend to this lower realm, to grant our humble request and fulfill our earnest hearts.”

The Dao Lord, foreseeing their intent, transformed into an ordinary person and wandered among them, conversing and imparting the Dao’s teachings. At times, he begged for alms and lodged among them, instructing them in building shelters and transforming raw into cooked. At times, he served as a guide, expounding the Dharma with skillful means. At times, he became a physician or shaman, healing their illnesses. At times, he was a farmer, teaching them cultivation. At times, he was a filial son, instructing them in kindness and righteousness. Adapting to their forms and inclinations, he established rulers and ministers, gradually reforming their ways, instilling order between elders and youth, and distinction between men and women. Through manifold teachings over fifteen years, harmonious qi flowed freely. The people gradually recognized the Dharma, erecting temples, transcribing scriptures, crafting images, and holding fasts and assemblies. They offered fragrant oils, lamps, and candles, joyfully dedicating their treasures, wholeheartedly revering the Dao. They practiced filial piety, benevolence, and righteousness, observing the rites between ruler and subject. Beings of other kinds were reborn, the dark realms opened to peace, and all creatures kept to their proper places, refraining from mutual harm.

Then, the Dao Lord, assuming the guise of a great master, dwelled in the cold mountains and forests. Sometimes, his disciples observed precepts and expounded the Dharma; at other times, he sat alone in silent contemplation or lectured and recited scriptures for others. At times, his words foretold fortune or misfortune with uncanny accuracy. His transformations were wondrous and unpredictable, ageless in appearance. The entire realm turned to him in devotion, offering all they possessed—burning incense, scattering flowers, and each voicing their heartfelt wishes, longing for the Heavenly Worthy to descend into the dust and defilement to awaken all beings. They prostrated themselves, gazing heavenward, their blood and tears staining the earth, weeping and wailing without cease for seven days and nights.

Then, by virtue of his great compassion, the Dao Lord, accompanied by a host of sages, rode upon nine-colored flowing essence and the true light of qi. Divine youths led the procession, scattering flowers and burning incense. A sacred wind stirred the flutes, and celestial beasts harmonized in song. Qilin danced and phoenixes sang as they floated through the air, halting five measures above the earth.

At that time, the one previously transformed—named Kongsheng—who had served as the foremost guide for all beings, spoke: “Has the Heavenly Worthy, in guiding and transforming us, not wearied? In your compassion, you fashion all things—are you not exhausted? Delaying your cloud-borne chariot, you condescend to descend to this lower realm. We, long mired in kalpas of stagnation, bound by the fetters of sin and defilement, have in an instant been cleansed by the mist, bathed in the Profound Stream. Yet our gratitude overflows beyond measure. The true source is distant and vast, the upper realms empty and boundless, while we, in these defiled bodies, have suddenly encountered great transformation. Our lives, brief as morning mushrooms, now gaze upon the eternal sun; the withered and decayed have blossomed anew. Born in this day of fortune, we dare to voice our humble wishes, though we fear to offend your august presence. We pray that your great compassion may grant us the resolve of ants and insects, unwavering in retreat. If there remain doubts in our hearts, truths yet ungrasped, we beseech your heavenly mercy to reveal our past lives, the causes and conditions of this land, and the origins of its beings. Grant us the favor of your profound insight, and deign to explain.”

Then, all beings in that realm, great and small, prostrated themselves, their blood and tears mingling. The Dao Lord, moved by great compassion, reflected deeply for a long while. He commanded forty-nine left-attendant immortal youths to strike the jade chimes of the Profound Cloud in unison, their voices joining in the celestial harmony of the *Great Elegance*, a melody that unites the divine. He then commanded thirty-six right-attendant immortal youths to play the nine-harmony flutes, blending with the phoenixes’ songs and the ethereal tones of the Eight Assemblies of Jade Capital. He ordered the jade youths of incense to burn the hundred-harmony soul-returning incense. He commanded the long-fanged left officer to strike the golden bell, and the right steward to sound the jade chime. After a long while, the myriad sounds converged. Auspicious clouds wove through the void, streaming radiance in all directions. A divine wind reached the eight extremities, and the celestial music fell silent.

Then, the Heavenly Worthy exhaled a fragrant light, and a great thunderous voice resounded, addressing Kongsheng: “You and all beings born in this land must now understand: the Dao’s compassionate power gives life to and completes all things. Thus, the myriad sounds are played, transforming and harmonizing all existence, uniting and generating qi to dispel afflictions. You and this multitude have come from the midst of afflictions, creating manifold evil karma, cycling through retribution, and falling into this borderland, where you have never heard the good Dao and have forgotten your original mind. This world is called the *Realm of Retribution*; it is also named the *Hell of Birth and Death*.”

These hells exist everywhere, yet beings dwell within them unaware, scorched day and night, awaiting annihilation. This river is called the *Drifting Waves of Karmic Retribution in Birth and Death*. These six great hells correspond to the six senses through which one commits transgressions—upon death, one enters them accordingly.

This boiling cauldron is named the *Boiling Cauldron Hell*; those in the world who scald living beings to death fall into this hell, unable to escape for kalpas. These mountains of blades and forests of swords are for worldly fools who delight in stabbing and slashing animals—they suffer this torment after death. Those who are flayed alive in life are worldly fools who rob others’ wealth, carve flesh from living fish, and endure suffering after death, their flesh torn from their bodies while still alive.

These venomous dragons and pythons are the retribution for evil persons who destroy merit and oppress the virtuous. The worms in this cesspool are worldly fools who harbor murderous intent toward their parents, uncles, aunts, sisters, or kin of the same surname, or who lust after their uncles, aunts, sisters, the six relations, parents, or teachers—upon death, they enter hell, unabsolved for ten thousand kalpas, and now take the form of these worms, forever dwelling in filth, feeding on foulness.

Kongsheng, know that the sins of those in the world who betray kin, commit incest, or harbor murderous intent are so vast that even ten thousand kalpas of explanation could not exhaust them. Such persons are certainly barred from the Dao; no divine spirits descend upon them, and no life-giving qi is bestowed. Kongsheng, you must now understand: such evil persons are irredeemable in body and mind, beyond teaching or transformation. You must distance yourself from them, refuse their offerings, avoid sitting on their beds, and never enter their doors—those who do violate the precepts and incur the envy of demonic spirits. Among the thirty-six thousand rules of conduct, this precept is the weightiest.

Thus, I earnestly reiterate this for you. Now widely propagate and recite this scripture. Those who are deaf or blind and cannot read it should constantly burn incense, bow in reverence, and make offerings to the scripture—its merit is boundless. The impoverished who cannot copy the scripture should visit households that possess it to practice the Dao and pay homage.

Kongsheng, know that according to the statutes of the Perfected, good men and women who delight in releasing living beings, aid the destitute, heal the sick, honor their parents, dwell in mountain forests, and recite the true scriptures—these five virtues are equal in merit, and those who embody them shall be delivered in life and attain the true Dao. Kongsheng, you must enlighten the unenlightened and awaken their understanding.

At that moment, the great assembly, having heard the Heavenly Worthy’s words, experienced awakening in body and mind. Overjoyed, they received the essential teachings, bowed in reverence, and departed.

**Chapter Three: The World**

Then, the Heavenly Worthy, accompanied by his retinue of divine attendants and perfected sages, soared through the air over the southern reaches of the Fiery Continent and entered the Pool of Radiant Refinement. There, he subdued the fire spirits with a scripture of the Black Emperor, and all returned at once. Proceeding eastward, they passed the southern shores of Fusang, traversing ninety million miles to a land of virtue and goodness.

This land spans over eighty thousand *li* in each direction, bordered by four seas, and is also called the *Realm of Ultimate Bliss*. Its king is named Flower Splendor, with eight hundred ministers, thirty-eight thousand attendants, and sixty-four great cities, along with six thousand four hundred smaller cities. The king governs with righteous law, never oppressing the people. The land is prosperous, abundant in treasures, with temperate seasons, harmonious winds and rains, ample grain and silk, and free from illness and suffering.

In the northwest of this land lies another city, square in shape and spanning two thousand five hundred and forty *li*, its walls towering seven thousand *ren* high. It has four great gates, each six thousand *ren* tall and a *li* wide, with towers of extraordinary splendor and magnificence. Within the city stand seven thousand jeweled terraces, each emanating the radiance of luminous moons, illuminating dawn and dusk. The city is inhabited solely by immortals and Daoists, their forms like gold and jade, nourished by the celestial kitchens.

This king, his ministers, and all attendants are divine beings incarnate, governing the realm with wisdom. Thrice daily, fragrant winds sweep away the dust, and sweet dew falls to moisten the earth. The land abounds with springs and pools, all connected to jade springs, where yellow marrow flows—those who drink this water take on forms like gold and jade.

Thrice daily, phoenixes sing, myriad sounds resonate in the void, fragrant clouds gather in the sky, and celestial music fills the air—elegant and refined, its subtle tones clear and bright. This is not by chance but the result of accumulated merit.

Then, the Heavenly Worthy and nine hundred million sages rested in this city, seated upon flying dragon thrones of a hundred treasures, each throne ten thousand *ren* high, rising above the city. Cloud brocade and jade gauze served as their cushions, and nine-colored canopies of flowing mist were spread, each adorned with luminous moon-jewels. At the four corners of the canopies, within the void, dragon candles shone, and divine phoenixes danced in the air. The wind harps resounded through the heavens, and fragrant vapors wafted, celestial incense drifting on the breeze.

Then, the Heavenly Perfected commanded the left immortal attendant to strike the golden divine bell, the right immortal attendant to sound the luminous chime, and the jade attendant of incense to burn the hundred harmonies of incense in the nine-dragon brazier. The true forms arrayed themselves, and the celestial melody unfolded.

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy emitted a fragrant light from his body, illuminating the world in myriad transformations beyond description. The sound of his finger-snap was like thunder. The men and women of the land, hearing it, awakened and said to one another: “What auspicious sign is this today? The fragrant light penetrates all, the winds and thunder harmonize, and all beings—whether rising or falling, flying or walking—leap and dance for joy. This is no ordinary event; let us hasten to see its cause!”

Then the king, princes, ministers, consorts, and royal kin turned to one another and said: “Our land is blessed with accumulated virtue, and great sages often descend here. This cannot be mere coincidence—it must be an auspicious omen. Each of you, prepare yourselves with all necessary provisions. Tomorrow, I shall lead you all to the jeweled city.”

The men and women of the realm arrived together, and from afar they saw the radiant brilliance within the city. Within that light, true immortals chanted sacred hymns. The king and his people bowed their heads in reverence, saying: “Today we are fortunate indeed to behold the Heavenly Worthy descending into this jeweled city. Joy and blessing converge beyond all thought.” Each burned incense and voiced their vows.

The king and his people stood at the southern gate, prostrating themselves upon the ground, remaining there for a long while. They reflected: “By what cause, through what blessed fortune, do we encounter this day? We dare not lift our gaze to the august countenance. We only pray that the great compassion of the exalted perfected ones may take pity upon us, awaken those who have not yet heard, and unravel the web of our doubts.”

After a long while, the Heavenly Worthy cleared his throat, snapped his fingers, and the celestial music ceased. He addressed the king: “This world of yours is a land of blessing, where exalted beings of the upper realms often wander. Yet the kalpas stretch far beyond your understanding. Before heaven and earth were illuminated, before the primordial chaos had divided, the Heavenly Worthy, the supreme sage, descended into this city. Even now, nine hundred million great kalpas have passed. Long ago, I came here with the Lord of Creation to assess the turning of the kalpas. Now I return to observe this world once more—such is the workings of karmic conditions, and I shall come again in due time.

Moreover, the late-learned immortals within this city have cultivated their practices to maturity. Though great sages descend, they have nothing left to teach. The men and women of this land have only just ascended to the first stage, reborn here through the karmic conditions of the Dao. Before long, a celestial assembly of perfected ones will convene, and the great transmission of the Dao will extend its grace to you. You must focus your minds, revere this jeweled city, uphold the precepts, practice generosity, and never waver in your resolve. Then the Dao will naturally descend upon you.”

Then from among the assembly, a youth named True Practice rose from his seat, stepped forward, and bowed. He addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: “Ever since I received the blessing of the celestial court and joined the ranks of the cloud-borne immortals, I have been steeped in the mysterious transformation for a hundred kalpas. I have wandered the ten directions, yet nowhere have I seen such splendor as this city—its magnificence and beauty, its prosperous people, its ranks of immortals arrayed like a forest, its jade groves and jeweled branches, its empty winds and myriad echoes, its return to pure simplicity, its harmonious qi, its towering virtue—all beyond measure. I only pray that your merciful light may illuminate our ignorance and grant this great assembly sudden awakening.”

The Heavenly Worthy replied: “Your admiration for this city reflects the longing in your heart. Never before have you seen such a world. Though this realm is called the Land of Ultimate Bliss, residual habits still linger. The people, immortals, and Daoists here are all beings from various karmic paths who, though their merits were not yet complete, were reborn here. They have not yet reached the profound stillness of the Dark Mystery. From time to time, sages descend to serve as their teachers, though they do not remain long.

Know this, True Practice: it is like the case of the Fragrant Accumulation Youth, who once said, ‘When the Dao’s extremity brought me to your presence, I held your canopy for half a kalpa, entreating you to expound the subtle and wondrous Dao. Only then did I begin to awaken.’ I then revealed to him the names of the Great Loftiness and the High Mystery. The youth departed to pay his respects and inquire into the profound principles, and he has not yet returned.

What you see now is no different. The mysteries of the hidden and secret cannot be lightly spoken. When your own Dao cultivation reaches its limit, you shall naturally perceive them.”

Then True Practice and the virtuous king, along with the ministers and people, still uncertain, again addressed the Heavenly Worthy: “We do not yet understand—by what past merits and practices did the immortals, Daoists, king, and people of the Land of Ultimate Bliss come to be reborn here?”

The Heavenly Worthy answered: “The methods of cultivation are many, not just one. Listen carefully, and I shall explain, transforming the understanding of this land.

There are four kinds of beings in the heavens and among men:

The first rank consists of those who in life honor and support their parents, serve their teachers, relieve the destitute, practice Daoist arts, uphold the precepts, recite scriptures, and never slacken in their morning and evening devotions. They perform rituals, make vows, repent their transgressions, and seek blessings, aspiring to ascend and be delivered. When their merits are complete and their practices perfected, they move the Paper-Heaven above. Their names are inscribed on the left register, their lives recorded in golden tablets. They gain mastery over their forms, soar through the Upper Clarity, conceal or manifest themselves at will, and their Dao equals that of the perfected ones. They become deathless, ascending to immortality in broad daylight, attaining the rank of the highest perfected, and serving as attendants to the Lord of the Dao. Though they may briefly pass through this realm—lingering for a kalpa or half a kalpa—they eventually return to the celestial realms. Such beings are called the highest rank.

The second rank consists of those who in life were wise and pure, aiding their nations and governing with beneficence. Their words brought benefit, their generosity was vast, and they promoted the true Dao, supporting the good. At death, they achieved liberation through the corpse, like a snake shedding its skin, and were reborn here. Such beings are also called those who ascend in their present forms.

Within this second rank, there is another kind: some encounter the grace of the Celestial Emperor, who delivers them from life and death. Their dry bones and lifeless corpses are transformed and refined into living beings, moved by the true qi to become immortals spontaneously. Others, having formed karmic bonds with the Dao in past lives, receive blessings that flow into their present existence, leading them to be reborn here.

The third rank consists of those who in life upheld the precepts and maintained goodness, refraining from wrongdoing. They built palaces and temples, provided incense and lamps, held fasts and lectures, organized assemblies, copied scriptures, and crafted images. Through their morning and evening recitations, they too achieved liberation through the corpse and were reborn here.

The fourth rank consists of those who, after death, are reborn here by inheriting the residual blessings of their ancestors’ accumulated virtue, even changing their surnames.

Then the youth True Practice and the assembly, still uncertain, again addressed the Heavenly Worthy: “We do not yet understand—by what merits did the ancestors of the fourth rank cultivate such abundant blessings that their descendants might be reborn here?”

The Heavenly Worthy, may you deign to expound further, that our minds may awaken to understanding.”

The Heavenly Worthy replied: “When I speak of the causes of blessed fortune, it may be that their ancestors in former lives gave wealth and food, released living beings, clothed and fed the destitute and cold, aided the orphaned and weak, succored the aged and sick, or provided for those dwelling in mountain retreats. Though their merit was not yet perfected and they withdrew midway, failing to attain liberation themselves, their blessings extended to their descendants. Or they may have been born into noble and wealthy families, endowed with keen intelligence. Or they may have sought the Dao but not yet fulfilled their practice, their destined time of liberation having arrived, and thus were reborn here. Such persons’ virtue extends through nine generations.

True Practice, you must understand: good and evil are alike in this. Those who accumulate transgressions also bring calamity upon nine generations. Just as in the world, where fools may inherit ancestral blessings and be born into wealth and nobility, yet rely on their strength and arrogance, disbelieving in past karma, and indulge in cruelty and peril—slaying living beings, plundering others’ wealth, wielding punishment without restraint, undermining the good Dao, slandering practitioners, envying those superior to themselves, oppressing the orphaned and weak, flogging the lowly, hunting and killing, boiling and roasting creatures, stabbing and piercing beings, disobeying parents, rebelling against rulers, indulging in wine and lust, defiling kin, violating others’ wives, cursing and humiliating elders, exposing the Three Luminaries, disrespecting the virtuous, occupying high positions with malice, belittling sacred altars, divulging scriptural treasures, breaking fasts and violating precepts, constantly stirring chaos, exploiting others’ misfortunes, and mutually entrapping one another—killing to seek life, betraying the Dao and virtue.

Such persons’ calamities also flow through nine generations. Their descendants of the nine ranks face ruin wherever they turn, reduced to servitude, constantly bound in shackles, ensnared by wicked destinies, dying to enter hell, reborn as the six kinds of livestock, roasted and seared by humans, suffering myriad torments, revolving through evil destinies, born without fixed form, drowning in the cycle of birth and death, adrift in waves of suffering.

True Practice, you must understand: I observe that among the beings of the lower realms, the matters of suffering and joy are not so different. Why is this so? You speak of the Land of Ultimate Bliss, where cities, terraces, and pavilions are not natural but wrought by divine labor, unlike the palaces of the upper realms, which arise naturally. It is like the Fragrant Accumulation Youth, who, having never beheld the Great Void and the Boundless Dao Realm, believed the rewards of the Land of Mercy to be supreme. My observation of your mind is no different.

True Practice, you must understand: the thirty-six thousand kinds of Dharma arise from human conditions and karmic affinities. Through cultivating practices and deeds, though one may speak of attaining the Dao, the pace varies. It is like the Treasure Light Youth, who in his past life received the teaching of extinction from the Ancient Master, yet after eighty thousand great kalpas of diligent cultivation, still could not attain the Dao. Only in his final incarnation did he encounter the Dragon’s First Assembly, where the heavenly Dao is vast, and he first entered the Dao’s ranks, yet remained in the upper grade of the seventh stage. Had he not met the Perfected One of the Primordial Sovereign, how could he have ascended into the formless realm?”

Thereupon, True Practice and the assembly, having heard the Heavenly Worthy’s discourse, felt their minds open and their understanding deepen. They bowed their heads in reverence and returned to their seats. The king, princes, ministers, and all the people, having heard the origins of karmic causes and conditions, rejoiced exceedingly. Each offered luminous moon-jewel treasures, presenting them to the Heavenly Worthy. The Heavenly Worthy accepted them and placed them within the city. The king and the assembly, overjoyed and exultant, paid their respects and departed.

At that moment, the Heavenly Worthy and the assembly of great sages gathered their divine powers and ascended into the formless realm, suddenly vanishing from sight.

**Chapter Four: The Sequence of Compassion and Precepts**

At that time, within the Jade Clarity Heaven, in the jeweled palaces of the Golden Perfected Queen and Sagely Heavenly Worthy, there once lived in the world of Many Joys a child of the Ji family. At the age of six, he understood profound texts, deeply grasped subtle principles, and thoroughly comprehended the obscure and minute. Thereupon, he abandoned his home to seek the Dao, entering the Longming Mountains. After ten years of refined contemplation, he moved the Western Numinous Void Heavenly Worthy to bestow upon him the essentials of the Dao.

At twenty-seven, he attained the six penetrations. Since achieving the Dao, he had traversed countless kalpas, ever employing the power of his vow to deliver sentient beings. Roaming the ten directions like the sun circling in illumination, he manifested forms in accordance with kinds and harmonized with their voices, employing expedient means to guide and benefit all, equal and undivided, with a single thought for all beings.

In the eighth year of the Yuanhua era, in the gengzi year, on the fifteenth day of the seventh month, he descended with thirty-six thousand sages to wander the Mystic Heaven, arriving at the Northern Ultimate’s Long Darkness World in the midst of the empty sky. Together, they sat upon rosy clouds, gazing upon the six directions. For a hundred minor kalpas, their bodies and minds remained unmoving, like a precious mountain. The assembly of sages likewise remained unmoving in body and mind for a hundred kalpas.

At that time, the world suddenly became radiant, as if in spring. Harmonious qi flowed unimpeded, wind and rain were well-balanced, clouds and mist gathered and dispersed, thunder resounded clearly, medicinal herbs flourished, the hundred grains grew in winter, the earth yielded sweet springs, exquisitely fragrant and delicious. Dragons and scaled creatures leapt, phoenixes and simurghs soared in dance, and beings of all kinds gathered, all drawing close in kinship. People and non-humans transformed in body and mind, all as if long accustomed to cultivation and teaching.

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy and the assembly of sages, serene and quiescent, uttered no words. Yet through the power of compassion, the myriad things of heaven and earth transformed of themselves. There was no radiant sound to be seen or heard; the obscure and the manifest merged in profound union, and the spirits harmonized in perfect accord. The Dao of non-action brought this about, yet even I know not how it came to be.

Though the Dao does not speak, its virtue and transformation spread forth. True qi stirs and excites, subtle principles respond with precision, yet without movement. The people of that land were likewise unaware, their minds lacking discriminating wisdom. Each remained in their place, every person keeping to their allotted role, living out their years and lifespans.

On the fifteenth day of the third month, in the Snow Mountains, there was a youth named Dharma Joy, who styled himself an immortal. With his retinue of one thousand two hundred fifty, including the Golden Topknot Youth, Golden Grain Youth, Jeweled Crown Youth, Tamed Youth, Ten Abodes Youth, Ocean Wisdom Youth, Seven Awakening Youths, Pervasive King Youth, Self-Mastering Youth, and Good Wealth Youth—eleven youths in all—who led the assembly as chief chanters, each likewise styling themselves immortals, they all rode white elephants to descend to the earth. Circumambulating in praise, they bowed from afar to the Heavenly Worthy, burned incense, scattered flowers, and offered various forms of reverence. Each declared their original vows and inquired after the Heavenly Worthy, saying:

“We, this assembly, fortunately bear the blessings of past lives. In the primordial kalpa, we encountered the Ancient Master, who took pity and transformed us, enabling us to enter the ranks of the Dao. He bestowed upon us the eye of wisdom, allowing us to see from afar the Heavenly Worthy descending to this world. Overjoyed and fortunate, we have come to pay our respects and seek your counsel. We only hope the Heavenly Worthy will take pity and instruct us.”

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy, knowing their intent, remained silent and did not reply. The immortals repeatedly entreated, each prostrating themselves upon the ground for a long while, bowing and raising their heads, saying: “We only hope the Heavenly Worthy will extend the power of compassion, take pity, and instruct us, revealing what we have not yet heard.”

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy, moved by their earnestness, commanded the Right Attendant Perfected Youth named Jeweled Form, saying: “What vows do you and this assembly seek, that you have come here?”

Thereupon, Dharma Joy and the great assembly bowed their heads again in reverence and said: “We see the Heavenly Worthy and the assembly of sages, their majesty and virtue solemn and awe-inspiring, as never before. This world now possesses such blessed virtue, yet without a word spoken, the myriad things transform of themselves. Heaven and earth are altered, the climate shifts, sun and moon shine brightly, stars align in proper measure, wind and rain disperse appropriately, the hundred grains ripen, medicinal herbs flourish, sweet springs flow abundantly, beasts leap in dance, beings of all kinds live in harmony, and the people abound in joy—never before has such a thing been seen. We do not know what meritorious deeds the Heavenly Worthy has cultivated to attain the secret and essential Dao of self-mastery over the transformation of the myriad things. We hope you will instruct and reveal it to us.”

Again, they prostrated themselves upon the ground for a long while, not rising.

Thereupon, Jeweled Form returned to the Heavenly Worthy and fully reported their intent.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy addressed them, saying: “The supreme great Dao employs only the power of compassion to give life to and transform the myriad things, sheltering and protecting sentient beings, without speech. If there were speech, it would give rise to form and trace. Though teachings of form and trace may accord with the ultimate Dao, they do not reach the subtlest principle. Why is this? One cannot employ form, trace, or speech to transform heaven and earth and give life to the myriad things. Why? Because form, trace, and speech are not constant in principle. If principle is not constant, how can it bring about transformation? Therefore, the great Dao is without form, trace, or speech, allowing things to transform of themselves.

O good men, you suppose that I have cultivated and practiced to achieve this transformation. If you now cultivate and practice, you too should achieve transformation. O good men, holding such a view, you have not yet departed from afflictions and remain bound in fetters. The supreme great Dao long ago departed from such views, its mind free from knots and bonds, non-active and non-creating, without arising or ceasing, without form or appearance, where speech and the Dao are cut off. What you see as my majestic divine power and virtue, solemn and awe-inspiring in form, transforming heaven and earth and giving life to the myriad things—this is your perverse view, a deluded and discriminating thought. The supreme great Dao is apart from perverse views and the discriminating thoughts of delusion.”

O good men, you speak of encountering the Ancient Master and attaining transformation and deliverance through him. This Ancient Master is my disciple. I sent him to teach and transform the borderlands, expounding the Three Vehicles to extinguish suffering and instructing beings in cultivating the fruits of future lives. Because those lands are difficult to transform, their people lack harmonious qi, their natures incomplete like those of mixed beasts—they drink blood and eat raw flesh, acting with violence and arrogance. Thus, he performed divine transformations, broadly expounded parables, and awakened those of dull faculties. Such methods do not exhaust the ultimate truth but provisionally manifest forms and traces. After the Master departed, he withdrew his traces and returned to the origin, his forms and traces gradually vanishing. Even if some remain, they are largely erroneous. Some style themselves as immortals, others claim to be Brahma Heaven; some sit silently in empty chambers, some burn their bodies to extinction, some plunge from high cliffs, some make offerings to water and fire; some fashion images of heavenly beings with three faces and a thousand hands, or various deities, slaughtering and sacrificing, gathering in crowds to perform rituals, crying out to seek extinction; or they intently observe luminous signs. Such methods are called false and erroneous. Though scriptures may exist, there is no true Dharma in them—orthodoxy and heterodoxy are mixed, and the Way cannot be attained.

Thereupon, Dharma Joy and the great assembly, having heard the Heavenly Worthy’s words, awakened in their hearts. They realized that their previous cultivation had not reached the essentials of the Dao. Again they prostrated and addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: “As in our land, what we have cultivated accords entirely with the Heavenly Worthy’s great compassionate insight—there is no difference. Yet we fear that our assembly’s karmic defilements are too deep to be saved. We only beseech the Heavenly Worthy to bestow upon us the Dharma-water, gradually to clarify and purify, washing away filth and impurity, opening the gate of expedient means, demonstrating the power of expedient means, granting us entry into the Dao. First, let us hear the rules of deportment and the precepts of fasting, so that we may gradually cultivate them, restraining body and mind, giving them a foundation.”

The Heavenly Worthy replied: “The land and qi of your region are yin and malign, and the people born there are likewise. Why is this? This is called the Metal Region, where mixed kinds of beings are born in these borderlands. They do not hear the true Dharma but only the parables of the Three Vehicles. They do not know the secret treasury of the great Dao—the celestial scripts in cloud-seal and dragon-chapter, phoenix-brilliance, the methods of sudden teaching to achieve perfection and enter the wondrous with the embodied self.”

Thereupon, Dharma Joy and the assembly, hearing the Heavenly Worthy’s words, feared their lives did not accord with the true Dao. The great assembly wept sorrowfully, kowtowing until blood flowed, and again addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: “The beings of that land dwell in a rank, foul, and stinking place. How could they hope to ascend and be delivered in this very body, forming a bond with the Dao? We only hope that in future lives we may be born in the Central Kingdom, a land where the Dao abides. We beseech the Heavenly Worthy’s great compassion to bestow upon us the rules of fasting, deportment, and precepts.”

Then the Heavenly Worthy, with the power of great compassion and not refusing their request, addressed them, saying: “The natures of the people of your land are manifold, and they should receive many precepts to restrain body and mind. They are not like the people of the Land of Abandoned Worthies, whose hearts are pure and simple. Even if they receive precepts, they do not exceed five kinds: the first, the Five Precepts; the second, the Ten Precepts; the third, the One Hundred Ninety-Nine Precepts; the fourth, the Three Hundred Great Precepts of Observing the Body. These are called the Four Categories. There are also the Thirty-Six Thousand Precepts of Deportment, which correspond to thirty-six thousand numinous powers. They encompass thirty-six thousand kinds of Dao, within which are thirty-six thousand life-spirits, and without, thirty-six thousand precept-spirits. Inner and outer guard and protect. Those who receive these precepts—if of the highest grade, achieve perfection; if of the middle grade, become immortals; if of the lowest grade, extend their lifespan. These precepts are the Jade Treasury’s Golden Rules, the prohibitions of the Highest Perfected. If one receives them and then lightly violates them, one’s body will be handed over to the dark officials, and nine generations of ancestors will suffer interrogation. Now I will briefly explain one category to you, dividing one category into three grades—high, middle, and low. Within each grade, further divide into three grades, making nine grades in all, completing the yang number. These nine grades of precepts require fasting and precepts together; they are not to be practiced singly or transmitted exclusively. Wherever you hold fasting lectures or establish assemblies, and on the days when kings, princes, great ministers, officials, scholars, men, and women gather for fasting, you should appoint one person with a clear voice to properly compose their deportment, face north, and read the precepts once to the assembly. The great assembly of people should prostrate and listen to the precept-words. Again, at the first night of the fast, read them once more to the assembly. This is the method for a one-day fast. For two, three, or seven days, you should read them once each day. If one is newly entering the Dao, first receive the precepts, and after a thousand days, gradually advance to other methods. If there are virtuous people who have previously committed no transgressions and have not yet been delivered, receive the precepts within three days—there is no need to wait a thousand days before transmitting the Dharma. If, after receiving the precepts, one commits the ten evils or the five rebellious acts, the Dharma-master should burn incense before the Three Treasures and repent, revoking the precepts. If one has not yet received the precepts, or after receiving them commits minor transgressions not among the ten evils, earnestly repent and seek to receive them again. The Dharma-master and disciple should face the fast, perform the six-times-daily prostrations and repentance, vowing never to transgress again, and then, after careful consideration, transmit the Dharma. You must be cautious, you must be cautious—do not violate my precepts, lest you incur the sin of rebellion and the gods not protect you.”

Thereupon, Dharma Joy and the great assembly each prostrated, brush in hand, listening as the Heavenly Worthy expounded the precepts.
