**Precept Categories, Fifth Section**

1. **Do not kill**—do not kill for pleasure, in play, for sport, for gain, or by enticement. Do not crave meat to cure illness; even medicinal portions must be entirely abandoned.
2. **Do not rebel against parents or rulers**, or cause chaos and ruin to family and state.
3. **Do not commit robbery**—whether through enmity, slander, or false accusation. **Do not slander**—whether by speech, writing, or formal accusation.

**Precept Categories, Fifth Section (continued)**

4. **Do not expose the Three Luminaries**—do not revile Heaven or curse Earth.
5. **Do not commit incest with kin**, thereby engendering punishment and harm.
6. **Do not destroy the good Dao**, sever others’ bonds of kinship, or extinguish others’ ancestral lines.
7. **Do not indulge in wine**—whether poisoned wine, matchmaking wine, or lustful wine.
8. **Do not harbor secret malice**, harming others through bodily, verbal, or written acts.
9. **Do not encroach upon or exploit the good and virtuous**, or seize from the orphaned and impoverished.
10. **Do not rob or desecrate corpses**, or scatter others’ skeletal remains.
11. **Do not strip the dead on battlefields**, or sever and take their hair.
12. **Do not deceive or exploit the elderly and infirm**, seizing their possessions without compassion.
13. **Do not destroy nests or dens**, or harm embryos and fledglings.
14. **Do not traffic in lives** to enrich oneself.
15. **Do not deliberately observe warfare**, or intentionally incite conflict between states.

These constitute the **Ten Evils and Five Heinous Crimes**. Those who violate them will suffer manifold torments in this life, and after death, share the same punishment as their nine generations of ancestors, never to be redeemed for ten thousand kalpas.

The Dao states: **In the rites of morning obeisance**, one must not perform obeisance from a high place to a low one; not glance about while performing obeisance; not perform obeisance in an impure state; not face the altar while spitting or sniveling; not gaze upward at the altar; not cast sidelong glances at the altar; not speak loudly at the altar; not raise one’s voice at the altar; not utter mistaken words at the altar; not speak perversely at the altar; not interrupt speech at the altar; not engage in extraneous talk at the altar; not gesture with the limbs at the altar; not touch one’s head while speaking at the altar; not speak with a playful expression at the altar.

The Dao states: **In entering the fasting and precept altar**, one must first cultivate compassion. First, do not harbor secret malice; second, do not dwell on lust; third, do not indulge in lewdness; fourth, do not contemplate killing; fifth, do not crave meat; sixth, do not seek dominance; seventh, do not practice deceit. Only then may one bathe with the five fragrant herbs, washing away worldly defilements, rectify one’s demeanor, and proceed to the altar.

Outside the altar, prepare two bathing areas with fragrant water, one each for men and women. Erect two screened enclosures, burning incense within, and set up proper clothing racks. In one enclosure, remove and hang one’s pure garments. Emerging from the screen, enter the bathing chamber, cleansing the body with towels and bean powder, ensuring all is in order. Do not boil and kill insects or larvae; strain water through silk to prepare broths and beverages. Do not burn worm-eaten firewood for the fast or offerings. Do not allow those who are menstruating, postpartum, afflicted with festering sores or pus, the licentious, or those guilty of the Ten Evils and Five Heinous Crimes to approach the fasting kitchen.

Once the proper offerings are arranged, the master dons pure robes, takes a clean censer with burning charcoal, and kindles incense. After completing the obeisances and sitting in their proper places, they maintain solemn silence, upright and composed, reflecting on the superior precepts with body and mind—first compassion, second mercy, third goodness, fourth faith.

Good men and women, you must now understand: it is through these four principles that I attained the Dao. These four are the gateway to all good Dao, the foundation of all good Dao, the essential mechanism of the Great Dao. Apart from these four, there is no Dao. Thus, I possess these four stages of good Dao to safeguard Heaven and Earth, generate and nurture the myriad things, harmonize the qi and seasons, govern the unseen and visible, avert disasters and eliminate calamities, and rescue those in dire straits. If you abandon these four, you may not enter the altar, nor receive offerings from kings, princes, ministers, or the multitudes; you may not accept reverence and obeisance from kings, princes, or all men and women; nor may you seek blessings or fulfill vows for yourself or others. I decree such a person a thief within the Dao and its laws, unfit to dwell among us, despised by humans and spirits, unsaved by the gods.

Good men, within the altar there are **three further principles**: first, contemplate filial piety; second, contemplate forbearance; third, contemplate humility.

Good men, within the altar there are **seven further principles**:
1. Regard all men and women as your parents.
2. Regard Dharma masters and virtuous people as heavenly beings.
3. Regard the sacred scriptures as rare and precious.
4. Regard the sound of Dharma teachings as difficult to encounter.
5. Regard the sick, poor, orphaned, and destitute as your own self.
6. Regard the frail and elderly as reminders of impermanence.
7. Regard all living beings with equanimity.

Good men, you must now understand: whether entering or leaving the altar, do not abandon great compassion, nor allow the mind to discriminate. Through non-discrimination, no evils arise. In all that you see, hear, know, do, stand, sit, lie, or dwell—apart from these precepts, there is no peace. There is no such thing as attaining the Dao while violating these precepts.

Good men, if you seek the Dao and wish to ascend and transcend this life, there is no such thing as attaining the Dao while violating these precepts. Good men, if you wish to be free from illness and escape the cycle of birth and death, there is no such thing as fulfilling your aspirations while violating these precepts. Good men, if you transgress these precepts, you will be envied by evil forces, punished by royal law, and your life will be cut short—unsaved by the gods.

The Dao states: **Within the altar**, one must not consume meat, nor allow impurity; not engage in excessive speech; not cast sidelong glances; not disrupt the assembly; not eavesdrop; not spit or snivel; not wear light or soiled clothing; not snore in sleep; not sit improperly; not sit with one’s back turned; not gaze upward; not laugh loudly or speak boisterously; not eat with exclamations; not conceal food; not hoard food; not speak while eating; not laugh while eating; not glance about while eating; not eat while reclining; not rinse the mouth while eating; not clatter utensils while eating; not pick at food; not disparage food; not eat repeatedly; not eat at improper times—one should eat at the proper time, with compassion.

Do not walk hastily; do not drag your feet or make noise while walking; do not shuffle your heels; do not move your head or hands while walking; do not glance about while walking; do not look upward while walking—walk with composure and uprightness.

If a Dao disciple receives alms or offerings, accept them with compassion, and do not repeatedly express thanks, repeatedly decline, or repeatedly glance about. Once accepted, make offerings according to the proper rites and distribute them in accordance with the Way.

All Dao disciples, whether men or women, must not frequently enter the dwellings of kings, princes, great ministers, officials, or laypeople. If, for karmic reasons, entry is necessary, maintain proper dignity and demeanor, stand outside the gate, state your purpose clearly, and do not enter their homes or sit upon their beds.

When Dao disciples interact with their parents, uncles, aunts, brothers, or sisters, they should show utmost reverence—how much more so with others.

Unless there is a grave reason, Dao disciples must not enter military camps or bustling markets. Dao disciples, whether men or women, must not enter butcher shops, brothels, places of entertainment, or the dwellings of those who commit the ten evils or the five heinous transgressions.

Dao disciples, whether men or women, must not share quarters, beds, or meals with those of improper kind, nor share clothing or adornments.

Dao disciples, whether men or women, must not keep many attendants out of desire, nor possess defiled writings.

Dao disciples, whether men or women, must not contend with laypeople over profit. If there is profit, it should be yielded to laypeople and to the ignorant, the young, or the weak.

Dao disciples, whether men or women, must not keep weapons or musical instruments, nor burn or fumigate with hides, furs, horns, bones, or foul-smelling substances.

Dao disciples, whether men or women, must not defile living grass, insects, or ants.

Dao disciples, whether men or women, must not relieve themselves facing north, nor look upward while doing so; must not pollute mountains, springs, or pure ground; must not dwell in mixed company, in lowly places, against the wind, in dampness, or without careful protection.

Dao disciples, whether men or women, and all Dao followers should solemnly adorn the Dao sanctuary, maintain halls and quiet abodes with vigilance and secrecy, sweep and cleanse the inner and outer areas, keeping them always pure. They must not sleep late or rise late, miss the proper times for morning rites, neglect proper conduct in matters great or small, or fail to show mutual respect.

Do not open the doors of the quiet abode without reason; do not leave scriptures and teachings exposed; do not return from lay dwellings without washing and purifying; do not allow women or close kin to stay in the Dao sanctuary without grave cause, nor gather with Dao followers without proper reason; do not borrow or lend permanent sanctuary property for other uses.

All permanent sanctuary property—incense, oil, lamps, candles, treasures—should have fixed uses and must not be diverted for other purposes.

Within the boundaries of the pure dwelling, do not allow the entry of miscellaneous livestock or defilement; do not trade in slaves or the six livestock to acquire goods for the quiet abode; do not use wealth obtained through the ten evils or five heinous transgressions to build the quiet abode; do not establish a quiet abode on defiled ground.

Those who violate these precepts will suffer bodily afflictions, fail in their studies, and if they take what is not returned, three generations will be afflicted. Be cautious!

The Dao states: All good men and women should uphold the law both internally and externally, forming a fortress of the law. Do not encroach upon or damage the pure abode; do not strip away its protective barriers.

Do not steal or fell fruit-bearing trees; do not steal the master’s fruit; do not encroach upon the master’s fields; do not waste or deplete the master’s grain or silk; do not damage the master’s ritual implements; do not borrow the master’s belongings and fail to return them for a long time; do not privately expend the property of the Dao; do not privately exchange the property of the Dao; do not privately employ the master’s livestock; do not gather in the sacred precinct to expound heterodox teachings; do not gather in the sacred precinct to gamble or shoot arrows; do not assemble in the Daoist sanctuary to collect alms, eat meat, or drink wine; do not allow women to lodge within the sacred precinct.

The Dao states: If Daoist men or women violate these precepts, the guardian spirits of the law and the Earth Officials will examine and punish them, extending the affliction to three generations. Be cautious!

The Dao states: When Daoist men or women copy the precious scriptures, do not place them in impure locations; do not allow impure persons to see the scriptures; do not allow unbelievers to hear the scriptures; do not allow corrupt persons to know the scriptures; do not allow corrupt persons to see the paper on which the scriptures are written; do not use impure wealth to purchase paper for copying scriptures. The method of copying requires that the scriptures be placed in a separate chamber, with incense constantly burned upon the table. Once a day, wash hands and body with five-fragrance water, and after relieving oneself or changing clothes, maintain constant purity when entering or exiting. Those who copy scriptures must not secretly use or divulge esoteric words, nor chant them aloud. Those who violate these precepts will immediately suffer afflictions, endure the trials of wind and blade after death, and forever be barred from hearing the Dao. Be cautious!

The Dao states: Those who study the Dao and cultivate themselves must first broadly seek scriptures, verify the precepts and regulations, and seek the master’s judgment. Guard carefully what you receive, and do not self-promote or seek worldly gain. Form bonds of like-mindedness—no more than three men or four women—engaging in profound contemplation in seclusion to await spiritual communion. Do not let others become aware of or witness your practices, nor allow their praise or criticism. Withdraw to the mountains and forests, avoiding the company of worldly people. Those who violate these precepts will not be protected by benevolent spirits, and myriad demonic forces will disturb and afflict them. Be cautious!

The Dao states: If any virtuous man seeks to heal illness, he must first broadly prepare Daoist arts, clearly understand the principles of medicinal formulas, and carefully follow the rituals of fasting and jiao offerings. He must uphold the precepts, practice forbearance, and not violate the nature of things. He should not shrink from hardship or toil, nor shun day or night, regardless of distance, treating foe and kin with equal regard. He must not regard wealth or beauty, nor discriminate between high and low, male and female, nor demand repayment in spirit or material. Should repayment come unexpectedly, he ought to devote it to meritorious deeds and not hoard it for personal gain. He must not create difficulties, harbor no deceit in his heart, and ever practice great compassion. Those who heal illness in this manner will move the heavens with their merit, and their cures will be swift. If one violates the regulations and precepts, fabricating falsehoods, spirits and humans will swiftly punish them, and they will descend into hell upon death. Be cautious! Be most cautious!

The Dao states: If any virtuous man or woman has a heart inclined toward the Dao, yet encounters unfavorable times and cannot journey to famous mountains, they should uphold the precepts at home, construct a refined abode, and build thick walls with double partitions so that sounds inside and out cannot be heard. Let it be kept pure and meticulously maintained, no different from the mountains and forests. When merit is fulfilled and practice perfected, the Dao will come to the secluded chamber, and the body will attain the true Dao. If one violates the regulations and precepts, carelessly reveals secrets, allows foul odors or impurities to mingle, or exposes sacred texts, their efforts over countless years will be in vain. They will not hear of my Dao, their body will swiftly collapse, and myriad demonic forces will slay them. Their body will not attain the Dao, and their soul will suffer punishment. Be cautious!

The Dao states: If a student of the Dao, having received the master’s teachings and been entrusted with sacred texts, encounters a time when the destiny aligns and the law demands service to the state—whether already holding office before meeting the master or receiving the supreme law afterward, yet unable to attain pure emptiness—should they assist in governing the people and aiding the realm, they must inwardly uphold the precepts and guard carefully what they have received. They must not recklessly reveal celestial patterns, lightly transgress prohibitions, lack filial piety or compassion, indulge in harsh punishments, covet wealth, or exploit the people, causing the hearts of all under heaven to harbor grievances and bitterness. Such a person bears only the name of aiding the realm but lacks the virtue of integrity. They will suffer three kinds of punishment: first, the supervising spirits within their body will confuse their mind, leading all their endeavors to ruin; second, the spirits governing the state will cause them to break the law and face execution; third, the officials of the earth will examine them, and their misfortune will extend through seven generations. You must be cautious of this.

All the immortals, having received the precepts, rejoiced and leapt with joy, deeply counting themselves fortunate. Each rose to pay respects, faithfully accepting and practicing them.

*Thus concludes the first scroll of the Supreme Dao Jade Clarity Scripture.*
*Beginning the second scroll of the Supreme Dao Jade Clarity Scripture.*

**Chapter Six: The Skillful Means of Compassion**

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy, together with all the great sages, was in the empty void of the upper realms. Through skillful means, wishing to deliver sentient beings, he entered the Great Samādhi of Formless Great Emptiness by the power of great compassion. Though the assembled immortals possessed spiritual powers, they could not perceive him, nor did they know his whereabouts, and so they believed the Heavenly Worthy had returned to the upper realms.

The immortals were filled with sorrow, regret, and distress, unable to compose themselves. Each saw his own body devoid of majesty and virtue, like a corpse; moreover, the elephants they had ridden transformed into putrid flesh. The assembly was bewildered, their minds in turmoil, knowing neither how to advance nor retreat, uncertain what to do. Each entered meditation, carefully observing causes and conditions, yet their minds remained clouded, unable to comprehend. It was as if they had entered a dream, seeing various phenomena without any certainty or reality.

Then the celestial charioteers addressed the assembly: “Our merit and virtue are meager, our Dao-power weak. We have not yet fully grasped the subtlest principles. Having only just begun our practice, our cultivation is insufficient. Though we possess spiritual powers, we cannot perceive clearly. We must abandon all we previously knew and saw, and take refuge in the formless void. Perhaps through our devotion, we may once again behold the Heavenly Worthy.”

Hearing these words, the immortals gained slight understanding. Each concentrated their minds, recollecting and taking refuge in the Great Emptiness. For seven days and seven nights, they bowed their heads in reverence, making vows without rest. In an instant, their minds awakened, as if rousing from sleep. Looking up into the void, they suddenly saw the Heavenly Worthy and the assembly of sages, majestic and unmoving, no different than before.

The immortals bowed their heads in worship, repenting their faults and reproaching themselves. They offered thanks to the Heavenly Worthy, saying: “We, this great assembly, have for kalpas uncountable cultivated narrow views and fragmentary understanding, discriminating with deluded thoughts, lost in confusion and perverse views. Deeply entangled and bound, our offenses are grave. We saw our own bodies like corpses, devoid of radiance, our mounts transformed into rotting flesh, the jewels in our topknots turned to shards of tile. Unpredictable changes befell us, leaving us bewildered and disoriented, as if seeing forms in a dream, unable to distinguish reality. We knew not what to do, but resolved in our hearts to abandon all we had previously known and seen, to take refuge in the Great Dao, and turn toward the void. Repenting our faults and reproaching ourselves, after seven days and seven nights, our minds suddenly became calm, as if awakening from a dream. Our joy is boundless. We only pray that the Heavenly Worthy will take pity on us and open our minds to awakening.”

Before the immortals had finished speaking, the Heavenly Worthy once more entered the Great Samādhi of Radiant Light. His entire body shone with brilliance, like the unobstructed sun. He caused the assembly of sages to each ride a feathered canopy, seated upon flying-dragon thrones, at the tip of a single hair on his left brow. He further caused all the immortals, along with the lands of the ten directions—the mountains, rivers, seas, cities, and people—to abide within a single hair on his right brow, yet without any sense of confinement. Each saw the Heavenly Worthy before them as he expounded the wondrous Dharma. When the immortals beheld this, their perception was clear and unobstructed.

They also saw their former dwelling in the sacred mountain, which now seemed close at hand, though six kalpas had passed. They had been unable to recognize the Heavenly Worthy’s boundless and unobstructed divine power.

Then, with a single sound, the Heavenly Worthy universally addressed all beings, each awakening according to their kind. The Heavenly Worthy asked the immortals: “You have witnessed this power of the Dao. What do you make of it in your hearts?”

The immortals replied: “We, this great assembly, know only the joy of hearing the Dharma. Our minds perceive nothing else.”

The Heavenly Worthy continued: “The compassionate power of the Great Dao is neither real nor illusory, neither arising nor ceasing, neither empty nor existent, neither this nor that, without going or coming. It is called the self-existing power of the Middle Way, the power of great compassion, the unobstructed power. It brings peace to the minds of the immortals, leaving them unaware and unknowing, able only to hear the Dharma, with no other perception.”

Hearing the Heavenly Worthy’s words, the immortals began to awaken. The assembly snapped their fingers in unison, marveling at what they had never before encountered.

The Heavenly Worthy then addressed the immortals: “You must now understand that the majestic power of the Great Dao is beyond measure, without comparison. Among all other teachings, it is like fireflies compared to the sun and moon, or a handful of water compared to the great sea. You should rejoice in the Dharma. You, the ancient masters who have entered the gate of the Dao, practice the Three Vehicles, but these are merely names without fixed reality. They abound in similes, teaching those of lower capacity. They do not transcend birth and death, nor do they ensure enduring existence. Though you may see blessings in your present form, with bones and flesh ascending together, this is not the eternal Dharma of the Perfected Ones—the body like true gold, unchanging; like vajra, indestructible.

“Good sons, the teachings of similes are for instructing the foolish beings of border regions. Those of middle and superior capacity should not cultivate them. For thousands of lives, you drift through suffering, unable to transcend the river of birth and death’s attachments. It is like planting weeds in fertile soil, which will never yield the five grains. The teachings of similes are likewise unable to lead one to the attainment of the true Dao.

“Good sons, I know your minds are confined to lesser teachings, lost in delusion and straying from the true path. Thus, I gathered you here to awaken you. Good sons, though you dwelt on Snow Mountain for hundreds of years, without cultivating the Great Dao, you would not escape death and would surely fall into hell. Though you call yourselves immortals, you lack the essence of immortality. By your past good fortune, you have now seen me and received this further deliverance. This is your karmic affinity; you are destined to receive rebirth.

“Good sons, though you have been here for six kalpas, by my Dao-power, I have condensed these six kalpas into six days.”

Moreover, I perceive these six kalpas as but a single instant.

“Good sons, the majestic power of the Great Dao is inconceivable; even were one to expound upon it for kalpas unending, it could not be exhausted.”

Thereupon, Fa Xi and the assembled immortals, their doubts unresolved, addressed the Heavenly Worthy once more: “Formerly, we received the Heavenly Worthy’s compassionate power, awakening us to teachings never before heard—unprecedented Dharma. Our hearts rejoice beyond measure, yet we know not how to express our gratitude.

“We, benighted and confined by our limited perceptions, have taken these as the ultimate truth, unable to fathom the boundless. The supreme Great Dao is profound, wondrous, and deeply mysterious; its majestic spirit vast and unobstructed, transcending all thought.

“Our dust-laden burdens remain unsevered, our habitual tendencies deeply ingrained. Yet by good fortune, we have encountered this noble assembly and met with this auspicious time, casting off our defilements and filth to attend upon your celestial presence. We only pray for your compassion, to accept our already-lost lives and revive these polluted bodies, that we may bathe in the mysterious transformation.”

Then, the entire assembly bowed their heads until blood flowed, prostrating upon the ground for a long while without rising. The Heavenly Worthy, moved by great compassion, addressed them: “Though you have heard my teachings throughout these six kalpas, you remain unenlightened—such is the weight of your defilements. Why is this? The beings of borderlands subsist on raw flesh and blood, devouring sheep and horses alive. Though the ancient sages refined and purified them, residual habits persist, causing this to be so.”

At that moment, the Heavenly Worthy, through the power of great compassion and skillful means, suddenly caused one thousand two hundred and fifty white elephants to merge into a single elephant. He then caused one thousand two hundred and fifty immortals to coalesce into one immortal, who sat atop this elephant. Furthermore, he condensed the lands of the ten directions into a single realm, no larger than a mote of dust, wherein all beings and the great assembly were gathered into one person, dwelling within the infinitesimal space of this dust-mote.

In an instant, the two within the mote beheld a true person, a thousand feet in height, of extraordinary countenance, leading eighty-four thousand great sages into the mote. The two emerged from the tip of the mote, then re-entered through the left brow’s tip, returning to the Heavenly Worthy’s original presence. The thirty-six thousand of the great assembly entered through two points at the right brow’s tip, moving freely within and without, unconstrained and unconfined. For nine days and nine nights, their minds knew no weariness, as if but a moment had passed, unaware of any change, no different from before. The two, desiring to hear the Dharma, rejoiced in body and mind.

The Heavenly Worthy spoke again: “Good sons, in former times you formed affinities with the Dao, yet your merit was slight and your deeds shallow; the powers you attained were not true. Mountains yield fine jade, yet in the south there is a stone also called ‘jade.’ The two names are confused, and ordinary people cannot distinguish them, unaware of which is true jade. You who call yourselves immortals are like that stone-jade, not true jade—only those of wisdom can clearly discern the difference.

“Good sons, the pearl in your topknot is in truth a fish’s eye, not a true pearl. You, likewise, are not true immortals. Good sons, from this day forward, bathe in the Dao’s transformation, purge your dust-laden burdens, and only then shall you be called true and upright, only then shall you enter the current of the Dharma.”

Upon hearing the Heavenly Worthy’s words, the two exclaimed in awe, saying: “Today we are fortunate indeed, to have encountered the exalted Worthy and received the true Dao, awakening us, dispelling our afflictions like a snake shedding its skin.”

Then, the Heavenly Worthy, moved by great compassion, addressed them: “Where now are all your assembled followers?” The two, at a loss for words, looked about and saw only the true person and the great sages seated upon dragon thrones, with but a single elephant remaining. They also beheld the lands of the ten directions close at hand before them. A glimmer of understanding arose in their minds, recognizing this as the Heavenly Worthy’s sovereign power.

Perceiving their thoughts, the Heavenly Worthy said: “Through my Dao-power, I take pity on you suffering beings, guiding you with skillful means and revealing these divine transformations to awaken your minds.” In an instant, all was restored to its original state. The great assembly, too, became aware of the coming and going of these manifestations. Such is the sovereign, divine power of the Dao—beyond conception.

It is not to be fathomed by the five supernatural powers, the three vehicles, the seven factors of enlightenment, the eight gates, or the three realms. It transcends thought, perception, knowledge, and awareness; it is neither existent nor non-existent, neither arising nor ceasing, neither cause nor effect. It cannot be spoken of, cannot be conceived; it is beyond all language, beyond all sight and sound. Only the ultimate power of the Dao fully penetrates all Dharma, leaving nothing unpervaded.

“Good sons, know this: though I manifest such transformations, my mind—from beginning to end—has never perceived them as transformations, as a single phenomenon. It is but the great compassion of a single childlike thought, universally delivering all beings.

“Good sons, though I deliver beings, my mind—from beginning to end—has never harbored the thought of delivering beings.

“Good sons, the power of the Great Dao, the spirit of the Great Dao, the transformation of the Great Dao, the mechanism of the Great Dao, the subtlety of the Great Dao, the emptiness of the Great Dao, the namelessness of the Great Dao—all are inconceivable. Liberation is inconceivable; knowledge and vision are inconceivable; skillful means are inconceivable; creation and transformation are inconceivable; arising and completion are inconceivable; activity and function are inconceivable.

“Good sons, you should cultivate a mind of rarity, a mind of rejoicing, a mind that cherishes the difficulty of encountering such teachings. Perfect your shame and reverence—all is inconceivable.”

Thereupon, the immortals, filled with joy and praise, exclaimed: “Our great assembly, bathed in the Heavenly Grace’s life-giving torrent, knows a joy beyond compare—like parting heavy clouds to behold the sun and moon, like a blind man seeing forms and colors, like a caged bird soaring freely, like a small fish swimming in the vast river and sea, like dry bones restored to life. Our boundless joy is lofty beyond description.”

At that moment, the Heavenly Venerable, moved by their earnest devotion, bestowed upon the one thousand two hundred and fifty individuals the office of True Youths, entrusting them to record the merits and transgressions of newly ordained Dao practitioners throughout the world, inscribing the ledgers of life and death. For the sake of karmic conditions, the assembly of thirty-seven thousand two hundred and fifty sages all radiated bodily light, illuminating the boundless worlds of the ten directions. Incense, flowers, banners, canopies, and ten thousand kinds of celestial music filled the air as the great earth trembled.

Then, the Heavenly Venerable and the assembly of sages each took their seats upon nine-colored cloud-dragon thrones, floating into the void and departing. In the vast, dark world below, the king, princes, ministers, and countless people gazed from afar as the Heavenly Venerable and the sacred host ascended toward the southeast. In an instant, streaming rosy clouds filled the four directions, and their whereabouts became unknown.

The men and women of the kingdom, now awakened, looked at one another in grief and weeping, repenting their past faults and reproaching themselves. In that world, there was a king named Zhenhui, wise and eloquent, who addressed the multitude, saying: “Do not grieve. Hear my words. Long ago, I once heard of the True One of Emptiness and Non-Being, who creates and transforms heaven and earth, gives life to the myriad things, wields divine power with ease, and dwells in profound stillness, enacting transformation without speech. The auspicious signs in our world must be the blessing of this True One of Emptiness and Non-Being, causing all this to be so. Now, we and all people should repay this grace. Let us seek the most exalted site in the gardens and erect a palace, offering incense and flowers in worship.”

When the people of the kingdom heard the king’s words, they spoke with one voice, all praising the plan. Each removed the priceless pearls from their bodies to pave the ground, and took fragrant woods to construct the palace. Towering and vast, it was adorned with a hundred treasures, furnished with various thrones, and arrayed with flowers, incense, lamps, and candles—every kind of offering, all the wealth of the world was poured forth.

From afar, the Heavenly Venerable perceived their intent and extended the ten-colored true light from the palm of his left hand, illuminating the palace. Morning and evening, it shone as brightly as daylight, and a constant fragrance pervaded the world. The people of that land, in dreams, beheld the Heavenly Venerable, who expounded the Dao to them, clarifying their minds and bodies. Upon awakening, they recorded the words in writing. When the people of the kingdom compared and verified the texts, the writings all matched perfectly, without a single discrepancy. Thus, they transcribed these words as the *Scripture of the Spontaneous Dao*.

Thereafter, the people redoubled their diligence. The kingdom knew great peace, the people prospered and rejoiced, and none died young. Moved by these extraordinary signs, where the unseen and visible worlds aligned, all cultivated with utmost devotion. Though without teachers, they refined their own minds, attaining immortal ranks and gradually merging with the subtle and wondrous—all inconceivable.

At that time, through the power of the Heavenly Venerable’s three great vows, the salvation of beings was accomplished, and his transforming presence knew no partiality. With the great assembly, he descended to the borders of the earthly realm and the abyss’s depths, entering a small heaven within the void. This heaven spanned six thousand seven hundred and fifty-four *li* in circumference, with a height of one hundred and ninety-nine *li*.

Within this realm, the transforming sovereign was named Immeasurable Life, and he had three great ministers: the first was named Virtue King, the second was named Abandoning Depravity, and the third was named Cloud Melody. All governed the world with the true Dharma, never wronging the people.

The men and women here stood seven *cun* tall, all discerning and clear-minded, wise and intelligent, filial and obedient to their parents, and reverent toward their transforming sovereign.

In this heaven, long ages past, the era was called the Dragon’s First Assembly. The Void-and-Without Heavenly Venerable commanded the Perfected of Creation and the Immortal of Vast Spirit to descend into this heaven, spreading boundlessly. They established a tranquil altar, inscribed jade tablets with script, and thereby secured this heaven. From then on, the people of this land cultivated the Daoist arts. By virtue of these merits, some were later reborn in the Middle Kingdom, changing their surnames to Yi, and were called divine youths—keen of mind and sharp of wit. Whether in one body, two, or no more than three, they encountered the Heavenly Venerable and attained deliverance, achieving immortality and never dying.

At that time, Dharma Joy and the twelve hundred and fifty divine youths, their minds unsettled by doubt, rose from their seats, stepped forward, and bowed. They addressed the Heavenly Venerable, saying: “We do not yet understand—how many kalpas have passed since the Heavenly Venerable spoke of the Dragon’s First Assembly? The Void-and-Without Heavenly Venerable commanded the Great Perfected of Creation to disperse primordial *qi*, transforming it into the ten thousand things. By what principle, through what method, was such effortless mastery attained? We beseech the Heavenly Venerable to take pity on our ignorance and instruct us in these unheard-of, unprecedented teachings.”

Thereupon, the Heavenly Venerable, moved by their earnestness, replied: “Good sons, this assembly took place in an age so remote that it spans the number of fine dust-motes in a hundred million worlds—an incalculable kalpas. Only the Dao and the Dao can truly know it. Even the fivefold-perfected immortals consider this a distant time. What I have witnessed does not exceed the fleeting instant between a downward glance and a blink. If you wish to know, the principle is this: the Dao of primordial *qi* is not something you have heard before.”

Then Dharma Joy and the great assembly bowed their heads again and addressed the Heavenly Venerable: “Disciples were born in the defiled realm, our studies impure, our minds dull and deluded. We met a skilled master by chance, yet clung to narrow, partial teachings, our vision confined to shallow and cramped views. Our spirits were dimmed, our minds deeply obscured. Who could have foreseen that the sun, impartial in its radiance, would disperse the mist, illuminating the dark? The Dao does not bestow favoritism, yet in your compassion, you spoke of the Dragon’s First Assembly, resolving our doubts about the origin of primordial *qi*. We beg you to reveal its mysteries, that we may taste the sweet dew, revive what is withered and decayed, bestow divine talismans, and restore life to dry bones. Disciples and the assembly rejoice beyond measure. We never dared hope to ride the swift winds of rosy clouds, ascending to the mysterious gates, bathing in your transforming grace. Our hearts, forgetting all bounds, press forward—yet we know we have erred. We implore your forgiveness.”

As they spoke, the entire assembly wept, the earth trembled, and the sun lost its brilliance. In the empty sky above, a sound like a dragon’s roar arose. All people, winged insects and crawling creatures alike, joined in lamentation. Grass and trees withered, metal and stone lost their luster, fragrant clouds lingered and congealed in the void. A divine wind surged, and harmonious *qi* failed to flow smoothly.

Then the divine youths, moved by the resonance of heaven and earth, and the sorrow of all beings, were joined by the men and women of the land in their entreaty, all longing to hear the Dharma.

Thereupon, the Heavenly Venerable, moved by their devotion, emitted a thousand rays of light from his mouth, illuminating all heavens and penetrating every realm. Heaven rained fragrant blossoms, and myriad sounds arose spontaneously in the air. The sun and moon shone doubly bright, a gentle breeze swept away the dust, and immortal flowers blanketed the earth. Canopies of rosy clouds veiled the sky, divine bells rang clear, true apparitions manifested on all sides, dragon scales gleamed, and lions uttered soft roars. Jade censers burned incense, and the divine youths scattered fragrant smoke. Heaven and earth proclaimed auspicious signs, and all beings united in harmony. The ten directions’ lands became radiantly visible. Heavenly sages from all realms descended through the void, and earthly immortals emerged from beneath the ground, all gathering in this heaven. The gods of heaven and earth, the lords of mountains and seas, and the kings of all beasts came to the assembly to listen to the Dharma.

Then the Heavenly Venerable cleared his throat, snapped his fingers, and addressed them: “Good sons, you asked about the Dao of primordial *qi* and its origin. Listen carefully now, and I will explain. Good sons, you should know that the Dao of primordial *qi* originates with the Void-and-Without Heavenly Venerable. It arises from emptiness and is naturally self-existent, enduring without end. It transforms and gives birth to primordial *qi*, primordial *qi* gives birth to the Supreme Ultimate, the Supreme Ultimate gives birth to heaven and earth, and heaven and earth give birth to the ten thousand things.

Good sons, the Dao of primordial *qi* is wondrous in this way. Thus, the Great Dao has no name, and primordial *qi* has no form. Because it is nameless, its activity is boundless. It flows and changes endlessly, and all—sentient and insentient—are born by virtue of the Dao. Those who treasure primordial *qi* endure forever. Primordial *qi* is spirit; when united with *qi*, one can enter the formless and merge with the true Dao.

Good sons, though the ten thousand kinds differ, primordial *qi* is one. It is like the great sea, boundless in its flow, allowing all to draw from it as they will. The wise dig deep channels to guide its current, enabling endless irrigation. The foolish clutch leaky vessels, approaching the river and sea, yet gain but little moisture. Some, like the blind, never see the sea at all and receive no benefit.

Good sons, you should know that the nature of water is still, yet its moisture varies in depth. The Dao of primordial *qi* is likewise—beyond conception.”

Then all in the great assembly, hearing the Heavenly Venerable’s words, opened their minds and understood, awakening to the principle of the formless and subtle. At that moment, heaven and earth, mountains and rivers, heavenly gods, earthly deities, and all creatures—winged, crawling, and moving—joined their voices in unison, like thunder, and praised:

“The Great Dao neither arises nor perishes,
Primordial *qi* never ends.
Those who lose it decay forever,
Those who attain it wander long.”

Gazing down upon the Six Directions,
all drift in the currents of birth and death.
Looking up to those within the rosy clouds,
they dwell in serene freedom, without sorrow.

Once this hymn resounded through the void, in but a moment, five-colored streaming rosy clouds gathered in the sky a hundred *zhang* above the earth, spontaneously forming the cloud-script of the Eightfold Celestial Writ. Each character measured a *zhang* square, its eight corners trailing radiant beams, their brilliance dazzling, illuminating the empty sky. The great assembly of people looked up at the celestial script, reverently prostrating in worship, and all spoke with one voice:

“This is the spontaneous true *qi* of the Heavenly Venerable, the primordial *qi* of the true youth responding to resonance, transforming to produce these words. We have only heard of the celestial writ but never beheld it with our own eyes—today, by fortunate chance, we have unexpectedly seen it. We dare not presume, Heavenly Venerable: though we are dust-laden and defiled, may we transcribe this celestial script, read and recite it?”

The Heavenly Venerable replied: “This is formed by the transformative power of the Great Dao’s majestic spirit. If you wish to transmit, transcribe, and venerate the true writ—its dragon-script and phoenix-characters—if you wish to worship, recite, and uphold it with single-minded devotion, you must first receive the precepts, refine your conduct, and distance yourselves from all defilement. Only then may you transcribe, receive, uphold, read, and recite it, in strict accordance with the precepts.”

Upon hearing the Heavenly Venerable’s instruction, the great assembly rejoiced and leapt with joy, faithfully accepting and vowing to practice. They bowed in reverence and departed.

**Chapter Seven: The Kalpa of the Auspicious Dragon—Expedient Means for Delivering Beings**

At that time, the Heavenly Venerable of the Golden Tower in the Jade Purity Heaven, together with the assembly of great sages as numerous as motes of dust, all embodied boundless compassion. With the six penetrations, they responded to transformations with effortless mastery, their divine power unhindered, enduring endlessly without beginning or end. In subtle resonance with the workings of the unseen, their refined perception was exquisitely attuned. Ever with the One Dao, they manifested in countless forms, adapting to each kind to bestow long life.

At that time, the Heavenly Venerable, through the power of great compassion, constantly roared the thunder of the Dharma to awaken beings, causing them to awaken. Ever did they cover beings with great clouds, shielding them from exposure. Ever did they moisten beings with the rain of the Dharma, quenching their thirst. Ever did they stir beings with the wind of compassion, establishing their roots of faith. Ever did they illuminate beings with the sun of wisdom, dispelling their darkness. Ever did they act as vast ferries, providing crossings, guiding beings to fulfillment, transporting them endlessly, nurturing, sheltering, and protecting them as their guiding teacher. With earnest instruction, like parents cherishing their children, they bestowed precious treasures upon all, allowing each to take what they needed, without the slightest reluctance.

Yet beings, unaware, turned to resentment and blame. Losing the Dao and corrupting virtue, they fabricated benevolence and righteousness, drifting with their karma, never turning back. Bewildered, they strayed onto crooked paths, forsaking the true Way. Each clung to their own heterodoxies, their five viscera assailed within; following evil factions, they contended with the six thieves without. Love and dust veiled them, their afflictions and knots multiplying. For the sake of the self, they created the three kinds of karma. Gradually, these multiplied until they committed the ten evils. A hundred blessings fled far away, and at death, they fell into the Nine Dark Realms, enduring every suffering. From attachment and love they arose, yet could not comprehend—how pitiable they were!

Unable to abandon them, the Heavenly Venerable earnestly taught and guided in myriad ways, lifting and leading them, preventing them from straying into perversity.

At that time, the Heavenly Venerable and the assembly of great sages, moved by compassion for beings, cared for them as a loving mother cherishes her child. Though the child might wander afar, the mother’s thoughts would inevitably turn to them, hastening to their side, providing food, shelter, and protection until they grew to maturity, never abandoning them. How much more so for an infant, whom she nurses morning and night, responding to their needs and wishes without fail.

At that time, six million years after the Kalpa of the Auspicious Dragon, the blessings of the people beneath the Four Heavens were exhausted. Heaven and earth collapsed, calamitous *qi* obscured the sky, the sun and moon lost their brightness, the stars deviated from their courses, wind and rain fell unseasonably, heaven and earth quaked, rivers and seas shrank, metals and stones scorched and withered, springs and sources dried up, the earth split open everywhere, mountains crumbled, ghosts wailed, medicinal herbs ceased to grow, trees withered and fell, the hundred grains bore no fruit. Black winds tore up houses, whirling sand and stones that struck together, sparking fires that burned across mountains and marshes.

A hundred thousand evil ghosts, each leading countless followers, raced across the world, breathing fire from their mouths that seared out people’s eyes. Birds fell from the sky, the six livestock died of themselves. Four great pythons, each six million *li* in length, coiled around Kunlun Mountain, their mouths gaping in the four directions. From the scales of these serpents emerged a hundred billion smaller snakes that scattered in all directions. Their venomous *qi* was fiercely potent—whoever was bitten instantly rotted away. Such suffering endured for six hundred years, and beings were utterly afflicted.

At that time, the Heavenly Venerable, together with an assembly of great sages as numerous as motes of dust, in the first year of the Mysterious Transformation, the year *xinmao*, on the fifteenth day of the seventh month, at noon, within the Cloud Palace of the Jade Purity Heaven, all emitted divine radiance that illuminated the lower realms, the domains of the Four Heavens. The light transformed into countless millions of rays, each ray containing a boundless, vast Dao realm. Within each were sun, moon, and stars, mountains and rivers, cities and towns, towers and palaces—all surpassingly magnificent. Each city and tower was encircled by springs and pools, from which golden lotus blossoms emerged. A gentle breeze stirred the flowers, releasing wondrous fragrance that suffused the empty sky. The flowers, towering and grand, rose from the Jade Purity Heaven. Within each flower floated a dragon throne. Upon each throne sat a celestial perfected great sage expounding the wondrous Dharma. Around the springs and pools stood jeweled trees, their branches of jade and coral, their canopies casting shade over the world. Seven-jeweled leaves and night-shining pearls adorned them. A gentle breeze stirred the jeweled trees, and from their leaves arose wondrous sounds, chanting the *Spontaneous Brahma Hymns of the Void*, the *Precious Chapters of Spirit-Generation*, and the *Stanzas of Soul-Return*, harmonizing the Three *Qi* to generate and transform the myriad things. Above the void, condensed light of nine colors formed a jeweled canopy that filled the world.

Beneath the palace terraces, seven *qi* floated in the void, upholding the celestial halls. On all four sides of the palace, within the dark emptiness, arose spontaneous music—resonant, clear, and pure, surpassing all harmony and elegance. Upon each terrace, perfected beings chanted the *Hymns of Congealing Embryos and Primal Transformation*, nurturing the myriad things and dispelling calamities.

At that time, on the fifteenth day of the tenth month at noon, the Heavenly Worthy and a host as vast as the motes of dust in the Great Microcosm descended together from the Cloud Palace within the Jade Purity Heaven, floating through the void into the four heavens above the morning stars. The Dipper’s jeweled chariot bore his divine feet, the Eastern Dipper supported his left, the Western Dipper his right, the Northern Dipper served as his parasol, and the Southern Dipper as his footstool. The sun attended upon his left, the moon upon his right. Floral canopies cast their shade, fragrant clouds enveloped the four directions, divine winds harmonized the void, sweet dew flowed in streams, heaven and earth returned to their places, mountains and peaks surged into being, the source rivers flowed clear, the bitter seas turned pure, the four *qi* harmonized, the three luminaries shone equally, withered bones became immortals, the dying were reborn, the hundred grains ripened in abundance, and the world knew great peace. Demons lost their essence, the true Dao spread abroad, the wicked turned to goodness, and humans and spirits alike upheld purity. Vast and boundless was this transformation—beyond naming.

Then, beneath the four heavens, kings, princes, ministers, consorts, and all officials, along with the countless men and women, both human and non-human, each gazed upward into the dark emptiness above. From afar, they beheld the Heavenly Worthy’s true form—radiant and resplendent, his divine countenance serene and luminous, his light shining brilliantly, his august visage majestic. A jeweled canopy filled the sky, long banners fluttered, dragon censers wafted incense, spirit-fragrance revived the dead, and myriad sounds joined in unison with celestial music. All entreated the beings to deeply recognize the causes of their karma.

At that moment, those who witnessed this marvel felt shame welling within, desiring to offer reverence and gratitude. Yet they doubted the distance was too great, fearing their prayers might not ascend. In their hearts, they silently wished, entreating the exalted Heavenly Worthy and great sages to descend their cloud-borne chariots to the impure earth. Each remained in their dwelling, turning their thoughts upward, bowing their heads in devotion, their blood and tears staining the ground. For nine days and nine nights, they burned incense and scattered flowers, their prayers unceasing. Though exhausted and their spirits dazed, as if in a dream, they did not falter.

Moved by their sincerity, the Heavenly Worthy then divided his body into a hundred million forms, each seated upon a cloud-dragon throne. Before each being, he appeared, adapting his voice to their kind, expounding the Dharma so that all might awaken. Throughout the four heavens below, none were excluded—all were as one.

In an instant, the four heavenly kings, each with a retinue of ten thousand myriad beings, heard the Heavenly Worthy speaking the wondrous Dharma within their own hearts. Their bodies and minds rejoiced, filled with joy and peace. Though overjoyed, they could not fully comprehend. Each bowed in reverence and asked the Heavenly Worthy about the origin of the Dharma-sound within their hearts, saying: “We, your servants, are blessed beyond measure to behold the Heavenly Worthy descending to the lower realms and bestowing upon us this wondrous Dharma. We bear the profound grace of your compassionate favor, yet we are deeply ashamed, not knowing how to repay it. Moreover, we hear the Dharma-sound arising within our hearts, and our bodies and minds are at ease, filled with joy and peace. We do not understand—what is the cause of this?”

Then the Heavenly Worthy replied to the kings: “Excellent, excellent, good sons! You should know that the awe-inspiring power of the supreme great Dao is inconceivable, omnipresent. Why would the Dharma-sound reside only within your hearts? Even within your limbs, pores, and hairs, as well as in heaven above and earth below, within every mote of dust and blade of grass, the *qi* of the Dao abides.

“Good sons, you kings should feel deep shame. Within your hearts, let the Dharma-mind ever observe, removing your perverse views, your wayward thoughts, your restless cravings, and your greed and attachments. Bathe in the Dao, cleansing away the dust of your burdens. Ever practice great compassion, reverently offering devotion to the supreme great Dao. Uphold the precepts, give alms, cultivate patience and diligence. When the defilements of affliction are exhausted, the wondrous light of the Dao-nature will manifest among you.”

At that time, all the kings and their peoples beneath the four heavens simultaneously beheld the Heavenly Worthy’s earnest teachings. For a long while, they gathered their thoughts, their bodies and minds unmoving.

In an instant, each saw the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion, together with the host of sages, erecting within their hearts, limbs, pores, and skin countless banners and canopies, innumerable as the motes of dust, emerging in perfect order. The banners and canopies were vast and boundless, filling the world.

Then, the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion, with these banners and canopies, guided all beings to the Kunlun Mountain within the four heavens. They halted in the void, ten thousand *ren* above the earth, entering the space within a single fine hair. There, with the great assembly, they sat in solemn stillness for nine days and nine nights. Divine light shone brilliantly, illuminating the void, and a great thunderous voice expounded the wondrous Dharma. Its sound carried far, pervading the ten directions without exception.

To all beings, he proclaimed in verse:
*The great Dao is ever compassionate,*
*Pitying all sentient beings.*
*The supreme Dharma universally transforms,*
*Both those who practice and those who do not.*
*I originally have no form or appearance,*
*Yet through movement, names and shapes arise.*
*Now, I freely allow your questions,*
*Responding to your thoughts with teachings.*
*Provisional and real—no dual wisdom,*
*Mysterious and quiescent—the one true essence.*
*The primordial qi flows widely,*
*Encompassing the insentient and the sentient.*

When the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion had spoken these words, he sat in silence with the great assembly.

Then, from the Azure Heaven of the East, the Heavenly Children, led by the Heavenly Child of No-Mind, arrived with their retinue—a host as numerous as the motes of dust in nine billion great lands—all to hear the Dharma. Bearing the treasures of the Azure Heaven and offerings, they burned incense, scattered flowers, and performed celestial music. Mounting their heavenly palaces, they raised azure standards, azure banners, azure canopies, and azure veils, seating themselves upon azure clouds at the highest peak. Their canopies stretched boundlessly, floating through the void to arrive.

By the power of the Dao’s majesty, they entered the infinitesimal realm, encircling, extolling, bowing, and greeting. Arranging the celestial regalia and offerings, they withdrew and sat facing east, solemn and unmoving.

Then, from the Vermilion Heaven of the South, the Heavenly Children, led by the Heavenly Child of Blazing Radiance, arrived with their retinue—a host as numerous as the motes of dust in eight billion great lands—all to hear the Dharma. Bearing the treasures of the Vermilion Heaven and offerings, they burned incense, scattered flowers, and performed celestial music. Mounting their heavenly palaces, they raised vermilion standards, vermilion banners, vermilion canopies, and vermilion veils, floating through the void to arrive. By the Dao’s spiritual power, they entered the infinitesimal realm, encircling the Heavenly Worthy to chant praises, bow in reverence, and present offerings. Arranging their majestic regalia, they withdrew and sat facing south, solemn and still.

Then, from the Luminous Heaven of the West, the Heavenly Children, led by the Heavenly Child of Pristine Truth, arrived with their retinue—a host as numerous as the motes of dust in six billion great lands—all to hear the Dharma. Bearing the treasures of the Luminous Heaven and offerings, they burned incense, scattered flowers, and performed celestial music. Mounting their heavenly palaces, they raised pristine standards, pristine banners, pristine canopies, and pristine veils, floating through the void to arrive. By the power of the Dao’s compassion, they entered the infinitesimal realm, encircling the Heavenly Worthy to chant praises, bow in reverence, and present offerings. Arranging their majestic regalia, they withdrew and sat facing west, solemn and unmoving.

Then, from the Mystic Heaven of the North, the Heavenly Children, led by the Heavenly Child of Profound Wisdom, arrived with their retinue—a host as numerous as the motes of dust in five billion great lands—all to hear the Dharma. Bearing the treasures of the Mystic Heaven and offerings, they burned incense, scattered flowers, and performed celestial music. Mounting their heavenly palaces, they raised mystic standards, mystic banners, mystic canopies, and mystic veils, floating through the void to arrive. By the power of the Dao’s compassion, they entered the infinitesimal realm, encircling the Heavenly Worthy to chant praises, bow in reverence, and present offerings. Arranging their majestic regalia, they withdrew and sat facing north, solemn and still.

Then, the great spirits of the Eight Seas and the Dragon Kings, Lords of Waters, arrived to hear the Dharma, riding towering waves that surged to the heavens. By the Dao’s spiritual power, they floated through the void and stationed themselves at the four quarters of the infinitesimal realm, vast as great clouds.

Next, the Five Emperors and the Earth Deity, with their retinues numbering five myriad billion worlds—each world complete with mountains, rivers, seas, lands, and peoples—came by the power of the Dao’s majesty to hear the Dharma. They gathered beyond the infinitesimal realm, standing with the Eight Sea Spirit Kings in the empty void, serene and still.

Then, the Great Sage of the Central Heaven, the Primordial Sovereign Dao Lord of the Void, arrived to echo the Dharma, accompanied by innumerable sages from the ten directions, assembling upon golden clouds in the sky, five hundred *ren* distant from the infinitesimal realm. When the two assemblies had fully arrayed themselves, the Central Dao Lord summoned the divine winds to stir the celestial pipes, intoning the subtle verses of the *Empty Cavern* and the numinous hymns of *Pacing the Void*. The thirty-seven thousand kinds of perfected beings in attendance chanted for ninety-nine days before concluding.

Then, within the infinitesimal realm, the Jade Clarity Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion commanded the nine myriad myriad immortals of the Grand Tenuity to wield the six myriad forty-two thousand four hundred and twenty talismanic verses of the *Returning Soul* and *Dispelling Demons*, along with the *Yin-Generated Melodies*, harmonizing the multitudes for eighty-eight days until the symphony was complete.

When the Heavenly Worthy had accomplished these two tasks in full detail, he sat in silence with the assembled sages.

At that moment, the Eight Sea Great Spirits and the Five Emperors and Earth Deity were suddenly seized by doubt and disbelief. The Heavenly Worthy, perceiving their hesitation, employed his compassionate power to cause the earth and waters to overturn and reverse seven times. He then made the great earth quake, split, and shatter into motes of dust, only to instantly restore it, compact as a mustard seed. He further caused the Eight Seas to scatter their waves, suddenly drying them utterly, exposing the forms of the Water Lords, dragons, and fish. In an instant, he reduced the Eight Seas to a single droplet, fine as a needle’s tip, and blew it into the void. In the blink of an eye, he restored all to its former state.

Witnessing this sovereign transformation of power, the Earth Deity and the Eight Sea Great Spirits were overcome with awe, though by the Dao’s power, they could not fathom the nature of all dharmas. Why? The earth and waters are yin in substance, and their spirits’ minds are dull; thus, they could not comprehend. After a long while, their minds stirred slightly with understanding. Then, beyond the infinitesimal realm, they prostrated to the north, repenting and reproaching themselves. Their five limbs pressed to the ground like a collapsing mountain, their bodies bathed in blood, weeping bitterly for a long time.

Thereupon, the Earth Deity addressed the Heavenly Worthy: “I, born in darkness and obscurity, am charged with upholding the earth. Though I oversee the nine lands without rest, I ride the Dao’s upright qi to nurture the myriad beings, aiding virtue and fostering transformation. I dare not falter in my toil, yet for the sake of all dust-like beings, I have failed to attain the Dao. I beseech the Heavenly Worthy to bestow great compassion and mercy.” Having spoken, he wept uncontrollably.

Next came the great spirits of the Eight Seas, the dragon kings and their retinues, and all the water-dwelling beings—numberless in their multitude. The Dragon King of the Black Pearl, keenest of wit among them, led the chorus of aquatic deities. Rising upon the waves, he addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying:

“By great fortune, I am entrusted with the watery realm, aiding the passage of boats and ferries, moistening all below, and assisting the Dao in its transformative work, washing away filth and cleansing dust. Though I have rendered slight service, my heart knows no reliance. Day and night, I am submerged, adrift in the surging waves. My coarse and massive form cannot ascend lightly, bound as I am to the turbid qi. Yet my perception is narrow and feeble, and I have not attained the profound and subtle. For years uncounted, I have yearned for the Most Venerable. Now, by the divine power of the Dao, I have come to this assembly to hear the Dharma, yet beyond the merest hair’s breadth, I cannot enter. My heart is filled with doubt and uncertainty. I beseech the Heavenly Worthy, by the power of great compassion, to grant me guidance and reception, that I may enter the infinitesimal.”

Having spoken, he reproached himself, his waves surging and overflowing, the waters rising to the heavens in tumult. His lamentation boiled forth, his sobs dark and mournful, his grief bitter and profound. In an instant, all rivers and seas seethed with blood. The Five Emperors and Earth Ancestors trembled, the great earth quaked, sharing in his sorrow. Metal and stone wept, grasses and trees shrouded themselves in mist, springs flowed backward, and the earth itself groaned like thunder. The beings within the earth quaked in terror, their eyes unable to blink. Birds fell from the sky, beasts flung themselves to the ground. The Five Emperors and Earth Deities wept blood from both eyes, staining the vast earth. The land and seas turned crimson, like a dawn of cinnabar, the hue lingering for eight months before fading.

At that time, the great spirit-kings, the deities of heaven and earth, thunder and lightning, wind and storm, gathered for the Dharma. Their winds and thunder roared, their lightning flashed with fierce brilliance, startling the creatures in their deep burrows, uprooting all things by their roots, and sweeping away the dust to assemble from the four directions, halting in the empty sky.

Then, too, the various kings of the earth—kings of great mountains, fragrant trees, divine herbs, fish, turtles, birds, horses, oxen, lions, wind-beasts, fierce beasts, celestial unicorns, celestial birds, celestial horses, celestial deer—all followed the great earth to the assembly. Though their ears heard the Dharma, their mouths could not speak. Seeing the divine spirits’ sorrow and anguish, they too wailed in grief, their eyes streaming blood, each prostrating upon the ground, unable to rise.

Then, the Heavenly Worthy, moved by the divine spirits’ entanglement in impurity and their inability to hear the true Dao, their suffering so profound, spoke to them in a voice like thunder:

“Excellent, excellent! You should now understand the nature of this assembly and the cause of its arising. I say to you: after six million years following the kalpa of dragons, when the blessings of heaven and earth are exhausted and calamities arise, unable to bear the sight, I and the great sages descend to the four continents to safeguard the kalpa, renewing the myriad beings and responding to the mandate to deliver humankind. Thus, I have come to this assembly. By my sovereign divine power, I have summoned you here. You should know that the great assembly gathered here has entered the infinitesimal from the boundless Dao-realms of the ten directions, yet it is not cramped. How then can the multitudes of your five trillion worlds—your great earths and eight seas—be considered vast? To doubt that this infinitesimal can contain you is a sign of your spirits’ impurity, evil views, and narrow minds, your failure to deeply trust in the awe-inspiring power of the supreme Dao.

If you wish to enter this infinitesimal realm, you must cast aside distracting thoughts, afflictions, attachments of love, greed, anger, and delusion, all inverted and perverse views, all doubts and hindrances of worldly toil. Sever all fettering habits, and only then may you enter this wondrous assembly. If you cling to perceptions and distinctions, judging good and evil, harboring enmity or affection, you will remain bound and forever barred from this subtle and marvelous gathering.”

Then, the Heavenly Worthy, employing his skillful means to subdue the divine spirits, declared:

“Your spirits’ transgressions are deep, your impurity and defilement profound. You have not yet entered this wondrous assembly. You must reflect and distance yourselves from dust and filth. In the future, you may behold me.”

Having spoken these words, the Heavenly Worthy emerged from the eastern cloud-gate of the infinitesimal. With his left hand, he gathered the great earth and mingled it with the sea waters, compressing them into a single mustard seed. He cast it into the empty void above, where it remained serene and unmoving for eighty thousand great kalpas.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy, within the infinitesimal, expounded the subtle and wondrous Dharma to the great assembly. After eighty thousand kalpas, when the teaching was complete, he retrieved the mustard seed from the empty void above and placed it upon the tip of the infinitesimal, restoring the great earth and seas to their original state. The Earth Deity, Water Emperor, human kings, and all beings remained unaware.

Then, perceiving that the hearts of these spirits had not yet awakened, the Heavenly Worthy manifested a vast form filling the empty sky. From the left side of the infinitesimal, he emerged with measured steps. With the tip of a needle, he drew in the great earth and seas, placing them within the infinitesimal’s northern void. Like a single speck of dust in the vastness of space, it caused no obstruction.

At that moment, the dragon spirits of the Eight Seas and the earth deities entered the infinitesimal, circling the Heavenly Worthy for kalpas uncounted, yet still unable to encircle him, even in flight. Only then did they awaken, marveling at what they had never before witnessed.

Within the great earth, kings, ministers, common folk, and all manner of beings who had entered from the earth remained unaware, perceiving neither departure nor arrival. Within this infinitesimal, there were boundless Dao-realms, each layered upon the next. Each realm contained all things—heavens and earths, suns and moons, mountains and rivers, seas and lands, countless peoples—numbering thirty-six thousand kinds of human and celestial beings.

At that time, among the assembly were twelve thousand kinds of beings from the Central Pillar, and among them was an elder named Wisdom-Life. Together with the great multitude, they beheld this divine power yet could not fathom it. Supporting one another, they came to the gathering place, bowed in reverence, and addressed the Heavenly Worthy:

"We do not understand: when the Heavenly Worthy first descended from the heavens, within the palaces, towers, lofty pavilions, and lotus flowers, did the Heavenly Worthy—the Great Sage—and those who first heard the Dao each have the Heavenly Worthy expounding the wondrous Dharma within their bodies and minds? And did the Compassionate Heavenly Worthy emerge from their hearts in tranquil majesty, surrounded by jeweled trees and spontaneous celestial music? And within this infinitesimal speck, were there lands and cities, banners and jeweled canopies, each seat lofty and wondrous, with such extraordinary transformations? We do not know—is this a matter of constancy or impermanence?"

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "Excellent, excellent, good man! Listen carefully, and I shall explain. When I descend from the heavens to the realm of ordinary beings, I manifest seven kinds of subtle and wondrous phenomena. You should know that the Supreme Great Dao always descends to transform the world through the Seven Awakening Sagely Ways, responding to the seven subtle and wondrous qi of spontaneity to accomplish the seven transformative Dharmas. Because the world is limited, the Great Dao responds with names and numbers—these names and numbers all correspond to the subtle and wondrous Dharmas of spontaneity.

Good man, you ask whether this wondrous attainment is constant or impermanent. You should know that the Dharma of the Great Dao is neither born nor destroyed. How then can one ask whether it is constant or impermanent? Good man, the divine power of the Great Dao leaves nothing undone, is nowhere absent, adapts to all circumstances, and responds to all things. Its true transformations are boundless, its spiritual roots profound. It pities the multitudes, manifests palaces in response, and even the slightest causes and conditions are not worth questioning. If it wills existence, it exists; if it wills non-existence, it ceases. If it wills constancy, it endures; if it wills cessation, it is cut off. Through the divine power of the Dao, nothing is obstructed.

You further ask whether the Heavenly Worthy within the lotus is my true qi, vast and pervasive—whether this is my own essence, not that of another sage. You also ask about those who first heard the Dao: when the wondrous Dharma-sound emerges from their bodies and minds, is this because the first human king to hear the Dao deeply believed and matured in faith, free from all attachments? Is this very body thus transformed into the Dharma-body, with all its bones and nine orifices infused with the Dao’s qi, making this person’s body no different from the Dao? All in this assembly are likewise so. Therefore, the Great Dao, in its compassion, manifests within their bodies.

Good man, you also doubt the myriad wonders within this wondrous assembly. You should know that the Great Dao takes this infinitesimal speck as one Dao-realm, and from one Dao-realm creates boundless Dao-realms—these realms are constant. Why? Ordinary beings call them impermanent, but the Sagely Way of constancy names them constant. Why? Because the lifespan of ordinary beings is uncertain, and due to this uncertainty, they deem the Great Dao impermanent. Yet the Sagely Way of constancy endures eternally, clearly illuminating the constant Dao.

Good man, if one were to speak of the constant Dao to ordinary beings, their minds would be filled with doubt, inverted views, and the growth of unwholesomeness. Therefore, the Great Dao adapts to conditions and responds to potentials. Why? Because the ordinary beings of the lower realms are diverse, their natures and dispositions varied. Those of the highest grade who hear the Dao devote themselves to cultivation, attain true immortality, and never regress—they are taught the constant. Those of the middle grade who hear the Dao have not yet fully believed, their minds wavering—they may be taught either the constant or the impermanent. Those of the lowest grade who hear the Dao give rise to slander—they are taught the impermanent, and their perceptions are likewise.

Within this wondrous assembly, the Celestial Perfected Sages name it constant, yet the Dharma they expound may be either constant or impermanent. Why? Because the Celestial Perfected Sages teach the Dharma to the demonic spirits, gods, and miscellaneous beings in this assembly as impermanent. Good man, the infinitesimal is likewise so. Ordinary beings do not perceive the constant Dao, do not comprehend its wondrous principle, and cannot attain the subtle and true ultimate. Though they ride the power of the Dao and temporarily enter diligent practice, they may later regress—this is called impermanent. The Heavenly Worthy and Great Sages are free from mental fetters, emerging from emptiness and entering the formless, never obstructed—this is called constant.

Good man, the majestic power of the wondrous Dao is inconceivable. Because it is inconceivable, it can cause all things in the ten directions—heavens and earths—to enter the infinitesimal, without constraint or confinement. Good man, if the power of the Supreme Dao were conceivable, then the myriad things of heaven and earth could not enter this wondrous assembly. Good man, you should know that all the sages and multitudes who enter this assembly dwell in the inconceivable, in liberation and wisdom. Why? Those who enter this assembly do not enter with the body, nor with the mind; they do not act with the body, nor with the mind; they do not enter through principle. It is solely through the power of the Great Dao’s compassion, forbearance, and patience that they are able to enter this infinitesimal assembly."

Then, the elder Wisdom-Life, together with his retinue of twelve thousand kinds of beings—a multitude as numerous as motes of dust—heard the words of the Heavenly Worthy. Their minds opened in understanding, and they bowed again in gratitude to the Heavenly Worthy, offering this hymn of praise:

"We bow to the Dark Wisdom, the Venerable of Emptiness,
We bow in devotion to the Lord of the Profound Mystery.
You fashion heaven and earth, yet cannot be named,
For all beings, You are the refuge and support.
Compassionate, You deliver the souls of the Five Paths’ turning wheel,
Pitying and rescuing those suffering in the Three Realms’ hells.
We devote ourselves to the Heavenly Worthy of the Golden Palace,
To the Compassionate Father of the Six Perfections.
We devote ourselves to the Supreme Perfected of Jade Purity,
Who transcends birth and death, eternally enduring.
Emerging from existence, entering emptiness, beholden to none,
You transform the withered and decayed into immortals.
Once in a thousand, ten thousand kalpas is such an encounter,
For the multitudes, You broadly expound the causes and conditions of karma."

Restoring the dead to life, granting eternal abiding,
You make my form and spirit free from change and decay.

Then, Elder Wisdom-Life, having spoken this hymn, prostrated himself fully to the ground, bowed in gratitude to the Heavenly Worthy, and addressed him thus: "We do not know how many kalpas have passed since the Heavenly Worthy attained the Dao. What virtues have you cultivated? How have you reached such majestic heights? By what karmic conditions have you attained deathlessness? By what virtues do you deliver those suffering in hell?"

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "Since I attained the Dao, the number of kalpas has been like the dust motes of the ten directions’ heavens and earths—incalculable. It is like empty space, immeasurable. Good man, I cultivate great compassion and great mercy, vowing to deliver all beings. I constantly practice forbearance and gentleness, never losing harmony and balance. Thus, I do not die. I constantly use the Six Perfections to deliver those in hell. Good man, though I have attained the Dao, I still do not depart from compassion, forbearance, and gentleness—how much more should ordinary beings do so?"

Then, Elder Wisdom-Life, together with his retinue of twelve thousand kinds of people, having heard the Heavenly Worthy’s words, rejoiced with great joy. They bowed their heads again, prostrated themselves before the Heavenly Worthy, and said: "By deep and abundant past blessings, we were born in this age of the Dao’s transformation. We have beheld the Compassionate Worthy face-to-face and heard the sound of the Dharma with our own ears. Yet our minds were once dim and dull, and though we received the secret essentials, we forgot much. Though foolish and ignorant, our hearts love virtue and the Dao. We fear that our bodies will decay and age, and we will not long remain. We constantly worry that one day we will suddenly be like ants, our bodies perishing into endless darkness, with no way to see the Dao. Once the root of life is lost, we will drift for ten thousand kalpas. Now, by good fortune, we have encountered a lofty sage. We wish to be delivered. We beg to receive the Dao of long life and enduring vision. We only hope that the Compassionate Worthy will bestow the gift of life."

Having spoken these words, they prostrated themselves fully to the ground, striking their heads in sorrow and weeping until their bodies streamed with blood.
