The Heavenly Worthy remained silent and did not consent. Then, the twelve thousand kinds of people, as numerous as dust motes, fainted in despair, beating their breasts upon the ground. At that time, the Heavenly Worthy, moved by their earnestness, rose and helped them up. After a long while, they revived.

The Heavenly Worthy said: "All of you, in past kalpas, once made offerings to the True Immortals of Emptiness and the Hosts of Virtue and the Dao. The blessings from this flow into your present lives, and your names are recorded in the left register. Moreover, our Dharma assembly has descended to teach in kalpa after kalpa. It is by this karmic condition that you have encountered me. You should diligently focus your minds, cast aside worldly entanglements, and retreat to fast and reflect on your faults. Return after three months, and I will transmit to you the essentials of the true Dao and long life."

Hearing this, the people rejoiced and leapt with joy. They bowed in gratitude to the Heavenly Worthy and returned to their homes, washing away worldly dust and purifying themselves inside and out. When the three months had passed, each brought incense, flowers, and offerings, and came to the assembly place.

At that time, in the dust-mote worlds of that assembly, all the kings, princes, ministers, common people, men and women—numberless—heard that Elder Wisdom-Life was to request the essentials of the Dao. Together, with one voice, they addressed the Heavenly Worthy and spoke this hymn:

"Our hidden affinity is fundamentally impartial,
Yet it responds to karmic conditions as they arise.
We wish to attain the Dao of long life,
To scatter and sow it in the fields of our hearts.
The water of the Six Perfections’ pure source
Flows boundlessly without shore."

When the great assembly had spoken this hymn, they all prostrated themselves at once, together requesting to receive deliverance.

At that time, the Five Great Demon Emperors, seeing these people prostrated and requesting the Dharma, each played stringed instruments, sang songs, and struck up music. After a long while, they ceased.

Then, the Great Demon Emperor of the Blue Realm spoke this hymn:

"To cultivate the Dao, one must accumulate merit.
To enter the trial depends on the heavenly demons.
Do not let your body commit transgressions,
Or I will vainly sing in the empty sky.
In an instant, I will seize your form—
Who then could resist me?
First, you must send away all desires,
Bathe and rinse in the recesses of famous mountains.
Do not be a person of the dust,
Hastening and hurrying in the waves of the world."

The Demon King of the Red Realm spoke this hymn:

"The Flaming Palace illumines the cinnabar skies,
Bright and clear, its radiant qi floats.
Evil winds stir the turbid dust,
Ever swirling without cease.
My realm is difficult to cross—
Whether you leave or linger, the time is now.
Merit and transgression distinguish themselves clearly;
The demons do not forcibly seek them."

The Demon King of the White Realm spoke this hymn:

"The Silver Palace emerges from the Great Void,
Its circular net illumines the night’s glow.
Ten thousand times it recites the numinous chapters,
Guiding wandering souls to follow the qi and return.
Those who turn their backs on the Dao enter the dark tombs,
Where bitter mists ever swirl.
Love and attachment waste the spirit;
The buried corpse loses all hope of flight.
My realm will not permit passage—
The demons vainly lament in the empty sky."

The Demon King of the Black Realm spoke this hymn:

"The mysterious sap nourishes the jade roots,
The jade liquid refines the true form.
As the setting sun returns to Fusang,
Form and spirit never decay.
Why then betray virtue and the Dao,
Ever grieving over rot and decay?
Who among the Six Heavens seeks to preserve you?
At the brink of peace, you turn back to greater peril."

The Demon King of the Yellow Realm spoke this hymn:

"The Cloud Palace, serene and remote, emerges from the cinnabar skies,
Floating through the void, its flying canopy ascends at dawn.
Secretly aligned with the numinous source, the six qi soar,
In emptiness, the true master naturally summons.
The celestial thoroughfare is lush with purple mist,
The mysterious path is swift with rosy clouds.
Who knows the suffering of sinking in my realm?
Why hesitate and refuse to transcend?
The world naturally drifts into long night—
It is not that the demon hosts forcibly invite you."

When the Five Great Demon Emperors had sung these songs, each emitted fragrant qi from their bodies to envelop the people. They also played five hundred kinds of demonic sounds to confuse the minds of the assembly. They raised demonic banners to disturb their eyes. Some appeared as beautiful women, inviting in various ways. Some took on strange forms, unknown in the world. Some emitted light from their bodies, illuminating a hundred miles. Some uttered terrible sounds, making the hearers’ hair stand on end. Some spat fire from their heads. Some walked on empty space. Some entered the earth. Some transformed their forms—old or young—skilled in creating illusions, their qi striking against people. Some touched people with their bodies. Some transformed into human shapes, or into people’s relatives and old acquaintances, flattering in various ways. Some entered people’s bodies, causing them to attain concentration, their eyes able to see clearly, their minds knowing the karmic conditions of two lifetimes—past and future. Their demeanor was extraordinary, and they skillfully expounded the essentials of the Dharma, confusing and disturbing people’s minds.

Yet the great assembly at this gathering, through the divine power of the Dao, focused their minds unwaveringly. The demons could not defeat them.

In an instant, the Five Great Demons of the Five Directions, along with their retinues, withdrew their awe-inspiring power. Facing north, they stood in attendance beside the Heavenly Worthy, reverently still to hear the Dharma.

At that time, the celestial beings of the Eastern Azure Heaven, rejoicing to hear the Dharma, leapt with joy. Through the divine power of the Dao, they aided and encouraged those of later generations, strengthening their resolve. They sang in praise to gladden their hearts and guide them to the true Dao, chanting:

*"At Fusang, the first rays dawn,
Lush and verdant, the green sprouts rise.
Divine qi floats o’er the cosmic net,
Spirit birds illumine the purple haze.
Attaining the Dao of eternal life,
They dwell in the silent, true abode."*

Next, the celestial beings of the Southern Vermilion Heaven sang:

*"Fiery qi floats o’er the crimson sky,
True light shines with numinous signs.
Flying auroras gleam like eightfold jade,
Divine nectar transforms to frost-like pearls.
Ninefold radiance glows in sacred vessels,
Streaming hues illumine the Dark Capital.
Eons pass in the blink of an eye,
Yet form and soul never wither.
Ascending, they enter the Great Subtlety,
Nine generations escape the long road."*

Then, the celestial beings of the Western White Heaven sang:

*"Mysterious truth halts the fading light,
The setting sun returns to its first glow.
Divine nectar sprinkles golden streams,
Suddenly draped in robes of flowing haze.
Vast and boundless, they return to the Supreme Emperor,
Misty and ethereal, they ascend the Purple Tenuity.
Guiding their chariots of divine light,
They merge in flight as eternal immortals."*

Next, the celestial beings of the Northern Dark Heaven sang:

*"Whirling the net, they tread with divine steps,
Soul and spirit assist true essence.
To the right, they support the White Prime Lord,
To the left, they guard the Everlasting Hero.
Mysterious nectar exhales numinous streams,
Auras of light follow the moon’s birth.
Thus do they regulate the children of the years,
Neither decaying nor inclining."*

At that time, the celestial beings, for the sake of hearing the Dharma, enriching sentient beings, aiding the Dao with expedient means, unfolding the great transformation, liberating the living, and realizing the fruition of the Dao, chanted these hymns of praise in natural tones to instruct those of later generations who seek to attain the true Dao. By reciting and contemplating them, secretly seeking the true accord without reckless disclosure, they would surely achieve the Dao without doubt.

After these hymns were sung, each returned to their original seats.

Then, the Supreme Sage Primordial Sovereign of the Central Upper Realm, the Heavenly Worthy of the Void, along with the assembly of sages, manifested as an echo of the Dharma to establish great faith. They protected and cherished those reborn in the world, guiding them to rectitude, dispelling chaotic thoughts, and leading them into the current of the Dao, forever free from birth and death. Thus, they came to dwell in the empty space above, in perfect accord with the Heavenly Worthy of the Jade Clarity Heaven in the wondrous assembly, responding and transforming in the lower realms, rightly stabilizing the celestial origin. Through kalpas unending, they have appeared—not only today.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy of the Void, for the sake of liberating beings, descended from the empty space above into the wondrous assembly with the hosts of sages from the ten directions, each riding celestial palaces. They arrived at the assembly of Great Compassion, sitting to the left of the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion on a shared seat—vast and towering, its summit reaching the limits of the ten directions. Through the power of compassion, even the tiniest hair’s original form remained unmoved, and the great assembly within it felt no constriction, as if unchanged from before.

At that time, the radiance of the two Heavenly Worthies’ bodies surpassed the rising sun, and the assembled sages shone likewise. To liberate sentient beings, they displayed the power of great compassion and expedient means. From the feet of the sages, light emerged in myriad transformations, gradually illuminating their entire forms until their bodies became translucent, like crystal. They gathered all heavens and earths, sun and moon, stars, mountains and rivers, seas, lands and peoples, and all sentient beings, lifting them into the instep of the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion’s left foot, within a single hair’s tip.

In an instant, they ascended to the instep of the Heavenly Worthy of the Void’s right foot, within a single hair’s tip. Then, in another instant, they rose into the empty space, nine billion miles above the earth, directly before the golden beak of the Heavenly Worthy of the Void. The Heavenly Worthy exhaled a subtle breath of fragrant qi, and all those heavens and earths crumbled into motes of dust, filling the void. Then, with another command, they reassembled as before.

In an instant, the Heavenly Worthy lifted all heavens, earths, and peoples into the empty space, directly before the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion. With the divine power of the Dao, the Heavenly Worthy blew upon these heavens and earths, causing the sun, moon, stars, mountains, rivers, seas, cities, peoples, birds, and beasts to merge into a single body, as small as a mustard seed—round, luminous, and translucent, indestructible as vajra. Then, in another instant, they were lifted into the palm of the Heavenly Worthy of the Void, within its lines, transforming into light and qi.

Within this light and qi, four kinds of qi appeared—clear, turbid, white, and black. Within the lines of the Heavenly Worthy’s palm, they gradually differentiated and expanded: the clear qi became heaven, the turbid qi became earth, the white qi became the sun, and the black qi became the moon. The sun became the essence of yang, the moon the essence of yin, giving rise to male and female, from which all things were transformed and born.

At that time, the celestial beings in the assembly witnessed this divine transformation and marveled, never having seen the like. Then, the Celestial Being of No-Intent from the Eastern Azure Heaven, for the sake of sentient beings, rose from his seat, advanced, and bowed. He addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: *"We beg to know—by what cause and condition did the Heavenly Worthy perform this divine transformation? By what cause and condition were heaven and earth destroyed and formed? By what cause and condition were things made to enter the void?"*

"By what cause and condition do things emerge from the void? This disciple’s understanding is shallow and fails to grasp the ultimate principle. We beseech the Heavenly Worthy to bestow insight into the wondrous workings. May you show compassion and instruct us in what we have never heard."

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy of the Void replied in verse:
*"Originally, for the sake of human blessings exhausted,
I descended to the four heavens below.
The true body is fundamentally ever-quiet,
Yet for beings, it responds to the illusory.
Transformations arise from pity for the living,
And lamentation cannot cease.
When the kalpa arrives and heaven and earth are destroyed,
Their formation arises from this body of mine.
Unable to bear witnessing such suffering,
I descend to the world to display my majestic power,
Guiding beings to return to their root,
That they may truly believe in karmic conditions.
The dust and turbidity naturally dissolve into emptiness,
Following the Dao to become perfected immortals.
Once all worldly burdens are fully dispelled,
The pure and limpid remain untouched by the rest.
Forever severing the path of birth and death,
They emerge serene into the Great Void."*

Then, having spoken this verse, the Heavenly Worthy addressed the assembly of celestial beings, saying: "Good sons, you should know that the method of delivering beings must not be taken lightly. Through the compassionate power of the Dao, one must first manifest various divine transformations to subdue their minds, observe their capacities, and then perform the appropriate method. I constantly show compassion, guiding them by the left hand, though I display breath and influence, I do not allow them to be startled or terrified. Though I manifest these various divine transformations of heaven, earth, and the myriad things, their fundamental nature remains profoundly still and unchanging. I have never forcibly performed divine transformations—it is simply through the one Dao, the one method, the one power of compassion for beings that, according to their capacities, they perceive various phenomena, though the nature of this Dharma is truly not manifold.

Good sons, you should now understand that the methods for delivering sentient beings are also manifold. The Heavenly Worthy, through the great sage’s divine power and self-mastery, employs skillful means to liberate them without their awareness—this is called the treasury of the Dao’s skillful means. Worldly ordinary people, when aiding goodness and transformation, propagating the Dao and its teachings, necessarily rely on written words, speech, and parables. Without these, there would be no way to gain their trust.

Good sons, at this assembly, I now deliver all men and women, inscribing them upon the left register. These multitudes attaining the Dao, I subtly circulate the qi of life to render them deathless, gathering all demonic trials to eliminate their disturbances."

At that time, the Venerable Elder of Wise Life, together with the great assembly, heard the Heavenly Worthy’s words, and their minds opened in awakening. All attained the six penetrations and the supreme fruition of the Dao. Then, the Five Thearchs of the Great Demons, witnessing the Heavenly Worthy’s power of the Dao, transformed in body and mind for the good. With their retinues, they advanced, bowed, and addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "We ghosts and spirits, receiving our unfortunate retribution, are born into perverse paths and lack self-mastery. Some are employed by heaven and earth, roaming the four heavens below to carry out poisonous harms; others are invaded by those who expose transgressions, recording sins in the ledgers, testing the newly initiated, and verifying the truly upright."

Their ceaseless toil knew no respite. Yet ashamed of their foul, restless bodies and grotesque forms, they harbored a private devotion to the Dao, reproaching themselves day and night. Filled with remorse and shame, they longed to beseech the Heavenly Worthy for the gift of transformation, to join the current of the Dao, and cast off their demonic forms—even in death, they would have no regrets. They implored the Heavenly Worthy to bestow the grace of the Dao’s revelation, to broadly deliver all without limit, that humans and spirits alike might be universally liberated.

Having spoken thus, they leapt into the empty sky, soaring six thousand *zhang* high, then hurled themselves to the earth, their bodies streaming blood. All the demons simultaneously expired. The Heavenly Worthy, moved by compassion, after a long while commanded the Incense-Bearing Golden Youth to burn the *Returning Soul Incense* and fumigate the demons. He then ordered the Supreme Harmony Immortals to disperse the *qi* of life, the Six Jia Attendants to bestow the talismans of *yin* rebirth upon the demons, the Lord of Life Dao Master to summon their hun-souls and po-souls, and the Master of Transformed Forms to alter their demonic bodies.

After a long while, the demons revived, their forms and spirits transformed, their essence and vitality pure and harmonious, their minds simple and unadulterated. Filled with great compassion, they attained the rank of the Dao’s portion and, in reverse contemplation, perceived the events of ninety thousand kalpas to come. All this was wrought by the power of the divine talismans.

The demons, now in attendance upon the Heavenly Worthy, bowed in gratitude for the gift of rebirth, leaping and rejoicing with delight. Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy bestowed upon the demons—five hundred million in number—the office of *Lingren*, commanding them to advance in the methods of the Primordial Upper Dao.

*Thus concludes the second scroll of the* Jade Clarity Scripture of the Supreme Great Dao.

**Chapter Eight: The Salvation of the Netherworld**

At that time, the *Lingren* and all others, having received deliverance and ascended to the realm of the Dao, felt shame and remorse in their hearts. They reflected thus: "Unlooked-for, in a single moment, we encountered the Heavenly Worthy, our bodies transformed and reborn, forever freed from affliction. We bear the grace of the Dao’s favor—such boundless mercy! In our private thoughts, we vow to rely upon the majesty and numinous power of the Dao, widely extending its reach to both the hidden and the manifest, swearing to deliver all from peril and hardship. We shall proclaim the teachings of the Dao, ensuring they never cease."

They spoke among themselves: "Recalling our past, we met no fortunate conditions, mired in filth and defilement, revolving endlessly through birth and death, falling into depravity, never hearing the true Dao. In those times of suffering, to whom could we turn? Though we now grieve and lament, the pain lingers in our hearts and eyes. Though we have been saved, we have not forgotten our former sorrows. Moreover, we fear that the Heavenly Worthy, the Great Sage, is bound to the Upper Primordial, while those below in the lower realms are meager in fortune, steeped in impurity and evil. The Perfected Immortals, dwelling in emptiness, will not long remain in the world. Though we in this assembly have received deliverance, there yet remain the Nine Netherworlds, where suffering spirits languish unseen by sun or moon, trapped in endless night through countless kalpas, with no means of liberation."

Then the *Lingren* of the Eastern Azure Emperor advanced, bowed, and addressed the Heavenly Worthy: "We humbly ask whether the Heavenly Worthy’s boundless transformation and deliverance extend to the Nine Netherworlds, freeing those in suffering from their torment. We, your disciples, remain ignorant and have not yet attained understanding. We beseech the Heavenly Worthy, in your great compassion, to deign to explain, that we may awaken."

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "Excellent, excellent, *Lingren*! Your question is not amiss in its great compassion. I manifest a responsive body and descend to transform and deliver the suffering souls in the hells—those not of the ten evils’ category, who may yet receive rebirth. But if their sins are deep and grave, there are limits beyond which the Dao’s transformation cannot reach. Why is this? Those who commit the ten evils bring calamity upon themselves; none other inflicts it. They invite misfortune and guilt, falling into hell. Some, in their lifetimes, did not heed their teachers’ instruction or encounter scriptural teachings; others were born in borderlands, meeting no good companions, knowing only theft and killing, committing all manner of unlawful acts, and so died to enter hell. Such persons’ sins are relatively light. Even those born in the central lands, though foolish, have heard the Dharma, yet still transgress in life and die to enter hell. These, in the cycle of birth and death, never believe in the Dao, following their own natures to create evil karma, revolving through retribution. They are like worldly men, fierce and stubborn, unafraid of death; though threatened, they remain unshaken—what can be done? Or like children who love play, heedless of their parents’ admonitions; though given treats and taught, their hearts do not change; even if beaten, they do not awaken. Those who commit the ten evils are likewise. Or like flies drawn to rot and stench, their nature compels them, and they cannot change. Those who commit the ten evils are the same. Like moths rushing toward light, they bring about their own burning destruction. Those who commit the ten evils are the same.

*Lingren*, know this: where those who commit the ten evils dwell, many evil companions abound. They skillfully devise means to contrive wicked deeds, and through such causes and conditions, they mislead and fall into evil. Moreover, they instruct their families, wives, and children to act unrighteously, perpetuating their wicked ways. Through such causes and conditions, the living and the dead become entangled, mutually bearing one another’s burdens. When descendants seek peace, sinful spirits endanger them; when sinful ghosts seek escape, descendants hinder them. The retribution of karma in birth and death is like a wheel, its end unseen. Trapped in endless night, there is no liberation; they suffer ceaselessly, never knowing rest.

*Lingren*, know that the Great Dao is ever-diligent, never abandoning even these. Yet beings, unaware, instead grow resentful and harmful. They do not practice the supreme Dao’s methods, nor do they follow its majestic rites and precepts. They refuse to embrace purity and emptiness, instead plunging heedlessly into the turbid filth of the world. They indulge in sensual pleasures, chasing after distraction, gluttonous for rich flavors, seeking sustenance through devious means. Merchants and traders take only treacherous paths, never once treading the safe and level Way. They kill living beings and harm lives without shame. Seeking only warmth and fullness, they hoard without limit; when impoverished, they harbor thieving hearts. They devise a hundred schemes to fulfill their desires, harming others to benefit themselves, never reflecting or retreating. In life, they perform no good deeds, only accumulating evil day by day. In death, they enter hell, their souls enduring retribution, suffering every torment. They bring calamity upon themselves—what can be done? Though the Dao is ever-diligent, the ignorant do not follow.

*Lingren*, know this: it is like the spring rain, which moistens all things, yet there are withered trees that do not receive its nourishment. Those untouched by the rain only rot further, never sprouting branches, leaves, flowers, or fruit. Those who commit the ten evils are the same: though they hear the Great Dao, they never arouse the supreme mind of the Dao."

Then the *Lingren* addressed the Heavenly Worthy: "We humbly ask: from what do those who commit the ten evils receive rebirth? Their perversity turns away from goodness, their evil roots run deep and cannot be uprooted."

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "Good and evil both arise from the same Dao. It is like travelers: one walks toward the Dao, the other turns away. Those who turn away from the Dao lose their way in dark mountains, straying into shadowed valleys. There, many vicious beasts, thorns, and poisonous brambles await; their clothes and provisions run out, and suffering presses upon them. A hundred afflictions arise, and they die in distress. Their souls revolve, receiving retribution according to their karma. Those who walk toward the Dao find their path unimpeded; whatever they seek, they attain. Moreover, they meet many good companions, finding shelter wherever they go. If they wish to see the king, they may go as they please. Because they walk toward the Dao, no benefit eludes them. These two kinds, though their practices differ and their directions diverge, are not so by the Dao’s design."

The Dao is inherently unobstructed; it is the practitioners who turn toward or away, their paths of opposition and compliance diverging. Those who commit the ten evils lose the Dao through their own actions, not because the Dao abandons them. Those who turn toward the Dao attain it through their own efforts, not because the Dao bestows it upon them.

Let the spiritually awakened know: our host of sages, kalpa after kalpa, descends to transform beings. Though those who commit the ten evils do not believe in the Dao, the Dao never departs from them.

Then the spiritually awakened one again addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "I fear that those who commit the ten evils, their karmic habits deeply ingrained, turn away from the Dao in life and death, making them beyond transformation and deliverance. It is like shards of pottery—once broken, they cannot be rejoined."

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "The majestic power of the Great Dao is like a great forge, smelting all gold—nothing remains unrefined. Know this, spiritually awakened one: those among the ten evils whom I have not yet transformed, I first let them endure suffering, waiting until they grow weary and repentant before transforming them. I shall reveal to them the supreme, majestic, and freely wielded transformations of the Dao, compelling them to submit and return."

The spiritually awakened one again asked: "I wonder, Heavenly Worthy, whether you will demonstrate your divine power as before or employ another method. I wish to witness it, that the nets of bondage may be untangled, gods and humans may prosper, and all—both hidden and manifest—be universally delivered. Would not such a vast and boundless transformation be most joyous?"

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "Wait but a moment, and you shall see."

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy, with boundless compassion unobstructed, transformed into one hundred thousand beings who had committed the ten evils. Their forms were tall and imposing, their strength robust, their words sharp and eloquent. Each confessed their crimes, unafraid of the karmic causes leading to birth, death, or hell. Before the Heavenly Worthy, in but a moment, he commanded a hundred thousand celestial immortals and direct envoys to bear banners of faith, descend into the Nine Dark Realms, and lead forth the sinful ghosts who had committed the ten evils. In an instant, all arrived together, joining the transformed beings in one place.

The Heavenly Worthy then transformed into a million mighty warriors, wielding great iron rods, interrogating the transformed beings about the reasons for their evil deeds. The transformed beings refused to submit. Thereupon, the warriors struck them with their rods, shattering them into fine dust.

Next, they questioned the sinful ghosts. Before the rods could be raised, the ghosts prostrated themselves in submission, begging to return to life and follow the Dao’s transformation.

Then the Heavenly Worthy commanded a million spiritually awakened ones, each grasping a left-hand tally, to fly in all directions, pursuing the descendants of the ghosts. In but a moment, countless billions, moved by the Dao’s majestic power, gathered at the assembly. Yet they did not return to faith, their hearts devoid of shame, claiming they should not have been suddenly summoned thrice.

Thereupon, the sinful ghosts, seeing their descendants, wailed in grief and gnashed their teeth, saying: "From whence have you, my fivefold treacherous and evil kin, come? Long have I desired to kill you but found no opportunity. When I am free, I shall exterminate your lineage."

Hearing this, the descendants’ hair stood on end. Instantly, their heads ached, and they suffered from cold, heat, and poisonous afflictions.

At that time, the sinful ghosts’ bodies were mutilated beyond recognition—some lacked hands or feet, some were flayed, some had their bellies split open, some were burned by fire or boiled in cauldrons, some had their flesh carved away, some had their eyes gouged out, some had their tongues torn out, some had their bones sawed apart, some were pierced all over with awls, some had their intestines hooked out, some were devoured by the six livestock. Their myriad sufferings defy description.

Those among the ghosts’ descendants who were born in the world had incurred debts to their ancestors and committed the ten evils, enduring countless karmic retributions and receiving their due in life. Some were blind, deaf, mute, or dumb; some had withered or paralyzed limbs; some were covered in malignant sores; some had lost their eyebrows and hair; some were riddled with bone-eating leprosy; some suffered from ulcers, fistulas, or swollen tumors; some had twisted faces; some oozed pus and blood; some were impoverished and destitute.

At that time, the sins of humans and ghosts were alike. After a long while, they looked at one another, weeping in sorrow, unable to bear it.

Then the Heavenly Worthy softly asked: "Why do you, humans and ghosts, both in life and death, remain in such a state, inferior to others? I now pity you and cannot bear to abandon you, so I have gathered you here from afar with the power of the Dao."

At that time, humans and ghosts, inwardly ashamed, gazed up at the Heavenly Worthy’s sacred body, radiant with purple-gold light, while the spiritually awakened ones shone like ice and snow.

Then, among the ten evils, one named Seeker of Profit stepped forward, bowed, and addressed the Heavenly Worthy: "I wonder, Heavenly Worthy, what meritorious deeds you have accomplished to attain such an extraordinary form, unmatched divine power, and flawless eloquence, unlike anything in the world. I wish you would tell me, that I may know the cause and origin of this."

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "There is no other practice among our sacred host but compassion, forbearance, diligence, upholding the precepts, generosity, and refraining from killing living beings. Through these causes and conditions, I have attained this state."

Hearing the Heavenly Worthy’s words, those who had committed the ten evils felt a slight turn toward goodness, silently repenting their past deeds, and prostrated themselves, unable to rise.

At that time, among the sinful ghosts, one named Return to the True saw his descendants and felt remorse for his past deeds. He also bowed and addressed the Heavenly Worthy: "I wonder, in the ghostly realm, can one still hear the Dharma? I lament my lifetime of evil, enduring the trials of ghosts and spirits, my karmic retribution unfinished, with no escape."

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "You need only contemplate the Dao, refrain from crooked ways, and in every place and circumstance, keep the Dao and its teachings in your heart. I shall save you."

At that time, the ghosts’ hearts turned toward faith, their sores and ulcers gradually diminishing, and the afflictions of the living also slightly improved.

In but a moment, the Ghost of Judgment and his underworld officers suddenly arrived, flying through the air. They addressed the Heavenly Worthy: "Earlier, we received your strict command to release the multitude of ghosts and dared not detain them. We wonder, Heavenly Worthy, by what cause and condition you have suddenly bestowed such great mercy, absolving the ten evils and erasing their vast sins. The records of these evil ghosts’ sins still exist, and their karmic retribution is unfinished."

The Heavenly Worthy, knowing their intent, employed skillful means to ask the Ghost of Judgment: "For what reasons did these ghosts, in life, die and enter hell, and for how many kalpas must they endure suffering?"

The Ghost of Judgment replied: "First, these ghosts in their lifetimes wantonly murdered their fathers, mothers, uncles, aunts, brothers, and sisters. Second, they rebelled against their sovereigns and wrongfully killed the multitudes. Third, during their lifetimes, they waylaid travelers on land and water, killing them to seize their wealth. Fourth, in their lifetimes, they defiled and scorned the Dao and its teachings, recklessly divulged scriptures, and undermined good deeds. Fifth, during their lifetimes, they trafficked their parents and kin for profit to enrich themselves. Sixth, in their lifetimes, they delighted in plundering households and nations. Seventh, in their lifetimes, they robbed corpses and desecrated tombs, scattering human remains. Eighth, in their lifetimes, they were unfilial to their parents, hoarding fine food for themselves. Ninth, in their lifetimes, they betrayed their teachers and turned their backs on the Dao, their hearts devoid of shame. Tenth, in their lifetimes, they bullied the orphaned and impoverished, secretly harmed the virtuous, and sowed discord with their tongues. For these sins, they died and entered hell, suffering for ten thousand kalpas."

The Heavenly Worthy, employing skillful means once more, further questioned the Ghost of Judgment regarding the ten evils: "What is meant by 'wantonly murdering fathers, mothers, uncles, aunts, brothers, and sisters'?"

The Ghost of Judgment answered: "Among the ten evils, some men lust after their mothers and kill their fathers; some women lust after their fathers and kill their mothers. The same applies to uncles, aunts, brothers, and sisters."

Upon hearing the Ghost of Judgment’s words, those guilty of the ten evils reflected on their own transgressions and the sins they had committed, which mirrored those of their ancestors. Fearing they too would descend into hell after death, their hair stood on end, their hearts trembled with terror, and they could not compose themselves. Overcome with remorse, they struck themselves until they bled.

The multitude of sinful ghosts wailed in unison, their cries like mountains collapsing.

The Ghost of Judgment continued: "The records of these ten evils’ sins in life and death are all in my keeping. I only inscribe their wickedness; no good is recorded. If neither the living nor the dead repent, how can the Heavenly Worthy intend to deliver these ten evils without meting out punishment, allowing them to ascend and be saved? If future fools see this and their sins multiply unchecked, where will the blameless seek refuge? I beseech the Heavenly Worthy not to deliver these people."

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "The Supreme Great Dao makes no distinction between friend and foe, ever extending impartial compassion and the power of a single vow to universally deliver all, without favor or bias. Know this, Ghost of Judgment: I first commanded one hundred thousand immortals of the middle realm to bear banners of faith and descend into the Nine Dark Realms, summoning forth the multitude of ghosts. Then I sent fifty thousand spirit messengers, clutching my left decree, to traverse the four directions and pursue the descendants of these ghosts. For these reasons, the law permits their deliverance, and the profound statutes of the Great Dao allow for their repentance. After repenting, if they transgress again, they may be seized, and my Dao will not save them."

Thereupon, the Ghost of Judgment, receiving the Heavenly Worthy’s decree, dared not speak further.

At that moment, those seeking profit and their assembly, gripped by fear, found their illnesses worsening. They implored the Heavenly Worthy for deliverance.

The Heavenly Worthy, perceiving their intent, addressed them: "You have all followed the ten evil deeds of your ancestors. The underworld has recorded your sins, identical to those of your forebears. How could you act like beasts, wantonly harming your kin, killing your own flesh and blood, secretly injuring the good, and feeling no shame? With such sinful bodies, you are unfit to bear the Dao. You must only refrain from committing the ten evil deeds, cultivate diligently day and night, and you may yet attain deliverance. The supreme secret Dao cannot yet be revealed to you."

Thereupon, each person inscribed the ten precepts, vowing to restrain body and mind and never transgress again.

Then, those seeking profit again addressed the Heavenly Worthy: "We do not know how to rescue the sinful souls of our ancestors and free them from suffering."

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "Return to your homes and establish pure abodes, upholding the Dao and its teachings. Morning and evening, perform rites of repentance, observe the precepts, practice generosity, and prepare incense and lamps, dedicating all your worldly possessions. Hold a grand nine-dark-realm fast for three days and three nights, offering incense and circumambulating the Dao, pouring out your sincerity and devotion three times in succession as a great act of atonement. Additionally, conduct the Zhongyuan Grand Offering to relieve the hungry ghosts. At that time, invite the assembly of the Dharma to recite this scripture, proclaiming it to the foolish, urging them to exhaust all inner and outer wisdom, so that merit may be perfected. By the power of this Dharma, your ancestors’ souls will be delivered to the Southern Palace and reborn in a land of the Dao. Without this, there is no means of deliverance."

Upon hearing this, each person bowed in gratitude and vowed to follow the teachings.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy addressed the spirit beings, saying: "Out of great compassion, I have delivered these ghosts from suffering. Moreover, I wish to devise a skillful means to leave these teachings for later generations, thus commanding the establishment of fasts to restrain their minds. Future beings who seek to rescue the deceased should follow this method to atone for past transgressions and resolve the retributions of their ancestors. Further, by performing rites of repentance, they may dissolve past offenses, continuously cultivate their minds, prevent negligence, sever the roots of evil, and increase virtuous karma. You must now understand the method of transformation and deliverance—it ought to be thus."

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy commanded the Lord of Life in the Southern Palace to receive the multitude of ghosts and swiftly grant them rebirth, allowing no delay. The ghosts then bowed in gratitude to the Heavenly Worthy and departed with sorrow and joy.

At that time, the spirit beings again addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "With humans and ghosts now delivered, boundless joy arises. Yet there remain those in the animal realm who seek salvation. Their offenses, too, originate from the ten evils, cycling through retribution. Once fallen into bestial form, they lose their original nature. Though lacking full wisdom, they possess the Dao-nature. They nurture their young with affection, feed and raise them, gather in groups by kind, and dwell in forests and thickets. Fearful and startled, they guard their lives, thinking only of water and grass, knowing nothing beyond—truly beyond comprehension. Pitying their lack of wisdom, their kind does not cease; they multiply endlessly, devouring one another. Unable to bear this, my heart finds no refuge."

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "Excellent, excellent! Spirit beings, you must now understand that the Great Dao constantly teaches and transforms all beings with earnest care, delivering the suffering souls of hell and the tormented spirits. To sever the path of animals, one must first purify its source, for then its flow will easily clear. Why is this? The animal realm arises from the human realm. Therefore, one must first transform the human realm. Once humans are transformed, myriad evils will not arise; with no evils arising, the animal realm will be severed. Have you not heard how I once expounded the essential Dharma to the Dragon Kings and Water Deities? This was precisely the reason. Yet now you have forgotten and recall nothing."

The spirit beings then reflected inwardly and at last awakened.

At that time, the Five Emperors and the Ghost Kings of Epidemic Diseases, hearing that the Heavenly Worthy had descended to deliver humans and ghosts, led their legions—five hundred million strong—to the assembly. They addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "By the fruit of our karma, we have become Ghost Kings, governing all beings in the realms of form and desire under heaven. The registers of life and death are entirely within our grasp. We bring sickness or vitality, never passing an idle moment. When people pray to us, we are sated with offerings, and the lives we sustain never lack for a moment."

In recent millennia, blessings and destinies have all but vanished, and humans have received the qi of the Dao—yet our teachings no longer prevail. For this reason, our fortunes have dwindled, and all our legions suffer from hunger and emptiness. This is entirely the doing of the Heavenly Worthy’s Dao qi. We only pray that the Heavenly Worthy will not remain in the world for long, for all things value self-preservation and do not harm one another. Yet today, the Heavenly Worthy has become a great harm to us."

Perceiving the intent of the ghosts, the Heavenly Worthy instantly transformed into a Great General of Ghost-Slaying, his body a hundred *zhang* tall, followed by countless legions of riders. On his left, he bore the Vajra-Shaking Divine Bell; on his right, he grasped the Jade Halberd, its radiance streaming like the Kunwu sword. In his hands, he wielded a divine sword and golden battle-axe, while thunder and lightning crashed around him. A dazzling brilliance flared, swirling and seething, as he descended before the Heavenly Worthy from the northwest upon a chariot of dark clouds. He prostrated before the Heavenly Worthy, offering boundless reverence. His vanguard and retinue resounded with ten thousand kinds of drums and horns.

At that moment, the transformed figure let forth a great thunderous voice, and all together they chanted the *Divine Chapter for Dispelling Demons*. The transformed figure then declared himself the Great General of Ghost-Slaying, attendant to the Heavenly Worthy. His eyes emitted streaming light like shooting stars.

When the Five Emperors and Ghost Kings, along with all their followers, beheld this awe-inspiring might, they trembled in fear, kneeling downwind and not daring to lift their gaze. The Great General rebuked the host of ghosts: "How dare you, demonic fiends and malevolent specters, act thus?" With a single roar, the Ghost Kings were thrown into disarray. After a long while, they rose, flustered and crawling on the ground.

The Great General then questioned the ghosts: "Beneath the Four Heavens, do the people suffer from unjust illnesses and untimely deaths—are these your doing?" They answered, "It is the gods who bring this about." The General asked again: "How many poisons can you ghosts inflict to afflict living beings with suffering? Answer me truthfully, and I shall spare you. If you conceal anything, I shall execute you."

Then the Azure Emperor Ghost King replied: "I govern the diseases of spring, causing people to suffer headaches, chills, fevers, and malignant sores." The Vermilion Emperor Ghost King answered: "I govern the diseases of summer, bringing scorching heat that torments people with agony and emaciation." The White Emperor Ghost King said: "I govern the diseases of autumn, causing people to suffer from cramps, vomiting, dysentery, wasting thirst, and vexation." The Black Emperor Ghost King replied: "I govern the diseases of winter, bringing damp and cold that penetrate people’s limbs and joints, causing swelling and pain." The Yellow Emperor Ghost King said: "I govern the diseases of the four seasons, causing people’s abdomens to harden and stab with pain."

When the ghosts had finished speaking, the transformed General commanded them to manifest these poisonous diseases. Then, brandishing the sound that dispels demons, he extinguished the ghosts’ qi. In that instant, the ghosts experienced a thousand deaths and ten thousand rebirths, their agony like being burned by fire, their cries of torment filling the air.

The Heavenly Worthy then commanded that the ghosts’ suffering be temporarily halted and addressed them: "You ghosts have accumulated evil, and today your sins are complete, hence you endure this suffering. The innocent among living beings suffer untimely deaths, and those who kill to prolong their own lives only compound their grave offenses, never to receive blessings or protection. All this stems from the greed, cruelty, and terror spread by malevolent spirits."

Thereupon, the transformed General glared fiercely once more, and the ghosts’ suffering redoubled, longing for death yet unable to die. Blood gushed from their pores, joints, ears, eyes, mouths, and noses. In such torment, their bodies and minds trembled, unable to flee, their limbs failing them as they writhed upon the ground. Like birds with clipped wings, they were utterly powerless.

The transformed figure then questioned the ghosts again: "Are the life records of all beings determined by you?" Terrified, the ghosts dared not lie and answered, "No." The General asked: "If not by you, then how can you cause living beings to suffer from illnesses?" They replied: "Ghosts cannot truly cause people to fall ill. Why? Because malevolent ghosts enter people only when they are already sick."

The General asked: "How do you enter those who are already sick?" They answered: "People living in the world fail to discern right from wrong. They indulge in anger, strife, gluttony, lust, and immoderate labor or leisure, exposing themselves to wind, cold, heat, and dampness, thus bringing illness upon themselves. Or, if not by their own doing, they may be unfilial to their parents, rebellious toward their teachers, disrespectful to heaven and earth, or fail to uphold the precepts—thus, heaven punishes them with illness. Malevolent spirits then exploit these circumstances, wielding their power to receive offerings and sustain their own lives. In truth, it is not the ghosts who kill the good and innocent. Those who turn their backs on the Dao and consort with evil, lacking moral discipline, are abandoned by protective spirits. But those who practice forbearance and diligence, cultivate great compassion, and harmonize body and mind with the Dao—such people cannot be harmed by ghosts."

When the spirit beings heard the ghosts’ words, they deemed them deceptive and evasive. They addressed the Heavenly Worthy: "We do not understand the principle behind the ghosts’ answers—what does it mean?" The Heavenly Worthy replied: "The ghosts’ answers are entirely reasonable. Witnessing the might of this transformed General, they marveled at what they had never seen before and now pay reverence to the Heavenly Worthy. You should know that the divine power of the Great Dao is unmatched, subduing all demons and crushing heterodox teachings. All dharmas return to the Great Dao. We petty ghosts, powerless to resist, have lost our original minds and no longer possess any might or virtue. We only pray that the Heavenly Worthy will spare our lives and allow us to serve as attendants forever, providing for the great assembly, guarding and protecting the disciples, never daring to be negligent."

After the ghosts made this vow, their pain ceased. The Heavenly Worthy, perceiving their intent, asked again: "For what reason did you ghosts suddenly suffer such torment and affliction? And by what cause has it now abated?" The ghosts replied: "The suffering we endured earlier arose from beholding the awe-inspiring might and radiance of the Great General of Ghost-Slaying. Suddenly stricken with illness, we sought death in vain, losing our original minds. We did not know why the pain was so unbearable. Now, our suffering has lessened because we could no longer endure it, trapped between life and death. In our desperation, we vowed in our hearts to be spared by the Heavenly Worthy, to serve as attendants forever, providing for the great assembly, guarding and protecting the disciples, never daring to be negligent."

Having made this vow, they gradually recovered. The Heavenly Worthy addressed them, saying: "You ghosts who afflict all people—your hearts know no shame or remorse. Now you have received this evil retribution, yet it was not wrought by the Great General of Ghost-Slaying. Though this general is named 'Ghost-Slayer,' he has ascended to the stage of true forbearance, entered the realm of compassion, and attained the six supernatural penetrations. His heart is as vast as the sea, and with wisdom and power, he slays only the thieves of affliction, never harming living beings with his body or hands. For this reason, he is called the Great General of Ghost-Slaying: he leads the armies of the Six Perfections, shatters the demonic foes, and guides sentient beings to the land of forbearance. Thus is he named Great General. You ghosts must not harbor perverse views, suspecting this general to be a true slayer. If you persist in such misguided thoughts, you will forever fall into the paths of evil, your wickedness growing ever greater, and your afflictions never abating."

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy spoke this verse:
*"The perverse and the upright are not two paths,
Pure and turbid share a single source.
The breath that issues from emptiness
Divides midway into awe and grace.
The Dao is foremost among all blessings,
While evil is the foe of birth and death.
When perversity prevails, the upright naturally arises;
Delusion at its extreme returns to the root.
It is so of itself—
The Great Dao has never spoken."*

When the Heavenly Worthy had finished reciting this verse, he again addressed the ghosts: "You ghosts must turn away in revulsion, reflect deeply, feel shame and remorse, reproach yourselves, and ponder: what karmic causes led you to fall into this ghostly realm, reeking of filth and stench, ever awaiting human misfortune, seeking prayers and sacrifices, taking lives without shame? You band together in gangs, delighting only in evil, envying virtue and morality, disrupting the good. You become omens of disaster, terrifying sentient beings. How can you perverse ghosts ever serve as true fields of merit for the people? You know not great compassion, only the destruction of life. You ghosts have long indulged in wickedness, filling yourselves with impurity and sin, destined for hell—burned by fire, boiled in cauldrons, sawed apart by wind-blades, enduring every torment to repay the beings you have wronged."

Then, perceiving that the ghosts’ hearts had not yet attained pure faith, the Heavenly Worthy commanded them to reflect deeply for a long while. With his sovereign spiritual power, he gathered the ghosts and led them into the Flaming Furnace Hell, then into the Cauldron of Boiling Oil Hell, past the Sawing Hell, the Mountain of Knives and Forest of Swords Hell, the Frozen Hell, and the Eternal Night Hell. He ordered the hell wardens to drive them with rods, allowing no respite. As the wardens raged, fire erupted from their seven orifices, scorching the throng of ghosts, who shrieked and fled in terror. All the gates of hell were sealed, leaving no escape.

Then the ghosts thought to themselves: *"May the Heavenly Worthy save our lives!"* In an instant, the Heavenly Worthy transformed into a virtuous man, accompanied by attendants, and opened the gates of hell, leading the ghosts out while commanding the wardens to release them. He guided the ghosts back to the assembly, where from afar they saw the Heavenly Worthy. Weeping bitterly, they recounted their suffering, confirming all that the Heavenly Worthy had foretold—they had endured the full weight of their karmic adversaries, unable to bear the torment. In their agony, they had yearned for the Great Dao, and some had seen a virtuous man open the gates of hell, leading them back to once more behold the Heavenly Worthy. Joy and fear mingled in their hearts, for they dreaded being cast again into the hellish sufferings, their bodies unable to endure. They begged the Heavenly Worthy to grant them deliverance, to free them from the ghostly realm and release them from the myriad torments of hell.

The Heavenly Worthy again addressed the ghosts: "The suffering you have endured arises from your past lives’ wanton destruction of life, your harm to the good and innocent, your creation of omens and terrors to frighten sentient beings. This is your retribution—none other has imposed it. You ghosts earlier declared your desire to serve the Great Dao as attendants. But your sins run deep, your yin-thieving nature remains unexpunged, your foul stench and filth would alarm the assembly. How could you dare, without cause, bring such a sinful body to offend the Great Sage?"

The evil ghosts replied: "We beg the Great Dao for the water of the Dharma, to bathe away the dust and grime, to refine body and mind. If not for this, how would we dare, without reason, bring this sinful form to trouble the Great Sage? We only pray that the Heavenly Worthy, in his boundless compassion, will overlook our filth and bestow the flow of the Dharma, washing away our foul stench, so we may receive the true qi. This would be the fortune of a thousand lifetimes, realized today."

When the ghosts had spoken thus, their wailing shook the earth. They beat their heads upon the ground until their eyes bled, fainting and reviving in turn.

Then the divine assembly, moved by the ghosts’ profound sorrow, wept from the north and spoke: "Disciples are fortunate to have been delivered, to enter the stream of the Dao, to serve the Heavenly Worthy. Through eons of deep karmic affinity, we have been moved without motion, bearing the weight of your grace, our hearts overwhelmed. Without presumption, we have troubled your divine thoughts, entreating your compassion to extend mercy, to turn your mind toward us, to offend your sacred heart by delivering these lowly ghosts—so earnest and burdensome is our plea. We reflect that these ghosts are as we once were: before knowing the Dao, we saw only external obstructions, our doubts inwardly piled high, wandering in darkness without cause for awakening. But upon glimpsing the sun of heaven, the long night brightened. Meeting the Compassionate Honored One, all doubts dissolved at once. Sheltered beneath the *qian* tree, we bathed in the dark stream, the dust of our burdens swept away, the nature of the Dao revealed. Like the sun melting accumulated snow, like a torch in the night dispelling deep gloom, the mist vanished, the layered ice dissolved. The rain of the Dharma poured forth, broadly nourishing the fields of the heart. The sprouts of the supreme Dao grew in season; the clouds of compassion spread wide, reviving the withered and rotted, transforming white bones into living beings—this we witness today. We only pray that the Heavenly Compassion will deliver these ghosts, for though in the past we were not two, we diverged midway. Now, reunited in thought, we return together beneath the One Dao. These ghosts, devoid of kind hearts, confined to dull senses and ignorant minds, are truly pitiable."

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "I shall display these rare and wondrous powers to entrust these ghosts to the Lord of the Southern Flourishing Palace, that they may be born into the world. By their earnest devotion, they shall serve as my attendants. I cannot bear to thwart the desires of these ghosts."

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy commanded the Left Immortal Youth to burn the incense of returning souls; He further commanded the Right Attendant Perfected to hold aloft the talisman of the Numinous Unity; and He commanded the Lord of the Spring Dao of the Azure Heaven to secretly infuse the qi of life, reviving the host of ghosts.

When the ghosts had thus been delivered, they rejoiced and gave thanks, encircling the Heavenly Worthy to bow and offer praise. They then made this vow: "Wherever the Heavenly Worthy may be, in any great assembly, should even a speck of dust arise, we shall lick it away—no sweeping shall be needed. If any newly ordained Daoist displays improper conduct, we shall correct it. Beneath the Four Heavens, all men and women who receive the Dao and its methods, we shall protect, ensuring their success. Should they require anything, we shall provide it, that they want for nothing."

Then the ghosts, their hearts and bodies transformed for the good, did not stray from their original vow. They cultivated merit to amend their faults, repaying the kindness of the Dao.

The Heavenly Worthy asked the ghosts: "Now that you have escaped all suffering, do you wish to be reborn in the world, or to enter the true rank of the Dao?"

The Ghost King of the Azure Emperor replied to the Heavenly Worthy: "Before we knew the Dao, we drifted through birth and death, emerging into the human realm only to die before a hundred years had passed. Buffeted by demonic influences, we wandered the Five Paths, reaping the consequences of our deeds without respite. Now, having encountered the Heavenly Worthy, we wish to cast off all suffering as one spits out what was eaten—never to taste it again. We, too, do not wish to be reborn in the body of an ordinary mortal. To be born among the common folk would be like eating what one has vomited—a rare and undesirable fate. To emerge into the world of mortals would be like treading upon boiling water or burning coals—how could one not be scorched? We are fortunate indeed to have beheld the Compassionate Worthy and escaped the blind path. We only pray that the Heavenly Worthy will take pity on us and permit us to serve as Your attendants."

The Heavenly Worthy declared: "The Great Dao is vast and unbounded; its Dharma knows no restrictions, save for the Ten Evils, and no goodness remains unmet."

Then the Heavenly Worthy, moved by compassion for the ghosts and knowing their hearts had turned toward the Way, bestowed upon them the ranks of the Five Departments and the Five Hundred Million Hosts, appointing them to the station of Good Spirits. They were charged with protecting the Daoist precincts, aiding new disciples, tending the pure censers, and perpetually supplying fragrant wood and ashes for the sacred fires.

When the numinous beings witnessed the deliverance of these ghosts, their hearts swelled with joy, and they offered this hymn of praise:

*"The divine wind stirs the dark stream,
suddenly raising waves of great compassion.
It washes away the filth of ignorance,
lightly bearing us beyond the river of desire.
How we grieved for you before your deliverance,
sighing deeply in our sorrow.
The clouds of compassion spread wide,
and the withered and rotted bloom anew.
Who could have foreseen that the children of the Nine Nether Realms
would return to our eternal immortal home?"*

Then the numinous beings sang again:

*"The world’s path is tangled, ceaselessly churning,
drowning in the currents of love and attachment.
Why not turn wholly to the effortless Dao,
and cease making enemies of birth and death?
Why refuse to dwell in stillness and emptiness,
and instead seek the bitter, the pungent, the dust-laden?
Why not gaze up at the heroic ones,
who ride the clouds, wielding their regalia, roaming free?"*

When the numinous beings had finished this song, they addressed the ghosts: "You are fortunate indeed to have witnessed the Great Dao opening the way to your deliverance. You must day and night diligently advance, aiding the Dao in its flourishing, protecting and cherishing the good, ever practicing compassion, and merging with the Dao. I and you shall forever serve as attendants to the Heavenly Worthy, never far apart, wherever we may be."

The Azure Emperor of Good Spirits replied to the numinous beings: "The Supreme Great Dao—I alone heard of it last. Though the sun and moon shine brightly, the blind cannot see. Now that we have received deliverance, grief and joy mingle within us. We never expected the awe-inspiring power of the Great Dao to be so incomparable, nurturing all goodness, ferrying all transformations, serving as the supreme field of merit for both the hidden and the manifest—beyond thought, beyond measure. Overcome with sorrow and joy, we bow in gratitude to the numinous beings and say: How fortunate is this meeting of goodness, occurring on this very day! We pray that Your compassion will often summon and instruct us, revealing the good path, that we may awaken and understand."

When the Heavenly Worthy saw the Good Spirits humbly thanking the numinous beings and knew their faith to be profound, He advanced these two immortals one stage in their attainment of the Dao.

Then the Cloud and Mist Spirits, the Four Heavenly Kings, and the Eighty Heavenly Spirits of the Four Directions of Kunlun, hearing from afar that the Heavenly Worthy had opened the Mystic Enclosure, led their retinues—one hundred and forty thousand strong—riding the winds to the assembly. Arriving at the gathering, they beheld the Heavenly Worthy’s thirty-two marks, eighty excellences, and eighteen divine powers. His feet pressed the earth, shaking the world; his body emanated water and fire; light streamed from his brow. Barefoot and unclothed, they prostrated themselves, touching their heads to the ground, kneeling in reverence from afar before the Cloud Gate.

The Heavenly Worthy, knowing these to be outsiders, commanded the Immortal Holding the Canopy to display his divine powers, seating himself in the void before the gate.

When the outsiders had finished their worship, doubt arose in their hearts. After a long while, gazing up and down, they recited this verse:

*"I dwell in the Lofty Cleft Mountain,
revered throughout the Three Realms.
Long have I heard of the Supreme Dao,
riding the mists to enter the Cloud Gate.
This is called the Heaven above Heavens—
who could have foreseen an Immortal without form?
The five senses differ not from the world,
the spirit’s knowledge has not yet transcended.
Though dwelling in the Cloud Palace above,
how can one be free from the bonds of birth and death?"*

Then the immortal, moved by the power of the Dao, responded to the demons’ verse. His body manifested all marks, his divine powers transformed myriadfold, and light radiated from every pore. The great earth trembled, and the demonic hosts could not stand firm. The demons bowed their heads in worship, gazing up at the immortal. Their five limbs trembled, their bodies drenched in sweat, shaken and awestruck, losing their composure. Their radiance vanished, and their forms became like heaps of ink.

Then the immortal addressed the demons again: "Why have you come?" Thrice he questioned the demonic hosts, yet none could lift their gaze to answer. After half a time, they at last found their voices, bowing their heads once more in reverence to the immortal: "We have heard that the supreme Great Dao abides eternally in the upper realms, its divine power unconstrained, its majesty and virtue unmatched. Neither eye nor ear may perceive it, nor footstep reach its domain. Morning and evening we yearn in reverence, yet cannot advance of our own accord. Thus we have come together today, daring to present our homage and entreat your mercy. We prostrate ourselves before you."

The immortal replied: "You who dwell below are revered by the world, styling yourselves with ten titles, seeking worldly gain and self-sufficiency in karmic retribution—why have you come here? This is the realm of the Dao, not a place for demons to ascend. Your sins run deep and heavy; you are unfit to behold the Dao. In the Desire Realm, you delude and confuse ordinary beings, calling yourselves *Tamer of Men*; some name themselves *Brahmā*, others *The Capable One*, seeking worldly offerings. Or you claim the title *Great Teacher of Gods and Men*, leading the good and virtuous astray, casting them into the river of birth and death. Those who receive your teachings do not trust in the Great Dao, bound as they are by countless fetters, their minds ensnared by false thoughts. You declare all dharmas of action to be impermanent, yet assert that your own bodies cannot be destroyed. Some preach annihilation as the supreme bliss of the Dharma, urging men to take their own lives, to sever and mutilate their bodies, that they may swiftly shed their mortal forms and attain adamantine bodies. Others speak of a distant Pure Land where rebirth is wondrous, where one sits upon a lotus throne, clothed and fed by nature, leaving this flesh behind to forever escape the cycle of birth and death.

You demons compare your defiled, ashen forms to the adamantine, wielding the Dharma of ignorance to falsely expound the six supernormal powers. You confuse and mislead the world, causing men to abandon filial piety and disrespect their parents. Such perverse teachings, when spread abroad, incite disciples and masters alike to licentious disorder. You perceive bodily marks yet claim to see nothing, prattling of unimpeded emptiness while failing to grasp the ultimate Dao. Adrift and unmoored, you forget your origin and lose the true path. Your minds are dimmed to the Middle Way, ever dwelling in excess. Bound to the cycle of rebirth, you cannot abide eternally, shackled by names and numbers—the thirty-two marks, the eighteen divine powers, the eighty excellences—all fetters of attachment, all conditioned by action, all fabricated by contrivance."

Their toes press the earth, trembling in fear; they make offerings to water and fire through perverse views and gluttonous cravings. They claim ten benefits, lusting after rank flesh, falsely proclaiming merit and virtue. You demonic beings are true outsiders, concealing your evil deeds to silence worldly criticism. You speak of ash and annihilation, trivializing karmic causes, feigning celestial immortals come to hear the Dharma—yet I, a true immortal, have never come to hear demonic teachings. You are true outsiders: shaving heads, plucking hair, baring bodies, going barefoot, committing the ten evils and five rebellions, slandering by nature, loathing the loyal and good, and denouncing the great Dao.

Moreover, when your perverse sects perform their rituals, masters and disciples—men and women—mingle in secluded chambers, hidden from view, concealing their flaws, dreading exposure. Your words and deeds are coarse and vile, your teachings hollow and groundless. For these reasons, you are unfit to perceive the Dao, for you disturb the customs of the world, delude the foolish, and fabricate false doctrines. You teach deviant meditations, conjuring bizarre visions, spreading confusion and deception to mislead the innocent. Your schemes are treacherous, gathering wicked factions, shaving the heads of the ignorant. You defile mortal forms, filling the desire realm with your corruption; you build empty tombs, burning and slaughtering mortal bodies. In throngs, you praise such acts, and thus descend into hell. Ignorance grows, hair shorn and plucked, yet the roots of evil remain uncut. With these perverse arts, you hope to escape entanglement—like carrying dry grass to extinguish a fire, or a fool fleeing illness to avoid disease. Like children running to escape their shadows, your filth and depravity overflow, choking the world. With such sinful bodies, you are unworthy to behold the Dao.

Then, the demonic hosts, hearing the immortal’s words, were struck to the heart. As one, they wept in sorrow, wailing and lamenting, repenting their errors. They beat their breasts, their bodies streaming blood, tearing out their hair as if burning foul grass. Tears streamed from their eyes, their limbs trembled, and baring their shoulders, they begged for mercy, prostrating at the immortal’s feet. Their anguish was beyond measure. The Heavenly Worthy of the Cloud Palace, moved by their repentance, emitted a radiant purple light from his divine eyes, illuminating the immortal from afar. The immortal, sensing the Heavenly Worthy’s compassion, addressed the outsiders: “Those who seek the Dao should not grieve. If you repent, simply change your hearts—do not mutilate your bodies or destroy your nature to seek atonement.”

Hearing these words, the demons ceased their lamentations. Then, among the demonic throng, an outsider who called himself Brahma-King, the foremost leader of the sect, knelt bare-chested, joined his palms, and spoke: “We do not know whether the Heavenly Worthy’s Dao saves the hidden and the manifest, whether its grace flows to the withered and decayed. All living beings long for deliverance—we humbly beg your mercy, that you transform our lowly selves, guide us to renewal, abandoning the perverse for the true. May we shelter beneath your soaring tree, bathe in the stream of your Dharma, step into the pure abyss, and dwell in the mysterious path. May we sweep your altar, attend your comings and goings, hold your canopy, drive your chariot, and serve you morning and night. We beseech the Heavenly Worthy to grant this in compassion.” With these words, he wept, his tears falling as he bowed his head.

The immortal replied: “I am not the Heavenly Worthy. My rank is but newly ascended to immortality, and I stand here to attend the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion.” Hearing this, the outsiders broke into a cold sweat, each thinking to themselves: “We dwell in the desire realm, having attained the four fruits of the path. Yet today, in this panic and dread, we lost ourselves—we know now that what we gained was not the true Dharma. The immortals of the upper realms possess unmatched divine power—how much greater must be the majesty and virtue of the Heavenly Worthy? We fear our defilements are too heavy, our impurities too thick, to be worthy of paying homage to the supreme Heavenly Worthy.” Hesitant and uncertain, they knew not how to proceed.

Then, sixty thousand outsiders at once removed the pearls and jeweled necklaces from their necks, piling them at the cloud gate, offering them from afar to the Heavenly Worthy. The immortal said: “The treasures of your lower realm are but gold, silver, lapis lazuli, giant clams, agate, coral, amber, and pearls. In the heavens above, there are ten thousand kinds of rare treasures—radiant mechanisms of the sun and moon, jeweled stars, golden essences in myriad transformations, lightning and flowing auroras. The Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion does not glance at such adornments; how could he desire your tainted necklaces in the Cloud Palace?”

The outsiders replied: “Beings of the desire realm value only these jeweled necklaces, for we do not recognize the wondrous treasures of the upper heavens. We offer them from the heart, to express our sincerity.” The immortal said: “The Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion treasures the jewel of the human heart, not these adornments.” The outsiders answered: “Our mortal bodies hold no jewel within.” The immortal said: “If your bodies lack jewels, why not offer your hearts?”

Then, the outsiders rose and sought a knife, intending to split open their hearts. The immortal, knowing their intent, gave them the blade. Brahma-King then opened his belly, revealing his five viscera. The other outsiders all wished to see their own hearts, but the immortal stopped them, saying: “To offer your heart is to remove your outsider views—your petty awakenings, petty knowledge, petty learning. Focus your minds on the great Dao—this is called offering the heart. It is not the offering of viscera, blood, flesh, bones, or marrow.”

Hearing this, the outsiders began to awaken. Then, the immortal, with a hand of great compassion, pressed Brahma-King’s intestines and viscera back into place, restoring them as before. The outsiders looked at one another, their qi harmonized and flowing smoothly. They all sighed in wonder: “Never have we seen the like!” Having heard the wondrous Dharma and witnessed divine power, they addressed the immortal: “Great Master of Heaven and Earth, you are truly the King of Physicians, curing chronic illnesses, resolving all doubts, restoring us completely without remnant. We wish to follow you and request the gift of life. Grant us the Dao of long life and deathlessness.”

The immortal replied: “What practices of the lower realm can prolong life for a kalpa or half a kalpa?”

The outsiders replied: “In the lower realm, beings who have not heard the true Dharma practice the Four Wishes. Though they may prolong life, it does not exceed eighty thousand great kalpas, after which they fall back and are reborn in the Desire Realm. I have already lived for over seventy thousand kalpas, yet I am constantly troubled by impermanence, birth, aging, sickness, and death. This method is limited—it does not transcend the Three Realms, nor does it surpass the Five Supernormal Powers, and it cannot escape birth and death.”

The immortal said: “The Dao of long life is not something ordinary beings can hear. You outsiders seek long life, but I fear your habitual tendencies run deep, your karmic roots are firmly bound, your years are advanced, your marrow and brain exhausted, your form and spirit sunk in turbidity, and your fluids stagnant and impure. Moreover, you have deceived and deluded the world, and your offenses are already recorded. The Three Offices pierce your deceit, and the Five Emperors expose your transgressions. For you to seek deliverance would be exceedingly difficult. Yet I follow the saving decree of the Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy’s golden mouth. Even if the Heavenly Worthy were to permit your deliverance, you should still retreat and fast for a thousand days to reflect on your faults before being saved.”

Hearing the immortal’s words, the outsiders gathered outside the Cloud Gate, bowing from afar to the Heavenly Worthy. They burned incense and made vows for seven days and nights, prostrating and bowing in repentance, seeking a response. At the height of their devotion, they suddenly sensed a divine fragrance penetrating their nostrils and flowing into their hearts. Their hearts rejoiced, afflictions dissolved, hunger and thirst vanished, and their ears and eyes grew sharper, surpassing their initial state. The outsiders snapped their fingers and looked at one another, remarking how their skin and complexion had become radiant and moist.

The immortal, knowing the Heavenly Worthy’s intent toward the outsiders, saw that they too had inwardly awakened. Overcome with joy, they dared not speak aloud but expressed their gratitude through reverence, their thoughts fixed from afar on the Great Compassionate True Emperor. For another seven days and nights, they knelt and bowed before the Cloud Gate.

The immortal said: “The Great Compassionate True Emperor always employs a single compassion to deliver all beings of different kinds, even those who cannot be instructed through words—this is the teaching of the Great Dao that proceeds without speech. It is like a loving mother who discerns her infant’s needs: hearing its cries, she knows whether it is hungry or thirsty, in pain or discomfort, and provides food, drink, or medicine as appropriate. Now you have obtained the power of the Dao.”

The outsiders replied: “It is just as you have perceived.”

The immortal asked: “What have you realized?”

They answered: “We sensed a fragrance penetrating our nostrils and flowing into our hearts, suddenly awakening us. Our hearts are at peace, many times more so than before. Our ears and eyes are sharp—it is the same.”

The immortal said: “You have obtained the power of the Dao and already renewed your nature and life. What cause is there for worry? Yet because your bodies have long been solitary in the dust, you are not yet fit to behold the Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy or to examine and wear the supreme essentials of the Dao. You and your followers should return for now to the Desire Realm, retreat in purification for three kalpas, refine body and mind, and only then come again to draw near the Heavenly Worthy.”

At that time, the outsiders replied to the immortal: “Our bodies are decrepit and aged; we fear our lives are not secure. Should we suddenly pass three kalpas in the lower realms, impermanence may swiftly overtake us, and we may lose the Dao in an instant. Our souls and consciousness would drift, following karma to receive retribution—when would we ever return to see the Heavenly Worthy? Great Master, you must know: in the Desire Realm, even the longest-lived heterodox immortals endure no more than eighty thousand great kalpas; those of middling lifespan, one or half a kalpa; and the shortest-lived differ not from ordinary mortals. This assembly cannot be assured of safety. Why then, Great Master, do you grant us only a minor method and merely prolong our years?”

The immortal answered: “The supreme Dao is greatly penetrating; there is no such thing as a minor method. Merely cultivating one practice, all may attain perfection.”

At that time, the outsiders persisted earnestly, each untying the precious pearl from their topknot to offer to the immortal. Knowing their wholehearted devotion, the immortal accepted their offerings and returned within the cloud gate. In but a moment, from within the cloud palace came the faint resonance of numinous tones, like the caress of metal and stone harmonizing with an ethereal zither—its melody flowing and turning, pure, elegant, and resplendent. Suddenly, seven-colored fragrant light lingered about the cloud gate, and within that radiance two immortal youths sat in empty stillness, facing east and west. Together they played cloud zithers and addressed the demons, saying:

“The true qi circulates, pervading the ten directions;
Thick darkness and vast night are illumined by dawn’s light.
The suffering in locked chambers awaits the hour of awakening;
Wandering souls, lost spirits, and divine fragrance draw near.
The hand of compassion wields the vajra sword;
The armor of gentle forbearance severs the blade of evil.
The mighty soldiers of the Six Perfections array their ranks,
All riding the dragon-drawn chariot of concentration and wisdom.
Loftily occupying the cloud gate, they dissolve the five sufferings,
Ever bearing the cinnabar banner to stabilize the eight directions.
Sweeping away the stench of marching corpses from the battlements,
Washing and anointing the withered bones, they make them fragrant and steadfast.”

When the two immortal youths had finished playing their zithers, they said to themselves: “The Desire Realm is thick with dust; its foul stench fills all, sweet dew does not moisten it, mists and veils obscure the heavenly court, and the stench of corpses assails one—ever more rank and surging.
