We marvel that the immortal can endure dwelling here so long.”

The immortal replied: “It is not that I am able to endure, but that I follow the luminous decree and have no choice.”

Then the immortal youths said to the outsiders: “The qi of humans in the realms of form and desire dries the heavens—why do you tarry? You should withdraw for purification. After three kalpas, when the fragrance of precepts has dispelled the turbid, when you have returned to rectitude and expelled evil, when you have consumed harmony and ingested the elixir, dissolving this demonic qi, your forms will become clear and bright, inwardly and outwardly fragrant and pure. Then you may ascend again. The Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy has already bestowed profound protection: fragrant light has suffused and dispelled your evil roots, extended your lifespan, and removed the threat of premature death.”

At that time, the demonic assembly rejoiced anew. The two immortal youths said: “When you return to the lower realms, abandon your heterodox views. Do not roar and clamor, proclaiming your ten titles to solicit offerings and thereby grow your evil roots. Do not claim to be teachers of others, gathering the young and ignorant to lead them into perversity. Do not burn and kill the foolish with poisonous fire, rejoicing in their praise. These are the great yin thieves, who harm through expedient means, who teach and praise death, who shave and sever the lives of ordinary people. This sin is most grave; the supreme Great Dao, compassionate and loving of life, ever abhors such acts.”

At that time, the outsiders assented and received the teachings. They took leave of the immortal youths and withdrew to the Desire Realm.

*Thus concludes Scroll Three of the Supreme Great Dao Jade Clarity Scripture.*
*Scroll Four of the Supreme Great Dao Jade Clarity Scripture.*

**Chapter Nine: The Upper Prime**

At that time, during the grand celebration of the Upper Prime, on the morning of the fourteenth day of the first month, the twin luminaries exchanged their radiance. The moon’s splendor withdrew, the stars’ essence gathered its brilliance, and the circular net of heaven unveiled the dawn. Beams of light and rosy clouds alternated in illumination; the great void grew serene and bright. Fragrant blossoms unfurled in succession; primordial qi arose, harmonious fluids entered the firmament. The earth exhaled a delicate mist; the heavens scattered floating haze. The seas stilled without waves; the dark source flowed with nectar. Flying canopies spread across the firmament; vermilion banners exhaled clouds. Divine pennants fluttered; blossoms swirled in the air. Celestial drums resounded endlessly; ethereal winds chanted without cease. The five essences led the way; twin luminaries flanked the imperial chariot.

At that time, the Supreme Heavenly Honored One of the Upper Prime, the Celestial August Thearch, along with his retinue, descended from his cloud-and-radiance throne in the Palace of the Sun. Aligning their divine steps, they rose in measured dignity and ascended the whirlwind wheel and the jade-carved chariot of concentrated essence. Fragrant clouds entwined the canopy; auspicious mists enveloped the four directions. The August One soared forth, adjusting the reins, guiding the golden radiance.

At the hour of the zenith, he gazed down upon the ten heavens, surveying the six directions, then proceeded to the Palace of Yang’s Vastness. At that time, the Heavenly Honored One and all the great sages together emitted a radiance of compassion from their hearts, illuminating the hidden and the manifest without omitting even the finest speck of dust. The light was not of a thousand hues, yet it knew no bounds. Heaven above and earth below shone clearly without obstruction. The Dharma Wheel turned ceaselessly; all beings gathered in assembly. He exhaled the Great Harmony to awaken sprouts, inhaled the soft and yielding to disperse rigidity. Armor split and coiled serpents scattered; all living beings hastened in joy. Jade-like greenery unfurled its blossoms; coral roots put forth luxuriant branches.

By the hour of noon on the fifteenth day, the immortals of the Three Heavens—numberless, beyond reckoning—assembled. Their minds transcended the five penetrations; their bodies dwelt in the deathless realm. They could command the six armies and subdue the ten great adversaries.

Amidst the outskirts, upon the ground of forbearance, a provisional city was established—its height and breadth beyond compare. Four great gates stood tall, their towers soaring into the clouds, all secured with the seven treasures. Moats deep and vast plunged into the abyss. Along the city’s edges were thirty-six thousand portals, latticed with pearl and silk, its foundations laid with azure stone. The pathways encircled it, level and expansive.

Within the city, palaces and halls rose in sublime splendor, their radiance illuminating the night, bright and unobscured. Rare treasures and silken fabrics filled the storehouses to overflowing. The immortals arrayed the celestial rites, the thunderous Dharma drums resounding. They grasped the Great Cinnabar Scepters, raised the Great Cinnabar Banners, wielded the Great Golden Axes, brandished the Great Divine Swords—sharp and keen as the horns of unicorns. Clad in great Dharma armor, soft as cloud robes, they repelled poisoned arrows, invulnerable to the five weapons. In their hands, they held hooked blades, their edges finely honed, leading the vanguard and guarding the rear, their might like the claws of phoenixes.

At dawn, they harnessed six dragons, drawing forth jeweled chariots to the outskirts, where they arrayed their majestic regalia. The drums thundered, the horns blared—before the command could even be given, the adversaries had already submitted. Armor was cast aside, garments discarded; their fierce spirits instantly withered. Gold melted, drums shattered, banners and scepters lay broken. Hair unbound, sashes loosened, hearts laid bare, they crawled forward on knees and elbows, prostrating themselves to seek alliance, their very lifeblood manifest.

The immortals each unfurled banners of command over the demonic spirits, guiding those who surrendered onto the path of the Great Mystery, into the source of the Pure Cavern, ascending the slopes of Eternal Radiance, mounting the altar of the Golden Phoenix. They burned incense that defied the wind, recited the left-hand tally, and feasted with the Dark Fluid.

Beholding the wondrous power of forbearance, the great adversaries knew its unmatched might. Their hearts transformed in an instant, and they vowed to become immortals, to serve as virtuous companions.

By the hour of the meal, the immortals and their retinues returned to the great city. There, they set aside their majestic regalia and gathered a hundred precious treasures and rare wonders from the divine realms, ascending to the Upper Clarity to offer them to the Heavenly Worthy: the Sun-and-Moon Treasure Pearls, the Star-Essence Treasure Pearls, the Solar-Mirror Treasure Pearls, the Lunar Treasure Pearls, the Radiant-Electric Treasure Pearls, the Black-Dragon Treasure Pearls, the Forbearance Treasure Pearls, the Great-Compassion Treasure Pearls, the Great-Loving-Kindness Treasure Pearls, the Six-Pāramitās Treasure Pearls, the Dust-Transcending Treasure Pearls, the Harmonious-Light Treasure Pearls, the Flawless Treasure Pearls, the Desire-Free Treasure Pearls, the True-Embracing Treasure Pearls, the Flourishing-Essence Treasure Pearls, the Unyielding Treasure Pearls, the Diligence Treasure Pearls, the Precept-Holding Treasure Pearls, the Heart-Ocean Treasure Pearls, the Wisdom Treasure Pearls, the Skillful-Means Treasure Pearls, the Cloud-Thunder Treasure Pearls, the Gentle-Breeze Treasure Pearls, the Sprouting Treasure Pearls, the Sweet-Dew Treasure Pearls, and the Wish-Fulfilling Treasure Pearls. These treasure pearls each shone with distinct radiance, yet all were equally luminous and perfect.

There were also three priceless virtuous treasures: the Great-Compassion Virtuous Treasure, the Frugality Virtuous Treasure, and the Humility Virtuous Treasure. Should any being hold these treasures, their desires would be fulfilled, no wish left unanswered. If any being suffered from illness and held these treasures, their ailments would vanish of their own accord. If any being harbored rebellious thoughts and held these treasures, they would naturally become gentle and compliant. Should a ruler’s land remain unenlightened, disasters and omens repeatedly appearing, neighboring states at war, weapons clashing, the five grains failing to ripen, floods and droughts unbalanced, ministers plotting in secret—if such a ruler held these treasures, the land would transform of its own accord, disasters would cease, neighboring states would befriend one another, weapons would lose their edge, the five grains would flourish in all four seasons, floods and droughts would find balance, ministers would remain loyal, and treacherous plots would vanish.

The immortals also offered four kinds of fragrant rice: the Abundant-Mountain Fragrant Rice, the Dragon-Mountain Fragrant Rice, the Floating-Mountain Fragrant Rice, and the Great-Harmony Fragrant Rice—its fragrance spreading far and wide, inexhaustible to those who partook. They further presented seven kinds of precious nectars: the Sun-Essence Precious Nectar, the Moon-Splendor Precious Nectar, the Star-Essence Precious Nectar, the Sweet-Dew Precious Nectar, the Golden-Fluid Precious Nectar, the Divine-Light Precious Nectar, and the Jade-Casket Precious Nectar, each contained in the precious vessels of the heavens. They also brought priceless treasure robes: the Spontaneous Jasper-Silk Treasure Robe, the Spontaneous Cloud-Brocade Treasure Robe, and the Spontaneous Flowing-Radiance Treasure Robe; as well as priceless incense: the Returning-Soul Incense, the Wind-Defying Incense, the Wind-Resisting Incense, and the Seven-Color Incense. They further offered the various celestial fruits: the Ten-Thousand-Year Divine Peach, the Hollow Divine Melon, the Frost Pear, the Jade Date, the Golden Blossom of the Infant—countless rare and wondrous delicacies, all brought to the assembly to offer to the Heavenly Worthy.

The great presentation of treasures filled the Mysterious Center, their fragrance suffusing the ten directions. The radiance of a hundred treasures illuminated the boundless expanse. The immortals encircled the Heavenly Worthy in hundreds of thousands of layers, striking celestial music and the melodies of Great Harmony, their variations infinite, their sounds harmonious and sublime, pure and resonant. Divine birds flapped their wings in dance, spirit beasts kept time in unison. Dragons chanted, phoenixes sang—all sounds converged in harmony. A gentle breeze stirred the crimson trees, and the incense wafted beneath the canopies. The sun and moon paused in their courses, the stars shone brightly, fragrant smoke curled and drifted, sweet dew poured like rain.

After a long while, the immortals stilled the clamor of the assembly, quieted the lofty rhythms yet unmet. They furled their soaring canopies, resting beside the soaring chariots, withdrawing their swift wheels to stand empty in the cloud courts. As one, they bowed their heads, inquiring of the Heavenly Worthy, saying: “We know not whether the Dharma-body of the Heavenly Worthy, in its boundless virtue, has wearied itself with earnest cultivation. The multitudes, lacking merit, weigh heavily upon your sacred mind. Yet the dust and filth obscure them, their roots and karma sunk in turbidity. We gaze in awe upon your mysterious blessings, our hearts ever open day and night. Our reverent sincerity ever before our eyes, we empty our forms to follow the Dao—yet we have no means to repay your grace.”

Once more, mindful of the gift of life and unable to forget its root, the dust-bound multitudes, following one another, have nurtured this humble resolve. Yet the Three Heavens are vast beyond measure—how dare we offer but specks of dust and dewdrops? Yet we rely upon the Great Celebration of the Upper Prime, the lofty assembly of the Merciful Honored One. The boundless grace of Heaven makes no distinction between dust and stench; we pray you accept the cinnabar hearts we offer.

With these words, they bowed their heads and prostrated themselves, awaiting the compassionate decree.

At that moment, the Heavenly Worthy gathered his thoughts and gazed into the distance, his divine radiance vast and serene. His golden countenance shone with brilliance, his true light illuminating all four directions. The myriad heavens dwelled within his eyes, his divine power fully arrayed. The dust-bound realms were not far—suddenly, the doubts in the hearts of the immortals dissolved like melting ice.

Then the Heavenly Worthy commanded the Golden Youth of the Right to burn a hundred blended incenses, their fragrant smoke curling in the wind. He commanded the Left Perfected Ministers, one thousand two hundred in number, to strike in unison the cloud-harmonizing chimes. He commanded the Left Attendants, the True Governors of the Upper Prime of Spring, one thousand two hundred in number, to strike together the divine golden celestial treasures of the Heavenly Bell. He commanded the Great Immortals of the Eastern Pole, nine thousand in number, to sound the ten-thousand-stone purple jade chimes. He commanded the Great Immortals of the Western Pole, six thousand in number, to strike in unison the divine mountain celestial treasures of square gold. He commanded the harmonizing winds to blow forth the ever-changing sounds of the empty and profound.

As the myriad instruments played in harmony, for a long while, nine-colored cloud-dragons coiled and soared in dance, eightfold auroras swirled in the sky, fragrant winds turned through the gardens, and soaring simurghs and phoenixes circled above. Divine birds and immortal beasts chanted in the empty courts, neither too slow nor too swift—like flying clouds wheeling through the heavens, like returning waves drawing the current. Amidst the symphony of sounds, the subtle words of the empty and profound were intoned, and the Heavenly Worthy addressed the immortals, saying:

The primal qi of the Upper Prime is all-natural,
Governing life as the August Ultimate for all conditions.
The purple chambers stir the misty vapors,
The Great Harmony flows forth, dissolving hardness and rigidity.
The Dao’s creation and sustenance follow thus—
Therefore I have moved my abode to govern this heaven.
Wind and thunder dissolve all knots and tangles,
The six qi can rouse those who slumber through the long night.
This too is the wondrous workings of divine power,
Not that I by force compel it to be so.
The myriad treasures arrayed form the realm of profound principle,
Which is itself the empty heart’s field of supreme blessing.

At that time, the immortals heard the subtle sounds from the void, naturally wondrous and clear, penetrating and empty. The flow of Dao and virtue was all-pervading, every principle present without omission. Joy filled their hearts, divine light shone forth from their forms, and all living beings burst into radiant bloom. Those rising and sinking, flying and running, leapt and danced in exultation. Precious trees and fragrant herbs blossomed in season, while all manner of roots and branches sprouted buds and unfurled leaves.

The immortals attained the six spiritual penetrations, and nine generations of their ancestors received blessings, freed from sorrow and suffering. Such is the power of the Upper Prime—its virtue is thus.

For three days and three nights, the celestial affairs were brought to completion.

Then, having received the offerings, the Heavenly Worthy turned to bestow upon the Heavenly Perfected without omission. Through the gift of the formless, like the divine power of the Dao, the karmic retribution is boundless. The fragrant rice and precious nectar remained undiminished; the sun and moon’s jeweled pearls grew ever brighter; the incense of the time, its fragrance unceasing.

Among the great assembly of immortals, there was an Upper Immortal named Changqi, who intoned a *bu xu*:

We harness and ascend the August Ultimate,
Riding the turning wheel into the Central Heaven.
Parting the void, we offer the treasure of the heart,
The wondrous awakening illumines the field of the body.
From the Palace of the Sun, harmonious qi scatters,
In the vast courts, the smoke of vows ascends.
The Great Dao is beyond thought and discourse,
Its boundless blessings bestow wisdom without end.
The empty form roams the realm of the Dao,
The dark heart enters the Great Nothingness.
Unfolding the profound, we seek the edge of the treasure,
The hidden accord naturally aligns.
Thus we clarify what lies beyond the illusory,
Exhaling the burdens that shackle the foolish masses.
Who knows the Dao of undying?
Its distant cause lies in the *Kongdong* texts.
The mysterious wind stirs the Great Nothingness,
Heavenly music intones the subtle sounds.
Dragon scripts reveal phoenix splendor,
Jade characters pluck the empty zither.
Swift wheels ascend the cloud paths,
Loosened hair scatters jeweled pins.
We bow our heads to the August Ultimate,
Burning incense to lay bare our hearts.

When the immortal had finished reciting the *bu xu*, he bowed once more and inquired of the Heavenly Worthy, saying: “At this lofty assembly of the Upper Prime, we have been blessed to behold your presence, bathed in your grace and transformation. With empty hearts, we bear the weight of your favor, our blessings extending to the hidden and the manifest, the living and the dead alike. We forget our transgressions and faults, and pray for your forgiveness. We wish to follow the Heavenly Worthy and make a single request: that for all beings beneath the Four Heavens, you deliver them from suffering and distress, freeing them from all calamities and hardships. We beseech the Heavenly Worthy to descend into the divine terraces of the Divine Continent, to broadly deliver the people of the world and all non-human beings.”

Thereupon, the August Ultimate Heavenly Worthy addressed the immortals, saying: “You should know that the lofty assemblies of the Three Primes occur on auspicious days of good omen, rooted in the primal qi. The primal qi transforms into the One Qi, and the One Qi transforms into the Qi of Equilibrium. These Three Qi correspond above to the Three Prime Heavenly Treasure Palaces—the Palaces of the Sun, the Moon, and the Stars. Each palace has its Honored One: I dwell in the Palace of the Sun, named the August Ultimate Heavenly Worthy, governing the Upper Prime on the fifteenth day of the first lunar month, the time of spring yang, when the myriad things come to life. The Perfected One of the Palace of the Moon is named the Orthodox Unity Heavenly Worthy, governing the Middle Prime on the fifteenth day of the seventh lunar month, when the myriad things reach maturity. The Perfected One of the Palace of the Stars is named the Multitudinous Wonders Heavenly Worthy, governing the Lower Prime on the fifteenth day of the tenth lunar month, when the myriad things are stored and nurtured. You need only focus your hearts upon the Divine Continent and the realms beneath the Four Heavens, teaching and transforming beings, leading them far from heterodox paths, and proclaiming the names of the Three Honored True Emperors, morning and evening, with devoted aspiration. On these days, the Three Honored Ones will descend together, visiting the grotto-heavens, manifesting in myriad forms to deliver the beings of heaven and earth.”

At that time, the assembled immortals reverently received the luminous decree. On the seventeenth day of the first lunar month, at dusk, they took leave of the Heavenly Worthy and returned to the lower realms. Passing through the midst of the Northern Dipper, they awaited the Perfected Ones by night and paid homage to the Divine Youths by day. After lingering for seven days, they descended to the Divine Continent, gathering upon the summit of Mount Shou. After three days and three nights of deliberation on the propagation of the teachings, they traveled east to the sunny side of Fusang, south to the sunny side of the Fire Pool of Yanzhou, west to the flowing gold beyond Mount Yanzi, and north beyond the Yin Valley’s accumulated snows. Then they proceeded to the mounds of *Qilong*, the Green Hills, Mount Kongtong, and Mount Juci, in turn announcing the news to those who had newly attained the Dao, just as the Heavenly Worthy of the Upper Prime August Ultimate had spoken from his golden mouth.

On the fourteenth day of the seventh month, the Grand Assembly in the Clouds saw the August Ultimate Heavenly Worthy of the Correct Dao descend to the Divine Continent. Each immortal was commanded to prepare in unison, singing hymns and chanting the names of the Perfected Emperors, so that the Four Heavens below might hear. On this day, all were to prepare celestial offerings, presenting every treasure of the world—arranging seats, banners, flowers, incense, and candles—while their hearts continuously held the thought.

On this day, beneath the Four Heavens, all minds harmonized as one. At dawn on the fourteenth, the immortals of the world, along with all kings and people, gazed upward, parched with anticipation. Then, the August Ultimate Heavenly Worthy, accompanied by a host of six thousand myriad perfected beings and great sages, each riding the palaces of the moon, descended among them. All witnessed their arrival, like clouds hanging low, alighting upon the earth to secure for humanity the supreme field of blessings.

The Heavenly Worthy, attended by two companions, descended to the Cinnabar Terrace, while the remaining perfected hosts dispersed to where they were summoned. The immortals of the Cinnabar Terrace stood in attendance around the Heavenly Worthy. At midday on the fifteenth, the immortals of Green Hills—eighty-one myriad in number—all rode chariots drawn by azure dragons, bearing offerings, and arrived at the assembly. The immortals of *Qilong*—sixty-four myriad in number—all rode chariots drawn by vermilion phoenixes, bearing offerings, and arrived at the assembly. The immortals of Mount Kongtong—thirty-six myriad in number—all rode chariots drawn by white tigers, bearing offerings, and arrived at the assembly. The immortals of Mount Juci—twenty-five myriad in number—all rode chariots drawn by dark warriors, bearing offerings, and arrived at the assembly. The celestial immortals of Mount Kongtong—twenty-five hundred myriad in number—all rode chariots drawn by yellow dragons, bearing offerings, and arrived at the assembly.

In an instant, from the distant lands of the Nine Yi in the east, the Eight Barbarians in the south, the Six Rong in the west, and the Five Di in the north, immortals bearing offerings arrived by the power of the Dao, floating through the air. Each presented their offerings to the Heavenly Worthy. Once the arrangements were complete, they circled the Heavenly Worthy, pacing the void while singing praises, burning incense, scattering flowers, and performing celestial music. The harmonious sounds filled the air, divine winds lingered, and fragrant light wove through the void. Taking their places in order, they bowed and rose in measured rhythm, aligning left and right, then knelt facing north, their words hushed and breaths still. They inquired after the Heavenly Worthy’s well-being and spoke thus:

“Though the multitudes teem in chaos, evil abounds while goodness is scarce. Unworthy as we are, we have moved your august presence to descend. We, these dust-born and defiled, dare to cherish the true Dao and presumptuously await deliverance. Our merits cannot outweigh our transgressions, nor can we rouse ourselves to effort. We fear that our nine generations of ancestors bear the burden of past faults, cast into dark prisons, or reborn in distant lands, assuming strange forms. Yet by this slender thread of fate, we have encountered the Great Sage. Though unmoved, you have responded, and this noble assembly marks a propitious hour. We, humble and fleeting beings, dare to seek abundant blessings. We only pray that the Heavenly Worthy will instruct us in what we have not heard, open your golden mouth, and expound the *Precious Scripture of the Middle Prime* to deliver future generations.”

Then the Heavenly Worthy lifted his gaze and looked deeply for a long while before speaking:

“The moon’s essence gathers, its net cradling radiance. The lowlands dispel heat, and the golden winds display their might. Fire and wood nurture in concealment, as the qi of warmth and coolness intermingle. The imperial blossoms drip nectar, reining in the vapors of chaos. This auspicious hour unfolds forgiveness, and the myriad emperors come to pay homage. The six dusts grow still without, and the three poisons dissolve within. Both this life and the next find peace, and boundless blessings are summoned. Before there was anywhere to go, the uncarved block scattered into primordial qi. After forms and names arose, demons and evils bore grudges. The myriad things forgot their roots, advancing and retreating against their origins. The propitious hour passes unheeded, and none reflect on the grace of the Dao. Oh, the countless multitudes—how their pain defies words.”

When the Heavenly Worthy had spoken these words, he bowed his head and flicked his fingers several times. The earth trembled, rivers and seas surged, the spirit-qi grew unsettled, and mournful winds lost their harmony. The assembled immortals rose to bow in gratitude and spoke thus:

“We do not understand why the Heavenly Worthy bowed and flicked his fingers, causing the earth to tremble, the sun and moon to dim, the spirit-qi to grow unsettled, and the mournful winds to lose their harmony. Our Dao is shallow, and we fail to grasp the profound principle. Our hearts are filled with doubt and fear, and we cannot find peace. We only pray that the Heavenly Worthy, in great compassion, will take pity on our ignorance and deign to explain what we have not heard.”

The Heavenly Worthy replied:

“Before I had a name, the great Dao flourished, and teachings had not yet been imparted. The world was transformed by virtue. But I see that in later ages, people grew cunning, each pursuing strange doctrines, prizing knowledge and appearances. Benevolence and righteousness arose in turn, while wealth and food became the bonds of kinship. The poor, the lowly, and the weak were abandoned. Fathers and sons grew estranged, rulers and ministers disloyal. The six relations fell into strife, neighboring states became enemies, and the four seas turned to war. For these reasons, evil multiplied, and the wheel of retribution turned without end. Even now, though the people are still good, and the first holy hosts have descended to the Four Heavens below, all beings seek wisdom to escape the path of folly. Yet gradually, deceit and competition will surge, and though the hells may now lie empty, they will soon be full again. It is for this reason that I flicked my fingers.”

When the immortals heard this, they could not help but grieve. Then the immortal of Mount Kongtong rose from his seat, bowed deeply, and asked the Heavenly Worthy:

“May we inquire whether the hearts of the deluded masses can be turned back? We pray that the Heavenly Worthy, through your boundless divine power, will suppress the roots of the myriad ills, restraining them before they sprout, so that all beings may return to their roots. Let the countless multitudes preserve their original nature, abide in the One Dao, and extinguish the distinctions among beings. Let their hearts know no arising or ceasing, and their forms merge with the Great Void.”

The Heavenly Worthy replied:

“Excellent, excellent, good man! What you have spoken is the twentieth child of the great Dao. Why is this so? The great Dao originates in the uncarved void. The void scatters into primordial qi, and the primordial qi naturally gives rise to forms and life. From life, names are established, and from names, words arise.”

From words arise the true teachings; from the true teachings, wisdom arises; from wisdom, craft and deceit arise. From craft and deceit, the distinctions between foolishness and wisdom arise; from these distinctions, right and wrong arise; from right and wrong, love and hatred arise; from love and hatred, conflict and war arise; from conflict and war, rulers and ministers are established; with rulers and ministers established, rewards and punishments sprout; from rewards and punishments, profit and harm appear; from profit and harm, hidden malice arises; from hidden malice, the tally of sins is bound; with the tally of sins bound, the Dark Bureau is established; with the Dark Bureau established, there come the punishments of water and fire. This cycle turns endlessly, unfolding thus of itself—not by the Dao’s design.

What you have spoken lies beneath the ten thousand mechanisms. Therefore it is said: My Dao, though luminous, when turned from, becomes dark; my Dao, though upright, when reversed, becomes perverse; my Dao, though yielding, when abandoned, becomes rigid; my Dao, though everlasting, when slighted, perishes. The great Dao shows no partiality; it befriends only the good.

I observe the transformations of the masses—they cannot be swiftly corrected. Yet among ten thousand, one may arise who responds to harmonious qi, returning to the root and restoring the origin. For this reason, the great Dao descends to establish the true teachings, illuminating the eyes of the multitude, that they may follow its shadow. And you, later disciples, are precisely such people.

At that time, the Immortal of Kongtong rose from his seat, bowed, and asked the Heavenly Worthy: “We do not yet understand the meaning of the punishments of water and fire. We humble ones fail to comprehend—we pray you distinguish them for us.”

The Heavenly Worthy replied: “The punishments of water and fire comprise four kinds, two transgressions of yin and yang, for which the Dark Bureau metes out retribution. Passing through water and fire—this is what is called the punishment of ice and embers. When filth accumulates equally, scorching and sinking calamities arrive; when heaven is obstructed and earth is negated, water and fire intermingle. When the yang of heaven reaches its extreme, the eight seas billow smoke, mountains and peaks turn to ash, the gates of heaven seal shut, gold and jade melt away, the three luminaries conceal their essence, wind and thunder fan the flames, fire veils spread their blaze, and heaven and earth become a furnace.

When earth is negated, yin completes its omen: the land shifts to become a vast sea, waves surge in the midst of heaven, and the assembled immortals relocate their abodes. The Water Mother of the northwest appears like a white banner. Flocks of birds fly south, gathering at the edge of the sky. Whirlwinds stir the waves, collapsing mountains and peaks. Metal and stone grind against one another, wearing away into mud and silt.

Good man, you must now understand: these two great disasters correspond to the world below and to the myriad people. Why is this so? When the world lacks the Dao, the myriad people fail to transform. These disasters are like the five viscera of beings turning against one another, their storage and discharge unregulated, naturally forming afflictions. How much more so when the world loses the Dao and virtue decays, and the dust of the multitude accumulates equally? Heaven and earth pity them and cannot desist. First they show the teaching as suffering, then they warn through qi, and finally they display the portent. Yet foolish people do not believe in the true teachings, do not understand the signs of qi, and do not reform their evil ways. Heaven has no choice but to display its great might.

It is like a minister or child whom the lord or father cherishes and thinks of with affection. Receiving favor, they grow arrogant and willful, their hearts change, and they lose loyalty, becoming unfilial to their lord or father, secretly harboring rebellion. When their schemes are exposed, even a benevolent lord or compassionate father does not immediately destroy them but first issues commands as a warning. If the minister or child still does not repent, they are then handed over to the executioners, though the lord or father still pities them—yet they can do no other. The Heavenly Emperor is the same.

When the assembled immortals heard the Heavenly Worthy’s words, they all sighed, saying, “Never has there been such a thing!” They bowed in gratitude to the Heavenly Worthy: “We have wearied your golden lips, who took pity on us humble ones and revealed what we had never heard. We bear the burden of this grace, this flowing and abundant blessing.” After their bows of gratitude were complete, the Heavenly Worthy gave instructions for them to return to their seats.

On the morning of the seventeenth day, the Orthodox Heavenly Worthy first arrived. When the true assembly had fulfilled its karmic conditions, they returned from the four heavens to the Cinnabar Terrace, inquiring of the Heavenly Worthy: “In your arising, dwelling, and transforming of the Dao, have you not wearied?” The Heavenly Worthy replied: “The transformation of the true is without toil; the transformation of the Dao is without limit. Have you, who attend to the myriad masses, grown weary or discontented?” The assembled immortals answered: “By the power and spirit of the Dao, how could we grow weary or discontented?”

The Heavenly Worthy then asked: “Have the two conditions of birth and death attained liberation?” The assembled immortals answered: “When the Heavenly Worthy descended to the Cinnabar Terrace, the sinful souls of hell were immediately liberated. Yet all the people beneath the four heavens, though liberated, have not attained release.”

At that time, the assembled immortals of the Cinnabar Terrace, hearing the words of the highest immortals, did not understand. Then the Immortal of the Prosperous Epoch rose from his seat, bowed to the Heavenly Worthy, and asked: “How is it that the sinful souls of hell, though they have not seen the Heavenly Worthy, attain liberation? How is it that all the people beneath the four heavens, though liberated, have not attained release? We pray you distinguish this for us.”

The Heavenly Worthy replied: “Good man, listen carefully, and I will explain it to you. The great Dao conceals its function: though it saves and delivers the myriad things, it does not claim credit. Its hidden virtue carries all—through this karmic condition, it enables sinful souls to attain liberation. Yet though they are liberated, they have not attained release—this refers to the people of the world, who, though they understand that the nature of afflictions is empty, cannot escape them. Why is this so? Ordinary people, though they understand the Dharma-nature, do not cultivate the true and constant. They merely comprehend the ultimate principle, their bodies remaining in accord with the Dao. Thus the Dao and principle diverge.

It is like a person sitting in a narrow room while their mind roams the ten directions without obstruction; or expounding the ultimate principle with unobstructed eloquence, separating and uniting at will—this is called the mind entering principle, not the body entering the Dao. For this reason, though principle accords with the Dao, it cannot enable the body to enter principle. It is like wandering in a dream: the body does not follow the mind. Thus beings’ minds may enter principle, but their bodies do not enter the Dao. The mind entering principle is called ‘understanding’; the body not entering the Dao is called ‘lacking understanding.’

The boundless great Dao is unimpeded in body and mind. It can cause the worlds of a mote of dust to respond to karmic conditions all at once—thus it is said that the great Dao is naturally liberated, able to make the worlds of the ten directions appear as if viewed in the palm of the hand. The same is true of the distant past.”

At that moment, the Heavenly Worthy, having spoken these words, extended the five fingers of his left hand, and ten kinds of radiance illuminated the empty void, causing the worlds of the ten directions to behold the light together. At that time, all the perfected, immortals, and numinous beings in the great assembly clearly perceived the worlds within a mote of dust. Within the light, they also saw the two bounds of time and the karmic deeds their bodies had undergone, all distinctly and vividly.

These immortals, gazing deeply into the subtle and profound, exhaustively witnessed the true and constant Dao. They all attained the sixfold spiritual penetrations and the power of spontaneous freedom. Nine generations of their ancestors received blessings, and they were reborn into the realm of the Dao. The Heavenly Worthy’s Middle Prime affinity having reached its fulfillment, at dawn on the seventh day, the Heavenly Worthy and the great assembly together ascended the cloud chariot. Mystic winds stirred the music, purple auroras soared through the void, empty valleys echoed with hymns, and celestial chants resounded in myriad tones.

Then the assembled immortals intoned the *Step Through the Void*, saying:

Auspicious light ascends in purple haze,
The cloud chariot glides through cinnabar skies.
Fragrant winds swirl and turn,
Canopies sway, floating mists arise.
Within the Dao, the Dao returns once more,
Within the Mysterious, the Mysterious deepens anew.
True radiance knows no bounds,
The great image ultimately has no form.
The Dharma-wheel turns of itself,
The subtle sound cannot be heard.
In emptiness, we attend the Three Treasures,
In stillness, we hear the *Cavern Scripture*.
Seven transformations—wandering souls return,
Myriad qi arrest the decline of years.
Fragrant winds waft the feathered canopy,
Ethereal breaths revolve the whirlwind car.
Cool and clear, we ascend the cloud path,
Subtle and distant, we enter the boundless void.
Pitying the dust-bound children,
We respond to the mandate and expound the sacred writ.
The wondrous fruit harmonizes with this day,
Darkly it accords with the natural tally.

Then the immortals, escorting the Heavenly Worthy on high, sang praises and hymns of admiration. They entered the cloud court and passed through forty celestial gates. At that time, the Heavenly Worthy halted the immortals, saying: “The celestial path is long and distant—there is no need for such a far send-off.”

The immortals hesitated, looking up and down, for a long while. The Heavenly Worthy, moved by their devotion, addressed them again: “You, in your future cultivation, though you attain the six penetrations and endure for thousands of millions of kalpas, will still possess human bodies. Compared to the natural essence of my great assembly, your luminous qi and subtle marvels cannot yet be fully the same.”

The Heavenly Worthy then commanded the perfected of the upper qi to harmonize the mystic winds. He exhaled the supreme, infinitely transforming numinous verses—thirty-nine chapters of cloud-harmonized, pure, and elegant *Great Mystery* hymns. At that time, the essence of the sun rose aloft, the fluid of the moon flowed downward, true qi followed its natural generation, the metal winds reversed to harmony, jade forests yielded their medicine, and jasper trees bloomed. The Dharma-wheel turned thrice, streaming auroras rippled in seven waves, celestial hymns echoed beyond the heavens, and empty voids resounded with songs. He enabled the immortals to discern the superiority and inferiority of the Dao.

He further addressed the immortals: “The rarity of the supreme Dao is most subtle; its divine power is most wondrous, beyond all description. I have briefly shown you these marvels to distinguish them for you.”

The immortals rejoiced, bowing in gratitude to the Heavenly Worthy: “We only pray that the Great Sage may often manifest his presence and influence.”

Having spoken, they took their leave and returned to the lower realms.

**Chapter Eleven: The Lower Prime**

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy of Myriad Wonders, on the morning of the fourteenth day of the tenth month, descended into the world in response to the mandate, accompanied by a host of fifty thousand myriad billions of perfected immortals from the stellar palace within the Cinnabar Heaven. His majesty and virtue transformed all beings. First, he drew the sun into his left eye and the moon into his right; the Dipper of the Left ascended his left ear, and the Dipper of the Right ascended his right ear. The Southern Dipper capped the apex of heaven, the Northern Dipper lay beneath his jade hairpin, and the Central Dipper rested between his divine feet. Azure auroras coiled around his left temple, white auroras around his right, cinnabar auroras illumined the three principles at his center, and dark clouds floated above his jade pillow. The Azure Dragon chanted on the left, the White Tiger roared on the right, the Golden Phoenix sang before him, and the Dark Warrior kept the rhythm. The five planets exhaled their qi in revolving circuits, yin radiance paused in the void to cast its light, auspicious auroras draped the celestial curtains, and immortal clouds arose like canopies. They chanted the numinous scriptures, and empty voids resounded with myriad tones.

Earth brought forth jeweled trees, hidden grasses sprouted tender shoots, orchids and irises pulsed with vitality, accumulated snow and ice melted, cold valleys warmed with harmonious qi, and deep springs emitted warmth. Divine mists blew in reverse, summoning souls and calling back spirits. Clouds and thunder wielded their sounds. Mighty numinous pheasant spirits chanted the sacred hymns, and empty voids echoed with celestial songs. The deaf and blind regained their hearing and sight, the crippled walked again, rivers and seas stilled their waves, and murky mists dispersed. True light floated in radiance, the vast heavens grew bright and clear, the five celestial bodies aligned in harmony, and the three luminaries shone together. Beings of different kinds lived in harmony, the hundred grains flourished, enemies released their sieges, and the world attained great peace. The true Dao prevailed, and demonic forces vanished.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy, riding the stellar palace, arrayed the cloud court. He announced auspicious tidings to all beings and responded to the numinous portents of the assembled immortals. He sounded the bellows of the floating void and gazed down upon the Great Nonbeing. The Lower Prime brought forth auspicious blessings, and boundless felicity was stored for all. Advancing the Dao and cultivating virtue, principle accorded with the divine tally. Purple treasuries intertwined, and the six palaces bloomed like flowers. Divine power transformed the lower realms, and true qi flowed through the great void. He governed the turning of the kalpas and wandered freely within the Mysterious.

Thus, myriad transformations were inexhaustible. In an instant, he caused winter forests to burst into bloom and withered trees to flower. He restored all living beings to their true nature and gathered all kinds to conceal their origins. The Dao withdrew into profound stillness, and he dwelled in lofty solitude. Such was his divine power, proclaimed from the golden mouth.

At that time, the immortal of the Cinnabar Terrace, having long received the decree from the golden mouth of the Heavenly Worthy of the Upper Prime and Supreme Pole, beheld these auspicious signs and knew that the Heavenly Worthy was descending to the divine continent. He emerged from the Cinnabar Terrace and saw from afar the radiant brilliance within the Mysterious, the exalted wonder of the stellar palace, banners and canopies filling the heavens, and the true numinous forms arrayed throughout the empty void.

All the immortals bowed their heads and entreated the Heavenly Worthy to descend upon the Cinnabar Terrace. In an instant, the Heavenly Worthy commanded one of the perfected of the left to convey his decree to the immortals: “I descend in response to the mandate to teach and transform, presiding over the Lower Prime, to guide all newly cultivated immortals toward perfection. For those who have accumulated good deeds, whose names are inscribed in the Azure Register, who morning and evening seek their vows, whose incense smoke rises to the imperial court, and whose pure chants reach the Supreme Unity—I shall reveal to them the path of cultivation. I shall command the demonic hosts to guard and protect the worldly beings who turn their hearts toward true sincerity and observe the Lower Prime’s precepts and fasts. For their nine generations of ancestors, I shall deliver both the living and the dead, enabling those who have not heard to hear, those who have not seen to see, and those who have not attained liberation to attain it.”

Those afflicted with illness and suffering, I shall heal and cure; those gripped by fear and dread, I shall grant peace and safety. Now, by the Dharma’s decree, I shall descend into the earth to proclaim the Dao and spread transformation. When the time of the Middle Prime arrives, the Supreme Unity of the Correct Dao shall descend from the Cinnabar Terrace to expound the Dharma for you.

Your merit and virtue are complete, possessing the six penetrations and unimpeded wisdom. Yet because your bodies are not self-arising and your enlightenment is newly attained, you have not yet ascended to the Great Canopy above. Those who cultivate and achieve the Dao may attain freedom, abide in eternal life without death, and have their names inscribed in the Left Register. Though eons pass like a blink, your forms renew with each dawn.

You, all the immortals, are the chosen ones. How lamentable that the multitudes of beings are as ephemeral as mayflies, born at dawn and dead by dusk, forever severed from the Dao. You must take heed of this.

At that moment, the immortals followed the Heavenly Worthy to briefly govern the earth, bestowing transformation during the Lower Prime to deliver all living beings. Then, the Heavenly Worthy, accompanied by a host of perfected immortals as numerous as motes of dust, rode upon floating rosy clouds and luminous star palaces, descending to the earth. Midway, they arrayed the palaces of the stars, hovering seven *ren* above the ground. They condensed nine-colored clouds of auspicious radiance into a great city, its towers and terraces formed from sevenfold-transforming luminous qi, its four gates forged from myriad-changing golden essence. The bolts and bars were made of adamantine radiance, the watchtowers of primordial true qi, the defenses of forbearance’s jewel-light, the moats of wisdom’s jewel-light. The springs and pools were of dark origin’s pure clarity, the stairways of fourfold-trust’s jewel-light, the trees of six perfections’ jewel-light. The flowers and fruits were of precept-pearl’s jewel-light, the banners and canopies of vermilion sparrow’s jewel-light, the divine standards of azure dragon’s jewel-light, the auspicious staffs of white tiger’s jewel-light, the bells and chimes of dark warrior’s jewel-light, the immortal music of mysterious wind’s jewel-light. The thunder of the Dharma’s jewel-light awakened all beings, the wheel of the Dharma’s jewel-light proclaimed transformation, the empty cavern’s jewel-light emitted sacred scriptures, the myriad-qi’s jewel-light summoned living souls, the divine talismans’ jewel-light called forth the dead, the yin-life’s jewel-light revived withered bones, the ninefold-transformed jewel-light eradicated chronic ailments. The celestial kitchens were of grand harmony’s jewel-light, the sweet springs of sweet dew’s jewel-light, the lamps and candles of sun-and-moon’s jewel-light, the flying canopies of fragrant clouds’ jewel-light, the mats and cushions of heavenly flowers’ jewel-light.

Then, the Heavenly Worthy, with a single flow of compassionate power, emitted rays of light that ascended to the utmost heights and descended to the lowest depths, illuminating all worlds in the ten directions. From afar, the Heavenly Worthy appeared as if present before their eyes. The great assembly beheld the ten directions as clearly as their own palms. The souls of the living and the dead all rode the light, gathering like clouds in an instant. The demonic hordes, their essence spent, also rode the light, crawling forward in submission.

At that moment, the spirits of earth and water shattered the solid ice, cleared away the piled snow, and rose halfway from the ground, drinking in the harmony of supreme transformation. The grasses and trees beneath the earth stirred their hidden roots and dormant buds, all surging forth. Though touched by frost and snow, their coiled shoots split open, ascending in clouds and exhaling crimson blossoms. In an instant, the divine peaks’ ice melted, the frozen seas thawed, and the earth’s milk—nectar of jade—flowed forth as the heavens bestowed sweet dew.

The Heavenly Worthy gazed for a long while, rejoicing in the myriad beings, knowing their hearts turned toward the Dao. Then, revealing his golden countenance, he opened his Dharma-mouth and smiled serenely. Myriad-transforming true light streamed from his golden lips. All worlds in the ten directions beheld the true form within the light, leaping with joy, unaware of their own rapture. Humans and non-humans alike fixed their thoughts and focused their minds upon the true light, which entered their hearts and eyes. For three days and nights, they remained still, untouched by weariness.

Within the true light, each saw their own souls encircling the Heavenly Worthy. In an instant, they transformed into infants, entering their bodies and sitting within their palaces, serene and unmoving. They felt their bodies renewed as youths, their complexions radiant, their hair dark, their strength like clouds.

The dead souls drank the harmonious life-qi and took human form, returning to truth and rebirth. The demonic hordes transformed their standards, their hearts now aligned with virtue and the Dao. The earth and water spirits, half-illumined by the light, attained their utmost numinosity. Those conceived in wombs, eggs, or hidden gestation were all safeguarded by their mothers, imbued with true qi. On the day of their emergence, they achieved completion according to their nature, swift and agile in flight or movement, free from premature death or harm. Chronic and recent ailments vanished at once. Venomous creatures ceased to sting, and poisonous plants and trees withered away.

The Celestial Worthy addressed all living beings: "This is not by nature, but all through the transformation of the Dao. In a single instant, divine power is fully manifested, and the myriad things are complete, receiving the true and upright qi. By the midday hour of the fifteenth day, the common folk of the lower realms each present their sincere devotion, bringing offerings of all they possess to celebrate the Lower Prime, making offerings to the Celestial Worthy with all that exists in the world."

The Celestial Worthy then addressed the assembled immortals: "The common folk differ in their offerings—some present sincere devotion, others precious treasures, grains, or silks. Even a single incense stick, a single flavor, a speck of dust, or a single hue—through the compassion of the Great Dao, all are accepted. I expound the true Dharma, demonstrate proper dignity, strengthen their roots of faith, and bring them joy. Through this cause and condition, they depart from perversity, escape the cycle of birth and death, and forever enter the stream of the Dao. How excellent! How excellent!"

At that moment, all the immortals and non-human beings, all that exists between heaven and earth—whether formed or formless—joined their voices as one, praising in unison. At that time, fragrant light lingered, rosy clouds spread across the four directions, the three luminaries intersected their paths, moving west and east in turn. True hymns filled the vastness, and celestial songs resounded in the great void. Jeweled canopies floated in mist, long banners caught the wind. Dragon kings bore censers, scattering the qi of returned souls. Immortal youths struck chimes at the four gates of the celestial city. Heavenly music harmonized, its echoes boundless. This enabled all beings to don the mysterious within the void, sit in stillness upon flying dragons, silently recite sacred scriptures, plant roots in past kalpas, and bear fruit in the future. In the present, they transcended all limits, forgot the two extremes, dissolved all defilements, and rested in the silent abyss of no-mind. From the darkness, light and qi emerged—soft yet firm, yielding yet unyielding.

When the Celestial Worthy had finished expounding this Dharma, he entered the Great Compassion Samadhi. In an instant, cold valleys exhaled winds that stirred the jeweled canopies, their bells ringing with hollow echoes that transformed into mournful sounds. Dark clouds ceased to drift, true light shone resplendent, divine mist enveloped the cosmos, the seven luminaries withdrew their radiance, the sun’s path shifted south, the moon’s course turned to the yin. The nine earths solidified once more, all rivers froze into stillness, water essences floated in light, wandering qi concealed their forms. The damp-dwelling clans retreated to the depths, shelled creatures coiled in stillness, insects and worms hid in silence, swallowing their voices.

Then, at the midday hour of the fifteenth day, the Celestial Worthy slightly moved his left hand, aligning his divine mind, and snapped his fingers three times. At that moment, the assembled immortals and common folk saw the Celestial Worthy emerge from the Great Compassion Samadhi. Joyfully, they bowed their heads and said: "We are humbled by the toil of the Merciful Venerable in transforming and delivering beings, liberating both the hidden and the manifest without end. Our joy is boundless, and both the sacred and the profane rejoice. Yet we do not understand: before delivering all beings, why did the Celestial Worthy’s golden countenance first break into a smile? After delivering them, why did he then enter great sorrow, causing the sun and moon to dim, the seven luminaries to withdraw their light, frost to congeal, fierce winds to blow, the imperial path to shift south, the moon’s course to turn yin, all things to wither, and the five viscera to hold grief? The sound of your snapping fingers made all hearts grieve. We beseech you to explain and resolve our doubts."

The Celestial Worthy replied: "Good sons, you should know that my initial smile arose from joy at the turning of beings toward the Dao, for they are easily delivered. Yet after their deliverance, one must not forget great compassion. To forget great compassion is to deliver yet not deliver. For this reason, I entered the Great Compassion Samadhi for all beings, snapped my fingers at my heart, demonstrating the harmony of inner and outer, and turned the Dharma Wheel three times for the multitude. The supreme Great Dao operates thus."

Upon hearing this, all doubts were instantly resolved. Again, they bowed their heads to the Celestial Worthy, saying: "We thank you for dispelling our confusion with your golden words. The appointed hour has come, and we now humbly request that the Celestial Worthy and the sacred assembly, in your compassion, accept the offerings of all beings—countless as motes of dust—fulfilling their aspirations. We pray you bestow your kindness."

At that time, the Celestial Worthy did not refuse their request. The great assembly arranged their seats and received the offerings. Then, through the power of expedient means, as the Celestial Worthy was about to receive the food, he commanded the Central Perfected of his left retinue to swiftly ascend to the Great Luo of the upper realm and retrieve two vessels of Supreme Void Jeweled Light, each perfectly round. These were placed upon his seat. From the mysterious void, one vessel was first filled with the natural celestial cuisine of the Great Luo Heaven—essence of the sun and moon. The other, an empty vessel, was prepared to receive the sincere offerings of the beings below.

At that moment, all the people beneath the four heavens, along with various non-human beings, presented their offerings—whether by hand, mouth, or heart. All arrived simultaneously before the Celestial Worthy’s seat, each harboring doubts about the smallness of the vessel. The Celestial Worthy, knowing their uncertainty, said to them: "Simply offer your gifts; do not嫌 the vessel’s size." The people, still doubtful, dared not reply. The Celestial Worthy said again: "Your hearts are hesitant, unable to decide. I know you嫌 this vessel too small."

Then the Celestial Worthy commanded the Central Perfected to lower the vessel, slightly tilting its mouth toward the assembly, and said: "Those who wish to offer gifts should first have the kings, then the ministers, the multitudes, and all non-human beings enter my vessel, each holding their sincere hearts." The assembly received the command and looked down at the vessel, suddenly seeing it boundless, its depth unfathomable. All the people beneath the four heavens presented their offerings at once, entering the vessel—some by cart, some by carriage, some on foot, some riding—ascending, descending, flying, or walking, all without obstruction. Those who had not yet entered saw the vessel as small, but upon entering, they realized it had no bounds. They marveled, saying: "Our petty wisdom sought to measure the Celestial Worthy’s vessel of the Great Void, which does not even receive dust or dew. This is the covering of our afflictions and hindrances, preventing us from knowing the Dharma vessel of the Great Dao. Had the Celestial Worthy not commanded the Central Perfected to tilt the vessel and show us, our hearts would have remained doubtful, and our offerings would have gained no merit."

At that time, when all the people had entered the precious vessel, they traversed its expanse without finding its limits. They beheld therein boundless worlds. Gazing upward, they saw heaven upon heaven in succession, while the sun, moon, and stars shone twice as brightly as in the lower realms. Within the vessel were Celestial Perfected and Great Sages, the void’s vast emptiness, seas of sweet dew, mountains of a hundred treasures, celestial birds and beasts, hidden herbs and jade trees, fragrant clouds and winds, Dharma thunder and Dharma rain. Then the assembly looked again at their offerings, which now seemed insignificant beyond words.

As they continued their journey, they suddenly arrived at the place where the Celestial Worthy expounded the Dharma. Emerging from the vessel, they did so unknowingly. At that moment, the radiant light remained undiminished, timeless at its center. The Celestial Worthy, moved by their wholehearted presentation of offerings, wished to reveal through expedient means the rare delicacies of the celestial kitchen. He addressed the kings, princes, ministers, multitudes, immortals, and non-human beings within the great assembly, saying: "I am humbled that you have come so far for the Dao to present these offerings to me. I have accepted them on your behalf."

The people, ashamed of the meagerness of their offerings, remained silent. Perceiving their thoughts, the Celestial Worthy spoke again: "The Great Celebration of the Lower Kalpa has arrived, and myriad blessings converge as the time of the fast approaches. Fearing you may grow hungry, I have first filled this vessel with the celestial kitchen of the Great Void of the upper realms, wishing to offer you the supreme Dharma food. You should now take your seats and receive this Dharma nourishment."

The people sat in order, but as they did so, they recalled their earlier offerings and their entry into the precious vessel of the Great Void. Each grew doubtful, saying to one another: "Were our offerings and entry into the vessel a dream, or were they waking reality? The vessel was so small—if this were waking reality, we should not have been able to enter; yet if it were a dream, we should not have had the intention to offer." Moreover, though the vessel was but a few inches in size, all the heavens and earth were contained within it. Bewildered, they could not discern the truth.

Then, among the assembly, a king named Resolute Mind addressed them: "Our great multitude has not yet attained the true Dao and constantly wanders as if in a dream. Whether the Dharma vessel is large or small, whether we enter or not, whether we offer or not—all is as one in a dream. Say no more; simply reflect. The appointed hour has come, and the Celestial Worthy, in his compassion, offers us the supreme Dharma food."

In an instant, the Celestial Worthy commanded seven youthful messengers to harness a six-dragon chariot and carry the celestial vessel, serving the Dharma food in turn to the great assembly, immortals, and multitudes, allowing each to take as much as they wished. Once sated, they stored the remaining food within the vessel, yet the celestial kitchen did not diminish in the least. As they ate, the flowers of their five viscera bloomed, their intestines and stomachs filled, their ears and eyes grew keen, their joints harmonized, all illnesses vanished forever, the six senses opened, and they reflected on the grace of the Dao. They attained the six penetrations of wisdom, and in reflecting on past and future, the karmic conditions of ninety thousand great kalpas became as clear as their own palms. Only then did they realize that their former minds had been as dreams and illusions.

Then Resolute Mind and the great assembly bowed to the Celestial Worthy and asked: "Does the celestial kitchen ever come to an end?" The Celestial Worthy replied: "Only when the void itself comes to an end will the celestial kitchen be exhausted. Thus does the Great Dao possess the inexhaustible treasury to provide for all beings."

Resolute Mind asked further: "What is the karmic retribution for partaking of this celestial kitchen?" The Celestial Worthy answered: "Those who eat of the celestial kitchen shall have boundless lifespans, their forms becoming as the Great Void."

Then the Celestial Worthy commanded the Central Perfected to tilt the precious vessel, scattering its contents into the celestial kitchen, which then settled into the empty void. Where it touched grasses and trees, they transformed into flowers and fruits; the essence of the sun and the fluid of the moon became sweet dew. That which drifted in the void became the true light and harmonious qi. After ten thousand kalpas, if there be a virtuous Son of Heaven or any seeker of the Dao who drinks this sweet dew or consumes this harmonious qi, or if ordinary people eat of these fruits, each shall receive benefit according to their inherent nature.

At that time, the assembly, witnessing these wondrous and inconceivable marvels, jointly addressed the Celestial Worthy: "The supreme and subtle Dharma of the Great Dao is unmatched in its divine power. This great assembly, having already received the Celestial Worthy’s compassionate grace, though unworthy and impure, now wishes to accompany you briefly on your celestial journey, traveling to the upper realms to fulfill our rites and aspirations. We hope this may be granted by your great compassion."

The Celestial Worthy asked: "After partaking of the Dharma food, how do your hearts feel?" The great assembly each replied: "After the Dharma food, we are ten thousand times better than before."

The Celestial Worthy asked further: "What of the mind of your former dreams—does it remain or has it vanished?" They answered: "After the Dharma food, all dream-thoughts have vanished at once."

The Celestial Worthy said: "You all wish to see the upper realms. Reflect once more, and you shall see for yourselves." The great assembly reflected for a long while.

The Celestial Worthy asked: "What do you see?" They answered: "We see nothing at all."

He asked again: "What do you hear?" They replied: "We hear nothing at all."

He asked further: "Where does your mind arise? Your eyes see nothing. Where does your mind cease? Your ears hear nothing."

They answered: "The mind does not arise; the eyes see nothing. The mind does not cease; the ears hear nothing."

The Celestial Worthy said: "To see without seeing is called true seeing; to hear without hearing is called true hearing. The supreme Great Dao is without arising or ceasing. Without hearing, without seeing, without going, without coming, without body, without mind, without light, without form—its form pervades the Great Void."

After speaking these words, the Celestial Worthy gathered the great assembly into the precious vessel of the Great Void and cast it upward. The two vessels ascended simultaneously, reaching the Great Firmament of the Supreme Void in the time it takes to snap one’s fingers. Then each person saw the Primordial Qi’s Revered One, solitary and serene, seated in the profound void. From its midst emerged the spontaneous and numinous verses of the empty cavern, yet without light or form—profound, dark, and still.

At that moment, each person in the assembly offered their reverent vows, bowing their heads for a long while. They inquired of the Celestial Worthy, saying: "We know not how the Great Sage, the Celestial Worthy, abides in solitary serenity, forever apart from the world, utterly beyond fame or renown—leaving those below, the common folk, yearning with earnest devotion, seeking abundant blessings yet finding nowhere to turn. We only pray that the Celestial Worthy will proclaim the transformative power of the Dao and deliver future generations." Again they bowed their heads for a long while, prostrating themselves without rising.

The Celestial Worthy made no reply. In an instant, the empty void dissolved into nothingness. Only a drifting, floating qi remained in the heavens, as if present yet absent. Then, faintly from the pure heavens above, there arose the subtle sound of the numinous verses of the empty cavern—audible when one bent to listen, yet vanished when one looked up. Endless and obscure, upon careful listening, one might catch the words, yet their meaning remained elusive and indistinct.

Then the Celestial Worthy raised his hand of great compassion amidst the assembly, reaching into the summit of existence to draw all the people back into the gathering. In an instant, he cast them forth again, encircling the ten directions and the worlds as numerous as motes of dust. In the time it takes to snap one’s fingers, they circled seven times before returning to the assembly. Each person then knew within themselves that by the divine power of the Dao, they had witnessed the boundless realms of the Dao throughout the ten directions. Emerging once more from the vessel, all was clear and distinct, their minds free of doubt. Only then did they realize that in the upper realms, the empty void holds nothing at all.

At that time, as the Celestial Worthy and the assembled multitude reached the third watch of the night on the sixteenth day, he gathered the celestial treasures of the Great Void, along with all the luminous qi and every majestic adornment, and entered the stellar palace. Then, all the immortals, divine beings, numinous beings, human kings, and the countless multitudes below knew that the Celestial Worthy’s true transformative work was complete and that he was about to return to the upper realms. Fearing that thereafter there would be no place to resolve their doubts, the newly initiated Daoists and all future generations, wishing to establish the Three Primes Offering, yet unclear about its rituals and methods, realized that never again would they witness such effortless liberation as the Celestial Worthy’s transformative grace that day. Together, they earnestly entreated the Celestial Worthy to instruct future disciples on how to establish blessings and cultivate merit, ensuring their eventual success.

The Celestial Worthy then addressed the assembly, saying: "The Great Celebration of the Three Primes is by nature the most auspicious time of the Dao’s spontaneous workings, the propitious day when the multitudes of perfected beings pay homage to the Supreme Ultimate. It is the crucial moment for those below—immortals and common folk alike—to cultivate themselves and deliver the departed. At this time, merits and transgressions are examined, fortunes and misfortunes are assessed. The Celestial Emperor gazes down, the officials of wrongdoing investigate and impeach; the earthly administrators submit their reports, the watery bureaus record the accounts. Those with merit attain perfection, while those with transgressions are demoted and punished. The underworld’s tribunals impose their judgments, and suffering defies description. If you wish to perform the offering, you must follow the proper method: for three days and three nights, burn incense, make reverent repentance, concentrate your thoughts on the Dao, chant the scriptures and precepts, and constantly maintain the Ten Remembrances:

First, remember the grace of the Dao;
Second, remember the grace of the scriptures;
Third, remember the grace of the masters;
Fourth, remember the grace of heaven;
Fifth, remember the grace of parents;
Sixth, remember the grace of the benevolent spirits;
Seventh, remember the grace of benefactors;
Eighth, remember the grace of good friends;
Ninth, remember the grace of the past;
Tenth, remember the grace of the present.

The Celestial Worthy declared: "If there are good men and women who cultivate these Ten Remembrances, they will be born into the Ten Virtuous Paths. Within each single virtue, ten spirits will protect and guard them—thus they are called the body of a hundred spirits. Those who lack the Ten Remembrances are called the body of a hundred evils, for the hundred kinds of benevolent spirits will turn against and plunder them. The superior person who cultivates the Ten Remembrances will attain true immortality; the middling person will extend their lifespan; the lesser person will attain longevity."

The Celestial Worthy continued: "For the Three Primes Offering, whether abundant or modest, what matters is the盛 purity and unity of inner and outer devotion. On this day, all the great sages of the heavens descend to observe, and the benevolent spirits oversee the offering, standing at your left and right. For three days and three nights, your merits and transgressions are reported above. You must be diligent and earnest, never negligent. The Dao dwells within the profound, yet it gazes upon your heart from afar."

**Chapter Twelve: The Circulation of the Precious Scripture of the Three Primes**

At that time, the heavenly kings of the four heavens below stepped forward to bow. The Heavenly King of Resolute Mind addressed the Celestial Worthy, saying: "We do not yet know by what name this scripture, expounded by the Celestial Worthy, should be called. How should it be upheld? How should it be circulated?"

"How is it to be revered? How is it to be entrusted? We humbly request that you distinguish and elucidate what we have not yet heard."

The Celestial Worthy declared: "Good men, this scripture is named *The Supreme Dao’s Precious Scripture of the Three Primes*. As the scripture instructs, it is to be reverently upheld and widely proclaimed throughout the four heavens below, ensuring it is never severed. Wherever this scripture resides, it shall be stored in a separate case, with incense burned in offering. It is to be entrusted to enlightened kings, princes, great ministers, and Dao-seeking scholars. In places of fasting and purification, they shall expound it to others, awakening those who have not yet heard."

At that moment, the great assembly, having heard the Celestial Worthy’s words, burned incense, scattered flowers, and circled in praise, obeying the divine command.

As the night reached the first watch of the fifth watch, the Celestial Worthy ascended into the void and departed. The immortals lingered upon the cloud-paths, gazing longingly at the celestial chariot, and chanted the *Step-in-Emptiness*:

*Swiftly we rise on the cloud-path,*
*Dimly we enter the endless dawn.*
*The star-officials recede into distance,*
*Eons stretch far beyond reckoning.*
*We strain to hear the golden countenance fade,*
*Yearning, we fix our thoughts on the divine radiance.*
*May we follow the rosy chariot,*
*Burning incense, bowing in reverence at dawn.*

*The mystic wind turns the flying canopy,*
*Purple qi suffuses the immortal carriage.*
*Floating aloft without need of steeds,*
*Merging with light, it suddenly ascends into nothingness.*
*Lingering, we mourn the world below,*
*Glancing back in compassion for all beings.*
*The true transformation of the Three Primes complete,*
*It vanishes effortlessly into the Great Void.*
*Myriad qi drift upward into the void,*
*A thousand lights merge with the Supreme Subtlety.*
*Between the clouds, we glimpse the radiant canopy,*
*In the emptiness, we catch sight of the rosy robes.*
*The true form enters the cloud-path,*
*Its perfect brilliance follows the wind in flight.*
*May we attend the assembly of the Three Primes,*
*And return with the golden countenance upon the turning of fate.*

Then, the immortals of the lower realms and the great assembly, having completed the *Step-in-Emptiness*, raised their gaze to the cloud-paths, straining to behold the divine radiance. Their eyes followed the rosy trail of the celestial chariot as they bowed in farewell to the True Emperor.

In an instant, purple clouds descended from the heavens, and a light mist arose from the earth. Mist and rosy clouds intertwined, and only the celestial music gradually faded into the distance.

The great assembly then returned to their respective lands, where they propagated the Dao and its teachings as proclaimed by the Golden Mouth, circulating the precious scripture, holding fasts, giving lectures, and convening assemblies. Throughout the four heavens below, all received the mysterious blessings, their fortune and virtue boundless.

Here ends Scroll Four of *The Jade Clarity Scripture of the Supreme Dao*.

---

**Scroll Five of *The Jade Clarity Scripture of the Supreme Dao***
**Chapter Thirteen: The Eight Seasonal Festivals**

At that time, the Western Numinous Supreme Immortal, together with one thousand two hundred attendants, on the morning of the twenty-sixth day of the eighth month in the third year of the August Emperor of the Void, harnessed their flying-dragon chariots, ascended the cloud paths, and entered the Jade Clarity Heaven to pay homage to the Highest Perfected Supreme Emperor, the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion. They sought to receive *The True Scripture of the Eight Seasonal Festivals* and to behold the august majesty of the Most Sagely, the wondrous and subtle transformations of the Central Heavenly Blessed Realm governed by the Supreme Dao.

Their hearts advanced toward the Heavenly Gate, their steps traversed the cloud courts. They arrayed their dignified bearing, then prostrated and knelt as one. After a long while, gazing upward toward the cloud palaces above, they beheld the True Emperor of Great Compassion—his divine countenance serene and luminous, his radiance vast and distant, his presence tranquil and flowing, abiding at the heart of heaven, seated amidst the light of clouds like ethereal dawn, faint against the dark sky, enveloped in floating clouds that cradled the morning glow. His eyes shone like the rising sun, his brows arched like the crescent moon; his hair, deep blue, coiled like mist, his lips, crimson, exhaled rosy clouds. Upon his head rested the golden essence of ten thousand transformations; his body was adorned with the jade silk of a hundred million revolutions. His hands soared to sustain the heavens, his feet trod the Turning Celestial Pivot. In subtlety and obscurity, in emptiness and profundity, he dwelled—where the Dao abides eternally, where principle accords with non-arising. True communion responds with essence, wondrous resonance stirs the spirit. Neither concealed nor manifest, neither turbid nor clear; as if present, as if absent, as if dim, as if bright. Bending to the realm of sentience, ascending into formlessness, he dwelt in boundless seclusion, expounding the true scriptures in silence. His divine chant, though soundless, resounded; his true form unmoving, yet his transformative work never ceased. His hands revolved the eight qi, his feet turned the seven meridians. He gathered all living beings, yet claimed no merit in nurturing and sustaining; his hidden virtue defied description—how could it be forcibly named? The radiance of the Dao knew no limit, the dark origin was unfathomable. Where did his heart reside? His form wandered beyond all bounds, vanishing into dim obscurity, vast and ever-empty. Merging past and future, he needed not abide in the center. Without arising, without ceasing, without beginning, without end. The True Sovereign was attended by a host of divine beings. Jade bells marked the rhythm, golden censers wafted fragrant mists; sweet dew flowed as nectar, numinous qi congealed into clouds. True light shone through, incense winds suffused the air, luminous and primordial, where the germ and the decayed were indistinct. Beyond naming, all arose naturally.

At that time, the assembled immortals gazed upon the True Emperor, their hearts never wearying. They forgot their forms, their awe and virtue utterly lost. They wished to speak yet could not voice their silence; the Dao’s mysteries were inexhaustible, their sincerity rare and profound. After a moment, they bowed again, their hearts desiring to express something, yet fearing they could not articulate it. Daring to brave his majestic presence, they could only reflect on the grace of the Dao.

Then the True Emperor, moved by their trembling reverence, commanded the Left Attendant Supreme Perfected to address the immortals: “You are immortals of the Three Heavens, fortunate by past blessings to have entered the Dao’s current, already ascended to the stage of no retreat. Yet you must still cultivate the supreme and secret essentials, serving as salvation for the world, never resting for even an instant. Why have you come here, yet remain silent?”

“We, the great sages, though supremely exalted, have not forgotten great compassion. Our every movement and rest pervades the Six Voids; our hearts roam amidst ten thousand affairs. Sincerity inevitably evokes response—nothing can oppose it.”

Then the immortals knelt and spoke: “We, your humble servants, unworthy though we are, have long cherished the path of true immortality. Our forms are worn, our bones coarse, utterly dust-laden and defiled. Yet by the boundless, universal compassion of heaven’s grace, we who were scattered and withered have been restored to flourishing. We have been bathed in the golden talismans, our bones nurtured by jade inscriptions. Our living corpses have drunk from the vast springs of the dark origin, sipped the flowing blessings of the Cavernous Clarity. We have heard that when the Dao is exhausted, it returns; when things reach their limit, they revert. Even the dust-laden and defiled constantly yearn for their origin.
