For countless kalpas, we have longed to behold the august presence of the Most High. Yet we feared our habitual tendencies had not dissolved and dared not approach lightly. In hesitation, eons have passed. Unexpectedly, we seized the opportunity of fate, stepped into the celestial courts, and encountered the Heavenly Worthy, fulfilling our long-held aspirations. We have long wished to consult and inquire but dared not voice our words. Gazing upon your true majesty, we were suddenly lost, our five senses unmoored, our mouths unable to speak. Only by the profound and abiding love of the Compassionate Worthy, who deigned to bestow guidance and lend your majestic light, have we found the courage to speak. Daring to exert our humble efforts, we express these meager sentiments.”

Then the Left Perfected, obeying the Heavenly Worthy’s decree, propagated the Dao and its teachings, resolving the doubts of later learners. He addressed the immortals: “What is your wish? Speak freely.”

The immortals, overjoyed, bowed in gratitude to the Perfected and said: “Though the Dao resides in people, it is not a matter of valuing the law over life. Through eons of toil and suffering, we have scaled peaks and traversed perilous paths, crossed waters and passed through fire, undaunted by hardship and danger. Thus, the Highest Perfected took pity on our ignorance and bestowed upon us the sacred texts. True qi spread boundless blessings; the Great Dao descended talismans of yin generation. We revived the endangered souls of the departed, restored the withered and decayed forms of the living. Above, we were ashamed before the ever-renewing Dao; below, we daily renewed our virtue in the lower realm. For countless kalpas, we have cycled through the Three Heavens. Unexpectedly, we ascended by fate, and the dust-laden entered the Jade Clarity’s realm. We parted the six mists, emerged through the eight heavens, tore through the nets of the three realms, and ascended to the seventh stage of enlightenment. Though we have cultivated the Dao’s subtle merits, we have not yet dissolved into the formless. Today, we are fortunate to enter the birthless birth of the Supreme Mystery—our birth in the Dao is secure. Our long-held aspirations have reached their culmination here. Yet with hearts still stirred, we wish to hear the essentials of the Eight Seasonal Festivals. By establishing fasts and performing meritorious deeds, we seek blessings, atone for transgressions, liberate beings from sorrow and suffering, open the path to life and death, and ascend into the source of the Dao.”

Then the Perfected, hearing the immortals’ words, exclaimed in surprise: “How is it that you, who dwell in the Three Heavens, have come to hear of the essentials of the Eight Seasonal Festivals? This is none other than the first chapter of *The Treasured Writ of the Spirit-Generating of the Supreme Ultimate*—a scripture concealed by the Heavenly Emperor, cultivated by the Supreme Perfected, transmitted orally, its text unseen. It is to be bestowed only upon those destined to achieve perfection in the future.”

"How have you come to hear of this?"

Then the immortals kowtowed and replied: "This humble one dwells far from the sages, and the true writs have long been hidden and lost. It was only at the first assembly of the Nine Perfected at the Dragon-Initiation, when we celebrated the Supreme One of the Void and Non-Being, the Heavenly Venerable, that the Great Sage emerged to bestow the Dharma and instruct the Perfected. Though we heard the titles of the scriptures chanted, we never beheld their texts. We have held them in our hearts ever since, never once forsaking them. Now, in our longing and reverence, we dare to speak of this, though we fear offending the will of Heaven. Yet in Your great compassion, we pray You show us kindness and mercy."

The Perfected One declared: "You bear the marks of truth and are worthy to hear the supreme Dharma. Your destiny aligns with the time to achieve perfection. I shall transmit this treasured scripture to one such as you. But to violate the precepts by careless disclosure is to forfeit the Dao and lose one’s true nature."

Then the immortals bowed and assented to the Perfected One, vowing to obey His teachings and never dare to be negligent or reckless.

Thereupon, the Perfected One commanded the Golden Youth to burn celestial incense of precious names, open the golden terrace’s treasure store, unlock the casket and reveal its contents. He brought forth *The Treasured Scripture of the Eight Seasonal Festivals*, placing it upon a jade table before the Heavenly Venerable. All the immortals bowed as one, prostrating themselves for a long while, too awestruck to speak.

The Heavenly Venerable, perceiving their intent, inclined His head in compassion and commanded the Perfected One to present the treasured scripture to the immortals. Having received it, they bowed again to the Heavenly Venerable.

The Perfected One said: "This scripture is the sacred text of the supreme Dao. Long ago, the Heavenly Venerable of Great Compassion gathered the clouds of qi to form its words, and all the Perfected Ones looked up to follow its teachings. The true qi of the great Dao transformed into cloud-seal script, and once its qi dispersed, the numinous chapters vanished into emptiness. If you wish to copy it, carve jade into tablets and inscribe them with purple gold. When the transcription is complete, you must return it to me."

The Perfected One continued: "You immortals shall now retire to the Western Terrace of the Numinous Palace to transcribe the true writ. There, a celestial kitchen will provide for all who study, and a cinnabar terrace amid jasper groves awaits your leisure and repose."

All the immortals joyfully accepted the command. They withdrew to the Western Terrace, where they carved jade and inlaid gold, transcribing the numinous script.

The *Precious Scripture of the Eight Solar Terms* by the Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy states:

On the day of *Lichun* (Beginning of Spring), the warming qi first arises. The Cloud Palace opens its northeastern gate, and the Three Offices present themselves in audience to determine good and evil.

On the day of *Chunfen* (Spring Equinox), the harmonizing qi first takes form. The Cloud Palace opens its due eastern gate, and the Three Offices present themselves in audience to determine good and evil.

On the day of *Lixia* (Beginning of Summer), the balmy qi first arises. The Cloud Palace opens its southeastern gate, and the Three Offices present themselves in audience to determine good and evil.

On the day of *Xiazhi* (Summer Solstice), the scorching qi first takes form. The Cloud Palace opens its due southern gate, and the Three Offices present themselves in audience to determine good and evil.

On the day of *Liqiu* (Beginning of Autumn), the cooling qi first arises. The Cloud Palace opens its southwestern gate, and the Three Offices present themselves in audience to determine good and evil.

On the day of *Qiufen* (Autumn Equinox), the chilling qi first takes form. The Cloud Palace opens its due western gate, and all the spirits assemble in audience to deliberate and record the registers of sin and blessing, life and death. Every deed of merit or transgression, no matter how minute, is laid bare. The Perfected Ones inscribe them in great detail, and all spirits receive their charges. Merit and fault, even to the finest degree, are reported without fail.

On the day of *Lidong* (Beginning of Winter), the stern qi first arises. The Cloud Palace opens its northwestern gate, and the Three Offices present themselves in audience to determine good and evil.

On the day of *Dongzhi* (Winter Solstice), the congealing qi first takes form. The Cloud Palace opens its due northern gate, and the Three Offices present themselves in audience to determine good and evil.

The Heavenly Worthy instructs those who would come to study the true Way: Cultivate my Dao of the Eight Solar Terms, establish merit and practice the teachings. Let your body never tread the path of wrongdoing, nor your will stray into crooked ways. Always observe purification rites to seek ascent and deliverance. Be steadfast from beginning to end, and provide for all necessities. With a sincere and diligent heart, ever strive to save the burning; with unwavering devotion, never forget in movement or stillness. Constantly reflect on the Way of the master as if he were present before you. In solitude within secluded groves, sever all worldly affairs. Perform the six-hour rites and prayers to seek secret union. Tirelessly and subtly, neither rise nor cease. When merit is complete and practice perfected, you shall meet with the Perfected Ones.

One day before each solar term, perform the Dao, offer prayers, and present what your heart desires, so that your qi harmonizes with the incense smoke. Let your every action in the six hours be heard above, and let your conduct conform to ritual. Sit in silent meditation and refine your thoughts for three days and nights to lift the karmic bonds of your nine generations of ancestors and atone for the gravest transgressions of your own life. First for the Son of Heaven, then for all the people. In the gate of those who uphold the Dao, exert your strength to perform meritorious deeds, provide for vegetarian feasts, and make offerings together. On these days, sincerity reaches all without fail, and the Dao hears all without exception. Let those who cherish the Dao practice diligently.

The superior practitioner maintains perpetual purification, not only at these times, but constantly prays for ascent and deliverance without the slightest respite. Let your form sever all external wanderings, and your will not seek crooked ends. If you cultivate life and attain life, what cause for worry remains?

Thereupon, the Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy expounded the *Scripture of the Lute-Heart, Upper Scroll*. Its text reads:

Turn your head to gaze upon the Round Net,
Converge the light to draw in the numinous radiance.
Restrain the hun-soul and govern the seven po,
In contemplation discern the central square.

In motion or stillness, bow to the Void,
In rest or sleep, repose in the Mystic Chamber.
When hungry, feast on the Yellow Jade Flower,
When thirsty, drink the Jade Root Nectar.
The spirit’s banner commands the great demons,
Unite the body to refine the true light.
Reflect again to contemplate the Great Nothingness,
Ever roaming within the emptiness.
At the edge of the people’s waves, the Perfect Permeation,
The true transformation knows no midway halt.
Profound and boundless, without end or beginning—
Let the practitioner clearly understand this.
In silence, forget doctrines and teachings,
Respond to the times to expound the grand principles.
The descending Dao does not reveal itself;
One must first enact what is to be bestowed.
Converging in the non-dual realm,
Following the heart, it naturally unites or parts.

The Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy says: Those of later generations who attain the Perfected and receive this text of mine shall regulate the Void Lute and practice accordingly. They shall ever stand beneath the Azure Canopy, riding a pair of white tigers, flanked by two red dragons. Before the kalpas began, the sages knew no end. After eighteen years, they shall witness the Great Peace. The origin of the true Dao—guard it well, do not recklessly proclaim it. If one’s seven ancestors are subjected to judgment, their bodies shall not attain immortality, and for countless kalpas, all hope shall be lost, severed from the Dao.

At that time, the immortal carved the jade scripture, returned the sutra to the Perfected One, and presented the new text to the Heavenly Worthy. The Heavenly Worthy declared: This precious scripture of the Supreme Dao may be transmitted to three persons in seven hundred years. If no such person exists in the world, conceal it in a jade coffer and forbid its reckless dissemination.

Thereupon, the immortal bowed deeply in reverence and gratitude: "This humble one is fortunate to have received this secret dharma. By the boundless compassion of the Venerable One, I am filled with joy beyond expression." Again, he bowed deeply.

The Heavenly Worthy declared: "You have received the precious scripture, and the true Dao is now complete within you. Diligently practice it, and you shall come to understand of your own accord."

The Heavenly Worthy continued: "Now go and wander through the jade realms of the Yuqing Dao. After the Autumn Equinox, return once more to the lower world."

Thereupon, the immortal, obeying the Heavenly Worthy’s decree, bowed in joyful reverence and gratitude, then paid homage to the Perfected One. The Perfected One said: "Your journey by grace follows the established law. In the Yuqing Heaven, the Heavenly Worthy possesses a chariot of true light, bestowed upon the immortals and perfected beings to traverse the ten directions. Those who ride this chariot shall circle the worlds of dust in an instant."

Having received these instructions, the immortal mounted the chariot of true light. In the blink of an eye, he arrived at the southwestern void of the Yuqing Heaven, a boundless expanse beyond measure. On the morning of the twenty-eighth day, at the time of the Autumn Equinox, he suddenly beheld countless heavenly immortals and perfected beings entering through the western gate of the cloud palace. They arrayed themselves in celestial order, setting forth offerings that filled the mysterious void. Incense burned, flowers scattered, and heavenly musicians played, singing praises as they paid homage to the Heavenly Worthy for three days and three nights.

The Three Offices reviewed the records of life and death, of sins and blessings. Those deemed worthy of deliverance had their names inscribed on blue bamboo slips. Cloud chariots descended from the heavens, lifting them into the void, flesh and bone ascending together, forever to become true immortals. Those whose sins piled like dust had their names recorded in the black ledger. Their years were diminished, their lifespans stolen, their corpses cast into the Nine Dark Realms, their sinful souls subjected to judgment, lost for ten thousand kalpas without hope of return.

At that time, the officials of the Three Offices each presented their reports. Ascending and descending in opposing motions, their tones differed in sorrow and joy. The celestial officials played harmonious and refined melodies; the terrestrial officials played solemn and measured tunes; the aquatic officials played the mournful songs of souls lost in eternal night. The winds howled, shattering metal and stone; the stern qi stirred the cries of wind and rain. These were the natural sounds of heaven and earth, ever present at the juncture of fortune and misfortune.

Though the cacophony was vast, the Great Dao’s Heavenly Worthy had never heard it. His mind remained serene in the mysterious, utterly undisturbed. The filth and clamor of the Three Offices did not reach his ears or eyes. In every response, he remained silent, communicating without words, intuitively perceiving the hearts of others. He weighed and acted as was fitting, bestowing life without claim to merit, his hidden virtues never erring.

Yet all living beings go about their days in ignorance. Though the Great Dao is lofty, its mirror is lowly. The Great Dao remains still, yet acts when the moment is ripe. It neither comes nor goes, neither hastens nor lingers, neither perishes nor endures, neither unites nor separates, neither empties nor fills. Its movements leave no trace.

My radiance unfurls like blossoms, twin lights gleaming. It cycles through the purple gates, resting in the golden chambers. The six qi flow downward, the three origins ascend. Neither swift nor slow, neither diminished nor increased, it shines of its own accord. It banishes death and welcomes life, acting without acting, moving without moving. The true spirit remains unmoved, yet transforms and harmonizes all things.

The true spirit’s original mind responds with original emotion. It can contract or expand, conceal or reveal. Neither dual nor centered, neither following nor meeting, neither rising nor falling, neither dying nor living. It takes form without form, is named without name. It is bright in darkness, clear in turbidity. Neither solitary nor gregarious, neither blended nor merged. Vast and subtle, it neither conforms nor resists. It goes without destination, comes without return, dwells without abode, moves without reliance. It strides the void without traversing, sits yet responds to all things. Elusive and indistinct, it remains undisturbed in profound stillness.

Many despise me, few cherish me. They chase foul scents like dust, how can they return to the numinous mechanism? Enveloped in delusion, their actions breed doubt. Turning from the Dao, they drift and perish—who shall return? Wandering alone on perilous paths, how pitiable their solitude. Adrift on the river without turning back, when shall they return against the current? Forever wailing in the Three Paths, eternally grieving through the Nine Nights, their suffering souls scattered, their sorrows heaped high.

I tell you, those yet to come: the Dao is like the morning sun, virtue like the flowing stream. It is ever new, ever returning. Below, it gathers the ten thousand rivers; above, it governs the thousand mechanisms. It illuminates without vexation, abides without dissipation. No emotion can reflect it, no mind can perceive it. The eight trigrams turn in emptiness, the seven luminaries revolve in void. Naturally, it weaves the warp and weft of existence, the essence of all living things. Subtle within the subtle, wondrous within the wondrous.

I tell you, those yet to come: in action, do not stray from the constant; in movement, do not depart from the void. Abide in constancy without faltering; root yourself deeply in the void. Constancy adapts to all, the void gives birth to all. Without moving, it reaches all; without effort, it brings forth life. Its reach is boundless, its generation all-encompassing. Pervasive yet not exhausted, all-encompassing yet never ceasing.

Its form is like clouds, its qi like flowing water. When the flow reaches its limit, it returns; when clouds sink low, they must rise. Returning, it holds being; rising, it holds emptiness.

I tell you, those yet to come: do not rely on your brightness. When brightness reaches its extreme, darkness follows; when darkness reaches its extreme, brightness returns. If you can constantly guard the dark, your body shall forever dwell in great peace. You shall repel the Three Disasters, dissolve the Five Weapons. The Ten Evils shall not approach, the Six Thieves shall not act. No battles shall arise at your borders, no alarms shall disturb your cities. A hundred harvests shall ripen, flowers and trees shall flourish. Wind and rain shall be harmonious, all things shall grow of their own accord.

I tell you, those yet to come: abandon emotion, forsake desire. Feast on the primordial, clothe yourself in the One. Embrace the Dao, hold fast to virtue. Gather good companions, drive away the yin thieves. Adorn yourself with majesty, restrain yourself with precepts. Indulgence in flavors harms the self; lustful cravings master the self. Your wishes shall not be fulfilled, your desires shall not be met.

Those who kill and steal to sustain themselves, who wield power and fortune with arrogance, who disregard the lowly, inflict harm, and mete out punishment—who curse heaven and revile earth, who rush about in distress—shall see their five spirits wage war within, their resentments bind without. Their yang qi shall leak and dissipate, their yin meridians shall meet with premature closure. Those who take the perverse as the Dao shall never reach its end.

Take heed, and do not treat these teachings lightly. Do not clothe the dead with my living scriptures. Do not harbor venomous intentions while holding my precious scriptures. Do not chant my true and orthodox teachings with perverse voices. Do not allow yin thieves into my Daoist sanctum. Do not entertain lustful thoughts while forcibly practicing my Dao. Do not seek the Way of wholeness with a corrupted body. Do not use a body steeped in the Ten Evils to destroy the Dao of the Ten Virtues."

Do not wield the sword of the Five Acts of Rebellion to sever your own five viscera. Do not cast evil eyes upon the virtuous. Do not enter my gate of stillness with a disordered mind. Do not seek my Six Penetrations with a body bound by the Six Obstructions. Do not gaze upon my soaring chariot with a body sunk in turbidity. Do not defile my Daoist sanctum with a body reeking of rot. Do not disrupt my Dharma with the heart of one who lusts after the mother and harms the father.

All good men who enter my Daoist sanctum—though but a single thought arise, though the mechanism has yet to be set in motion—already the tally of sins is established. How much more so when the body personally enacts them? Ten thousand blessings shall depart, a hundred calamities shall gather, the heavy sins of life and death shall be repaid without end.

Good men who practice my Dao: be vigilant in emptiness, do not deceive the Great Void, and take the Dao as your companion. Those who follow my precepts shall find the true Dao easy to seek; those who turn their backs on my precepts shall know endless sorrow in life and death. Can you not be cautious? Can you not be cautious?

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy again addressed the immortals, saying: The rites of audience and reverence are not confined to the eight seasonal festivals alone. On the first, eighth, fourteenth, fifteenth, eighteenth, twenty-third, twenty-fourth, twenty-eighth, twenty-ninth, and thirtieth days of each month, on these days, cultivate the body and repent of transgressions. The Great Dao, carefree and all-seeing, shall witness as if present before you.

All who study the Dao—whether at the beginning, middle, or end—should maintain a mind of equanimity, seek blessings without surfeit, and cultivate the body without weariness. Good men and women who single-mindedly guard the One shall attain my Dao. Those who embrace emptiness and act with authenticity shall perfect my Dao. Those who practice compassion, forbearance, and unrelenting diligence shall fulfill my Dao. They shall be companions to divine beings and served by a multitude of spirits. If you do otherwise, you shall waste your life in vain. I speak to those yet to come: who among you will ponder my words?

At that time, the immortals, receiving the solemn decree of the Heavenly Worthy, rejoiced and bowed their heads in gratitude, their aspirations fulfilled. They dared not speak, fearing to profane the sacred, and silently prostrated themselves to receive the Heavenly Worthy’s luminous command.

Then the Heavenly Worthy again addressed the immortals, saying: The Jade Clarity Realm of the Dao is naturally unlearned, hence it is called "emptiness and spontaneity." The Celestial Worthy of Primordial Beginning is not achieved through study. Out of great compassion, I bestow upon you the true Dao. Return to the lower realms and treasure it in practice. From this day forward, for ninety thousand great kalpas, the later sages of the Golden Towers shall descend to the Four Heavens and dwell in the divine continent. At that time, all the perfected ones of the upper realms, the Heavenly Worthies of the ten directions, and the upper immortals shall descend in accordance with the Dharma. At that moment, you shall naturally behold me. When these matters are concluded, you may return once more to the lower realms. Those who later attain the Dao and govern shall not remain here but may temporarily journey there to seek the Dharma and resolve doubts.

At that time, the immortals, receiving the Heavenly Worthy’s decree, each burned incense, bowed their heads, and took leave of the soaring chariot of the upper realms to return to the lower heavens. At that time, the immortals, having sought the Dharma before and after, traversed thirty-six thousand celestial gates and paid homage to thirty-six thousand secret Dharma teachings. Though their rank was that of lower immortals, their conduct equaled that of the highest perfected. With minds and eyes clear, they comprehended the three times without omission. Through this cause and condition, they obtained the true essential teachings of the Heavenly Worthy. Through cultivation, they swiftly attained enlightenment and penetrated the future.

Good men and women who love the Dao but do not encounter a wise teacher often harbor doubts and lack steadfastness. As the years pass, the body decays, skin and flesh wither, marrow and brain are exhausted. Though they possess ears and eyes, in truth they are deaf and blind. Further bound by attachments, clinging to their dens of greed, entangled in myriad conditions, they cannot let go. Like birds tethered by a cord, their thoughts are spent in vain, ever craving sustenance and possessions, insatiable in their desires. A hundred illnesses arise, with no means of cure, gradually worsening. In but a moment, the hour of death approaches. Though they ransom their lives with all their wealth, they shall never attain the Dharma. At the final moment, they shall regret not having practiced goodness. What use are the last gasps of breath? What can they do then?

Good men and women, I ever pity all sentient beings. Though they know food, they rarely distinguish the five flavors. Though they know how to sustain life, they seldom nurture the Dao. They die for profit and harm, are ruined by sound and beauty. They gallop in reckless abandon, exhausted and distressed.

Resentment and hatred breed strife, turning kin into sworn foes. When smoke scatters and embers fade, and life’s breath is spent, vengeful spirits and sinful ghosts swarm in ceaseless litigation, their retributions unending. They are reborn among mortals, perpetuating wicked deeds, thus falling into such plight. Disregarding the Dao’s precepts, they scorn the law of karma, mock the most sacred, slander the virtuous, slaughter the innocent, steal and plunder, bully the aged and infirm, exploit the orphaned and weak. Relying on their power, they mete out punishments at will. Even before their qi is exhausted, they already endure the torments of the unseen realm—every deed, whether weighty or trifling, is recorded without omission.

I exhort those yet to come: dwell in tranquil reverence upon the sacred scriptures, diligently cultivate the precepts, and let no transgression mar your practice. The profound mirror of the Great Dao aligns the hidden and the manifest; when peril nears, safety is found—thus is the power of the numinous first revealed.

At that moment, the Immortal once more descended to the Western Numinous Treasure Palace in the Lower Heavens, his divine radiance shining afar, a thousand myriad times brighter than before. The Three Heavens’ immortals came to greet him, marveling at this rare sight, their eyes never having beheld the like. They discerned at once the disparity—how virtue and the Dao differed—and each bowed in reverence, longing to hear the essential teachings.

Then the Western Numinous Supreme Immortal addressed the assembled immortals: “Though the Dao has no intent, it may be sought through devotion. Defiance breeds discord, while compliance with goodness flows as naturally as a river. I have traversed the heavens without bound, and through the compassion of the True Emperor, who pitied my earnest seeking, I was granted the supreme essence. He charged me to refine my practice and, in turn, proclaim the precepts and dignified rites to future generations. Moreover, after ninety thousand great kalpas, the Golden Portal Emperor shall descend to the divine continent, accompanied by the celestial lords of the Upper Heavens. The Dao’s great deliverance shall prevail—what cause have you for sorrow?”

At that time, eighty myriad billion great immortals of the Yu-Yu Heaven, hearing that the Western Numinous Supreme Immortal had descended to the Western Numinous Treasure Palace in the Three Heavens, gathered with the multitudes to pay their respects. They burned incense, scattered flowers, and played celestial music, pacing the void in solemn procession as they encircled the Supreme Immortal. Bowing deeply, they inquired after his well-being: “Your journey through the ten thousand heavens in pursuit of the Dao must have been arduous. Your divine radiance now shines a hundred millionfold brighter than before. Since the Great Dao has flourished, it shall universally benefit all conditions.”

The assembled immortals prostrated themselves, entreating the Transcendent Sage with compassion and pity to disseminate the transformative teachings of the Dao and reveal what had not yet been heard.

The Supreme Immortal replied: “I have received the supreme precepts from the Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy of the Jade Clarity Heaven in the Upper Mystery, and their regulations are strict and clear. The esoteric essentials of the Great Dao must not be rashly proclaimed. If you but hold sincerity in your heart, you must refine your thoughts with utmost diligence. After ninety thousand kalpas, the Heavenly Worthy of the Golden Portal shall descend to the Divine Continent. At that time, all the great sages of the heavens shall arrive together, and the vast deliverance of the Dao’s teachings shall universally succor gods and humans. For billions of kalpas, they shall admonish and instruct all future generations. At that time, you shall journey with me.”

Just then, among the assembly there was a lesser immortal named Rongzhen, who had attained the Dao only six years prior. Not yet comprehending the three temporal realms, he remained in the stage of study. His heart doubted the vastness of ninety thousand kalpas, and he further questioned whether a lesser immortal’s lifespan could endure until that time. He stepped forward to bow but had not yet spoken when the Supreme Immortal, already perceiving his thoughts, addressed him: “Good man, I know your heart harbors doubts about the kalpas and the lifespan of immortals. Good man, you must now understand: when mortals of the lower realms cultivate and attain the Dao, they are called ‘later sages.’ Once they enter the immortal rank, they never regress. I was born in the Western Numinous Treasure Palace, and though it seems but yesterday, already ninety trillion great kalpas have passed. To the eyes of the upper sages, this appears but the blink of an eye; ninety thousand kalpas are but a moment.

You have attained the Dao and become an immortal only six years ago, still like an infant seeking milk, lacking other wisdom, and thus doubting the kalpas and lifespan. Pitying your childlike ignorance of the supreme Dao, your dim and shallow understanding, you lightly voice such narrow views. Good man, the primordial source of the supreme Great Dao is profoundly pure, fathomless and immeasurable, the Great Mystery and Great Void, boundless and beginningless, naturally and utterly real. The later sages are likewise—unaware that in the dust-laden, foul, and perverse customs of the lower realms, those who cultivate heterodox methods may live for eighty thousand kalpas before regressing and falling. This is the way of demonic and worldly heterodoxy, which does not transcend the Three Realms, attain the Six Penetrations, comprehend the three temporal realms, or escape birth and death. With trivial and minor skills, they style themselves ‘great immortals.’

It is like the worldly term ‘vajra’—when the foolish hear it, they assume such a person is indestructible and mighty, their body imperishable. But the wise understand that this is not true indestructibility; ‘vajra’ is but a borrowed name, and in a moment, it shall perish. So too with heterodoxy: they usurp the title of ‘immortal’ to adorn their walking corpses. Just as worldly fools falsely claim the name of ‘heavenly beings,’ or as those in the dust-laden, perverse customs of the lower realms call themselves ‘great immortals.’ The wise clearly know that orthodoxy and heterodoxy are opposites, their lifespans and fates utterly distinct—eighty thousand kalpas are to them but a moment, like the fleeting life of lightning or mushrooms.

In the dust-laden lower realms, many falsely claim the name of ‘immortal.’ When they hear that immortals within the supreme Dao endure forever without perishing, yet their eyes and ears have never witnessed this, they assume the true Dao is no different from those demonic and perverse teachings. Through written records and transmitted accounts, they confuse and mislead the walking corpses. The weak and deluded, hearing such things, incline toward perversity. Deceiving themselves with illusory blessings, they invite retribution and punishment, drifting for billions of kalpas, turning their backs on the Dao in the cycle of birth and death. Practicing heterodox methods, they cry out for annihilation, amassing like ants and swarming like flies, performing all manner of ascetic practices, yet unable to attain the Dao—all because they have lost the true path and resorted to perversity.

They loathe and despise their bodies as if they were spittle, hastening to seek their own destruction, unaware that this body is the Dharma-body. In restless pursuit of external things, they abandon the inner Dharma, extensively practicing heterodox texts, slandering the Great Dao, forsaking the root to chase the branches. Such perversity arises from the borderlands and barbarian regions, and does not exist in the Divine Continent. How then, good man, do you harbor such perverse thoughts within the true Dao?

Good man, those who cultivate the inner Dharma and attain the Dao—regardless of whether they are early or late, high or low in rank—once they reach the immortal rank, endure forever, free and unobstructed. This is unlike the heterodox methods of the lower realms, where covering the body in ashes is deemed attainment of the Dao, and decay is taken as proof of fruition. These are the ways of heterodoxy, bound within birth and death, lacking freedom. They conceal their perversity and deceit to avoid worldly censure, hiding their cunning and treachery, gathering the young and ignorant, feigning marvels and wonders to mislead all, diligently seeking worldly trust, coveting wealth and sensual pleasures, their conduct deviating from the proper path, their clothing and food unjustly acquired. They nourish hidden malevolence, constantly scheming to harm others, sustaining their walking corpses, harboring the Three Poisons, corrupting good roots, killing to seek life, lacking merit to redress transgressions.

Some disobey their masters, secretly consuming potent medicines, stealing minor methods to slightly benefit themselves, then claiming to have reached the ultimate Dao. This is called ‘departing in darkness and arriving by night,’ allowing ignorance to grow. The heterodox and worldly who usurp the name of ‘immortal’ do not practice the Dao of pure and unwavering unity, nor the Dao of natural emptiness and non-being, nor the Dao of the Compassionate Worthy’s forbearance, nor the Dao of the Six Perfections and Six Penetrations, nor the primordial and supreme Great Dao, nor the Dao of unobstructed liberation, nor the Dao of eternal life and deathlessness.

Good man, if you hear of any miscellaneous methods that diverge from the Great Dao, know that these are heterodox methods, from which one cannot escape old age, sickness, death, hunger, cold, and suffering. Good man, do not harbor doubts about the Great Dao. Who is your master? What methods have you cultivated? Your aspirations are narrow and weak, utterly lacking the qi of the Dao. How can you transform the world, verify the blessings of others, and deliver beings from birth and death?

Good man, though you have attained non-regression and the freedom to fly, you are not yet equal to the great sages who are without self. You must continue your cultivation and not be complacent. When the measure of the Dao is fulfilled, your body and mind shall attain great penetration, and the affairs of the three temporal realms shall be as clear as your own palm. Ninety thousand kalpas shall not even amount to a single instant, for in my Great Dao, a hundred billion great kalpas as numerous as the dust motes of a hundred million lands are but a single breath.”

How could there be any doubt?

At that moment, the immortal Rongzhen bowed his head in reverence and offered his thanks: "This humble one is benighted, having defiled the celestial court with dust. Yet by past blessings, I have been fortunate to encounter the Perfected Ones of Heaven. Gazing down upon the six directions, I grieved with earnest sincerity and was granted the *Lingfu* of Hidden Life. Through its cultivation, I preserved my destiny and have witnessed this day—though the supreme Daoist methods remain beyond my comprehension. I humbly beseech your compassion for my ignorance and bestow upon me what I have never heard."

The Perfected One replied: "I recognize your heart, know your master, and see your cultivation. I now tell you all at once—this cannot be otherwise. In but a moment, the immortals of the thirty-seven heavens below, numbering in the billions, all assembled on the twentieth day of the tenth month to celebrate the *Lidong* festival, paying homage to the Western Numinous Perfected. Each burned incense of renown, ascending to the heavens to reverently bow from afar before the Great Emperor of the Void Sovereign Heavenly Worthy. The Three Bureaus recorded their merits, and the Water Palace reported above. The thirty-seven heavens each arrayed their celestial rites, setting forth offerings to remotely present to the Supreme Lord of the Boundless Dao. For three days and nights, they circled the void in step, while the earthly realms resounded with music to delight the immortal perfected. The Five Demons chanted long, wishing all transformations to return to the Mysterious. Liezi tuned the winds, and Yunjiang gathered the mists. Heavenly blossoms swirled in the air, and fragrant vapors dispersed into the void. Attendant immortal youths chanted the sacred scriptures.

In but a moment, the Eight Qi warmed and softened, radiant clouds soared, the celestial court brightened, and the Mysterious Path opened in the heavens. Beholding the boundless vastness of the Great Void, they saw the Primordial Harmony spread wide. The Three-in-One Venerable Spirits and the Lords of the Myriad Qi—serene as abyssal depths, drifting like clouds—held no distinction between provisional and real, now merging, now parting.

Then, all at once, they abided at the center, their forms merging into the formless. Ascending to the immortal abodes, they wandered below in the Golden City, rinsing with jade nectar, inhaling purple clouds, exhaling luminous vapors. Their forms renewed with each day, and the dust-mote kalpas returned to infancy. Neither departing nor arriving, neither perishing nor arising, they dwelled in the subtle and indistinct, beyond all names. The Mysterious Dao is without intent, yet meets all who can practice. In that exalted state, the dust-mote kalpas abide in eternal peace. To turn from the Dao and oppose Heaven—I have never heard of such a thing."

At that moment, the Great Constant Void Sovereign Heavenly Worthy emitted a radiant light from afar, illuminating the ten thousand heavens. It warmed and nourished the hidden and the manifest, bathing the gloomy and the joyful, moistening the parched, washing away filth and defilement. It unsealed the deaf and blind, mended all insufficiencies, nurtured life and healed illness, subdued the myriad demons, dissolved calamitous qi, and bestowed blessings upon all worlds in the ten directions. Birth and death opened to prosperity, and gods and humans rejoiced. At this time, the majesty was beyond thought. In the span of a finger-snap, blessings and wisdom pervaded all. The awe-inspiring power of the Great Dao is inconceivable, immeasurable, and inexpressible.

At that moment, the great assembly fixed their minds in devotion, each wishing their Daoist practice to be universally perfected so they might ascend into the Great Void and personally attend the Heavenly Worthy. They wished the Mysterious Gate to open wide, delivering boundless beings; the Five Sufferings to cease, and the souls of the Three Wretched Realms to be pardoned; all beings in borderlands to practice the Dao; chronic and stubborn illnesses to be wholly cured; and all sentient and insentient beings to avoid premature death.

As the great assembly made these seven vows, the Seven Awakening Ways became complete, and the Seven Qi Heavenly Lords rejoiced in praise. Then, seven-colored auspicious clouds descended and enveloped the assembly. Seven-colored fragrant lights illuminated the Great Mystery, and sevenfold celestial music harmonized the Seven Spirits. The Seven Perfected Ones of the Void took form with the qi.

When the assembly of immortals had completed their homage, the sounds of light and music stilled. On the morning of the twenty-fourth day, they bowed from afar to the upper realms, took leave of the Perfected Emperor, and descended through the void.

At that time, the Western Numinous Perfected Immortal entered the Great Samādhi of Concentrated Spirit. His body and mind remained unmoving, his true light serene as the hanging moon. For nine great kalpas, he remained fixed without blinking.

**Chapter Fourteen: The Precepts of Fasting and Abstinence**

At that time, in the world of Abandoned Worthiness, the household of the Huang clan had long cultivated the Ten Virtues. Free from unjust punishments or harm, they constantly observed fasting and abstinence, establishing offerings in tranquility. On the Three Primes and Eight Festivals, they burned incense and bowed to the Void. On the ten auspicious days, they paid homage and repented of transgressions. Their devotion to the Great Dao was sincere, without flattery or desire. Their household was abundant in wealth and resources, with many servants. They often gave alms at crossroads, aiding the destitute and sheltering travelers, bestowing vast charity. Each winter, when frost accumulated in the wilds, they showed kindness to birds and beasts, pitying the poor, sick, elderly, young, orphaned, and weak, providing for their needs so nothing was lacking. In hosting fasting lectures and assemblies, their hearts never wearied.

The elder had a wife, née Feng, who one day at noon fell asleep at home. In her dream, she saw a bright pearl descend from the heavens into her bosom. Then, sunlight shone upon her body. Awakening from her nap, she realized she had conceived. From that time onward, her heart was joyful, her complexion radiant, her steps light, and her strength doubled. After ten months, on the eighth day of the fourth month, she ascended a terrace to enjoy the view. Suddenly, at noon, she saw a purple cloud hovering a hundred *zhang* above the earth, moving southeast. From within the purple cloud, she heard a voice say: "Immortal child, why do you not come forth?" The lady looked up and heard celestial music within the purple cloud. In an instant, fragrant light filled the terrace, perfuming her nostrils, and her heart felt at ease. Then, she felt an infant emerge from beneath her left armpit. Knowing this was no ordinary child, she instructed her maid to inform the elder.

In the blink of an eye, the Dragon King spat water to bathe the infant, and heavenly flowers rained down to serve as a mat. When the elder arrived and saw the child’s divine signs, he raised the boy on the terrace, naming him Immortal Child. A purple cloud constantly hovered above his head, his breath was fragrant, and his hair and complexion were purple. By the age of three, his nails were red as cowrie shells, his teeth like beads, his eyes bore double pupils, his arms hung past his knees, and his voice rang like a bell.

With the gaze of a tiger and the stride of a dragon, his movements were like a soaring phoenix—wherever he trod, no trace remained, and from his crown emanated a radiance of purple light.

By the age of five, he could recite ten thousand words in a day. Of all the classics, he grasped their depths entirely. His bearing was measured, his demeanor dignified. His eloquence flowed like a suspended river, his virtue akin to a dragon’s. His mystical insight reached its utmost, unmatched in the world. He honored and served his parents, often reciting the true scriptures at their knees, plumbing their profound meanings. He understood the principles of earth below, and there was no art he did not master.

At seven, wherever he wandered, he followed proper ways. His words revealed hidden truths, and his voice carried to distant lands. His virtue shone beyond the world, his fame reached the Heavenly Kings. Though offered the position of state preceptor, he declined the summons, devoting himself instead to filial piety. He attended his parents as though revering heaven, gazing upon their faces, ensuring warmth in winter and coolness in summer—never once failing in the slightest. Whenever he received fine food, he would not taste it first but always offered the freshest portions to his parents.

As his parents grew old, surpassing a hundred years, infirmity and illness assailed them. For three years, the Immortal Child tended to them day and night, enduring hardship. Moved by his sincere devotion, the heavens took pity, and the gods of the various heavens descended to his home. Earth Treasury emerged from the valley to provide sustenance. The Great Medicine True King transformed his appearance to that of an ordinary man and descended to heal their ailments, restoring them to health. They lived to the age of one hundred and thirty before passing away in their hall.

Though possessed of wisdom, he lacked steadfast cultivation and could not attain the true Dao in this lifetime. At that time, the Immortal Child cried out in grief, his sobs choking him until he fainted, reviving only to collapse again. His entire body was wracked with sorrow, tears mingling with blood, his lament shaking heaven and earth. Birds fell from the sky, beasts ceased nursing their young, bitter mists gathered, and desolate dew congealed. Earth spirits sounded their drums, and mountains echoed his sorrow. The king, upon hearing of this, sent silks as funeral offerings, while people from near and far, their faces gaunt with grief, rushed to his side. Birds carried soil in their beaks to build his parents’ tomb.

For three years, the Immortal Child prostrated himself at the burial mound, planting fine trees that spread their shade across the wilds. Birds gathered there, crying out mournfully morning and evening. After three years, he returned home, using his parents’ estate to fund meritorious deeds. He converted their residence into a Daoist sanctuary, lighting fragrant oil lamps and offering banners and flowers in worship. He swept the grounds himself, practicing the Ten Good Deeds his parents had observed in life, holding fasts and lectures, and aiding the poor and destitute.

Often in his dreams, he saw his parents, who said to him: *"In our lifetime, though we practiced the Ten Good Deeds and relieved the suffering of the poor, we lacked proper cultivation. Our lives were not firmly rooted, and we now cycle through rebirth, born into wealth and nobility. Yet by virtue of our past good deeds, we are not bound in confinement. Though we face no karmic retribution, we still bear the residual burdens of nine generations of ancestors, lingering in the Great Yin, unable to cross the Southern Palace. The fasts and offerings you have made on our behalf, though sincere, have not yet established a connection. You must perform a proper fast to deliver us and our nine generations of ancestors."*

Awakening from the dream, the Immortal Child sighed deeply, his thoughts turning to his parents, his sorrow redoubling. The next morning, he burned incense, kowtowed, and prayed, recounting the dream’s words to the Great Dao.

Then, the Jade Pure Heavenly Worthy, sensing his devotion from afar, commanded the Perfected One of Fixed Radiance, along with fourteen attendants, to descend to the southern slope of the Five Terraces. There, they manifested as the Cold-Dwelling Master, appearing in the world to respond to fasts and rescue those in peril.

Hearing that the Cold-Dwelling Master resided on the Five Terraces, the Immortal Child knew him to be a true immortal and sage. He prostrated himself and went to invite him, returning home to make offerings in his honor.

When the Immortal Child reached the southern slope of the Five Terraces, clouds and mist gathered, grasses and trees loomed dense, and fierce beasts blocked the path, preventing his advance. Leaning against a cliff, he sighed and addressed the beasts: *"I am a child of the Huang clan from the World of Abandoned Worthies. My family has long practiced the Ten Good Deeds and believed in the Great Dao, never harming living beings. I bear no grudge against you. I grieve for my parents, who have departed this world, and wish to perform meritorious deeds in their memory. There are no true masters in the world, but I have heard that a Cold-Dwelling Immortal dwells in these mountains, deeply versed in the highest principles and skilled in fasts and precepts. I have come from afar to invite him to my home for offerings. I beg you to clear the path so I may pass."*

Hearing the Immortal Child’s words, the beasts bared their fangs, unsheathed their claws, glared fiercely, licked their lips, and roared, their ferocity intensifying. The Immortal Child pondered for a long while, then thought to himself: *"I have lived without awareness of any transgression. Yet if I press forward, these beasts may devour me. If I abandon my filial resolve and fail to complete this meritorious deed, it would be unfilial. But if I do not force my way through, I will not meet the great master—this, too, would be unfilial."* Wiping his tears, he said: *"May the Great Dao have spirit and grant me distant aid. May the gods of heaven and earth take pity on me. Let the beasts open the path so I may see the great master, fulfill my meritorious deed, and realize my filial heart."*

After weeping for a long time, he suddenly heard a voice from within the clouds and mist: *"Good man, you have come for this purpose, but there is another reason as well."* The Immortal Child replied: *"I dare not seek other reasons—I have traveled through these famous mountains only for this."* The earth spirit, moved by his devotion, then addressed him: *"Your parents, in their lifetime, extended kindness even to insects. Heaven above and earth below praised them without cease. You have come for a great purpose, seeking a true master. I dare not obstruct you, but the great master has only recently descended here. We mountain spirits have not yet had our fill of gazing upon him, nor have we made offerings. For this reason, the beasts have blocked the path. You are a child of the Ten Good Deeds, supported by a hundred blessings. Though I am but a mountain spirit, I wish to hear the Dharma alongside you, a good child."*

The Immortal Child replied: *"A good guide need not be of one kind. The hidden and the manifest converge, humans and spirits are not divided. Inner and outer support one another—only then can good deeds be accomplished."*

The mountain spirit withdrew the ferocious beasts, then revealed its true form and conversed with the Immortal Child. After speaking, it led the way, and the Immortal Child followed, with the fierce beasts escorting them on either side. Ascending halfway up the mountain, they saw the Great Master of Cold Abode dwelling beneath a sheer cliff. His abode was of jade, his couch of gold, with dragons and tigers arrayed in attendance, divine beings and humans standing by. Purple clouds congealed above as a canopy, crystal trays bore incense burners, golden perfected ones held ritual tablets, and jade lads burned incense.

At that moment, the Immortal Child prostrated and rose, bowing deeply to say: *"This disciple was born under misfortune, spared not by calamity, my heart devoid of filial devotion, as heaven claimed both my parents. Above and below, I have no refuge—only the true Dao to rely upon. Entangled in worldly bonds and manifold burdens, the causes of birth and death torment my heart like poison, the pain beyond words. I wish to prepare a fast and invite you, Master, to sever the roots of my sins. I have heard of your compassion in responding to karmic conditions. Dare I humbly request your presence to witness this field of merit?"* Having spoken, he kowtowed, hoping to hear a reply.

The Perfected One declared: *"Your parents in life constantly cultivated the Ten Good Deeds, aiding the destitute and saving even insects. Their fame resounded in the heavens, their merit reached the imperial court. The Heavenly Worthy commanded me to descend. I am a Perfected One from the Cloud Palace, serving the Heavenly Worthy. For this reason, I have descended to this mountain. You are a divine child, born into the gate of the Ten Good Deeds, manifesting filial devotion as a model for the world. Though temporarily dwelling in a mortal womb, you will soon ascend as an immortal. When I once called you, it was my own self—briefly journeying to the lower world, sometimes riding the flowing clouds."*

Hearing the Perfected One’s words, the Immortal Child suddenly awakened, joy and sorrow mingling within. The Perfected One continued: *"If you wish to establish merit and hold a fast, do not proceed lightly. First return home and prepare a pure and solemn Daoist sanctuary."*

The Immortal Child bowed deeply, kowtowing to ask: *"I do not yet know the ritual forms for heavenly fasts, nor the requisite adornments for establishing a sanctuary. Pray, instruct me in their details."*

The Perfected One replied: *"The ritual forms for heavenly fasts differ from those below; the methods of the lower realm cannot compare. Immortal Child, first instruct your servants and laborers—those who perform tasks—to purify themselves of grime and grease, bathing in the five fragrances. Men and women should dwell separately, their impure breaths not intermingling. Scented mud should coat the ground, beds and seats thoroughly cleansed, all utensils and vessels for washing and drinking rinsed with fragrant water. The kitchen must be spotless, no worm-eaten firewood burned. Soap beans and floral water should be placed everywhere upon the yellow altar, fresh earth added and smoothed over. Ensure all is meticulous: vermilion pillars immaculate, lamps and candles radiant, every task executed with utmost care. Do not haggle over prices for market goods. Do not use impure wealth to fund the fast and precepts—such as ill-gotten gains or unjust acquisitions. Those lacking compassion should not enter the sanctuary or approach the fast’s kitchen. Guard these matters carefully for seven days before and after. Though the fast’s day concludes, maintain an equanimous mind, avoiding untimely or reckless eating—how much less should one tread in filth, drink wine, eat meat, indulge in wayward thoughts, or harbor unequal intentions. If, while seated in the sanctuary, one’s mind mingles with worldly defilements, such a fast will not offset transgressions. The incense smoke will be wasted, the Celestial Court will not hear, sins will remain unresolved, the sinful soul unliberated, a hundred blessings will not assist, calamities will not vanish, the true Dao will not descend, and demonic forces will respond instead."*

At that time, the mountain spirit and the host of Five Peaks deities stood attending the Perfected One. Hearing the Immortal Child’s intent to invite the Perfected One to his home to witness the field of merit, they all wished to follow the Heavenly Worthy on his journey to the human realm. Then the spirit of Mount Wutai stepped forward, bowed, and addressed the Perfected One: *"In this world, only the Immortal Child’s household, devoted to the Ten Good Deeds and harboring no enmity toward any being, is beloved by all—humans and spirits alike—who wish to aid in accomplishing his good deeds."*

The Perfected One assented. Hearing the mountain spirit’s words, the Immortal Child then asked the assembled deities: *"The supreme Great Dao is venerated in villages and hamlets. What offerings do the divine spirits require for the fast?"*

The mountain spirit replied: *"When the Great Dao descends to the world, the Five Emperors, great demons, and earth deities all attend in service, following its majestic power. They require nothing. We only wish to be your good guides, guarding and protecting the sanctuary. Should heretics, evil persons, or those with malicious intent disrupt or disturb good people—slandering, envying, flattering, or deceiving—we shall destroy them, causing their tongues to wither and retract, their bodies to erupt in leprous sores, their faces to break out in boils, their eyebrows and hair to fall out. Such external and internal retributions are called ‘Dharma protection.’ We have always aided the Dao, promoting and illuminating the true teaching—this is not merely for today."*

Hearing these words, the Immortal Child rejoiced and returned home, instructing his household to follow the Perfected One’s golden decree precisely. When his kinsfolk heard of his return, they hastened to inquire. The Immortal Child recounted all that had transpired. Hearing this, though their bodies sat still, their thoughts soared afar, pondering deeply day and night without sleep. All longed for the true Dao to descend upon their homes and sought the Immortal Child’s guidance. Then the divine instructions were revealed, and each person copied and transmitted them, teaching their households and instructing their relatives, all adhering to the precepts. Each purified their home according to their means, wholeheartedly making offerings, their thoughts reaching far as if the Perfected One stood before them.

The Immortal Child then prepared and adorned the altar sanctuary, completing every task. He returned to the mountain to welcome the Perfected One, and all wished to accompany him. At that time, one thousand two hundred people—including the Elders of Sun-and-Moon Love, Vast Heart, Great Authority, Virtue King, Life’s End, and Heart Ocean, who led the assembly—each bearing incense and flowers, followed the Immortal Child toward Mount Wutai. After twelve days, they arrived at the mountain gate, where all burned incense and bowed from afar to the mountain spirit.

In the space of a meal’s time, gazing upward toward the mountain, they beheld lions, tigers, and wolves flanking the path, while coiling dragons entwined threefold around the Perfected Lord. Earth spirits played music, immortal ministers burned incense, and the Immortal Child prostrated himself, inquiring after the Dao Lord, expressing gratitude above for his cloud-borne descent to this empty mountain, and lamenting below that the beings of the lower realms had nothing worthy to offer.

Again he bowed twice. At that moment, the six great Elders, beholding the true majesty of the Perfected One, all lost themselves in awe, their limbs trembling, joy and fear intermingling. They prostrated without pause, sweat streaming like water, gazing upon his golden countenance until words failed them. Overcome with reverence and dread, they stood unsteadily, unable to remain still.

Then the mountain spirit spoke: "Noble Immortal Child, you have returned once more. But who are these six elders? Do they possess roots of goodness from past cultivation, or have they only now turned toward the Way? I fear their hearts lack constancy, their resolve is not truly firm—what brings them here? Moreover, their minds have not yet merged with the true, their bodies remain impure and worldly. They defile my sacred precincts; their mortal stench is unfit to meet the Perfected Lord. Though I am but the spirit of this renowned mountain, my form is free of impurity, my shape fixed. Though I cannot embody the Dao, I have always served as an outer guardian to the Perfected Lord, and I do not wish for the foul and base to offend the true."

The Immortal Child replied: "These six elders are my kin in the Dharma. Hearing of my invitation to the Dao, their hearts rejoiced in support. Though they may not practice the Ten Virtues perfectly, they bear no grave transgressions. Though they dwell in the world, their hearts are good."

Hearing of the true Dao yet never having beheld it with their own eyes, their distant longing and yearning thoughts are truly pitiable. Upon hearing the Immortal Child’s words, the mountain spirit addressed the elders once more: "If what the Immortal Child says is true, compose yourselves and steady your hearts—there is no need for fear. Contemplate the orthodox Dharma and cultivate in accordance with its teachings."

Then the elders bowed and withdrew.

*Thus concludes Scroll Five of the Supreme Great Dao Jade Clarity Scripture*

*Scroll Six of the Supreme Great Dao Jade Clarity Scripture*
*Chapter Fifteen: The Luminous Numinous*

At that time, in the Southern Prosperity Palace, there was an upper immortal named Luminous Numinous, accompanied by fifteen thousand attendants—all of whom had first received deliverance in their mortal forms at the Assembly of Dragons, cultivated the Dao to attain sagehood, and possessed the power of compassion. Their bodies had achieved the six penetrations, allowing them to roam without obstruction, and their lifespans were fixed, like refined true gold, immutable and unchanging. They ascended in sovereign freedom, their wisdom vast and immeasurable, their bodies and minds unbound, like empty space itself.

On the fifteenth day of the seventh month, they ascended to the Great Empyrean, entering the Jade Clarity Heaven to pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy in the Cloud Palace. Prostrating before the Dao, they inquired after his well-being and spoke thus:

"Though I am but dust, defiled and base, I have presumptuously undertaken the task of salvation. In the past, I was undeservingly favored by the great Dao’s compassion, lifted and granted longevity, and bestowed with the supreme Dharma. From that time onward, I have cultivated in accordance with the precepts, and my hopes have borne fruit. By right, I should attend upon the Heavenly Worthy morning and night, ever ready to serve. Yet I remain bound to the foul, decaying forms of the mortal realm below, and the path to heaven is long and distant, beyond the reach of ordinary beings—thus I have failed in my duty to attend you. Each day, I yearn for the azure clouds above and revere the purple gates of your compassion, but my person is humble and my Dao shallow, leaving my heart’s desire unfulfilled. This sorrow has lingered through kalpas, and my longing remains unassuaged. Unable to bear the sincerity of my devotion, I have ventured through clouds and mist to brave your august presence, that I might behold your sacred countenance and offer my reverent homage."

With these words, he prostrated himself again, overcome with joy.

The Heavenly Worthy, desiring to respond, addressed the immortal, saying: "The Dao of generation and transformation accords with spontaneity by principle. I have never deliberately bestowed anything, nor do I stir beings with emotion—how then could I have given birth to you? Good man, just as when a person loves extinction, the Dao has no mind to oppose their inclination and give them life; so too, when your heart cherishes life, the Dao has no mind to defy your inclination and diminish you. If one follows the inclinations of the myriad beings to their utmost, fulfilling their aspirations for ascent or descent, then in the meeting of circumstances, all is spontaneously accomplished. The Dao abides at the ultimate mystery, thus it can flow with things like water—whether in generation or extinction, the Dao cannot oppose it. If something is born yet does not perish, my Dao, though without mind, can diminish it; if something perishes yet does not arise, the Dao, though without mind, can give it life. That you have obtained life now is due to your own karmic power of aspiration—the Dao, without mind, gives life to you. Hearts turn toward or away, each upholding its own resolve; though the power of the Dao exists, it cannot precede them. When you first aspired to study the Dao, it arose from your own heart—self-cause, self-effect—it is not something I know. This is what is called the spontaneous Dao, the mind of spontaneity in its obscurity."

At that moment, the assembled immortals, hearing the words of the Heavenly Worthy, dared not offer any reply.

The Heavenly Worthy continued: "The path to heaven is long and distant—why have you come here?"

The immortal answered: "I came to offer my gratitude and to behold the subtle and wondrous supreme Dharma."

The Heavenly Worthy declared: "The supreme Dao blends and transforms all, indistinguishable as grains of dust, like an embryo yet undifferentiated, akin to primordial chaos without origin. It discards wisdom and abandons knowledge, neither obscure nor manifest, boundless as the cosmic waters—how then could there be anything wondrous for you to behold? The supreme Dao, whether in transformation, arising, ceasing, receiving, upholding, dwelling, raising, or revealing—when shown to the multitude, it becomes a matter of doubt. There is no such thing. The supreme Dao is also without subtlety or wonder—profoundly empty and still, self-awakening and awakening others, without mind to observe or discriminate. This and that—how could there be anything wondrous for you to behold? Without form or appearance, it is like empty space, without inside or outside.

"Good man, if you wish to behold it, go to the northeast of the Cloud Palace, a distance of as many miles as there are motes of dust in a great land. Within the Great Void, three supreme perfected beings are cultivating the supreme Dao there in the emptiness. Now they have entered the Great Samādhi of Congealing Spirit, which has already endured for nine hundred million great kalpas. Next, they will enter the Great Samādhi of Forgetting Form for eight hundred million great kalpas, then the Great Samādhi of the Six Voids for seven hundred million great kalpas, then the Great Samādhi of Unobstructedness for six hundred million great kalpas, then the Great Samādhi of the Great Void for five hundred million great kalpas. Afterward, they will enter the Samādhi of Penetrating Wisdom for one million great kalpas, then the Samādhi of Generative Wisdom for one hundred thousand great kalpas. In the future, they will descend to observe the thirty-seven heavens, then wander through the realms of mortals. Together, they will be called the Later Sage Heavenly Worthy of Great Peace. Leading their retinue of billions upon billions of followers, they will expound the Dharma of Non-Action to deliver sentient beings. At that time, the number of those who attain the Dao will be as countless as motes of dust. If you wish to behold it, behold the subtle and wondrous Dharma of this Heavenly Worthy."

Then, the immortal, hearing the Heavenly Worthy’s instruction, bowed in joy and reverence, taking leave of the Heavenly Worthy. At that time, the assembled immortals together mounted auspicious clouds and drifted away through the sky. In an instant, they arrived at the Great Void and saw from afar the three perfected beings in the midst of emptiness—subtly veiled in the vast obscurity, resting within the purple clouds, faintly shimmering above the radiant rosy dawn. The cinnabar heavens wove their patterns, yellow essence formed their couch; the three qi congealed into nectar, the two luminaries held their brilliance. The Great Void served as their window, the empty realm as their casement. Before the beginning of the embryo, at the primordial origin of chaos, they absorbed qi and concealed their true nature, silent and remote, utterly devoid of form. The ten thousand transformations had not yet taken root; their spirit-bodies were empty and serene. The five flowers secretly bloomed, the three palaces nurtured the true; the six viscera congealed spirit, the three hun souls did not float, the seven po souls did not wander. Spirit and essence remained unmoved, true qi did not flow. Serene and limpid, they abided without seeking anything.

At that moment, the immortals, beholding this subtlety and wonder, descended from their auspicious clouds. Treading lightly upon the mist, they drifted through the void and approached, prostrating themselves and drinking in the qi, not daring to speak. Kneeling in the profound emptiness, they lost track of kalpas. Fixing their minds on observing the wondrous, they forgot their own bodies. In an instant, the three perfected beings vanished—the radiant canopy revealed nothing of their whereabouts. After a long while, the empty canopy suddenly disappeared, leaving only the luminous qi, faintly aglow. After another long while, the three perfected beings suddenly emerged from the void into the formless, now present, now absent, their breath stirring wind and clouds, now merging, now parting. After a long while, they vanished utterly, their forms and qi completely gone. After yet another long while, the numinous wind shook the eight directions, the divine qi surged in the four quarters, blowing and fanning, now manifest, now hidden. After another long while, they arose without movement, accomplished without effort. The three dawns spread their clarity, the ten thousand transformations secretly sprouted. The roots of numinous potency were planted in the purple essence, the spirit-souls dispersed into the cloud chambers. They stirred the dust of emptiness in the formless, flowed primordial harmony into the vast azure, exhaled the myriad qi into the thriving growth, spread true essence into the ten thousand sprouts. They extended their divine feet into the numinous net, firmly grasped the original infant. Emerging from the Six Voids yet without accomplishment, they became the window through which the multitude of beings peered. Neither sinking nor floating, they abided in emptiness; neither moving nor still, they traversed transformation. Form without form, life without life. Dwelling in darkness yet luminous, dwelling in obscurity yet bright. Turning inward to reflect, the wondrous body was without form. Eternally abiding, unchanging—how could it be altered? The mind, profoundly still, lodged without disturbance. Neither governing nor dividing, neither teaching nor commanding, neither wise nor foolish, neither commanding nor acting. Serene in the use of the Dao, without emotional contention, they cast aside mechanism and released defilement, their empty minds naturally mirroring."

Sealing cavities and blocking crevices, withdrawing sight and reversing hearing—though influences and echoes were manifold, the centered mind remained unchanged. Obscured within the Great Void, form knew no realm of death.

At that moment, the immortal, beholding this divine transformation, lost all five senses. Though eons passed, they remained oblivious, sunk in darkness. Suddenly, they saw the Perfected One enter the flux of life and awakening, only then realizing how wind and clouds shift and all things stir into being.

Thereupon, the immortal prostrated in midair, vowing vows amid the clouds. Though sustained by the power of the Dao, joy and fear left them unable to find peace. Then the Three Perfected Ones, moved by the immortals, discerned their intent and, with a thunderous whisper, addressed them: "Why have you come, enduring the hardships of the cloud-path? You and I share the same Dao—what is there to observe beyond?"

The immortal dared not speak, only pleading for compassion and the gift of deliverance. Then the Most Peaceful Dao Lord said to them: "Why not entrust your spirit and qi to the fleeting and boundless, surrendering to nature amid being and nonbeing? Follow union and separation, yield to the flow of change. In an instant, drift through emptiness—your body does not abide. Abide in formlessness, silence your voice, and cleanse your thoughts. Be vast as the endless void, your spirit obscure and unlocated, mirroring emptiness and reflecting the sky. Ingest qi and conceal the true. Merge with the numinous root of purple essence, conceal your soul in the cloud-chamber, dissolve the light dust in the Great Beginning, and still primordial harmony in the vast heavens. Let things arise on their own, follow the true through darkness and light. Light as the edge of a cloud-cliff, you may remain unmoving yet ever in motion; dwelling in inner emptiness, you stand as if an infant yet unborn. Neither listening nor peering, you follow the flow of feeling. Neither releasing nor grasping, neither full nor empty—obliterated yet boundless, this is called the Mysterious Sameness."

At that moment, the immortal, hearing the True Lord’s words as if in a void, uttered a faint assent—yet before the echo faded, they looked up to see the Perfected One already ascending to the farthest reaches of emptiness. They could not catch up, could not speak, could not be heard. Form entered the Great Nonbeing, qi dissolved like floating clouds. Their heart filled with longing and devotion, they wished to attend and follow. Half their sincere intent was voiced: "I am unattached and unbound—why should I linger? You have not yet wholly forgotten, riding clouds and commanding qi."

Just as the immortal was about to speak, they saw the Supreme Perfected One soaring through the void, swifter than a shooting star, faster than lightning. The immortal pondered for a long while, then suddenly beheld the True Lord’s golden countenance in the dark, its radiance pervading all forms, drifting like mist in the void—beyond sight or hearing, yet knowing the subtlety of divine transformation.

Then the immortal and their retinue stood in the void, their hearts empty as they gazed upward, longing to grasp the essential truth and follow the Most Peaceful Heavenly Worthy into the lower realms. Their thoughts and wishes remained unwavering. The Heavenly Worthy, moved by this, spoke to them from the darkness: "The supreme Dao of all laws is natural. Though divine power and transformation follow the mind, the mind is never wearied; though they follow the body, the body does not act. This is called *non-doing that does*, *non-acting that acts*. *Non-acting that acts*—there is nothing it does not accomplish; *non-doing that does*—there is nothing it does not fulfill. If one *does* in order to *do*, the doing is incomplete; if one *acts* in order to *act*, the acting is not universal. Not enslaved to the mind, not laboring the body—the mind, unburdened, becomes numinous; the body, unwearied, brings forth life. When life and numinosity merge, there is nothing that does not come to be. This is called *not acting yet accomplishing*, *not doing yet generating*. The Dao is ever without doing, yet there is nothing it does not do. The root of the Primal Chaos, its principle exhausted here.

Good man, I too have no mind in performing these divine transformations. I merely follow the turning of descent and union, harmonizing the qi of life, establishing the Dharma-gate for all sentient beings—it cannot be otherwise. You should now know that the supreme Dao, though it becomes the dust of the world, passes through heart and mouth. The way of compassion is such by nature. Just as you, in the past, dwelled in the dust and encountered the great Dao, widely establishing ferries and crossings, nurturing and embracing all, delivering the withered and decayed—this too is the great Dao bestowing the kindness of a compassionate mother. It cradles, nourishes, feeds, shelters, and teaches in myriad ways. Though it does not labor, it too passes through the heart.

The Dao of Heaven is vast, yet its responses are subtle. It does not move without being stirred, nor has it ever been known to refuse a plea. The Dao is like the sea, the destination of all streams; the Dao is like the sky, the support of all things.

Good man, the days I do not wander are few. In the blink of ten thousand eons, time has already passed. Before this, I must ascend to the Great Luo above to pay homage to the Primal Worthy. Then I will traverse the heavens to address the host of Perfected Ones. Though you are high immortals, your method of roaming has not yet reached the highest heavens. For now, return to the Southern Florescence Palace. After a hundred thousand eons, I will descend to the Southern Florescence, and you shall see me then."

Thereupon, the high immortal received the teaching of the Most Peaceful Heavenly Worthy, bowed in farewell, and departed for the Southern Florescence Palace. Then the Heavenly Worthy, with the fleeting life of mortals, ascended to the Great Luo to pay homage to the Primal Worthy. They met in silence, communing through spirit alone. Then they ascended above the Great Luo to pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of the Void, also in silence. The Most High remained in profound stillness, the realm of the Dao silent and unmoving—no homage, no speech.

Then they entered the realm of the Great Void, where nothing was to be seen, and the Most Peaceful Heavenly Worthy too was formless. After what seemed three eons, they drifted down like a faint breath of mist. Thus the Three Worthies ascended through the twelve thousand heavens above, formless and silent. Then they entered the twelve thousand heavens of the middle, where form existed but no words were spoken. Then they entered the twelve thousand heavens below, where speech at last began.

Later, the Heavenly Worthy arrived at the Jade Clarity Heaven, where within the Cloud Palace they saw the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion. They spoke of the turning of the kalpa’s days, the time having come to labor in the transformation of the Dao.

The Heavenly Worthy of Great Peace replied, "For this cause, I ascended to pay homage to the True Thearchs, roughly completing the circuit."

At that time, the three sacred bodies of the Heavenly Worthy of Great Peace shared a single seat. After another ten eons had passed, they sat in silent stillness with the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion.

Then the Supreme Immortal of Southern Prosperity beheld the true radiance of the Heavenly Worthy shining afar—unlike anything ordinary. From the Jade Clarity Heaven downward, countless disciples who had attained the Dao—upper, middle, and lower immortals in the hundreds of millions—each bearing offerings, incense, flowers, banners, canopies, and performing various musical arts, floated through the air to come and celebrate the Heavenly Worthy of Great Peace, while also paying homage to the True Thearch of Great Compassion. They burned incense, scattered flowers, chanted praises, and played music, encircling the Cloud Palace for seven days and seven nights. The heavens rained blossoms, fragrant smoke congealed in the void, jeweled forests bloomed with flowers to receive the sweet dew. Golden mountains surged forth, jade nectar flowed in streams, dragon mushrooms rose in rosy clouds, hidden herbs lifted mist, dragons hummed in the empty sky, immortal mists veiled the heavens, white tigers sang in chorus, and gentle winds brushed the dust. The immortals surrounded the four quarters, while the true lords arranged the banquet.
