Then all the immortals descended from the floating clouds, arrayed in solemn dignity, and at once prostrated themselves, kneeling to gaze upward. They beheld the Heavenly Worthies each seated in their three palaces, draped in rosy clouds, their spirit-awareness like that of infants. Before their gaze could fully take them in, the Worthies had already entered formlessness. The three palaces’ purple clouds arose in the empty sky, and after a long while, suddenly one Heavenly Worthy was seen sitting alone in a palace. After another long interval, two Heavenly Worthies were seen seated side by side in attendance. Sometimes they flickered between presence and absence, now merging three into one, now scattering one into three—emerging from being, entering non-being, their bodies never abiding in constancy.

Then the immortals bowed their heads for a long time. The Illuminating Immortal of Southern Prosperity’s Upper Palace, the Radiant Spirit Immortal, rose into the empty sky and spoke: "Long ago in the Great Void, I beheld the Heavenly Worthy and stood in attendance through countless eons in the empty sky, never wavering in devotion. I was undeservingly favored with your grace, shown the appointed time of meeting, and lifted beyond my station. Since taking leave, my sincerity has remained as it was before."

The lower realms have known repeated cycles of decay and renewal. My heart, ever earnest in its devotion, has remained as parched and hungry as ever. Suddenly, I beheld the true light shining from afar—no different from its original radiance.

When the Heavenly Worthy had completed this round of affairs, he led the assembled immortals to purify the celestial court of its dust and defilement. Again, they bowed twice. The Heavenly Worthy declared: "I know your heart; no further words are needed. Each of you, return to your seats."

Then the immortals bowed once more and, obeying the command, resumed their places. The Heavenly Worthy spoke again: "I have no words of my own, nor do I recall what is in my heart. Yet through the empty echo of response, I mysteriously meet the emptiness of your devotion. Do you understand?"

The immortals replied: "We humbly receive your instruction and dare not fail to comprehend."

The Heavenly Worthy acknowledged this. Then the great assembly sat in silence for a hundred eons, utterly still. At that time, from the cloud palaces in the four directions of the mysterious void, there arose the sound of a spontaneously generated four-character hymn in Sanskrit. Its meaning was elusive, flickering like the wind stirring empty strings, or jade trees yielding celestial tones—harmonious and flowing, its words and principles subtle and wondrous, beyond full comprehension.

The assembled immortals dared not gaze or listen directly; only in their hearts did they retain fragments, at times grasping half a verse. Its text read:

The灵芝 grows rootless, the origin of all transformations.
Within, the seven *po* congeal; the three *hun* are masterfully bound.
The twenty-four Perfected Ones enter and exit without gate.
The essence of the dark and obscure flickers, elusive and without emotion.
It endures through kalpas of existence and decay, born with the ebb and flow of *qi*.
Externally, it solidifies the undifferentiated primordial; internally, it nurtures the seven meridians.
The five spirits plant blossoms; the Three Terraces spread their glory.
The Purple Pass and the White Youth reverse form to return to infancy.
They ascend on clouds, gallop through mists to manifest in the void.
Within, the Jade Perfected One is named Divine Lord.
To his left stands Wu Ying; to his right, Bai Yuan guards.
The Dark Beast halts behind; the Vermilion Phoenix flanks before.
Above floats an emerald canopy; below surges a golden lotus.
Fragrant clouds congeal in the void; sweet dew flows without end.
Used without exhaustion, its source never exhausted.

At that time, the assembled immortals heard the inner scripture of the celestial hymn from the void above, yet could not retain it. After a hundred kalpas, the Illustrious Spirit Immortal lifted his gaze to the Heavenly Worthy’s countenance and saw five-colored fragrant clouds issuing from the Heavenly Worthy’s mouth, ascending into the Great Void. Then, the Illustrious Spirit Immortal rose with the assembly, bowed, and inquired: "We do not presume to ask why, after the Heavenly Worthy sat in silence for a hundred kalpas without sound, fragrant clouds now issue from your mouth. We wish to know the Heavenly Worthy’s purpose and cause—pray, distinguish and reveal it to enlighten the unenlightened."

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "The fragrant clouds from my mouth respond to the Golden Portal Sovereign of Later Saints. I previously descended among the Four Heavens, and the appointed time has now arrived. At this moment, each sage fulfills their destined task. When this occurs, Heaven and Earth also respond. When Heaven responds, the Three Luminaries herald auspices, and five-colored radiant clouds form a double wheel. When Earth responds, the Five Peaks manifest omens, the Earth Treasury releases its store, and gold and jade reveal their forms. Such are the signs: the Golden Portal Sovereign will soon descend to the world, though the exact day remains unappointed. At this time, I too observe these events."

Then, the Illustrious Spirit Immortal further inquired about the origin and cause of the inner scripture of the celestial hymn. The Heavenly Worthy of Great Peace addressed the immortal: "Do you not know? The Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion governs within this palace of the void, where true *qi* produces this sound—the spontaneous celestial scripture, numinous verses, and precious texts—rarely encountered. Even later sages and immortals who hear it do not comprehend. This sound harmonizes to generate spirit and regulate the true *qi*—a path unknown to the common world. I know your heart seeks to record what is not yours to record. You and these immortals are not yet destined to receive and uphold the spontaneous inner scripture of the celestial hymn."

The Illustrious Spirit Immortal replied to the Heavenly Worthy: "This disciple, though unworthy, shall recite and contemplate the scripture. I humbly beg your pardon and permission to receive and uphold it." The Heavenly Worthy said: "That you have heard it is your karmic destiny; the Dharma ordains your attainment of truth. Guard it well, and do not recklessly disseminate it. Cultivate it in silence, and your learning will not betray others. If you leak it, calamity arises; if you keep it secret, blessings accrue."

Then, the entire assembly rose and bowed, receiving the inner scripture. In that moment, within the void above, cloud-seal script appeared in the empty clarity—each character a *zhang* in size, with eight corners trailing radiance, glowing brilliantly. The immortals then inscribed the jade script anew, each treasuring a copy and concealing it in a brocade pouch. At that time, the cloud-seal script lingered in the void, never fading. The Heavenly Worthy declared: "Where true *qi* covers, the longer it endures, the more abundant it becomes. If you cultivate it, you too shall be thus—your lifespan boundless, your form renewed with each day. What the highest Perfected Ones treasure is not bestowed upon lesser immortals. Those whose Dao-number is insufficient—how much less the common world?"

The Heavenly Worthy addressed the Illustrious Spirit: "Know that the supreme Dao in all matters must not be recklessly divulged—how much less the celestial scripture? Treasure it, and do not transmit the inner scripture downward." The minds of the common world cannot attain this.

Then, the Illustrious Spirit Immortal bowed and knelt, addressing the Heavenly Worthy: "Though the common world below dwells in impurity, there are those who know the Dao and cultivate to attain truth. Might such a person receive transmission?" The Heavenly Worthy replied: "Such people are as rare as one in a hundred million. How can you discern one who harmonizes with truth?"

The Illustrious Spirit answered: "In your disciple’s Southern Prosperity Palace, there are records of true immortals. At the Three Primes and Eight Festivals, the lower offices report to the upper, presenting merits and transgressions without omission." The Heavenly Worthy said: "The minds of the common world below are difficult to distinguish. Some feign cultivation of my Dao, concealing impurity and harboring deceit, their hearts seeking external gains, their resolve unstable. Examine their faults, scrutinize their spirits. Without this, purity and turbidity remain indistinguishable. Some pursue fame and profit, clinging to the gate of mystery, peering at the lower currents, prizing only extensive learning. If you wish to teach the common world, you must clarify such people."

Then, the Illustrious Spirit Immortal, not yet understanding the sagely decree, further inquired: "I do not presume to ask how to scrutinize their spirits—pray, reveal it, for my heart delights in hearing it." The Heavenly Worthy said: "Within each person’s body resides a spirit, stationed in the heart. Whatever the heart desires, the spirit already knows. When the body intends evil, the spirit does not follow. The yin traitors within the body—the *hun* are not restrained, the *po* are not controlled—at the Three Primes and Eight Festivals, they report to the Supreme Emperor. Through this, one may know. If a person possesses hidden virtue, the three *hun* do not depart, the seven *po* do not scatter; good spirits assist, and heavenly soldiers guard. Through this, they naturally harmonize with the Dao.

"Good man, the supreme great Dao knows without being spoken. I fear you have not yet grasped this—you must deeply guard against it and not lightly disseminate it. Good man, you have encountered me in the Great Void across countless kalpas. Now, you have again met me and heard the wondrous Dharma. In no long time, you shall naturally comprehend all Dharmas. The hearts of truth and falsehood will be as clear as if before your eyes, with nothing left un-discerned. This is the thorough penetration of body and mind with the Dao, enabling unobstructed understanding."

Then, the assembled immortals, hearing the Heavenly Worthy’s compassion, rejoiced among themselves. They bowed and knelt, each commanding their attendants to perform music in celebration.

A thousand tones harmonized in resonance, the Dharma drums pierced the heavens. At that moment, floating rosy clouds drifted and swirled, incense smoke coiled through the void, flying canopies wheeled in the sky, long banners danced in the wind, dragons chanted across the distant heavens, phoenixes sang in the empty courtyard. Heaven and earth trembled; the two luminaries hung like wheels. The divine toad emerged from the moon, treading upon the numinous void, while the sun-crow flapped its wings and soared through the sky.

At this time, thirty-seven celestial disciples from the lower realms, having attained immortality upon witnessing these auspicious signs, simultaneously ascended into the void, rising to the Jade Purity Heaven like intersecting clouds. The Heavenly Worthy of Great Peace addressed Zhao Ling, saying: "Immortals, regardless of rank, can all move heaven and earth, command the myriad spirits. You should know the inconceivable power of the Dao, so that all lower immortals may hear and understand."

Then, the thirty-seven heavens’ immortals—countless millions—filled the Cloud Palace. They burned incense, scattered flowers, and each declared their original vows. The Heavenly Worthy, perceiving their intentions, entered the great samadhi of compassion, gathering their minds and inscribing them into the Register of the Numinous. There, they merged with the Dao of the Nine Natural Transformations, which manifested as the Nine Heavens. Within them, the Nine Qi coalesced, forming the Nine Palaces. The Three Worthies then divided and resided within the Nine Palaces, each seated upon a nine-dragon throne. At that moment, they were named the Perfected of the Nine Palaces.

The Lord of the Great Peace led the immortals into the Nine Palaces. The Heavenly Worthy then expounded the Dao of the Nine Immortals to them, aligning above with the Nine Heavens, at the center with the Nine Palaces, mysteriously corresponding to the Nine Qi, and below governing the Nine Springs—able to enter the unobstructed. This is what is meant by "one generates three, three generates nine, nine times nine is eighty-one," presiding over the law of primordial generation, endlessly revolving. Those who study hereafter, able to generate and perfect, will abide in the primordial and naturally attain perfection.

The assembled immortals, beholding this subtlety, dared not speak, each knowing they had thus received life, unaware that the Heavenly Worthy was now revealing it. With earnest devotion and humble reverence, they harbored shame, not knowing how to express their gratitude. The Heavenly Worthy, anticipating their thoughts, addressed them: "The supreme great Dao requires nothing; why speak further? My body sits in the Dao-field, my spirit communes with the myriad emperors. I am no ordinary being, yet I receive empty words. If one claims to have attained the Dao, even lowly ghosts and commoners—except for the mute—have never been without speech, yet cannot attain it. I do not say that when the great Dao responds to the mundane, all words are entirely absent. My true body is before you, and you are no ordinary beings. For this reason, you fail to comprehend here, seeking answers with your minds. Listen in silence: the supreme great Dao’s Dharma requires no words of gratitude."

The immortals, receiving the Heavenly Worthy’s teaching, each bowed their heads, contemplating the grace of the Dao. After a long while, Zhao Ling, the Supreme Immortal of the Southern Prosperity Palace, prostrated and said: "Formerly, I received the Heavenly Worthy’s decree to descend into the world, traveling the ten directions. The appointed time has not yet come. I humbly request the Heavenly Worthy to briefly descend to the Southern Prosperity Palace, if only for a fleeting moment, so that my long-held sincerity across ten thousand kalpas may be fulfilled in this wish." The assembly bowed their heads, prostrating for a long time, awaiting the response.

The Heavenly Worthy declared: "I have already taken leave of the Great Emperor and bid farewell to all the Worthies. Upon returning to the Cloud Palace, my karmic conditions will be complete. If you wish to invite me, I shall not refuse your heart." The immortals, hearing the Heavenly Worthy’s decree, rejoiced immeasurably.

The Heavenly Worthy continued: "You immortals should now depart. The Cloud Palace has always been serene; it is not fitting to linger amidst the defilements of the world. When the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion of the Cloud Palace formerly manifested in the world, there were brief teachings. Now, returning to the Cloud Palace, I revert to emptiness and non-being. I have come here for the sake of the Heavenly Worthy’s great compassion, to look upon those who study hereafter. You immortals should understand this."

Then, Zhao Ling, the Supreme Immortal, again inquired of the Heavenly Worthy: "May I ask when the Heavenly Worthy will come again?" The Heavenly Worthy replied: "Before long, after twenty thousand kalpas, I shall soon return."

At that time, the immortals assented, bowing twice before taking leave of the Heavenly Worthy. They then bid farewell to the True Emperor of Great Compassion, prostrated, and withdrew. Looking up at the high seat, they no longer saw the Heavenly Worthy. Gazing around, they saw the Three Sages had also entered the void. Only the Cloud Palace remained, silent and empty, with a faint fragrant breeze stirring and incense smoke lingering. Flying canopies hovered in the sky, banners stood in the void, celestial music fell silent, and all sounds ceased.

The immortals, witnessing the majestic spiritual power of the supreme Dao—suddenly manifesting from being and returning to non-being—lingered for a long while, lost and without support. They boarded their cloud chariots and followed one another back. Then, all the immortals accompanied Zhao Ling, the Supreme Immortal, returning to the Southern Prosperity Palace, where they cultivated the *Heavenly Scriptures of the Hidden Life* and the *Precious Canon*. After eighteen years, they all attained the true Dao. For twenty thousand kalpas, they awaited with empty hearts.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy, from within the Cloud Palace, saw from afar that the immortals had attained the true Dao. From the Cloud Palace, the Heavenly Worthy’s great compassion manifested his left hand. At that moment, the thirty-three heavens opened their gates. All the celestial beings saw the Heavenly Worthy’s left hand, like a white rainbow spanning the great void, its five fingernails emitting five-colored radiance that illuminated the Southern Prosperity Palace.

The Perfected ones all prostrated and bowed twice to the left hand. Within its light, they saw from afar the Heavenly Worthy in the emptiness of the Cloud Palace, holding the Heavenly Script’s left tally, its single character radiating eight-colored light. The Perfected ones leapt with joy, knowing the Heavenly Worthy had come from afar to bestow his seal. The Dao is not dual in its words; seeing his left hand in the Cloud Palace, it remained for ten thousand kalpas before withdrawing back into the Cloud Palace. The light, likewise, after ten thousand kalpas, followed the hand and returned.

After twenty thousand kalpas, the Perfected ones trod upon the void and stood in emptiness, gazing afar toward the upper realms. At dawn on the first day of the first month, they saw a three-colored radiance of qi descending straight from the rising sun in the east into the Southern Prosperity Palace, coiling and swirling throughout the great void. The fragrance of the wind was intensely rich, unlike anything ordinary. For ninety thousand years, this occurred every morning without fail. Each dawn, the Perfected ones bowed their heads to receive the qi, performing ninety cycles of scripture recitation. After thirty years, the numinous qi permeated their bodies, congealing within, then emerged from behind their necks and surged upward into the heavens—azure, crimson, and white—never to fade again.

After another twenty thousand kalpas, at dawn on the first day of the seventh month, they suddenly beheld the Three Sacred Manifestations of the Heavenly Worthy of Great Peace seated within the threefold qi. Then, the Heavenly Worthy emitted his primordial radiance from the heart, at first faint as a firefly. In an instant, it suffused his entire form, inside and out, illuminating the Southern Prosperity Upper Palace. For a long while, the Heavenly Worthy’s Dao-body became like light itself, undifferentiated, merging with the heavens in boundless brilliance—like the full sun, yet without scorching heat. Its splendor dazzled the eyes, its rays piercing all, neither dim nor excessive. This endured for a thousand kalpas. The Perfected immortals, abiding within this light, rejoiced and delighted, their forms reverting to youth, their complexions like those of children. They trod upon the void as if treading on light clouds. Such was the power of the true radiance. Though countless kalpas passed, their hearts knew no sorrow, for they found joy in the Dao, forgetting all else.

After a thousand kalpas, the Three Sacred Manifestations suddenly saw within the light an innumerable host of Perfected immortals—myriad millions—gazing upward, standing in long obeisance, silent and reverent. The Heavenly Worthy knew their hearts. These immortals had all attained great penetration, possessing divine communion; they also knew the Heavenly Worthy’s compassion for the multitude, his broad opening of the Dharma-gate, and his merciful perfection of all beings. Unobstructed, they wielded the powers of the Dao—able to perform seven transformations and nine transmutations, perceiving all dharmas with clarity. Yet they knew not the Heavenly Worthy’s thousandfold, myriad transformations, his boundless mastery, his power to turn others’ mortal forms into Dharma-bodies in but a moment. Above heaven and below earth, he alone was revered among the ten thousand Ways. His divine power was peerless, beyond all conception.

**Chapter Sixteen: The Subjugation of Demons**

At that time, from the six desire-realms of the form and formless worlds, there came eighty-four thousand heretical immortals of the six rebellious factions, fond of debate and contention. They often vied in divine powers in the lower realms, skilled in illusions and transformations, their hearts arrogant and proud. They styled themselves great masters, roaming the three realms alone, possessing the five penetrations, and living for eighty thousand great kalpas. Hearing that the Heavenly Worthy had descended to the Southern Prosperity Upper Palace, they led their followers, riding upon lions, and after six minor kalpas, arrived at the Southern Prosperity Palace, desiring to see the Heavenly Worthy and compare their divine powers, testing their Daoist arts.

The Heavenly Worthy, already knowing their intent, remained silent and unmoving with the great assembly, seated upon a dragon throne seven ren above the earth. Then, the eighty-four thousand heretical immortals arrived all at once. Gazing up at the sacred assembly, they felt no reverence, nor did they recognize the ranks of the Heavenly Worthy of Great Peace and the true immortals. They sought to ascend the high seat, yet none could mount it.

Among the heretical immortals was a great immortal named Rābila, the foremost leader of the heretical host. Changing countenance, he declared: “I am the great master of the three realms, uniquely enlightened to fortune and misfortune. I have heard of the supreme Great Dao—yet among this great assembly, who is the most revered?”

Then, the Heavenly Worthy pointed to the Illustrious Numinous Perfected One, designating him as the Heavenly Worthy. Thereupon, Rābila cried out harshly: “Do you possess the Dao?”

The Illustrious Numinous One replied: “I have no Dao.”

Rābila said: “If you have no Daoist arts, by what mysterious method do you claim this high seat? I wish to sit and discourse—let me ascend at once.”

The Illustrious Numinous One answered: “This high seat is named the Seat of the Great Dao’s Compassion. Even if you exhaust your strength to climb it, you will not ascend. If you force your way up, you will never succeed.”

Rābila asked: “Why can I not ascend?”

The Illustrious Numinous One replied: “You are a straight-legged demon of the lower form and desire realms, falsely assuming the guise of an immortal.”

Then, all the heretical immortals raised their legs, only to find them rigid and unbending, unable to flex. Even when they sought to sit upon the ground, they could not.

At that moment, Rābila exhausted his divine power, raising his voice to chant spells. His followers—eighty-four thousand in number—threw themselves from the sky, their movements synchronized with the urgency of his incantation. Then, Rābila once more summoned all his spiritual might, seeking to shake heaven and earth; his disciples all collapsed to the ground, rolling and flipping uncontrollably, unable to cease.

Yet Rābila’s heart remained unconvinced. He demanded to test his art of invisibility against the Perfected One, Illustrious Numinous. The Perfected One, moved by great compassion, granted his request.

Rābila said: “You conceal yourself first.”

At once, the assembly of sagely beings in the palace vanished entirely. The eighty-four thousand heretical immortals, though they soared through the air arm in arm, could perceive nothing. Returning to their original place, they marveled at what they had never before witnessed. In but a moment, the great assembly reappeared, as if they had never moved at all.

The Lord of the Dao, Illustrious Numinous, then commanded Rābila to conceal himself along with his followers. Rābila strained every ounce of his might and transformed into a mass of black qi. The Perfected One exhaled once, and the eighty-four thousand demons collapsed like lifeless corpses, senseless and inert. After a long while, the Lord of the Dao gently breathed upon them, and they revived as one, rising to repent their errors, their faith now turned toward submission.

Then, the Lord of the Dao intoned the Chapter of the Whisk for Subduing Demons with compassionate power, causing the eighty-four thousand heretical immortals to hover between life and death. After a long while, when the demons had revived and caught their breath, they became aware of their bodies reeking of decay and gasping for air. Bowing their heads before the Dao, they spoke: “We do not know by what method the Heavenly Worthy has cultivated, that his divine power is thus. How long is his lifespan?”

The Lord of the Dao replied: “I cultivate the supreme Dao, the practice of compassion, forbearance, and humility. My body knows no realm of death, and my divine power is unconstrained.”

The Lord of the Dao, testing them with his great compassion, asked in turn: “By what method do you cultivate? How long is your lifespan?”

Rābila answered: “I practice the divine spells of the Four Heavens of the Desire Realm, one of which is called *As-You-Wish*. It suffices to extend my life to eighty thousand great eons. No lifespan in the upper realms exceeds this. Yet when my allotted time ends, I shall be reborn according to my karma.”

And in my teaching, though one may cultivate diligently and attain the five supernatural powers, still one cannot escape old age and death; though one may comprehend the principle of emptiness, there is no method for eternal life.”

At that moment, the Lord of the Dao, perceiving their thoughts, did not answer. Instead, he asked Rābila: “Do you know the root of your own teaching?”

Rābila replied: “I do not. This matter is of great antiquity, difficult to investigate in detail.”

The Lord of the Dao said: “Your teaching originates from the spirit of Mount Kunlun in your heaven, who styles himself the Lord of the Four Heavens, or the Four Heavenly Immortal Kings, or the Divine Kings. He promulgated this teaching to transform the beings of the Form and Desire Realms in the borderlands. Your own master derives from this same origin—it is not the spontaneous, supreme Dao of the Great Way. In the lower two realms and borderlands, beings practice a minor skill and call themselves immortals. Thus, these false immortals imitate one another, unaware of the supreme, unsurpassed teaching of the Great Dao.”

Rābila asked again: “How many methods are there in the supreme Dao? How many ranks of immortals? What are the names of the scriptures? I have heard of the Heavenly Worthy but have never beheld him. Yet in this great assembly, all are called Heavenly Worthies, with other titles besides—all are upper immortals, though there are also lesser immortals.”

Then the Perfected One said to Rābila: “The supreme Dao is one, but in its branches, there are thirty-six thousand kinds of teachings, all originating from the one Dao. The ranks of immortals and perfected beings number one hundred and twenty grades, all revering the Heavenly Worthy. The cloud-script forms natural celestial writings—hence, the *Celestial Scriptures*. The Heavenly Worthy of Supreme Peace, the Void and Non-Being, ever abides in the Mystery. With your mortal eyes and the limited vision of the five powers, you cannot behold the true countenance of the Three Worthies. I have studied the Dao for countless eons and only now attained the rank of Perfected One. All in this assembly are upper immortals.”

Rābila asked again: “The divine power of the Perfected One is already incomparable. How much greater must be the majesty of the Heavenly Worthy?”

The Perfected One replied: “It is not what your eyes can see or your ears can hear. After tens of thousands of great eons, he will descend to transform the world. With your perilous lifespan of eighty thousand eons, you will not live to see that time. Do not ask of this—it is beyond your reach. Your body reeks of foulness and decay, the stench of impermanence. If you would not defile my celestial palace, you must depart at once and not linger.”

At that moment, Rābila had no place to stand. He returned to the lower realm. The celestial path was long, and though he had ascended in his youth, taking six minor eons to do so, he had dallied too long. Now, aged and decrepit, his divine power waning, his spirit confused, and his mind bewildered, he had no recourse. Gazing at one another in sorrow, tears streaming down, they bid farewell to the Perfected One and hastily returned to the Desire Realm. Circling Mount Kunlun, they sought out the False King and recounted their journey to the upper realms, their encounter with the Perfected Ones of the Great Dao, the display of divine power, and the revelation of their origins.

Hearing this, the False King trembled in all five spirits, swooned, and revived only after a long while. Coming to his senses, he said to Rābila: “Stop, say no more! If the gods hear of this, they will spread word among humans that our arts are ineffectual.” Thereafter, the false immortals retreated to the southern mountains, dwelling by the waters. At the four seasons and eight solar terms, they would possess people, singing, chanting, and roaring, calling themselves Immortal Kings. They sought offerings and prayers, practiced illusions, and roamed the lower world, creating branches of their own, altering and fabricating false teachings, and presumptuously establishing ranks—over six hundred in all. When the Heavenly Worthy of the Golden Portal appears in response to the kalpa, these false immortals will be utterly destroyed, leaving no trace.

Then the Illustrious Numinous Lord of the Dao addressed the assembly of Perfected Ones: “When the false immortals first arrived, the Heavenly Worthy, the Great Sage, did not personally confront these vulgar beings of the lower realms. He commanded me, a minor adept, to display divine majesty before them. It was by the power of the Great Dao and this assembly that I overawed these heterodox immortals—not by my own ability alone. Such defilement is truly unseemly. Yet when the supreme Great Dao responds to the needs of the time, such measures may be necessary. It is not to be wondered at.”

Then Dān Huò, the Cavern Perfected named Tōng Xuán, rose from his seat, knelt, and asked the Illustrious Numinous Lord of the Dao: “May the *Chapter on Subduing Demons* be recorded? I wish to receive and practice it.”

The Illustrious Numinous Lord of the Dao replied: “Though this is an assembly of celestial perfected beings, I dare not transmit it on my own authority. First, I must report above.”

Then the two Perfected Ones presented the matter to the Heavenly Worthy of Supreme Peace, who instructed: “To overawe the demonic beings of the lower teachings, first strike the golden bell thirty-six times on the left, then recite the *Mantra of Majesty* three times. Its text reads:

*Golden bells bound with lightning and fire,
Fierce roars shake the Nine Origins.*”

Murderous qi surges and flames scatter to dust,
Ten thousand demons are extirpated, a thousand fiends meet their end.
The Thunder Father treads the void,
Thunderbolts and whirlwinds reverse their course.
Sever heads and slit the noses of the vile,
Uproot the demonic and annihilate their roots.
Those who defy me perish,
Those who submit to me endure.
The Seven Stars drip blood,
The Metal Deity blazes with lightning.
The spirit blade flashes with lightning,
The jade axe bears frost.
Mighty warriors march ahead—
What ghost dares stand in their way?
Those who contend in qi are destroyed,
Those who resist meet calamity.
Above, the Purple Canopy floats,
Below, the Golden Throne is seated.
Cinnabar clouds interlace and shimmer,
Sun and moon serve as its light.
The gate is guarded by the numinous toad,
Corpses ward it with golden radiance.
The Five Poisons conceal treachery,
Ten thousand demons are annihilated.
The Seven Perfected cultivate within,
A thousand mights expand without.
Souls return to the Purple Palace,
Spirits enter the Cinnabar Chamber.

The Heavenly Worthy declared: “This is the *Inner Might Mantra of Supreme Mystery*, which destroys the inauspicious and slays the perverse. Later learners among the immortals and Daoists who have not yet attained the utmost mystery may, if they fear much inauspicious killing, recite this divine mantra and, following the rites, secure their defense. A thousand perversities will lose their essence, ten thousand demons will forfeit their qi. The spirit will be at peace, the body secure, and all will be bright and fearless.”

The Heavenly Worthy declared: “The method of the Supreme Dao is perfected spontaneously without intent; there is no need to recite this mighty chapter. This is the *Mighty Register of Numinous Might* within the *Dao-Field of Supreme Mystery’s Emptiness and Quiescence*. To the left of the demonic gate, strike the golden bell thirty-six times to summon the mighty warriors. To the right, sound the jade chime fourteen times to gather the perfected numina. In the center, beat the Dharma drum twelve times to announce it to the Supreme Emperor. The gods of life array themselves within, the mighty warriors expand without. The twin luminaries enter the eyes, the mouth emits numinous radiance. The head bears the Seven Stars, the feet tread the Mysterious Net. The jade censer wafts incense, the body sits upon the Golden Throne. Ten thousand essences forfeit their qi, a thousand fiends perish of themselves.”

The Heavenly Worthy said: “If mortals of the lower realms practice this method alone without grasping its true essentials, they may live to two hundred and forty years, and ghosts cannot harm them.”

Thereupon, Dān Huò, the Cavern Perfected, received the essential words with reverence, joyfully announced his gratitude, and bowed in thanks. He then put them into practice.

At that time, Dān Huò, the Cavern Perfected, together with thirty-seven heavens’ host of perfected immortals—countless myriads—simultaneously prostrated themselves, knelt, and addressed the Heavenly Worthy: “I have long been blessed with residual fortune and have chanced to encounter the Highly Exalted One. You have bestowed compassion upon me, lifting me from the depths of sinking, and enabled me to transform my mortal frame. I have presumptuously taken the foremost place, rashly ascending the heights of the mystery, and my excess is more than enough. Not measuring my foolish insignificance, I now resolve to abandon thoughts of retreat. I shall remain here, sheltered in the shadow of Nanchang, awaiting the time when the Compassionate Exalted One descends to the world. I wish to accompany your cloud-borne carriage, attending and guarding you morning and evening, bearing the canopy and tending the censer. I only pray that the Heavenly Worthy, in your great compassion, will grant this request.”

Having finished speaking, he bowed twice more and prostrated himself to receive the teaching.

The Heavenly Worthy declared: “The Great Dao is impartial; good responds to good. You have inherited the power of your vow—what need is there for further entreaty? The appointed time is not far off. Within the span of tens of thousands of kalpas, the celestial halls are vast and distant—roam and dwell there as you will. When the time comes to descend to the world, you too must assist in proclaiming the true Dharma and spreading its transformation in the lower realms. We Three Sages each transform the Three Realms. At that time, the number of those delivered will also be beyond count.”

Thereupon, the perfected beings, hearing the Heavenly Worthy’s gracious assent to their attendance, saw their deepest wishes fulfilled. Overjoyed and exultant, they all bowed in thanks.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy addressed the later perfected ones: “Your Dao is still shallow; you have not yet penetrated the ultimate principle. First, enter the *Great Samādhi of Concentrating the Spirit* for one kalpa and exhaust all thoughts. Next, enter the *Great Samādhi of Forgetting Form*, where all responses and perceptions are empty. Next, enter the *Great Samādhi of the Six Voids*, where you respond as circumstances arise. Next, enter the *Great Samādhi of the Supreme Void*, where you divide your body into ten thousand millions. Next, enter the *Great Samādhi of Dynamic Potency*, which is the root of all transformations. Next, enter the *Great Samādhi of Generative Potency*, which pervades and generates all things. Next, enter the *Great Samādhi of Great Compassion*, which nurtures and matures all things. Next, enter the *Great Samādhi of Great Mercy*, which conceals and sustains all things. If you can accomplish these eight, you will then ascend to the rank of the Supreme Perfected and be numbered among the Later Sages. You will be commissioned by the Great Dao to respond in due order to the movements of the times, and exalted titles will be bestowed upon you. If you wish to follow me in descending to the world to teach and transform, but your mind is not settled, you will be unable to generate transformations. Your true responses will be obstructed, and you will be unable to initiate resonances.”

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy, having spoken these words, immediately entered the *Great Samādhi of Concentrating the Spirit*, motionless and indistinguishable from his original state. The perfected ones also followed the Heavenly Worthy into the *Great Samādhi of Concentrating the Spirit*.

The Heavenly Worthy emerged from this samādhi and entered the *Great Samādhi of Forgetting Form*. The perfected ones likewise followed the Heavenly Worthy into the *Great Samādhi of Forgetting Form*.

Having emerged from this samādhi, the Heavenly Worthy entered the *Great Samādhi of the Six Voids*. The perfected ones also followed the Heavenly Worthy into the *Great Samādhi of the Six Voids*.

Having emerged from the *Great Samādhi of the Six Voids*, the Heavenly Worthy entered the *Great Samādhi of the Supreme Void*. The perfected ones likewise followed the Heavenly Worthy into the *Great Samādhi of the Supreme Void*.

The Heavenly Worthy emerged from this samādhi and entered the *Great Samādhi of Dynamic Potency*. The perfected ones also followed the Heavenly Worthy into the *Great Samādhi of Dynamic Potency*.

The Heavenly Worthy emerged from the *Great Samādhi of Dynamic Potency* and entered the *Great Samādhi of Generative Potency*. The perfected ones likewise followed the Heavenly Worthy into the *Great Samādhi of Generative Potency*.

The Heavenly Worthy emerged from the *Great Samādhi of Generative Potency* and entered the *Great Samādhi of Great Compassion*. The perfected ones also followed the Heavenly Worthy into the *Great Samādhi of Great Compassion*.

The Heavenly Worthy emerged from the *Great Samādhi of Great Compassion* and entered the *Great Samādhi of Great Mercy*. The perfected ones likewise followed the Heavenly Worthy into the *Great Samādhi of Great Mercy*.

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy emerged from the samādhis of potency and, entering into the power of spontaneous spiritual freedom, suddenly ascended into the mystery. Treading the void in inverted light, in an instant he traversed the thirty-six thousand heavens and returned to his original place, motionless and still, harboring within himself thirty-six thousand suns and moons. Within his body, he opened thirty-six thousand celestial gates. Within his body, he manifested thirty-six thousand Heavenly Emperors, and within each Heavenly Emperor’s body, he beheld thirty-six thousand celestial gates. He also saw that each of the thirty-six thousand Heavenly Emperors had thirty-six thousand attendants, and each attendant sat upon a dragon throne. Each dragon throne was shaded by a flying canopy, and the canopies, vast and wide, covered all the realms.

In an instant, the thirty-six thousand heavens and earths trembled as one, celestial blossoms rained from the sky, and jeweled mountains surged from the ground.

Then, from within the Heavenly Venerable’s body emerged thirty-six thousand dragon wheels, bearing thirty-six thousand suns and moons, returning to the heavens.

At that moment, all withered bones within the three realms arose and transformed into living beings, reversing the course of age—hoary hair turned black, fallen teeth regrew, the five viscera bloomed like flowers, and ears and eyes regained their sharpness.

In another instant, the thirty-six thousand heavens were swept by great winds and thunder, sweet rains poured in torrents, all phenomena quickened to life, blossoms unfurled in splendor, celestial nectar descended, jade marrow flowed freely, perfected immortals of formless purity chanted in clarity, their voices resounding through the boundless void.

Then, the star palaces arrayed themselves in the empty sky as cloud chambers, above congealing into purple mists, below forming adamantine foundations. Tenfold radiance draped the heavens, jeweled canopies stretched high, windows opened to bright moons, doors gleamed with numinous light. White jade served as tables, golden essence as couches; true sovereigns stood in attendance, immortal youths burned incense.

At that time, the Heavenly Venerable and the assembled perfected ones took their places in the cloud chambers, seated upon dragon thrones. Phoenixes sang and dragons intoned, immortal birds danced in the courtyard, and the divine power shifted myriad forms at will.

The perfected ones marveled at what they had never before witnessed.

Then the Heavenly Venerable addressed them: "The methods of the supreme Dao—its divine power transforms endlessly. Yet if one has not awakened to its essence, stillness and wisdom remain empty and unobstructed, for it operates without intent. The mind does not strive, yet accomplishment arises of itself; wisdom does not act, yet illumination shines forth. Forced effort yields no clarity; forced action bears no fruit. It is most rare, most subtle—difficult to name. When you attain great penetration, it will naturally be thus."

All the perfected ones rose as one, bowing in gratitude, and vowed to receive these essential words.

The Heavenly Venerable continued: "Such divine transformations and the cultivation of stillness and wisdom are but steps upon the great Dao’s path. They are the methods of responding to the times and delivering the world—such is the Dharma."

Then, knowing that the perfected ones’ bodies and minds were unobstructed and their wisdom and power vast, capable of great tasks, the Heavenly Venerable led them to ascend above the Great Net, where they paid homage to the Heavenly Venerable of the Formless and received their appointments as supreme perfected ones. After countless kalpas, they would be granted honorific titles and ascend once more to the Great Net to pay homage to the Heavenly Venerable of the Formless.

The Heavenly Venerable declared: "Your Dao has reached its culmination; it is fitting to bestow upon you the office of supreme perfected ones. Each of you shall serve in the bureaus of the perfected ones." The jade scrolls and azure tablets were inscribed, and the perfected ones were commanded to read the tablets and behold their names, their honorific titles now fixed. They bowed again in reverence.

The Heavenly Venerable said: "Thus, in profound silence."

The perfected ones received their charge and returned to the cloud chambers of Southern Florescence. Seated in grand assembly, they celebrated for seven days and seven nights as celestial blossoms rained down, shaking the thirty-seven heavens. From the great earth, mountains and peaks surged forth in response to the heavens above. Heaven and earth resounded as one, praising the goodness of the moment.

At that time, the Three Venerables of Great Peace and the assembled perfected ones entered the great stillness of profound samādhi. The celestial palaces fell utterly silent, save for the fragrant smoke rising ceaselessly from the incense officials, enduring for a full kalpa.

After one kalpa, the Heavenly Venerable emerged from the great stillness and entered the wisdom of movement. In an instant, divine mists spread in all directions, warm qi surged from the eight directions, gentle winds stirred the fragrant smoke, and sweet dew softened the dust.

Then, the Heavenly Venerable emerged from the wisdom of movement and entered the wisdom of generation. In the blink of an eye, all phenomena arose from emptiness—clouds and mists soared upward, thunder rumbled and lightning flashed, divine herbs bloomed with blossoms, phoenixes sang in jade groves, and canopies stirred as rosy clouds arose.

The Heavenly Venerable addressed the perfected ones: "The method of movement and generation responds to the advent of the Later Sage of the Golden Portal, whose arrival is not far off. The great sages of the ten directions together proclaim these auspicious signs—not I alone."

When the Heavenly Venerable had spoken these words, all the assembled sages sat in silent stillness. The golden censers and fragrant blossoms remained ever fragrant and abundant. As they descended, myriad transformations unfolded. On that day, rare and wondrous divine powers manifested in full.

*Thus concludes Scroll Six of the* Supreme Dao Jade Clarity Scripture.
*Scroll Seven of the* Supreme Dao Jade Clarity Scripture *begins.*

**Chapter Seventeen: The Dao’s Transformation of the Four Barbarians**

At that time, in the Right Jade Terrace of the Jade Clarity Heaven, there resided a perfected one named Treasure Radiance, who served as the Supreme Prime. By reckoning the descent of his destiny, he descended to the gate of the Divine Continent’s Heavenly King, Haoyuan. On the fifteenth day of the seventh month at noon, he rode a chariot of purple clouds, accompanied by two immortals. Together, they transformed into sunlight and entered the womb of the Lady of the Xuanshi clan while she slept, entering through her mouth and dwelling in her womb for three years.

At that time, the lady was but eighteen years of age. One day, as she napped, she awoke to find herself with child. A divine fragrance arose, thick and intense, and her faculties grew keen. Her countenance bloomed with beauty, her form robust and flourishing. When alone, she constantly heard the sounds of metal and stone nearby, or faintly discerned the recitation of scriptures, as if chanting the verses of the true scriptures in harmony with her heart. Her body felt light and strong, surpassing her usual state.

Three months later, on the third day of the third month at noon, the lady, accompanied by three hundred maidens, went to the eastern city to enjoy the gardens. Resting upon the Fragrant Grove Terrace, she suddenly smelled a fragrance assailing her senses. In an instant, two embroidered-robed youths appeared beside her, each holding a golden tally. The lady asked, “Who are you?” The youths replied, “We are divine youths in service to the Jade Clarity Heaven, dispatched by the Heavenly Venerable of Jade Clarity. We have come here on his command.” The lady asked, “Why have you come?” The youths answered, “The Supreme Emperor has sent this tally to summon the Great King.” The lady replied, “The king is not here.” The youths said, “The king is within your womb.” Overjoyed, the lady immediately sat upon the edge of her bed. Suddenly, she felt the infant emerge from her left side. The lady then gathered her attendants to hold the newborn. The two immortal messengers knelt and greeted him, saying, “We have long awaited these three years, laboring for your descent into the world.” The infant shook his head, smiling for a long while. Beneath his eyes shone double pupils, casting a distant glow of purple light. He laughed three times, then ceased, his laughter vanishing in an instant.

At that moment, before the Fragrant Spring Terrace, the moon pond surged with waves. Five-colored dragon kings emerged from the pool, their mouths filled with fragrant water to bathe the infant. When the father-king heard the news, he hastened to the scene in his chariot. The ministers offered their congratulations, and the entire kingdom rejoiced with music. A general amnesty was declared throughout the land. The father-king commanded his ministers and the palace maidens to prepare grand music, lavish gifts of silk, and fragrant flowers beneath canopies to welcome the child back to the palace. As the procession entered the city, a seven-day celebration ensued.

The infant was brought forth, and the great ministers deliberated, investing him as the crown prince. They bestowed upon him a hundred offices, enriching him with favor and emoluments. At that time, auspicious clouds flowed downward, and celestial beasts came to guard him. The father-king named this child *Double Radiance*, with the style *Heaven’s Eminence*, and reared him in the Cloud-Soaring Palace. Five wet nurses took turns holding and nurturing him, while eight hundred maidens attended him day and night.

At times when he was carried from his bed curtains, the child would see the sky and sun, always laughing upward, his mouth emitting purple radiance that rose to the heavens like a cord, while sweet dew descended in strands straight into his mouth. Jade maidens scattered flowers to brush his body. Divine birds hovered in the air, spreading their wings to shade the sun, while fragrant officials wafted incense to perfume the palace.

By the age of three, *Double Radiance* could speak, his voice carrying a hundred paces, and he delighted in sitting alone, no longer needing to be held. At four, he laughed and conversed in solitude, his words transcending the mundane world. By seven, he knew without learning, his thoughts profound and gaze far-reaching, a light about him illuminating the entire chamber. He sat and stood as steadfast as a mountain, walked with the stride of a dragon, and when lying on his side, his head to the east, his limbs half-extended. His hair was dark blue, his brows emerald; his eyes opened wide at the temples, their light suffused with purple. His mouth was square, his nose rounded, his ears five inches long, with three perfect curves. His teeth were white and even, thirty-six in number, his lips red as cinnabar. His broad forehead was level, his cheekbones high, his philtrum marked by four ridges, twelve *fen* in length. His jade-like nape bore a star-like prominence, his hair neither tangled nor uneven, soft and lustrous. His neck bore three folds, his four nipples aligned with his elbows, his chest broad and slightly arched, his heart’s region deep and full. His arms were round and straight, his hands hanging past his knees, his nails firm and red, perpetually aglow. His palms bore floral patterns, three lines running clearly, their centers purple, his fingers six inches long. His navel was deep and round, with a hidden bone beneath; his cheeks dimpled, his flanks smooth, his abdomen marked by white moles. His shoulder bones were square and straight, his ankles concealed. His insteps were slightly arched, sinews and veins unseen, the soles of his feet full and level, their patterns like sun wheels. His toenails were deeply set, their tips slightly raised. His skin was fine and soft, suffused with fragrance and purity. His bones were blue, his marrow white, his five organs like lotus blossoms. His stomach and intestines were purple, and he ate but half-grains. Whether turning his gaze or shifting his body, he sat and stood with perfect poise.

By nineteen, he stood a full *zhang* in height, his voice resonant as a bell, its tones startling the dust to flight. From afar, a purple void canopy perpetually hovered above his head, and wherever he dwelled, frost and snow never fell. The air was harmonious and mild, winds never raged, and gentle rains fell in due measure. He was warm, benevolent, loyal, and forgiving, enduring insults with compassion and humility. Gazing at the clouds and sky, he discerned the warp and weft of the Dao with clarity.

All arts and skills he mastered without study. His profound communion reached its utmost, foreknowing all that had yet to unfold. The king his father treasured him, gathering his ministers to deliberate the abdication of the throne. Thrice he declined, yet could not refuse. At that moment, the Five Peaks echoed in response, and the void resounded with myriad cries of "Long live the king!" Auspicious omens assembled in full, the unseen and manifest harmonizing as one. With great reluctance, he at last accepted the throne.

He governed the people and served Heaven, propagating the Dao to pacify the world. His governance was upright yet effortless, never taxing the hearts of the people. He esteemed virtue and exalted goodness, so that all followed without command. His benevolence flowed to the orphaned and weak, his kindness extended even to insects. Humans and spirits alike submitted to him, and creatures of every kind lived in harmony.

Each autumn and winter, sweet dew descended from the heavens, and five-colored clouds encircled the sun and moon. City gates stood unbarred, borders required no defense. The Four Seas were as one, and the myriad states united. Auspicious grain and propitious grasses grew with shared roots and separate ears. A single tree bore ten branches, each ripening in its season. Celestial maidens spread across the fields, their radiant silks stretching across the plains, woven into patterns to clothe the people. Salt pools and sweet springs welled forth wherever needed. Glowing lingzhi and night-shining herbs flourished throughout the gardens. Divine birds and wondrous beasts grew tame along the palace walls. Unicorns and phoenixes gathered in flocks, their morning and evening calls harmonizing in song.

At that time, beyond the Black Waters to the north, among the Zang and Di tribes of the snowy highlands—where the river’s source winds slantwise and the sun shines upon the southern face of the Snow Mountains—there dwelt the mixed-herd Rong, a people of cunning nature and untamable disposition. Secretly they hatched a treacherous scheme, and hearing of the king’s virtuous governance, how he ruled without martial might, they mustered their forces and marched upon his kingdom.

No sooner had they reached the eastern slopes of the Snow Mountains than their sheep and horses sickened and died; the Di and Rong fell prey to plague. Ghosts materialized in broad daylight, slaughtering the barbarian hordes until only seven in ten remained. Midway through their march, the survivors repented in terror, falling to their knees in prostration.

The king, though aware of their treacherous intent, refused to strike, allowing them to advance or retreat as they chose. He issued a decree throughout his realm: “The border tribes, ignorant and rebellious, have harbored treachery in their hearts. Heaven has already punished them, and they have turned back of their own accord. No blade need be drawn; let the myriad people of the realm remain untroubled. If I were without the Dao, Heaven would surely cast me down.”

Within three days, word came from the frontier: the invaders had withdrawn. Yet as the tribes retreated, their armies were enveloped in a miasma of death. Heaven had claimed eight in ten of their number; pestilence and plague now raged unchecked. The borderlands trembled in fear, and the people gathered in dread, murmuring among themselves. They offered sacrifices to the spirits and prayed to Heaven, but the calamity only worsened.

Among the barbarian tribes, there was one chieftain who possessed some small understanding of worldly affairs. Addressing his people, he declared: “The lord of this great kingdom aligns his virtue with Heaven. He cultivates the Dao and upholds righteousness, his will unswayed by perversity. Ten thousand blessings sustain him; a hundred spirits guard his realm. How could we, in our folly, muster our forces and defy such supreme goodness? The disasters befalling our lands must surely stem from this. We must swiftly inform the neighboring kings, prepare our tribute, and hasten to offer our apologies.”

Thereupon, one hundred and twenty-five chieftains of the border tribes, along with eighty-four thousand attendants, mounted white elephants and bore offerings of incense, flowers, and jeweled garlands. They galloped into the great kingdom, their breath held as they approached the jade palace. Prostrating themselves before the king, they presented their treasures, their arms trembling, their voices breaking in supplication. Blood streamed from their noses; they tore out their hair in clumps, beating their breasts until their bodies were bruised and swollen. Their cries—half beast, half bird—were unintelligible, and interpreters struggled to convey their remorse.

“We of the borderlands,” they confessed, “do not follow the proper calendar. We are steeped in the turbid qi of the Three Realms, our forms misshapen like the Two Images. We are a mongrel breed, blind to kindness and beauty. Though we draw breath, we are not of the true qi. In our folly, we gave rise to wickedness, our hearts set on rebellion. We allowed our bestial natures to stir, defiling this great kingdom. No sooner had we gathered than Heaven struck us down. Our lands are ravaged by death, eight in ten of our people lost. The poisonous qi has not yet abated, and the calamity grows ever more severe. Those who sought to appease the spirits only invited greater wrath. Heaven has unleashed its fury, and our sacrifices have only worsened our plight. We dare now to beg the Great Heaven for mercy.”

With these words, they cast themselves to the ground, tearing their hair and wailing in despair. The king addressed them: “I have inherited the rule of a virtuous sovereign, entrusted with the governance of all under Heaven. I walk only the path of goodness, seeking nothing beyond. If I do not pity myself, how can I pity you? To me, all beings are as one child; I show no partiality, even to the hidden and obscure. You harbored treachery and came against me, but I remained unaware, leaving your fate to Heaven. I do not condemn you with emotion, nor does Heaven strike you with intent. The punishment you suffer is like spitting at the sky—it falls back upon your own face; like shooting an arrow at the heavens—it returns to pierce your own body. Such is the natural Dao; its principle admits no error.

The incense, flowers, and jeweled garlands you offer are not what I treasure. In this kingdom, we cultivate only virtue and power. As for the grains and silks, the necklaces and ornaments with which your people adorn themselves—these are the trappings of perverse customs, not true valuables. They only burden the body and cling like dust. Why? Because they are mere external adornments, and thus unworthy of esteem. In this kingdom, all people practice forbearance, humility, diligence, and frugality as their adornments. Virtue, precepts, and moral conduct are our incense and flowers; we have no need of your offerings.”

When the barbarian chieftains saw that the king would not accept their tribute, they grew fearful, believing their misfortune would not be dispelled. Weeping, they turned to one another and said: “The king’s refusal to accept our offerings may stem from their meagerness. Let us each present him with a white elephant, that he may show us mercy.”

The king replied: “Jeweled garlands and precious pearls are not what I value; how much less so white elephants, with their foul stench, their ravenous appetites, and their need for vast pastures and herdsmen? They would only burden my kingdom. Even the light and wondrous dragons and phoenixes I do not require.”

The barbarians, overwhelmed with grief and despair, tore out their hair and wailed: “The king will not accept our offerings. We are without fortune and shall surely perish. Better to take our own lives than face this calamity.”

The king instructed them: “Those who seek blessing must serve the Dao with an empty heart. When both body and mind are empty, the Dao too becomes void. Through this emptiness, misfortune is averted. Free from misfortune, one attains blessing. Moreover, those who seek blessing must harbor no desires, no expectations. Your offerings are made with hope, and thus I cannot accept them. In this kingdom, the wise and virtuous adorn themselves with goodness, not with garlands or white elephants.

The king continued: “In this kingdom, we strive only to follow the supreme Great Dao, seeking nothing beyond. You must understand: those who seek blessing must keep their hearts free from perversity, acting with impartiality. They do not chase profit, nor do they shun harm. They do not transform misfortune into blessing, nor do they cling to fortune. Thus they remain free from calamity. Why? Because evil cannot overcome goodness; the inauspicious naturally gives way to the auspicious. Misfortune vanishes of its own accord, and blessing is not something one perceives.

If you seek to avoid misfortune and pursue blessing, you are deluded, unable to grasp the true nature of fortune and misfortune. Your heart turns away from the truth. Why? Because fortune and misfortune share the same gate, rooted in the void.”

Consider carefully: from where does this misfortune arise as retribution? Know the origin of misfortune, and the root of blessing will become clear. Those who seek blessing must first understand misfortune. It is like a skilled physician who, wishing to cure all illnesses, first identifies their source before prescribing medicine. When illness and remedy align, no disease remains uncured.

Yet you, all you tribes, cling to misfortune while seeking blessing, failing to eradicate its root—hoping for blessing to descend is like one who grasps a staff to reconcile with an enemy, or carries water in search of fire. Though you toil for ages, you shall never attain it. The misfortune you face arises within your own being. How then can you seek blessing while destroying your very self? For to destroy the self is not called blessing.

Why do you, tribes of the wilds, willingly destroy yourselves? The body is the root of blessing—how can you destroy it? All who destroy the body are called destroyers of blessing. Moreover, the body is the root of the Dao; those who destroy the body are called destroyers of the Dao, not destroyers of misfortune.

Those who truly eradicate misfortune do not rely on blessing to dispel it; those who seek blessing do not achieve it through misfortune.

At that time, the tribes of the wilds, hearing the Great King’s decree, could not discern its meaning. They requested an interpreter to convey it, then gathered their robes in awe and trepidation. Unable to respond, they knew only to bow in reverence, their hearts filled with deep shame, kneeling uneasily.

Among the Yin tribes, there was a chieftain named Shitoufen, who asked the interpreter to relay his words. He declared himself the king of Jambudvīpa in India and spoke thus: “We are humbled that the Great Heaven has expounded such rare Dharma for our assembly. Yet we, dwellers of the frontier, possess shallow understanding and have not fathomed the ultimate Dao. Misled by distant hearsay, we have long languished in the ford of delusion, not only today but across kalpas. We beseech the Great Heaven to pity our benighted confusion.”

“These wild Hu, ignorant and unknowing, cannot grasp the truth. We implore you to grant us a single word to express our humble intent. We have heard the Great Heaven declare that this land reveres only the Great Dao, the supreme and most perfect. May we hear of it?”

The Great King replied: “The supreme Great Dao is ever subtle in its silence, yet the deaf cannot hear it. The Dao is most profound, yet the blind cannot see it. Though you beings possess eyes, you cannot gaze rightly; though you possess ears, you cannot hear rightly. A riot of colors distracts your clarity; the wails of false sounds stifle your wisdom. Though you have eyes and ears, you differ not from the deaf and blind. For this reason, you cannot hear the Dao.”

“If you wish to hear the Dao, rid yourself of false hearing. If you wish to contemplate the Dao, rid yourself of false thoughts. If you wish to cultivate the Dao, rid yourself of false cultivation. If you wish to practice the Dao, rid yourself of false conduct. To walk the path of right action—compassionate, kind, and yielding—is called the practice of the Dao. Those who walk this path shall naturally hear the Dao; having heard it, they shall also see it; having practiced it, they shall attain equanimity, perceiving all beings as no different from themselves. Their touch gives rise to compassion, and their minds make no distinctions. First establish this sincerity, then you may hear the Dao.”

Then the tribes again inquired: “Great King, what is the essence of the supreme Great Dao’s most wondrous practice? It preserves life in its perfection, ascends into formlessness, endures ceaselessly, and stands beyond all dependence or burden. We humbly beseech your instruction to dispel our confusion.”

The Great King declared: “The supreme Dao takes eternal life as its essence, and this very body as its Dharma-body. It holds compassion and equanimity as paramount, patience and gentleness as its function, expedient means and beneficence as its benefit, non-action and emptiness as its tranquility, wisdom and unimpeded insight as its penetration, the Dao-eye’s illumination as its attainment, vastness and receptivity as its emptiness, the form’s submission to the spirit as its formlessness, spontaneity as its naturalness, and formlessness as its eternal life.”

Upon hearing the Great King’s words, the tribes all exclaimed: “Never have we heard such! Though our minds are dull and our understanding dim, we have not fully grasped it and remain in doubt.”

Then the Great King resolved the doubts of the frontier tribes, opening their hearts and enlightening their minds. On the eighth day of the eighth month, he invited Master Hanlin for the tribes, summoning all ordained Daoists within the realm to assemble with full ceremonial dignity. For seven days and nights, they performed purification rites and repented of transgressions for the frontier peoples.

He also returned the precious offerings and jeweled garlands they had presented. The tribes said: “We dare not disobey your decree and must accept them.” Having received them, they then offered them to Master Hanlin. The Master accepted and divided the garlands into two portions: one for the poor and lowly attendants among the assembly, and the other for the tribes. The white elephant was returned to the tribes, and they adorned it with the garlands.

At that moment, twenty-four thousand great elephants, wearing the garlands, knelt as one before Master Hanlin. The elephants then scattered, plucking flowers with their trunks and offering them to the Master. The lowly attendants who wore the garlands felt shame arise in their hearts and sighed, saying: “The Master regards all things with impartiality, bestowing the treasure of jeweled garlands upon the people of the world and the white elephants alike.” They bowed their heads in gratitude.

Master Hanlin said: “The supreme treasure of the Great Dao transforms the mundane into the sacred, yet it bestows its blessings upon all beings with impartiality, without claiming merit. These garlands are mere external adornments, worldly embellishments for the body—what are they compared to the dust and blemishes of defilement? You, dwellers of distant lands, do not understand the offering of the heart. You presented these to me, and I accepted them, only to return them to you. Why do you thank me? Simply accept them without doubt.”

On the fifteenth day of the month at noon, the Master and ninety-seven thousand Daoist practitioners partook of their meal together. Afterward, he rinsed his mouth with a jeweled flask, and the remaining water, scattered toward the south, west, and north, instantly transformed into clouds and rain, accompanied by wind, thunder, and lightning. The Master then exhaled toward the three directions, and golden light issued from his mouth, illuminating distant lands. At that moment, those among the border tribes afflicted with illness were instantly cured, and all saw the Master from afar within the light as if he stood before them. The wind and rain cleansed their filth, the thunder’s voice proclaimed their transgressions, and every disaster and misfortune vanished in an instant. He also allowed eighty-four thousand barbarian warriors to see their families within the light.

By the twentieth day, the tribal chieftains each dispatched envoys to hasten into the great kingdom, reporting peace and recounting the auspicious signs they had witnessed as before. Then, the tribesmen, their hair unbound, prostrated themselves in repentance, rejoicing before the Way. They knelt, pressing their heads to the ground, and asked the Master: “We do not know what method the Great Master cultivates. How is it that your divine transformations are so boundless and unobstructed? Are you only called ‘Great Master,’ or do you bear other titles? We have heard the king’s decree that the great kingdom reveres the Great Dao. Is the Dao you practice the same as or different from the Supreme Great Dao? We are ignorant and do not understand. We only hope the Great Master will broadly distinguish and enlighten us on what we have not yet heard.”

At that time, the Master snapped his fingers and coughed lightly, then addressed the assembled tribesmen: “Excellent, excellent! You dwell in remote lands, yet you pity and inquire with such wisdom—this is inconceivable. Listen carefully, and I will explain to you. I am the Supreme Perfected One of the Eastern Terrace of the Cloud Palace in the Jade Clarity Heaven, naturally and emptily born, named the Supreme Dao. I cultivate nothing, yet through great compassion and great mercy, I manifest divine transformations in response to the world, accomplishing them as my heart wills. Without intention, I act, and my body is not wearied. The king and I appeared in the world at the same time to govern the multitudes and kings, temporarily dwelling in mortal form. I provisionally bear the title of Master, residing in Hanlin. We serve as guest and host, subtly influencing one another, neither identical nor different, neither residing in the middle. You, the various tribes, are born into the Desire Realm, assuming the form of border barbarians. Your hearts lack compassion, dwelling in desolation and depravity. By nature, you harm and do not cherish life. You drink blood and consume raw flesh, your bodies restless and foul, your spirits congealed with turbid qi, your forms bound by partial essence. You uproot the fundamental and obstruct the source, suppressing the root while exalting the branches. You value wealth and goods but do not treasure the Great Dao. This has been so for kalpas, not merely in this age. The Great Dao has not been practiced for a long time. Yet though you are thus, all things turn in cycles: sin becomes the root of virtue, and evil is the source of compassion. If you had not harbored rebellious hearts, you would never have seen me. The Great Dao is impartial, making no distinction between foe and kin. It repays enmity with virtue and does not abandon great compassion. Thus, the king invited me and my assembly of practitioners to repent on your behalf and dispel your disasters. With a heart of impartial compassion and no differing thoughts, I caused clouds and rain to scatter and light and sound to universally reach you.”

At that time, the Great Emperor of the kingdom, along with the Great Consort, the prince, and the assembled ministers, had not initially known that the Master of Hanlin and the king were both incarnations of the same divine Master. When he first arrived, the people of the kingdom, great and small, all believed the Master to be an ordinary man. Later, witnessing the Master’s divine transformations at will, the entire kingdom took refuge in him. Filled with remorse, they reproached themselves, and regardless of wealth or poverty, they prepared offerings. The land’s treasures gathered in the eastern city, filling the Terrace of Fragrant Spring. A grand vegetarian feast was held, and the kingdom’s men and women thronged the roads, their carriages stirring dust like mist. Then, the king had a high seat prepared, exhausting the kingdom’s treasures to adorn the ritual arena. He opened the great treasury, bestowing grain and silk to aid the destitute. Exquisite incense was burned, its smoke rising to the heavens, forming canopies of condensed clouds. Music and entertainment resounded, startling the sky and deafening the earth. The Five Peaks trembled, and the Four Seas surged. Cool winds harmonized the seasons, and the radiant springtime warmth returned. Forests bloomed anew, orioles sang again, birds soared and danced, fish and dragons leapt, and the kingdom was blessed with auspicious qi from heaven and earth.

The assembly rejoiced immeasurably, circumambulating in procession, their songs and praises overflowing. The practitioners chanted the *Step of Emptiness*, their Sanskrit hymns resounding in praise. Then, the Master ascended the seat, resting his hand upon the armrest, his presence as steadfast as a mountain. His heart was filled with a thousand virtues, his body formed of ten thousand blessings. The assembly gazed upon him with joy, beholding his true form. All awakened the heart of the Dao, their voices united as one, their hundred minds in harmony. They paid homage to the Lord of the Dao, wishing to hear the rare and wondrous.

Then, for the sake of all beings, the Supreme Lord of the Great Dao commanded the king, Chongguang, to take three pinches of incense, bow from afar to the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion in the Cloud Palace, and kneel to make vows. The first vow: may the transformative power of the Dao spread, and may all under heaven embrace virtue. The second: may all sentient beings awaken to the Dao. The third: may the sorrowful souls of the nine nights all be liberated. The fourth: may the lonely and unsupported all receive rebirth. The fifth: may the world be at peace and the hundred grains ripen. The sixth: may ministers be loyal and children filial, rulers benevolent and fathers kind. The seventh: may the Four Seas be united, and foes and kin reconciled. The eighth: may those concealed in wombs and shells all be born and grow. The ninth: may chronic and new illnesses be instantly cured. The tenth: may the destitute and exposed all have ample clothing and food.

Then, the king presented these ten vows, rose to bow to the Master, and spoke: “We only hope the Great Master will remain among the people for a long time, descending in form to dwell among mortals, not abandoning the dust and filth.” After the king spoke these words, heaven and earth were moved. Flowers rained from the void, sweet dew descended from the sky, and myriad celestial musics resounded, startling the firmament. Heaven and earth trembled, unicorns hummed and phoenixes sang, dragons and fish stirred the depths.

At that moment, the Dao Lord’s countenance radiated with penetrating true light, vast and boundless, its numinous sound resonating afar, harmonizing and transforming all beings. The drowned in death received new life; withered forests burst into bloom. Sentient and insentient alike held their essence and blossomed. Though the Dao spoke not, all dharmas were already complete. This assembly was filled with awe, arising naturally, of itself—even I know not how it came to be.

Then, the various barbarians gazed upward, forgetting to blink, losing their forms, motionless as withered trees. In but a moment, the Cloud Palace Heavenly Worthy descended in response, accompanied by nine hundred million high perfected ones, alighting upon the azure clouds above. A canopy of auspicious mist coalesced, spanning ten thousand leagues. Its expanse stretched level as the earth in all four directions, where the perfected ones arrayed themselves at its edges. At the center of the auspicious mist stood a seat of purple radiance, borne by intertwining five-colored cloud-dragons. The seat rose eighty-four thousand nine hundred and nine *ren* in height. The Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion ascended and sat upon it, gradually descending through the mystery until seven hundred and eight *ren* above the earth, directly over the eastern city, profound and empty, serene and unmoving. Only the crimson glow above the luminous mist was visible, its vermilion hue blending indistinctly. As all eyes looked up, they suddenly beheld the Heavenly Perfected One’s emanation body ascend and enter the clouds, returning to the seat it had occupied before. Then, two true ones appeared, their countenances identical. For a long while, the two assemblies fell silent, without sound or movement, their true forms still as golden mountains. Their radiance shone brilliantly, its bounds unfathomable.

Within the great assembly, humans and non-humans alike sat motionless, their minds free from weariness or aversion. Joyfully they gazed upward, delighting in the vision of the true form, their hearts fixed in single-pointed devotion, forgetting even their own bodies. For nine days and nine nights, they remained without hunger or thirst, their bodies and minds unmoving.

Then, the barbarians beheld once more the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion upon the floating clouds, attended by his majestic retinue. Overcome with terror, they tore out their hair in remorse, blaming themselves, slashing their noses with blades until their bodies ran with blood. They leapt and flung themselves down as if mountains had collapsed. Witnessing this rarity, they cried out, vowing to offer their eyes, their heads, to burn their bodies, to break their bones as offerings, their voices reaching the king. The king then issued a decree, addressing the barbarians:

“The supreme Dao and its dharma cherish life and abhor killing. Do not defile our great realm with your crude and barbaric ways. To burn your bodies in atonement is to invite ruin—your souls will suffer harm, forever losing the human path. To burn the body in pursuit of the Dao is to seek the Dao through annihilation; to annihilate the body in pursuit of the Dao is to mistake the Dao for a path of destruction. How can one seek the Dao through self-destruction?

You barbarians have entered our great land, yet remain untouched by its refinement. How then can you hope to hear the supreme Dao? If you wish to hear the Dao, preserve the root of hearing—do not seek the Dao through the ear. If you wish to see the Dao, preserve the root of sight—do not seek the Dao through a ruined eye. If you wish to practice the Dao, you must preserve life—do not practice the Dao through death. If you wish to practice the Dao, first preserve your body—do not practice the Dao through a broken or defiled form. If you wish to embrace the Dao, first abandon the ten evils—do not practice the Dao with a heart of the five inversions.

You must now understand: those whose lives are not whole cannot hear the Dao; those whose bodies are not whole cannot study the Dao.
