Though you barbarians are not vessels of the dharma, having beheld the Heavenly Worthy, after ten thousand kalpas you will inherit this merit. You will be reborn in a great land, a realm of the Dao. If you can vow thus, you will never again be reborn in wild and uncivilized lands. From this day forward, preserve your forms. Do not tear your hair, burn your bodies, or break your bones—such acts defy heaven and earth, lack compassion and obedience, and lead to rebirth in evil paths, forever barring you from the Dao.”

Then, all the barbarians knelt and bowed, answering the king: “In our customs, to maim the body or destroy life, to burn the body to ashes or crush the bones, letting the smoke rise—this we call ascending to heaven. Or to cast the corpse into deep waters—this we call becoming a water immortal. Or to abandon the corpse in the wilds, to be devoured by birds and beasts.”

The barbarians do not value the deliverance of their living bodies, finding long life a burden. The king declared: “You Rong and Di regard longevity as toil and your own flesh as encumbrance. In this great kingdom’s law, birth and death are the true burden. Thus we seek the Dao of eternal existence without birth, ascending into formlessness, free from affliction. We do not maim the body or destroy life to escape toil—yet without such acts, toil vanishes of itself.

You barbarians cling to perverse minds, following heterodox ways. You do not abandon the ten evils, delighting in the cycle of birth and death, nor dispel the three poisons. Your forms are human, but your hearts are those of beasts—unworthy to behold the Dao. Do not defile my great land with your barbarian customs.”

Then, the barbarians bowed in apology, vowing never again to tear their hair, burn their bodies, or break their bones. They said: “We did not comprehend the supreme Dao and rashly spoke false words, offending the upright. We believed life must end in death, so we sought extinction. We did not know the boundless, supreme Dao grants eternal life, ascending into formlessness, free from all burdens. We beg your compassion and grant us renewal.”

The king then admonished the barbarians: “Your wild natures are dull and ignorant. Unaware of virtue and the Dao, you brought this calamity upon yourselves, inviting punishment. Now you come to repent. The Dao is merciful, pitying your ignorance. The True Master of Hanlin bestows upon you blessed fortune; the Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy pities your foolish stubbornness. The Supreme Great Sage has come to our land. Ten thousand souls fall silent, their hearts fixed upon the mystery, devoted to the Great Dao. Yet you barbarians rashly voice shallow views, unable to remain still, disturbing the assembly, disrupting others and yourselves, forfeiting wisdom and benefit. Remain silent. Though you do not understand the law, your souls will gradually be nourished.”

The barbarians obeyed the king’s command, kneeling in silence without movement for seven days and nights. At dusk on the seventh day, suddenly three great heavenly demons from the south, west, and north flew from the earthly bureaus through the sky. They bowed to the True Lord, prostrated before the king, then turned to rebuke the barbarians, their eyes blazing with fury, teeth gritted, and spoke harshly:

“In the king’s land of the Dao, people are free from the three poisons, long removed from the ten evils. They uphold righteousness, cultivate benevolence, honor the Dao, and revere virtue. The kingdom has no treacherous ministers; households have no rebellious sons. Yet you mad barbarians bring these sinful ghosts and walking corpses to defile the royal land, seeking repentance and blessings, hoping to hear the Dao? Heaven’s statutes and earth’s laws allow no pardon for the ten evils. To rebel against one’s lord and father—no crime is greater! You deserve to be ground to bone-ash, your sinews torn and blood spilled, your five viscera carved out, your gall and heart exposed, your tongue ripped out—still insufficient to atone for your wicked words. Your eyes gouged out—still insufficient to repay your evil gaze. Your homeland will suffer disaster; your descendants will perish. One traitor brings ruin to ten thousand people.”

At these words, the barbarians’ hair stood on end in terror. Their sorrow and dread were so great their livers and gall seemed to split, their bodies convulsed, sweat poured like rain, their breath came in gasps, their mouths clamped shut, and their five spirits scattered in panic. The earthly officials presented their records to the king.

The king addressed the demons: “The supreme Dao makes no distinction between foe and kin. They cannot harm me—why would you attack them? Even if they could harm me, I would not retaliate.”

The king asked the demons: “Suppose an infant, holding tiles, wood, awls, or knives, wounded its parents—would you kill it?”

The demon kings replied: “No.”

The king said: “I am the same. I would rather suffer harm than ever intentionally injure a living being. How much less these mad barbarians, whose wisdom is shallower than an infant’s, who cannot harm me? If heaven strikes them, inflicting cruel suffering, my heart aches with pity.”

Hearing the king’s words, the heavenly demons snapped their fingers in unison, exclaiming: “This is unprecedented!” They looked at one another and said: “The sage-king of this great land is vast in heart and kindness. His great compassion extends even to you. His virtue equals creation itself. Though he is but a temporary king, he already possesses all the marks of perfection. His body is founded on ten thousand virtues; a thousand blessings shape his heart. Soon he will bear the title Heavenly Worthy. We have come to this assembly, which will not last long. He will surely deliver many. The Great Dao is rare to encounter; the wondrous law is rare to hear. We beseech the great king to remain.”

The king, understanding their intent, replied: “The Great Dao is vast and boundless, like empty space without obstruction. In this assembly, the Dao is the law. The law makes no distinctions, knows no arising or ceasing, no seeing or hearing, no inside or outside, nor any middle ground. The law transcends birth and death. In this assembly, all is pure and undivided, united in the single law of compassion. You demons who wish to remain must abide by this law.”

Hearing the king’s words, the demons stood in solemn reverence. They returned to stand among the barbarians for three days and nights. At dawn on the third day, they saw from the land of Jianmu sixty-eight thousand immortals and Daoist masters, each shaded by flying canopies, holding flowered banners, passing over the dragon palace. Each bore luminous moon pearls and purple jade灵芝, flying through the sky to offer them to the Heavenly Perfected. Behind them came eighty-one kings of island barbarians, each wearing robes of five-colored phoenix patterns, accompanied by eight thousand attendants. These kings brought divine medicines and rare incense, arriving together to present them to the great king: the seven luminous tiger foams, dragon embryo śarīra, golden radiance blazing brilliantly, illuminating the sky.

These śarīra were transformed from eight kinds of frost-like jade. If the king consumes them, his body will take on a golden hue and jade-like complexion. The seven luminous tiger foams and dragon embryo elixirs—if the king consumes them, he will instantly gain the power of flight, performing a thousand transformations, shaping all things at will.

In my past cultivation of the Dao, I studied under Master Changsang Daojun, who bestowed upon me divine medicines. By consuming them, I attained immortality. Later, I received the essential teachings of the Dao and descended to govern the Nine Barbarian Lands. I heard that you have descended into the world to bring joy to all beings. Furthermore, I learned that the Jade Purity Heavenly Worthy has manifested in response, while the Left Terrace Perfected Ones have taken refuge in the Cold Forest. Drawn by this karmic convergence, the resounding echoes of rare harmony shook the eight directions, and all heard it; the empty radiance pierced the void, illuminating the ten quarters. Thus, I have come here to pay my respects.

At that moment, after the eighty-one immortals spoke these words, they ascended into the sky, rising a hundred *ren* above the earth. They bowed in reverence to the Heavenly Worthy and remained suspended in the air.

Then, from the eastern lands, a ghostly general named Lightning Boar appeared. His form stood three *zhang* tall, with jagged teeth and chiseled fangs, a copper head and iron bristles, a hooked tongue and fiery breath. His eyes blazed like shooting stars, his face was black, his body crimson, his teeth like those of a goshawk, and his hooves like those of a horse. His voice thundered like a struck drum, and his exhalations formed clouds. Leading a retinue of over six hundred million ghosts, he had heard from afar that a Perfected One had descended to become king, governing the realm with the Dao, never oppressing living beings. Wishing to guard the borders and assist the great king, they all rode black clouds and arrived floating through the air. Prostrating before the king, they spoke:

"Your servant is the king of the ghostly realms, commanding wandering spirits. Any demons or malevolent beings who refuse to submit, I devour at will, holding life and death in my grasp. From afar, I have heard that the people of your kingdom are kind and virtuous. Thus, I lead my followers to purify your land and humbly offer to serve as its guardians. Wherever great sages and immortals reside, I shall attend them, serving morning and night. At places of fasting and scripture recitation, I shall lead my followers to provide external protection. If any heretics or evil persons slander the true Dao or harm the community of the faithful, I shall destroy them, afflicting them with grave illnesses, causing their hair to fall out and inflicting them with severe maladies. If any beings within the sacred precincts behave improperly—casting sidelong glances or harboring impure thoughts—I shall punish them, causing these wicked ones to suffer bodily afflictions in life and descend into hell upon death, their sins extending to seven generations of ancestors. But if any beings are kind and filial, reciting scriptures and precepts, making offerings to the great Dao, and holding the Dao in their hearts, I shall draw near to them, constantly guarding and protecting them, ensuring no evil ghosts gain advantage over them. I only beseech the great king to permit my followers to safeguard the sacred precincts."

The king replied, "Excellent, excellent! I regard all beings as my own children. To you, I extend the same impartial heart. Though the seen and unseen differ, I grant your wish to join in virtuous recognition."

At that moment, the ghosts rejoiced, receiving the king’s words with gratitude. They encircled the Fragrant Spring Terrace east of the city, bowing in reverence to the Perfected One before prostrating and remaining in place.

Then, over sixty thousand fire-wreathed, murderous ghosts appeared. Each stood three *zhang* tall, their heads radiating light like scattered fireflies. Their bodies were entirely black, their eyes red as flames, and they wielded iron rods. Their breath scorched those it touched, causing them to collapse to the ground, their hair standing on end, their bodies wracked with cold, their senses reeling, and blood flowing from their noses and mouths. Having heard that the king governed with the Dao, never harming living beings, they wished to assist in subduing the wicked and rebellious. Riding black winds, they arrived from the north, kneeling before the king and speaking:

"We have heard that the king governs with the Dao, his benevolence vast and far-reaching, showering all—seen and unseen—with grace. Thus, we lead our followers, wishing to serve, bring peace to the kingdom, and protect the virtuous. At any gathering of the Dao, we shall provide external protection, crushing malevolent demons and rectifying deviant paths. If any beings desecrate the sacred precincts, secretly harboring malice, casting wicked glances at the faithful, we shall strike them dead with our iron rods, tear out their tongues, or cause their eyebrows and hair to fall out. If any beings enter the sacred precincts with defiled bodies or arrogant disdain, we shall afflict them with leprosy, various calamities, and unrest wherever they go, naturally filling them with terror."

The king then addressed the murderous ghosts: "Your radiance and venom are too fierce to approach people. Though you possess mighty spiritual power, do not harm the innocent. Instead, cherish all beings, support the virtuous, and wish to hear the Dao’s teachings, so that they may swiftly transform and attain the supreme Dao."

The murderous ghosts received the decree and remained in joyful compliance.

At that moment, eighty-five thousand Vajra deities descended from the sky. Each stood sixteen feet tall, their strength and valor unmatched, their divine power surpassing all but the gods of the path. They arrived in a sudden rush, their origin unknown. They served as guardians of the great Dao, first bowing to the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion above, then to the Perfected One, greeting the king as if they were old acquaintances. They spoke:

"As a true immortal descends into the world, the Dao’s transformation nurtures all life. Inner and outer realms align, humans and spirits converge in harmony, and all nations gather, their borderlands submitting as one. Yet purity and impurity mingle, truth and falsehood blur. The great sage, in boundless magnanimity, does not distinguish between the wise and the foolish. This assembly’s karmic cause is neither trivial nor small. It is deeply fitting to enforce strict discipline to eradicate falsehood. I only beseech the true king to heed my counsel: rectify the sacred precincts, bestow blessings upon the virtuous, transform and eradicate the malevolent, so that both humans and non-humans alike revere the true Dao."

The king silently assented.

Then, amidst the great assembly, the Vajra deities closed their eyes and leapt once, ascending into the azure clouds. They surged forward, shaking the earth and splitting stones, whipping up winds and scattering dust until the sun was obscured. Their glaring eyes flashed like lightning, their gnashing teeth rumbled like thunder. With a single roar, they subdued a thousand spirits, driving away any who dared resist. Rolling up their sleeves and flexing their arms, they raised their voices in a mighty cry, causing heretics to lose their essence and ghosts to faint in terror.

At that moment, the Vajra deities glanced around and declared: "We are the Dharma-protecting Vajra deities, attendants of the great Dao, servants of the Heavenly Perfected. We shadow the sacred precincts, uphold the virtuous, expose sins and transgressions, and ferret out deceit and evil."

Let no being dare offend the might of these divine spirits. Minor transgressions shall bring bloodshed; grave offenses, annihilation of form. Maintain discipline within and without, and let no laxity arise.

Then, all in the assembly—men and women, young and old—rose in reverence, bowing to the Vajra deities before resuming their seats. At that moment, the Vajra, for the sake of protecting the Dharma, subdued the minds of both the seen and unseen multitudes, and spoke this incantation:

"Thunder and fire illuminate the void; divine radiance brightens the hidden.
Four venomous dragons encircle; eight spirit-tigers surround.
The headband bears the Seven Stars; the feet tread upon Dipper and Ox.
Celestial power arrays the constellations; golden hooks gleam with essence.
The primal sovereign commands the mighty host, striding through the empty sky.
At the center, demons and heretics are severed; below, wandering spirits are extinguished.
Livers are torn out, gallbladders drawn forth; intestines are overturned, veins ripped away.
Left they are slain, right they are crushed; before they are boiled, behind they are beheaded.
Demons are cut off without origin; grievances are gathered and bound.
Ghost-devouring messengers shatter and swallow them whole.
Sorcerers and shamans with their drums and songs, drinking blood and eating flesh—
their forms reek of stench, their bones of foulness; goblins and specters are overthrown.
Rank and filthy, base and restless, their hearts and forms full of deceit and slander—
the divine pestle smashes their skulls; the golden blade slits their bellies.
Those who conceal malice and harm are suddenly subdued.
In the left hand, the golden talisman; in the right, the ledger of sins.
The Great One’s golden bell, the Jade Stave of the Heavenly Sovereign.
Those who know their faults yet do not amend shall have their heads suspended and severed.
What demon shall not perish? What spirit shall not be destroyed?
The Six Spirits shall not hide; the Seven Stars shall split with blood.
Above stands the Perfected Master; below, the Vajra deities.
Together they descend with qi, their mouths emitting divine rays.
They drink from the Moon Pool, bathe in the Mystic Frost.
The five viscera bloom with flowers, enduring forever, never withering."

Then, the Great Ghost-King, his four eyes flashing like lightning, joined in protecting the Dharma, dispelling all misfortune. Guarding the sacred precincts, he examined for deceit and corrected transgressions, subduing evil men, heretics, and all those lacking true faith. He spoke this incantation:

"Divine winds sweep away dust, uprooting the roots of evil.
The Six Heavens lose their essence; the Five Poisons dispel their grudges.
Golden heads and iron teeth devour ghosts and halt souls.
They pierce the radiant door, twin lights illuminating the gate.
Shooting stars carry killing qi, resplendent and fearless.
A hundred meridians flow like rivers; the seven channels are harmonized.
Spirits are at peace, bodies balanced—ever abiding, never dying."

When the Great Ghost-King finished reciting this incantation, he bowed from afar to the heavens above, then prostrated before the Perfected Lord, and addressed the ghosts: "You are the guardians of the Dao, protectors of the virtuous. Those who expound the Dharma differ not from the Dao. You must not oppose the true and upright qi. Capture and report any who do—eternal damnation awaits."

Then, the Great Ghost-King spoke to all in the Dharma assembly: "I am the Heavenly Emperor’s servant, bound to the Dao in duty. I support the newly initiated, all men and women entering the Dao’s first gate. I quell wayward thoughts—you must not cast sidelong glances or heed those who violate the precepts. In vigilance and protection, both the living and the dead shall be examined. Not only do I slay ghosts, but I also subdue the violent, quell wayward hearts, and regulate the living. Those lacking true faith, upon hearing this divine incantation, should rise in reverence. This incantation is the Heavenly Emperor’s mighty decree, the scripture of the natural order. The demon kings of all heavens, the ghost-generals of the five directions, the Perfected Officials and earthly administrators—all assist the Dao’s flourishing transformation, guarding households and nations, pacifying sacred precincts, and protecting the virtuous. All recite this mighty decree to subdue the impure, behead the malevolent, and shatter the blades of evil. Heretics and wicked men lose their essence and qi; venomous specters and goblins, hearing it from afar, bow in awe. Wherever there are Dharma assemblies, fasting lectures, sacred precincts, or lay dwellings, my followers and I shall ever observe them, fasting and maintaining the precepts as prescribed. When sincerity guides the act, the great Dao descends, and blessings swiftly arrive. But those whose hearts are divided, who act for profit or fame, who fast only when compelled—we shall not guard them, nor shall the great Dao descend. Goblins, wandering spirits, venomous ghosts, and lesser demons shall attend their offerings. Those who slight the Dao and scorn the Dharma shall be investigated by the Three Offices. The Dao does not act in vain; it responds only to sincere hearts, not to barter or trade. Disciples of the Dao, take heed."

When the Ghost-General finished speaking, he stepped back and stood motionless, solemn and still.

Then, the Great King’s chariot journeyed to the Western Regions to welcome and escort his parents. The hundred ministers and nobles all held floral banners and played music, their grand procession resplendent in majesty. They welcomed his parents and returned to the Fragrant Spring Terrace, where they burned incense and bowed their heads. The Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy next paid homage to the Perfected Master, inquiring after the Dharma assembly with joy and solicitude. The Heavenly Emperor was aged, and his consort likewise frail. The Great King, filial and devoted, watched their countenances with a heart ever torn between joy and fear.

Then, the Perfected Master bade them sit once more and addressed the Heavenly Emperor: "You and your son are noble friends in the Dao. You are the essence of the Purple Tenuity, incarnated in mortal form to rule as emperor by the mandate of heaven. The Great King Chongguang is an Upper Perfected of the Jade Clarity, born into your lineage. Though he reigns as a worldly emperor, his form does not age—all is the natural, supreme Dharma-body."

Then, the Perfected Master spoke to the Great King: "The immortals of the Nine Barbarians have bestowed upon you divine medicine to reverse aging. Bid your parents face east and take it with cinnabar water."

At that moment, Chongguang opened his treasure casket, took the medicine and water, and offered them to his parents. They received it, knelt facing east, and consumed it. The Great King took eighty cups, dividing them into three portions: one offered to the Perfected Master, who declined; the others given to his parents, who drank the cinnabar water. After seven days, their faces bore the luster of gold and jade, their steps light as flight. Their feet barely touched the ground, yet their bodies seemed to restrain themselves, yielding to their forms, and they rose into the air. They then received from the Perfected Master the sacred scripture of cloud-seal characters, the *Harmonizing the Spirits and Preserving Life* in thirty-six thousand words, which they recited morning and night. The five qi floated above their crowns; their eyes shone with radiant light. Their spirits were clear and serene, their bearing majestic and refined. Their voices carried with fragrance, piercing and pure; purple qi connected to the heavens. Their countenances reverted to youth, their white hair turned black. They moved between existence and non-existence.

Between their advances and retreats, they joined the assembly in joy, offering obeisance to the king. Gazing upward, they saw the azure vault suddenly transform into a radiance of blue light, illuminating the east. After a long while, it shifted into red light, illuminating the south. Again, after a long while, it turned to white light, illuminating the west. Once more, after a long while, it became black light, illuminating the north. And yet again, after a long while, it turned to yellow light, illuminating the center. Within each of the five colored lights resounded a tone, harmonizing and flowing in transformation, ethereal and pure, elegant and refined. The five lights stretched across the clouds like a celestial rainbow, luminous and penetrating.

In an instant, the Perfected Master at the assembly once more emitted from between his brows four hues of radiant light, responding to the heavens above—what are called the Light of Compassion, the Light of Mercy, the Light of Goodness, and the Light of Faith. At that moment, the entire assembly, gazing upon the true light, forgot their weariness in body and mind. They then heard within the eight-colored radiance the music of the natural realm, their minds awakening as if they had tasted sweet dew.

At that time, over eighty thousand of the Rong tribesmen, having witnessed this light, were struck blind and their hearts bewildered, as though deeply intoxicated. Their six senses sealed, they collapsed senseless. Then, a great minister of the kingdom named Shouzheng, seeing the barbarians fallen and insensate, stepped forward and addressed the Perfected Master, saying: "By our accumulated fortune, we were born in an age of the Dao and have been blessed to behold the Perfected Master, to witness the majesty of the Dao, our minds opened and our thoughts awakened, our ears and eyes made keen. Our hearts pour forth into the mysterious, joyful and tireless. Yet we do not understand why these tribesmen lie fallen, their six senses sealed, their spirits as though stupefied by drink."

"What sins have their bodies borne to fall thus into confusion and lose their will? We only pray that the Perfected Master reveal what we have not heard, that all may awaken and understand the causes and karmic conditions."

The Perfected Master replied: "Great indeed are the deep-rooted karmic bonds of their unwholesome deeds. Listen carefully, and I shall explain.

"Good man, you must now understand: these Rong and Di tribesmen first harbored rebellious hearts, gathering treachery and peril. Heaven loosed its poison upon them, and the underworld’s ghosts assailed them. All their valiant warriors were annihilated at once. Their lands lay desolate, nine-tenths lost. Then plague struck, bringing suffering and pestilence. Their sheep and horses perished, and the tribesmen, starving and freezing, died in numbers beyond count.

"These Hu ghosts all appealed to the Heavenly Emperor, lodging grievances against their lords. Their vengeful spirits seized them, their evil karma unforgotten. Though these Rong and Di tribesmen later repented their sins, never imagining they would encounter the Dao, even in this secondary birth, their death-qi remained unresolved. Their bodily spirits were bound, their forms hollow, their souls absent. For this reason, they lie fallen, lost in stupor, sunk in deep slumber—thus the work of evil.

When the Perfected Master finished speaking, the assembly turned as one to gaze upon the tribesmen. Suddenly, they saw black qi rising from the earth, leveling at a height of ten feet, shrouding the tribesmen. Its color was like pooled ink, dark and indistinct. From within the black qi came the wails of vengeful spirits, some loud, some faint, their cries mournful and choked.

In their sleep, the Rong and Di tribesmen saw their own kin, facing them in sorrow. They beat their eyes shut, their bodies streaming blood, howling and roaring, their shrieks like the cries of wild boars—terrifying to hear. The entire assembly grieved, snapping their fingers and weeping.

The Perfected Master declared: "The karma of good and evil follows one through life and death, like shadow clinging to form, never parting even for a moment. Though the Dao pities them, what can be done?

"This black qi is called yin-qi, also known as killing-qi, resentment-qi, corpse-qi, or turbid-qi. It is the qi of Kun-Mother Earth. Heaven rained black ash upon the tribesmen’s bodies, their hair curling, their forms filthy and greasy."

Then the Perfected One stooped and snapped his fingers. The great earth trembled. In an instant, from the auspicious clouds above, a fine sweet rain descended, bathing the Hu tribesmen. A fragrant wind flowed down, perfuming them. For six days and nights, their eyes could not open. After twelve days, the black qi began to dissipate.

The tribesmen’s bodies were all emaciated, their complexions gone. Boiling blood flowed from their noses, tears streamed from their eyes. Corpse-qi clung to their bodies, their forms blackened through. Their minds and eyes were dim, their sight and hearing unclear. They trembled and faltered, as if mad, each seeing in their eyes their enemies, along with various beasts and ghosts brandishing blades and driving them forth.

The tribesmen raised their hands to grasp at emptiness, scattering in all directions, fleeing beyond the city walls. The elephants they had once ridden, seeing them, bolted in terror, hiding in the grassy marshes, nowhere to be found.

The Rong and Di tribesmen, confronted by their karmic adversaries, lost their eyebrows and hair, blood flowing from their seven orifices. Worms and sores ate into their bones. They forgot their original minds, their good and evil karma responding like echo to sound, like valleys to voices—devoid of feeling, answering only to what was called.

All good and evil is thus, unchanging.

Then the great king, moved by their plight, emerged in distress and prostrated himself before the Dao. The Mystic Master gathered the vengeful spirits of the tribesmen and expounded the Dharma to liberate them.

At that time, the Mystic Master rose from his seat, thrice pinched incense, and bowed from afar to the Jade Pure Heavenly Worthy above. Having completed his obeisance, he returned to his seat. In an instant, his form multiplied into ten thousand millions, gathering the Rong ghosts and bringing them into the assembly. He taught them the foremost meaning of the Three Treasures: that compassion and forbearance lead all practices, the greatest of all virtues. All beings, seen or unseen, who depart from this will long fall into evil destinies, never hearing the Dharma.

He further expounded the Dharma of liberation from birth and death, of non-inversion and non-attachment. Again, he revealed the true mark of reality—emptiness, with nothing substantial. Discriminating thoughts create the illusion of enemies and kin. When the true mark is empty, enemies and kin are also empty.

Then the Perfected Master poured forth a great deluge of mysterious rain, bathing the multitude of ghosts. Next, he taught them the supreme Daoist Dharma: the One Dao, the One Dharma, the One Power of Compassion, the One Rebirth, forever unchanging. The Dharma transforms the Dharma, forever free from birth and death. Without birth and death, there are no karmic adversaries.

"All the fetters and attachments of the law plunge one into the bottomless river of birth and death, tossed by the winds of karma, its waves ceaseless. Departing from this shore of the Dharma, one sinks forever in the mire.

"You ghosts, if you wish to escape birth and death, you must relinquish great enmity and always practice single-minded compassion. Even if others harm or diminish you, receive it as emptiness, never repaying them with an evil heart. This is called relinquishing great enmity. If you relinquish great enmity, you will distance yourself from the enmity of birth and death. When the great matter is settled, nothing remains. No terror can shake you. Your roots will be deep, your stems firm, unshaken by the winds of karma.

"Like a great being who does not begrudge wealth, swiftly repaying debts, refusing to accept what is owed, cutting off and expelling all vengeful creditors—seek the treasure of the Dao, become a patron of the Dharma, not begrudging the filthy wealth of ignorance."

When the multitude of ghosts heard the Mystic Master’s subtle and wondrous Dharma, they abandoned their original minds, leaping for joy, all arousing the mind of forbearance and the supreme Dao. The Supreme Perfected Emperor of the Upper Primordial, his heart opened, radiated a flood of compassionate light, illuminating the multitude of ghosts.

The ghosts, witnessing this divine power, deeply believed in the Daoist Dharma. They awakened to the Dao of eternal life and abiding truth, their minds unwavering. They relinquished their karmic adversaries, emptied themselves, and cultivated harmony and reverence. All beings of different kinds became their companions, desiring to hear the Dharma and enter the Daoist sanctuary.

The Perfected One granted their request. The assembly bowed in reverence, then seated themselves facing north, composed and unmoving.

At that moment, the ailments afflicting the various barbarians were instantly healed, and each simultaneously beheld the Perfected One expounding the Dharma to them. Their bodies and minds awakened, all aroused the intention for the Dao, and together attained liberation.

The Mystic Master addressed them, saying: "You, the various barbarians, have sins and karmic obstructions deeply entrenched, your hindrances not yet dissolved, and thus cannot enter this assembly. For now, remain outside the city in tents of felt, single-mindedly vowing and reflecting, each repenting your transgressions. Six times daily, bow from afar toward the Dharma assembly within the city."

At that time, the gatekeeper named Shenling, having witnessed this, stepped forward, bowed, and inquired of the Perfected One, saying: "I do not understand—why, due to what past or present sins, are these barbarians unable to draw near the site of the Dharma assembly?"

The Perfected One, seated, explained in detail: "These various barbarians were once people of this very kingdom, dwelling on the shady side of the Dark Valley. In a former life, they served as patrons of a great fast. After the feast, they joined together in hunting, setting fire to the mountains and slaughtering over three hundred birds and beasts. Because the merit of their fast was incomplete, they were reborn in borderlands as barbarian chieftains, continuing thus for three lifetimes. Yet by the residual blessing of those creatures, they have now beheld me. Had they not killed living beings, they would have been born into wealthy and noble families within the Central Kingdom. In this life, their residual retribution is not yet exhausted; they conspire to rebel, plotting to harm the Heavenly King of Dao and Virtue. The multitude of ghosts unleashed their poison, slaughtering nine-tenths of their households and kingdom. The wronged spirits lodged their grievances above, and the spirits of these barbarians were seized. For these reasons, they cannot enter the Dao or partake of the Orthodox Dharma, and so are commanded to remain outside the city, bowing from afar toward the Dharma assembly."

The gatekeeper, having heard this, further inquired of the Perfected One: "Your disciple’s duty is to guard and protect, overseeing the imperial carriages. The city gates are bustling, with all directions converging. By imperial decree, I am stationed here, arranging the ranks, ensuring the order of chariots and cavalry as they enter and depart, and instructing those who come to hear the Dharma in proper conduct. Due to these pressing duties, I cannot enter the assembly to bow and listen to the Dharma. Morning and evening, I yearn with all my heart, longing to the utmost. I only beseech the Perfected One to take pity on this solitary and exposed one, and be my refuge and support."

The Perfected One replied: "As long as you possess the heart, single-minded and sincere in resolve, the Great Dao perceives from afar, making no distinction between inner and outer, near and far. The Great Dao ever aids beings with impartiality; even the distant barbarian souls are touched by its mysterious transformation. You, by virtue of your good fortune, personally guard the city gates. All good people come and go morning and evening. You have the most extensive connections with others—now, having beheld me, you have found a true and good spiritual companion."

Recalling past kalpas, I descended for karmic conditions, dwelling upon Mount Danhuo. For seventy minor kalpas, I sat within a forest, expounding to the immortals the method of dwelling and longevity in the Thirty-Two Heavens. At that time, you took the form of a mandarin duck. For three hundred lives, you nested in the cinnabar forest, beholding me morning and evening. At times, you would even carry jujubes and fruits in your beak to offer and supply the Dharma assembly. By virtue of this karmic affinity, you were born in the Middle Kingdom and have once more beheld me."

Hearing the Perfected One’s words, the gatekeeper wept in sorrow and lamentation, prostrating himself upon the ground. Then, the Perfected Lord again addressed the gatekeeper, saying: "Arise and fetch water to bathe your body." When the bathing was complete, the Perfected One said further: "Burn incense, pay reverence, and bow to the Great Compassionate True Emperor in the auspicious clouds above, then prostrate yourself upon the ground."

At that moment, the Perfected One employed his sovereign divine power, causing the gatekeeper’s heart to suddenly awaken. He beheld with perfect clarity the karmic conditions of his past lives. Rising to bow to the Perfected Lord, he wailed and wept in grief. The Perfected Lord said: "For a minor transgression, you have not yet attained the Dao in this life. On your account, I reveal that your beatings of men and beasts were recorded by the netherworld officials, for your heart was poisonous. Had you not committed these acts, your present body would have been liberated. You must strive diligently, ever vigilant and cautious, to avoid official transgressions and all evils. In your next life, you shall surely ascend and be delivered."

The gatekeeper wept and again addressed the Perfected One: "I do not know—can this fault be confessed and repented?" The Perfected One replied: "If you repent throughout your life, you may then be absolved of your sins."

The gatekeeper further inquired: "I do not know—might the secret essentials of the method by which the Venerable Dao expounded dwelling and longevity to the immortals in past kalpas be heard?" The Perfected One replied: "I have divided my body, and even now, within this assembly, I appear as immortals, Daoists, the Heavenly King Father, and the Great Emperor. I shall now expound the method of dwelling and longevity in the heavens above. If you wish to hear it, follow me and listen."

The gatekeeper answered: "I am bound by my duty to guard the gates and dare not wander far." The Perfected Lord said: "I have already divided your body into two." The gatekeeper looked back and saw another self attending to his duties. Thus, he knew the wondrous power of the supreme Dao of the Perfected Master, which transforms according to the heart’s intent. He then followed the Perfected Master into the assembly to listen to the Dharma.

Again, he saw upon the seat a Perfected Master whose golden countenance was identical, and the multitude of people could not distinguish between the true and the responsive manifestations. At that time, the gatekeeper asked the Perfected Master: "The Supreme Great Dao, most true and wondrous, divides its form and scatters its body—how many bodies does it assume?"

The answer came: "The Supreme Great Dao divides its body into qi, pervading everywhere between heaven and earth. Though spoken of as true and responsive, in truth, it is never distinct."

The assembly sighed, saying: "The Dao is present in all things." Then they understood that all beings possess the nature of the Dao, and those who attain the One Dao shall know perfect peace.

At that time, the Dao Lord addressed the great assembly, saying: "Within this Desire Realm, there is one heaven, yet in the four directions, it is spoken of as the Four Heavens. Within these Four Heavens, there are also true immortals who do not wish to ascend further, governing within these heavens. Though the names of the heavens differ, the longevity of the immortals above and below is equal, with no distinction of superiority or inferiority, and all abide without retrogression. Some manifest responsive bodies that undergo birth and death, while their divine transformations conceal and shift, subtly and eternally abiding, serene and unmoving.

Below these Four Heavens, good men and women who perfect their cultivation and become later sages may dwell in this world, their lifespans long or short as they wish. Some enter renowned mountains and grotto palaces, or dwell within the lesser heavens for hundreds of millions of kalpas. When they later wish to ascend, they first enter the Great Yellow Heaven, dwelling for one hundred million kalpas. Next, they ascend to the Great Bright Heaven, dwelling for two hundred million kalpas. Then, they ascend to the Heavens of Hétóng, dwelling for three hundred million kalpas. Next, they ascend to the Heaven of Peaceful Nurturance, dwelling for four hundred million kalpas. Then, they ascend to the Heaven of Primordial Brightness, dwelling for five hundred million kalpas. Next, they ascend to the Seven Luminaries Heaven, dwelling for six hundred million kalpas. Then, they ascend to the Heaven of Zhàohéng, dwelling for seven hundred million kalpas. Next, they ascend to the Heaven of Misty Veil, dwelling for eight hundred million kalpas. Then, they ascend to the Heaven of Harmonious Yang, dwelling for nine hundred million kalpas. Next, they ascend to the Heaven of Reverent Splendor, dwelling for one billion kalpas. Then, they ascend to the Heaven of Radiant Brightness, dwelling for eleven billion kalpas. Next, they ascend to the Heaven of Zhúlùo, dwelling for twelve billion kalpas.

For those true immortals who wish to dwell in these heavens and do not desire further ascent, they may follow their inclination, and their sublime retribution shall be inexhaustible, with no distinction between above and below.

Next, they ascend into the Heaven of Empty Brightness, dwelling for thirteen billion kalpas. Then, they ascend into the Heaven of Serene Stillness, dwelling for fourteen billion kalpas. Next, they ascend into the Heaven of Mysterious Brightness, dwelling for fifteen trillion kalpas. Then, they ascend into the Heaven of Ultimate Jade, dwelling for sixteen trillion kalpas. Next, they ascend into the Heaven of Primordial Bearing, dwelling for seventeen trillion kalpas. Then, they ascend into the Heaven of August Cliff, dwelling for eighteen trillion kalpas. Next, they ascend into the Heaven of Manifest Concentration, dwelling for nineteen trillion kalpas. Then, they ascend into the Heaven of Primordial August, dwelling for twenty trillion kalpas. Next, they ascend into the Heaven of Floating Capaciousness, dwelling for thirty trillion kalpas. Then, they ascend into the Heaven of No-Thought, dwelling for forty trillion kalpas. Next, they ascend into the Heaven of Yuànlè, dwelling for eighty thousand trillion kalpas. Then, they ascend into the Heaven of Boundlessness, dwelling for ninety thousand trillion kalpas. Next, they ascend into the Heaven of Luminous Court, dwelling for one hundred thousand trillion kalpas. Then, they ascend into the Heaven of Primordial Grotto, dwelling for one thousand thousand trillion kalpas. Next, they ascend into the Heaven of Wondrous Completion, dwelling for ten thousand ten-thousand trillion trillion kalpas. Then, they ascend into the Heaven of Forbidden Heights, dwelling for one hundred million trillion trillion kalpas. Next, they ascend into the Heaven of Constant Fusion, dwelling for kalpas as numerous as the atoms of a billion trillion worlds. Finally, they ascend into the Heaven of Jade Prosperity, dwelling for kalpas as numerous as the atoms of a trillion trillion great earths."

Next, they ascend into the Heaven of Brahmā’s Ascent, dwelling freely in the Heaven of Level Peace. Above, they rise into the Great Void, journeying onward to the Great Net, entering the formless, the vast and profound darkness.

From the Heaven of August Layers upward to the Heaven of Great Void, there is no count of kalpas for formation or dissolution. These are reckoned in the kalpas of the Desire Realm to instruct sentient beings.

The Dao-realms above are called the Void and Nothingness. The Dao itself arises from emptiness, its form natural, its body composed of luminous qi, beyond naming or speech. The great sages of the Heavens above the August Layers are likewise.

Even within the four heavens of the Desire Realm, in the grotto-palaces of sacred mountains, later sages and perfected immortals, though they witness the kalpas of heaven and earth, renew their forms day by day. Their spiritual power grows ever greater, never retreating or changing, eternally abiding without alteration.

At each stage of immortal rank, they forever sever the cycle of birth and death, enduring endlessly, beyond all conception. This is not like the heterodox teachings found in the scriptures and commentaries of worldly cults, where demonic impostors usurp the titles of immortals, enjoying celestial pleasures for ninety thousand great kalpas, only to fall back and regress.

These are but essence-ghosts and specters, utterly opposed to the true and correct Dao. Those who hear such teachings hear only falsehood, not the true and right.

At that time, the left attendant of the Supreme Thearch, named Great Chapter, keen and upright in wisdom, steadfast in his nature and fond of the Dao, had not yet attained the true Thearch. His heart still harbored doubt. He stepped forward, bowed deeply, and addressed the Dao Lord, saying:

"Your servant has lived twenty-five years, serving as an inner scribe, attending directly upon the Supreme Ultimate, the most revered in the human world. The people of the four seas come as children, all offices provide for me, and the world looks up in veneration. The karmic retribution is beyond measure.

Yet over a hundred years have passed, and worldly toils weigh heavy with ten thousand cares. Though I dwell in the ancestral temple, my heart wanders far beyond. Governing the people and serving heaven, my mind labors even in sleep and waking."

My steps falter, ears and eyes grow dull, sinews wither and strength wanes, marrow and brain run dry, qi and vigor weaken—every movement brings bitterness and toil. Each glance at my reflection cuts the five emotions like a knife; grief and sorrow compound, leaving no peace in sleep or meal. Not yet a hundred years have passed, yet ten thousand kinds of affliction poison my life.

I know not how true immortals endure through dust and kalpas, their form and spirit unperishing, enduring hunger, toil, and hardship.

Before Great Chapter could finish speaking, the true master’s divine power swiftly restored the Thearch’s countenance to youth—his complexion smooth as congealed fat, his flesh full and radiant. The Thearch’s consort, fair of face with raven hair, skin like ice and snow, teeth white and even, her strength doubled beyond the ordinary, instantly ascended to the joyous heavens above to pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy. She could perform the five transformations: entering wood as wood, entering fire as fire, entering metal as metal, entering water and earth as water and earth. She ascended the mysterious void, stepping lightly without encumbrance.

Then the true lord vanished into formlessness, his whereabouts unknown. After a long while, he reappeared, seated in empty space a thousand *zhang* above the earth, his divine feet cradled by eight-colored cloud-dragons, his form sheltered by seven-hued joyous heavens that followed and responded. The three luminaries encircled and illumined him; his body radiated a penetrating light of compassion. Serene and composed, he spoke to Great Chapter:

"Sevenfold radiance scatters like foam, five-colored relics descend as two elixirs. If even the parents of a great king consume them and gain such divine, untrammeled power—how much more so the supreme Dao? Mere walking corpses with shallow vision dare stand before the Dao, doubting the great sage. I have shown you but a minor path—how do you find its power?

The unsurpassed great Dao transforms the mortal into the sacred, allowing this very body to ascend into formlessness. Vast, it has no exterior; minute, it enters the infinitesimal. My Dao accomplishes this. All other paths, by contrast, aim only for annihilation and cannot instantly transform this body into the dharma-body. Their external methods leave the spirit weak and feeble, unable to preserve or sustain. Life itself becomes a burden: cold and heat break the body, right and wrong clash in the heart, illness and hunger, satiety and ten thousand afflictions poison existence.

Birth, aging, sickness, death—the form of ignorance cannot endure long and seeks early extinction. How much better to follow the supreme Dao, turning the mortal into the sacred, the body like vajra, kalpas like a blink, form renewed with each day, moving in and out without obstruction—what care for burdens? The cycle of birth and death is severed, afflictions do not continue—who can weary such a one? Ascending into formlessness, who can destroy them? Returning to the original void, merging with the great emptiness—who can see them? Divine transformations are free and unconstrained; existence and nonexistence flicker like illusion—who can know them? If the beginning is unknown, how can the end be known?

The ten thousand heavens reside in the heart; the dusty world enters a single hair—yet the original nature remains unchanged. What say you to this?"

Then Great Chapter prostrated himself before the dais, loosened his hair, and knocked his head upon the ground, repenting and reproaching himself. The Great King, Chongguang, seeing his parents suddenly ascend to the mysterious, burned incense and gazed heavenward, knocking his head in reverence to the Heavenly Worthy and the true lord, bowing in shame before the nine barbarians and eighty-one immortals. He spoke thus:

"All conditions harmonize in fulfillment; sacred and profane rejoice together. May the southern Man, western Rong, northern Di, and all frontier tribes—those in distant lands who have not heard the true Dharma, who wear horns and fur, beast-hearted yet human-faced, sentient but unenlightened, who drink blood and eat raw flesh, all moving and breathing beings, both hidden and manifest, humans and ghosts—may they all awaken to the cycle of birth and death and enter the stream of the Dao."

When these words were spoken, the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion from the Joyous Heavens above, together with the true lord seated beside him, radiated a light of compassion that illumined the lower realms. Their voices of mercy reached all, and the various beings each saw the Heavenly Worthy descend before them, expounding the six perfections and the six supernatural powers—the gateway to supreme, unobstructed liberation.

At that time, the great assembly, hearing the Heavenly Worthy’s words, opened their hearts and awakened their minds. They understood that conditioned dharmas do not escape birth and death, and that those who leave the household life to cultivate the Dao all attain enduring existence.

Then the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion poured forth the rain of Dharma, moistening each according to their karmic conditions—some deeply, some shallowly—yet appearing equally in form. Though the assembly beheld the same countenance, their faces differed; though a single voice expounded the Dharma, each received it differently, their understanding and faith varying, their responses dissimilar.

Among this assembly, there were three kinds of beings: the parents of the great king, whose fortunate karmic conditions, though unmoving, evoked a response, attaining the Dao in an instant. The men and women of the divine realm received its blessings and benefits, enabling their bodies to attain longevity, preserving purity and emptiness, pairing with the Dao, and receiving deliverance in this very life. Their form and spirit would not decay, indestructible as vajra.

When the various Rong and Di tribes heard of long life, their minds grew confused, their spirits frenzied, their body hair stood on end. Some slackened in all four limbs, unable to control themselves; others grew dazed and fell into deep sleep, roaring without awareness. The great Dao, moved by compassion, did not abandon them.

Then the true master addressed the tribes, saying: "Each of you, rise and burn incense, and make your vows and practices known."

When the various tribes had finished burning incense, their karmic conditions bound them, leaving them unable to speak further. They all vowed to cultivate the Dharma of karmic conditions and together entreated the true master of the great Dao to expound the path of extinction and deliverance. The true master assented. The assembly rejoiced, bowing as one, and heard the true master expound the Dharma of extinction and deliverance. The various Rong and Di tribes were freed from the affliction of resentment toward the Confucian way.

The true master further instructed the tribes, saying: "Good sons, cultivating the Dao and planting karmic roots is like a skilled farmer. In the season of the three yangs, he diligently harnesses his oxen, guiding them with hooks and ropes, reinforcing embankments tightly, treading through mud and mire. He enriches the soil with fine manure, then selects good seed, clearing away weeds and refuse, ensuring proper warmth and moisture. Next, he tends the seedlings, removing harmful grasses, mounding earth around the roots, watching over them morning and evening, preventing the six kinds of livestock from trampling or eating them. Thus, after three months, the seedlings flourish, lush and verdant, their beauty unmatched on land or water, free from harm or blight."

When cool autumn brings the harvest to fruition, the crops ripen evenly across high and low fields. The master then commands servants and laborers to gather and store the yield, with warehouse keepers overseeing its safekeeping, preventing any loss or waste. The grain serves only for sustenance, its reserves ever-growing, ensuring the household’s abundance. Surplus is shared with the poor, relieving hunger and want, its generosity vast and far-reaching. Such boundless virtue and kindness ascend to the heavens, and all beings—seen and unseen—guard the good. Blessings and power thus come to fruition, harmonizing all endeavors, fulfilling every desire, leaving no wish unanswered. Just as the skilled farmer reaps immeasurable profit in the end, so too, good sons, must you, the great assembly, diligently cultivate the field of Dao and blessings, your hearts unwavering in effort. Like that farmer, you shall surely attain your reward without fail.

Good sons, in a past kalpa, north of the Dark Valley, the queen of King Xiuchou of the Resting Chieftains conceived and bore twin sons. Until the age of six, their appearances were identical, and the king cherished them, often holding them in his arms. At seven, they were sent afar to seek a master’s instruction, receiving the same teachings.

The king himself named these sons: the first was called Shaoguang, the second Shaoming. The two studied together, and the king would often go in person to admonish them, urging them not to grow idle or lazy. Their master instructed them in proper conduct and imparted his arts and skills.

At that time, the two sons would gather each morning to receive their lessons. Once their studies were complete, they would each return to their own quarters to ponder the meaning. Shaoguang recited aloud, then sat in silent contemplation, rising early and retiring late without sleep. Shaoming, however, was by nature indolent and prone to drowsiness, indulging in wine and sensual pleasures, his spirit restless and agitated. Though he read the texts, he gave no thought to their meaning. When he saw his father, he would cunningly feign diligence, never letting the scroll leave his hands. His nature, too, was dark and malicious. Their master dared not discipline him strictly, for Shaoming always carried a blade, his temper violent and rebellious.

When he reached seventeen, the king assembled his ministers to discuss the succession, commanding the nobles to examine the princes before the assembly and compare their merits. Shaoguang’s skills and arts were flawless, his answers without fault; he mastered all worldly arts, and his nature was kind and benevolent. When Shaoming was questioned, he could not respond to even a single query, having distorted his master’s teachings and misled his peers. The master addressed the king: “The prince is of a violent disposition, disobedient to instruction, and refuses to heed my teachings. His nature is treacherous and dangerous.” The king, unwilling to believe this, ordered a search of his person, and indeed, a blade was found. The master said, “If I cannot even protect myself, how dare I instruct him?” The king then banished Shaoming beyond the city walls.

Later, harboring resentment, Shaoming plotted rebellion. Before he could gather his followers, his scheme was discovered. Fearing punishment, he fled to the borderlands, but the neighboring kingdom refused him refuge and seized him, sending him back. Ashamed to face his father, he held his breath and died. The ministers deliberated and declared him a traitorous son and rebellious minister; they refused to bury him, casting his body into the wilderness. Birds, beasts, insects, and ants shunned his malevolence, leaving his flesh untouched. His fat and marrow flowed like rivers, soaking the grasses and marshes. For his lack of faith, he brought about his own destruction. Heaven and earth showed no pity; gods and men alike despised him. His soul was exiled, condemned for ten thousand kalpas, never to be redeemed. Even if he were reborn, he would lose his human form.

Shaoguang was then enthroned as crown prince. He convened the nobles, granted a general amnesty throughout the land, and ascended the throne in a cloud of incense. Gazing into the distance like a deity, his countenance was upright and his demeanor gentle, his virtue as warm as spring. The four seas were at peace, and the realm prospered. Sages from distant lands gathered like turtles and phoenixes, aiding and supporting the kingdom, uniting the wills of men and gods. Wind and rain came in their seasons, and the hundred grains ripened.

The crown prince was temperate, benevolent, loyal, and forgiving, kind and filial. At thirty, the king abdicated the throne, entrusting the governance of the realm to him. The prince declined three times, but fearing disobedience would make him an unfilial son, he bowed to his father and accepted the throne. He ruled by the Dao, issuing no extraneous decrees. Before a year had passed, praises filled the roads; men and gods alike submitted to him. Auspicious signs flourished: lingzhi mushrooms filled the courtyards, unicorns and phoenixes soared and gathered, immortals descended to wander, and clouds of immortals spread in all directions. The True Lords of the Upper Prime took him as their disciple, imparting to him the essentials of the Dao. He wore the Register of Life at his waist, and divine might protected and aided him.

At ninety, though aged, he became youthful again, his complexion like that of a child, his ears and eyes sharp, his vital qi abundant and nourishing. His five viscera flourished, his white hair turned black, and his decayed teeth regrew. The Immortal King of Supreme Medicine compounded divine elixirs for him, restoring his qi and form so that he never aged. At one hundred and seventy, he one day relinquished his kingdom and ascended to the Great Empyrean. To this day, he reigns in the Heaven of Supreme Purity, dwelling in the Jade Flower and Jasper Terrace, enduring without end, ever cultivating the supreme Daoist arts.

For his lifelong faith, his destiny was fulfilled. The Dao does not fail those who do not fail it—this is the meaning here. Good sons, all of you in this assembly must establish faith in the Dao, diligently cultivate meritorious deeds, and avoid untimely death. This is the foundation of the Dao.

At that time, the various tribes, having heard the supreme Dharma, received it with joy. The great assembly bowed their heads in reverence, all at once awakening to the causes and conditions of the Dao, their hearts free from worldly attachments. They prepared their attire, mounted their elephants, bid farewell to the Perfected Ones, and returned to their homelands. By the power of this Dharma, the barbarian spirits crossed the Southern Palace and were reborn in the Land of Ultimate Bliss in the Eastern Realm of the Dao.

The Chinese men likewise returned to their homes, revering and cultivating the supreme Dharma. Among the Daoist priests present, ninety-seven thousand attained the six penetrations and unrestrained freedom. Some followed others to wander the lower realms. The immortals of the Nine Barbarians ascended into the formless, their whereabouts unknown.

The king’s parents likewise ascended to the Celebratory Empyrean, where the Jade Purity Heavenly Worthy bestowed upon the king the title of Supreme Emperor, naming him Master of the Cavernous Mystery and Great Mystery. He also conferred upon the queen the title of Immortal Lady of the Mystic Terrace, granting her twenty-four female immortals as attendants, flying canopies and swift chariots, to ascend to the Cavernous Heavens and preside over newly initiated female Daoist priests.

At that time, the Perfected Master, still dwelling in the Cold Forest to save the world from its flames, remained with the True Lords of the Jade Purity in the Mystic Realm, serene and unmoving. On the four seasons and eight solar terms, they would emit radiant sounds. All living beings relied upon them for sustenance.

Thus concludes the seventh scroll of *The Jade Purity Scripture of the Great Dao of the Supreme*.
Beginning of the eighth scroll of *The Jade Purity Scripture of the Great Dao*.

**Scroll the Eighteenth: Secluded Dwelling**

At that time, in the Cloud Palace of the Jade Purity Heaven, the Right Terrace’s Perfected Sovereign of the Upper Prime, named Compassionate Forbearance and also called Penetrating Mystery, oversaw the thirty-four heavens above, governing the rise and fall of the Three Realms and the fortunes of calamity or blessing. He held the pivot of all heavens and grasped the mechanisms of the nine earths. Turning the numinous net and revolving the jade balance, he polished the Two Radiant Sceneries and illumined the Five Celestial Luminaries, sprinkling sweet dew and steaming forth clouds and rain, transforming the untransformed and compiling the hidden storehouses. All beings that partake of qi were thus provided their proper due.

He commanded the host of dragons and drove the myriad spirits, regulating and guiding the upright qi, diffusing benevolence and harmony. Thus the four seasons never faltered, the eight solar terms remained constant, and the twenty-four qi never strayed from their eternal norms. He rectified the Yellow Path and opened the primordial heavens, curbing the yin to form the vast darkness and anchoring the yang to perpetuate the limpid waves. He dispelled the fire essence in the southern blaze and extinguished the water spirits in the northern cove, planted the Five Sacred Fungi in the celestial fields, and nurtured the Responsive Emperor in the Purple Tenuity. The Twelve Perfected Officials transformed and nourished all living beings, while the Sixfold Ceremonial Might of the numinous spirits encircled and aided their forms and souls.

Cloud-script manifested of itself, and the celestial scriptures shone in the void. The myriad multitudes followed his example, and wisdom arose daily. Without speech, he transformed; without action, he accomplished. He suppressed the partial qi of the Six Heavens, established the Four Offices to govern life, cultivated the hundred grains to sustain existence, and revealed divine medicines to guide the living. For hundreds of millions of kalpas, his deep roots stood unshaken. By the Dao he mended what was broken—thus did he attain such mastery.

At that time, in the Great Tang world, there was a king who practiced the Dao, named Zhaode, of the Xuan clan. The entire kingdom—ministers and subjects alike—devoted their hearts to the practice of the Dao. In that era, thirty-six thousand petty kingdoms along the frontiers, their kings gazing from afar at his majestic power, turned their thoughts inward and reflected. Each led their ministers and officials in grand ceremonial display, bearing incense, flowers, banners, and canopies, performing exquisite music. With utmost sincerity and open hearts, they spared no effort from the moment of their initial resolve. Arriving at the sacred precinct, their thoughts flowed in unbroken succession, free of杂念. Assembled before the great kingdom, they burned incense and made their vows, yearning with reverent longing toward the vast emptiness of the upper firmament, their earnest aspirations fixed as if awaiting something. They prayed for the Ninefold Mystery and Seven Ancestors, for all the multitudes of the people, and for the king himself, saying: "May we attain the supreme Great Dao, that it may shelter and pity us, prolong the kalpic destiny, compassionately create all beings, release them from the snares of existence, and absolve all transgressions. May those in darkness and light alike awaken together. May the root of faith be established, that they may bear the ultimate Dharma and realize enlightenment in this very body."

These kings presented their lofty vows for a day and a night, supplicating six times; for a day and a night, they performed music six times. Their melodies were harmonious and refined, subtle and pure, so clear that all who heard them were moved to awaken the Dao-mind, abandon evil, and embrace goodness without doubt or hesitation. The fragrance of incense rose and suffused the imperial court; their whispered words, pure and flowing, reached the ears of the Perfected Lords.

At that moment, on the morning of the seventh day of the first month, the Heavenly Worthy of the Cloud Palace responded to the living with formlessness and taught sentient beings with silent sound. Extending his divine feet beyond the vast emptiness, he plucked the Dharma-finger in the distant void. True light eclipsed the sun, illuminating even the deepest obscurities; subtle tones, pure and flowing, were answered by all in attendance. He polished the eyes of the mundane, unsealed the ears of the vulgar, and swept forth the resounding music of the empty void, praising their compassion and forbearance: "Excellent, excellent! Compassion and forbearance protect the world—no power compares. Ever with the Dao-eye he gazes upon beings, ever with the Dao-heart he pities beings, ever with the Dao-hand he guides beings, ever with the Dao-body he transforms beings, ever with the Dao-feet he leads beings, ever as the Dao-father he cherishes beings, ever as the Dao-mother he nurtures beings, ever as the Dao-friend he befriends beings."

Then the various heavenly youths, hearing from afar the radiant tones from above, rejoiced and gathered their thoughts, each saying: "The Dao does not act in vain—today its fruition is manifest!" These heavenly youths redoubled their diligence, casting aside杂念, letting the Dao govern itself, and desiring nothing else. Though they heard the rare sound, it was still bounded by thirty-six thousand heavens and earths. They wished only that the supreme Dao would not depart, dared to hope for its mysterious regard, and prayed that flesh and bone might together ascend, becoming true immortals forever, that the nine ancestors might receive blessings, their souls delivered to the Southern Palace—thus would the world know great peace and the people rejoice.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy of the Cloud Palace again expounded in subtle tones, addressing the kings: "The Son of Heaven follows Heaven without contrivance; the people serve the Son of Heaven without toil. When the Son of Heaven and the people together know peace, then there is no sorrow, no care. Good men, though the supreme Great Dao dwells above thirty-six thousand mysterious heavens, it looks down upon the mortal realm as if upon its own palm. You kings who diligently cultivate the supreme Dao without laxity—none shall fail to become an exalted sage. It is like a skilled farmer who plants well: having sown the mother, he must reap the child. You who uphold the Dao of great peace—how could you not abide in eternal joy? I bestow the ultimate Dharma, and the Perfected Lords above know all things and attain great peace. When the Perfected transform those below, it is no different from my own work. If you wish to serve the Dao, and aspire to be delivered in this very body, this is not difficult—only ask how resolute your will may be. None who study fail to succeed; none who sow fail to grow. Examine the source, and the stream will follow of itself—this is the natural principle, certain and without doubt."

At that time, though the kings revered and assented to the teaching, their minds had not yet penetrated the truth. Secretly, they wished to behold the Heavenly Worthy. The Heavenly Worthy, knowing their intent, commanded the Perfected Lord Tongxuan to strike the divine chime of the great void and play the words of the empty zither, saying to the kings: "Emptiness and purity are the root of the Dao; the great void is the body of the Dao. Emptiness and purity are unstained; the root of the Dao is without deviation. The true person values the ultimate Dharma; the vulgar world craves clamor and noise."

"Those who wish to gaze upon the walking corpses among men
Rush headlong in pursuit of glory and splendor.
Beholding these cloud-palace Perfected Ones,
All who turn toward the Dao grow proud and extravagant.

Eyes and ears no longer see or hear;
Discernment knows no obstruction.
Abiding in stillness, they guard non-action,
Restraining their wills from tangled blossoms.

Perfect penetration holds no divergent aims;
Forgotten thoughts are the true home.
The Dharma-body ever abides in emptiness and nothingness,
Its measure embracing the great void.

Only then may one rend the net of dust,
Crush the thicket of afflictions.
Standing alone beyond the flow of俗,
Darkly one merges with the Dao.

The Dao’s root admits no seeing;
Inward vision observes the mind itself.
Knots and fetters cannot endure,
Obstructions and burdens daily dissolve and sink.

Lofty steps tread the edge of cloud-cliffs,
Within the void they savor the tones of virtue.
Seated unmoving in their place,
The worthy and sage naturally seek one another.

Wherever they dwell, they store kindness and benefit,
Withdrawing their traces to roost in mountain forests.
Donning coarse robes, they draw in streaming radiance,
Burning incense, they lay bare their hearts.

When merit is complete, they merge with the Dao’s body;
The myriad transformations all ascend without fail.
Though dust-kalpas have not yet dawned,
In profound obscurity there is no beginning or end.

I tell you the mechanism of ascending to Perfection:
When virtue is full, the Dao grows ever more vast."

At that time, the kings beheld these numinous wonders,
Sighing in awe at what they had never before seen.
Each turned to the others and said:
"The Dao’s majesty and spirit are present everywhere.
The voice of the great void still utters subtle words;
The golden mouth’s speech—how wondrously refined!

Reflecting on our change of heart,
Scarcely three months have passed,
Yet we have already seen and heard the supreme, peerless Dharma.
If we cultivate it lifelong, we shall surely not abandon it.

We and our followers have received the Dao’s grace;
We must not retreat and lose our former merit.
Let each of us relinquish our thrones,
Leave the world to follow the Dao, and take up the homeless life.
To be delivered in this very body—what joy could surpass it?

To indulge in glory and fame,
To wield power over the four seas—
All this cannot escape the terrors of punishment,
The loss of good fortune,
Birth, aging, sickness, death,
Withering decay and putrefaction,
Sinking into the dregs of filth—
Truly, this is cause for lament."

Then the heavenly kings at once abdicated,
Entrusting their thrones to meritorious ministers.
Seven months and seven days later,
They burned incense and paid homage to the void.

The great ministers vowed:
"We wish to follow the great Dao,
Seek to leave the world’s afflictions,
Dwell hidden in mountain forests,
And enter the Mystery Terrace."

Having made this vow,
At that time, thirty-six thousand Perfected Ones of the Mysterious Heavens,
And the luminous portals of the ten directions’ lands,
Outshone their usual brilliance.
Immortal mists and auspicious clouds
Poured forth sweet dew.
Nine-colored clouds
Wove phoenix patterns,
Enveloping the four heavens,
Their light illuminating the world below.
Gentle winds intoned the flutes,
Breathing forth sacred hymns.
Heavenly music played of itself,
Chanting the true scriptures.
The harmonious assembly of sounds
Defied all naming.

All this was the Dao’s qi flowing forth from the cloud-palace Perfected Emperors,
Uttering the correct tones,
Transforming the kings’ bodies,
Causing their true qi to swiftly respond,
Turning the common into the sagely.

At that time, the Perfected Emperors merely used their majestic spirit
To respond to the kings’ karmic resonance.
They did not manifest their Dharma-bodies to the common,
Expounding as heaven does—
For the Dao speaks without speaking,
Yet through the four seasons transforms the myriad things.

Heaven, as the Dao’s disciple,
Can yet accomplish this.
The supreme great Dao transforms things through qi,
Its true essence flowing and changing,
Invisible and inaudible.

Only those who receive deliverance
See and hear for themselves;
Those who do not receive deliverance
Cannot attain such vision."

At that time, each of the kings gazed upward and recited the celestial scriptures and cloud-borne sacred verses—thirty-nine chapters in all. On the seventh day of the tenth month, they burned incense and made vows, entreating entry into the Mystic Terrace. By then, the kings could already pass in and out of formlessness, sitting yet vanishing, their presence elusive and unfathomable. Their eyes emitted flowing light, and their bodies generated the five qi.

Once within the Mystic Terrace, each sat beneath a jade tree, shaded by its jeweled branches, resting upon golden thrones. Cloud-dragons flanked their seats, while immortal youths stood in attendance. Heaven bestowed fragrant flowers to uphold their rightful steps. Behind them rose walls of azure jade, and before them lay pools of golden essence and the numinous waters of the Five Rivers, moistened by nectarous streams. The Mother of the Nine Earths planted golden mushrooms, and dragon blossoms exhaled their qi, their fragrance suffusing all.

At that moment, the kings’ spiritual eyes grew luminous, and they beheld the Perfected Emperors as though near at hand. The knots of their mortal coils dissolved, and their perception became boundless and unimpeded. Not only the thirty-six thousand heavens and earths, but the ten directions of the cosmos lay before them like the palm of a hand. Each king sat beneath the jade groves, remaining in that place for nine hundred million great kalpas without shifting.

Then the Perfected Emperors of the Cloud Palace bestowed upon the kings the title of *Middle Perfected*. After another hundred million great kalpas, they conferred the rank of *Upper Perfected*. After yet another ten thousand million great kalpas, they appointed them as *Posterior Sage Dao Lords*, granting the title *Supreme Void Perfected Kings*, who to this day govern within the Ever-Mystic Heaven.

For the sake of hearing the Dao, the kings’ forms reverted to youth, their appearance as radiant as in their prime. Even the sixteen youths could divide their bodies to fill the void, withdrawing their forms into nothingness, transcending the perceptions of ordinary beings—something no lesser immortal or member of the four assemblies could comprehend. Such was the subtlety of their hidden efficacy, their wondrous subtlety beyond all comparison. At times they appeared in form yet spoke no word; at others, they spoke yet left no trace. In accomplishing one task, they fulfilled the essence of the myriad Dao, the gateway to all mysteries—thus their transformations knew no bounds.

Yet the world’s decline brings only turmoil, empty debates, and false distinctions, laboring in vain from beginning to end, with no true refuge. How grievous the suffering of the lost, sunk in dissipation and drowning in delusion! Without enlightened teachers or true scriptures, how can they find protection and escape the peril of death? Those who cherish the true must refine their discernment, carefully distinguishing authenticity from falsehood, testing orthodoxy from heresy. Seek the pivotal essence without doubt. Devote yourself wholeheartedly to deliverance, and you will know no confusion.

The superior practitioner of the Dao attains sagehood in this very body. The middling practitioner undergoes transformation, vanishing like a cicada’s molt—though appearing to die, they do not perish. The inferior practitioner toils for kalpas without end, passing through birth and death for countless ages.

The Dao declares: These kings, too, labored through birth and death, enduring kalpas of toil, governing the people and serving heaven, their merit known to the Supreme Emperor. They trusted in the great Dao, renounced worldly glory, entered the mountains to seek the Way, tasted a hundred herbs, expelled the old and absorbed the new, diligently studied the supreme scriptures, and grasped their profound meaning. They practiced compassion ceaselessly, benefiting all beings, and remained single-minded in their devotion, guarding the One. Distancing themselves from the world’s defilement, the Dao willed it so. Together, they received deliverance and became Posterior Sages.

After countless hundreds of millions of great kalpas, the *Primordial Perfected Dao of the Upper Origin* ascended to become the *Posterior Sage Dao Lords of the Thirty-Six Thousand Heavens*, each governing a single heaven and overseeing the transformation of the world in turn. The *Primordial Perfected Emperors* ascended into formlessness, ceasing all movement and activity. Though still and silent, vast and empty, they responded without intention, their influence mirroring the resonance of spirit and echo. Without emotion, they yet acted, unaware of their own doing—thus it is called *ceasing all movement and activity*.

At that time, in the world of Great Tang, the Dao flourished for nine kalpas. Eight years later, in the year *renzi*, on the seventh day of the first month, there was a great minister named Guangde, of the Wang clan, already a hundred years old. His hearing remained keen, his vitality strong. He governed with righteousness, never betraying the people’s trust. All living beings, even the lowliest, basked in his virtue. At the turning of the four seasons and the eight solar terms, he established altars for fasting, exhausting his wealth to make offerings with utmost sincerity.

The ministers of neighboring lands, hearing of his integrity, revered his virtuous reputation from afar and secretly dispatched envoys bearing gifts to honor the great minister. Such tributes continued unbroken for nine years. Minister Guangde, sensing their devotion, burned incense morning and night. The fragrant smoke subtly perfumed the ministers of the neighboring lands, their bodies suffused with its scent.

Each night, they dreamed of a divine being, sixteen feet tall, standing close before them. The ministers thought to themselves: *Could this be the virtuous man we honor? Has the great Dao taken notice of us, revealing his majestic presence?* Their faith deepened, and their reverence grew.
