They, too, burned incense morning and night, making vows, and maintained purity for a thousand days.

On the seventh day of the tenth month, at midnight, they suddenly saw in the courtyard two youths holding divine candles, who proclaimed the minister’s teaching: *If you wish to meet him, come discuss the Dao and its virtue.* The ministers, hearing the youths’ words, crawled out in prostration, bowing to the youths while gazing at the divine candles, too awestruck to bid farewell. After taking eight steps, they suddenly found themselves before a great city, its towers and palaces resplendent. There they beheld Minister Guangde, bowing and exchanging greetings.

After a long while, they marveled at the wonder, realizing they had traversed over eight thousand *li*. The nearest ministers had come from three to five thousand *li* away. In an instant, they had arrived in the Central Kingdom. In all, fifty-nine thousand ministers, moved by the Dao, vowed to renounce their ranks and enter the mountains to cultivate the Way.

The candle-bearing youths numbered one hundred eighteen thousand. All were *Middle Perfected* attendants of the Right Terrace of the Cloud Palace, who, sensing those of sincere devotion, illuminated them with divine candles to steady their minds and bodies, keeping their eyes from straying and their ears from wayward sounds. They grasped the essentials of the Dao and hastened to the sacred precinct.

Within and without, harmony and goodness ripened, their karmic fruits now fully mature. Swiftly they attained the radiance of the divine candles of the Dao-perfected. Such were their merits and virtues.

Then the youths gathered all the divine candles into a single torch of wisdom, its breadth and length precisely over six hundred *li*. Its light was cool and clear, penetrating and illuminating without end. Beholding this torch of wisdom, the ministers’ hearts and eyes became perfectly lucid, and all exclaimed in wonder: “Never before have we seen such a thing!” First they bowed to the youths, then to the torch of wisdom, and spoke thus:

“Disciples are but coarse flesh, reeking of blood and bone, devoid of past blessings, having planted no good causes. Our virtue is meager, our merit slight—unworthy to hear the Dao. Yet the Great Dao, in its compassion, has shown us this rarity. We are overwhelmed by its grace and favor, joy and awe intermingling.”

The youths replied: “The Great Dao is merciful; there is no need for self-deprecation. You, all of you, have abandoned worldly honors and emoluments to dwell in the mountains and seek the Dao. First, you must enter this torch of wisdom. Then, holding fast to your resolve, you shall dispel demons, dwell high among cliffs and peaks, chew the true scriptures, and chant the celestial texts. Brush away the drifting dust from the round mirror, wield the golden essence that subdues the sun. Let the chamber of spirit congeal its pearl, let the Eight Might emit their rays, let incense smoke ascend to convey your hearts’ devotion. Your merits shall be heard in the imperial court, and you shall ascend to the Purple Dawn. Before long, through diligent toil in the mountain forests, you shall attain it. Our Dao is most divine—what is heard and seen is never false. Only those of utmost sincerity may obtain it.

If you wish to dwell in the mountains, you must uphold the luminous precepts: do no harm to what you hold dear, be it the young or the frail; avoid all impurity, and keep every movement and stillness pure. A single lapse topples ten thousand paths. How can you hope to attain clarity without first seeing and hearing these truths?”

Then the assembled ministers emerged from the radiance of the torch, kneeling in reverence to receive the precepts. The Youth addressed them, saying: "The precepts are caution itself. Though you possess wisdom, you have yet to discern the subtle. Those of keen intellect, relying on their own cleverness, lightly transgress what is forbidden, unafraid of the divine might. Before attaining the Dao, they remain bound by form and measure, their every movement and stillness flawed, their toil yielding no hope. Only when one attains freedom, moving without hindrance, ascending into formlessness, and forgetting all appearances—"

At that moment, the Youth expounded the precepts to the ministers, saying: "If you wish to dwell in the mountains, first cast aside the burdens of worldly affairs. What the Dao does not do, do not force yourself to do; what the true path does not tread, do not force yourself to tread. Simply know how to practice the Dao and preserve your body, without coveting other matters. Those who wish to abandon the human world and dwell in mountain forests should first seek like-minded companions, no more than three or five. The superior practitioner dwells in the mountains with no more than two or three. Too many bring noise and distraction, the mind cannot focus, and mutual scrutiny may lightly offend the divine might.

Do not tread in filth, nor mix with men and women indiscriminately. Do not discuss worldly affairs, nor sit or lie in carelessness. Do not let the mind wander into depravity, nor heed external matters. Though dwelling in the mountains, if the heart’s resolve is not single-minded, defilement will flow like a river, and perverse winds will come and go. The marrow and brain will wither, the teeth will decay, and the eyes will lose their brightness. Slothful in bathing, the skin will accumulate grime. The true qi will depart far away, leaving nothing to hope for. Exposed to the Three Luminaries, the benevolent spirits will not protect you. Indulging in sleep and rising late, neglecting offerings and rituals—on the Azure Tablets of the True Lords, no merit will be recorded. With sins uncorrected, the Nine Mysteries will be examined, the Four Offices will impeach, and you will be immediately dismissed in disgrace.

If thoughts are not focused and杂念纷扰, the true essence will not be preserved, and evil spirits will take hold. Unable to distinguish right from wrong, you will entertain perverse views. When true persons build their chambers, you will fail to show reverence. Clothing, ritual implements, and miscellaneous objects will be used improperly, their defilement flowing like a flood, causing the hun and shen to sink and stagnate. Even in relieving yourself, you will not know the proper orientation, polluting the sacred springs. The Earth Officials will record your transgressions, and your sins will fill the Black Register, to be borne by your living body.

Some may secretly peruse the celestial scriptures, recklessly transmitting what is not true, and when the scriptures are recited, their errors will implicate the Nine Mysteries. Some may reveal hidden secrets, treating the true texts with disdain. Some may speak boastfully, indulging in great anger or excessive joy, leaking the hidden classics and disrupting inner and outer harmony. Some may reveal true teachings, recounting their own dreams and fancies. Some may eat meat, drink wine, and crave pungent flavors, disturbing the spirit with vexation and losing the upright qi. Some may burn incense and pay homage at dawn, yet glance around, inviting demons to bring calamity—such offerings the Heavenly Emperor will not hear.

These prohibitions are what the true Dao abhors. Those who conceal their learning must deeply guard against them." Then the Youth addressed the ministers, saying: "Good men, those who study the Dao as the Dao, seek the perverse as the perverse. By analogy, this may be understood. Though you are worthy, you have not yet discerned the sacred teachings. Those who study the sacred Dao follow the sacred words, which are upright. By seeking it with uprightness, one may then escape the calamities of death and endure eternally.

Good men, those who cultivate my Dao will refine their form and spirit, transforming the mortal into the sacred, no longer subject to death. They will ascend into formlessness, free from all entanglements." Then the ministers rose from the ground, kneeling in response: "Though we have the heart to turn toward the Dao, we have not yet understood its principles, nor grasped the subtle mysteries of its regulations. We fear that we have not cultivated merit in the past and have no virtue to rely upon. Our years are already advanced, our strength and vigor declining. If misfortune suddenly strikes, we will be forever cut off from the path of life. Our hearts are heavy with sorrow, and afflictions weigh upon us.

Moreover, we have heard worldly people slander the great Dao, saying: 'Those who study the Dao cannot escape life and death.' They recklessly spread such worldly talk, offending the True Lords. We beg you to resolve our doubts and dispel our anxieties." The True Youth replied: "Good men, what you have heard are the mad words of fools, not the teachings of the utmost sages. Why is this so? In times past, there was a foolish band of three brothers who heard that the perfected ones avoid harm, dwelling in mountain forests, sipping from the mysterious stream, savoring the sweet dew, their form and spirit unwaning, their complexion like that of youths, enduring for billions of kalpas. Not understanding the subtlety of the supreme method, the emptiness and purity of the mysterious and wondrous, the three brothers, relying on their own shallow views, sought immortality.

The eldest brother, named Dark Child, chiseled into a sheer cliff, forged iron chains, and bound himself to a bed, sitting suspended in midair. Without food or drink, he died of hunger and thirst. The second brother, named Great Gatekeeper, rode a raft into the sea. Suddenly encountering a great wind, he drowned. The third brother, named Dullard, thought to evade death by entering deep into a stone cave, but was suddenly devoured by a poisonous dragon. From then on, the ignorant have followed in their footsteps without cease, recording these tales and spreading them as grand stories. Not grasping their profound meaning, they claim that the perfected ones study the Dao in the same way, spreading confusion and recklessly misleading those below.

The deaf and blind of the world are truly pitiable. I sigh for you all, who wish to study the true Dao—do not believe such perverse teachings, lest you waste your entire life. Not only this life, but in countless lives to come, you will not encounter the Dao. Those who plant trees, though they may experience the initial causes, must surely know that they will reap the corresponding fruits. If one dwells in evil causes while cultivating merit, even after billions of kalpas of cycling through evil causes, one cannot attain the fruit. Just as those who study the perverse are bound to it life after life, the perverse cause unbroken, they will have no opportunity to enter the upright path. The same is true for those who study the upright.

The true persons and superior practitioners are upright in all things—what is called upright body, upright heart, upright wisdom, upright life. If life has an end, it is not called upright life; if wisdom is perverse, it is not called upright wisdom. Good men, you must now understand: the Dao does not act in vain; it is transmitted only to the right person."

To transmit it to the unworthy is called reckless leakage. The prohibitions and precepts are solemn and weighty—this must not be unknown.

At that time, the assembled ministers, having received the prohibitions and precepts, again entreated the Perfected Youth, seeking to receive the *Scripture of Preserving the Spirit Within* and the Dao of nurturing the nascent soul and fostering the embryonic spirit. The Perfected Youth replied: "The *Scripture of Preserving the Spirit Within* and the Dao of nurturing the nascent soul and fostering the embryonic spirit are both dragon-script and phoenix-writings, celestial seal-characters of cloud-seal and heavenly patterns, radiant and resplendent, reviving the dead and restoring the bones. It is also called the *Precious Writ of All Heavens*. Without this writ, Heaven cannot broadly cover; Earth cannot generate and complete; Sun and Moon cannot illuminate; the constellations cannot align their courses; rivers and seas would dry at their sources. Without this writ, the Son of Heaven cannot transform the myriad multitudes. This scripture is treasured by the Supreme Sovereign, descending to the world but once in ninety thousand great kalpas.

Though I have received the golden edict of the Supreme Perfected Emperor, granting you the ordinances for entering the mountains, I have not yet received separate instruction to bestow the token of the precious scripture. If you wish to hear and see it, wait but a moment."

Thereupon, the youth burned incense and entered still contemplation, bowing from afar toward the upper realms and kneeling in reverence. At that time, the assembled ministers also burned incense, prostrating themselves with their heads to the ground. At mid-morning, suddenly they sensed an intense divine fragrance from above, suffusing all present. Fragrant blossoms advanced with the sun, nine-colored silken veils shimmering, filling their eyes with luster. As day turned to night, after the second watch, nine-colored streaming auroras illuminated the vast heavens. A fragrant wind blew the auroras into formation, shaping celestial script—each character a full *zhang* in size, its radiance dazzling, eclipsing the stars and moon. Then they heard celestial music pervading the ten directions, harmonious and serene, beyond all comparison. For nine days and nine nights, the sound continued before ceasing.

In an instant, from within the streaming auroras, a voice began to chant the opening of the *Inner Chapters of Preserving Life*—ethereal and resonant, vast and flowing, measured and harmonious, its melody stirring the floating clouds. Heaven rained fragrant blossoms in a dense, drifting haze. The streaming auroras now appeared withered, now moist, now dense, now sparse. Suddenly, golden visages and august forms appeared, seated in countless ranks, like dragons first assembling in the clouds or the Nine Perfected gathering in grand convocation. Their majestic bearing was composed, their raiment of auroral hues and rainbow robes swirling with the wind, sinuous and graceful, like dragons soaring in the void or phoenixes dancing in the sky. To their left hung bells, to their right chimes, their tones intertwining in harmony, now near, now far, now high, now low.

The heavens were clear, the air bright; the four seas were calm. Creatures of land, water, and air, all manner of beings, gathered in familiarity, gazing upward to listen to the Dharma-sound. The titles of the chapters were: *Seven Qi Perfect the Perfected*, *Six Rites Move the Void*, *Five Spirits Continue the Severed*, *Two Luminaries Support the Declining*. They traversed the celestial net, stepped upon the void, and soared into the cloud palaces. The embryo has its beginning; the dust-kalpas have no end. Within the golden city, the essence is conceived; within the jade cavern, the spirit is congealed. The true qi is nurtured within, thereby perfecting the sage. Above, they enter the Six Voids; below, they penetrate the dark springs and cloud-palace treasure pavilions. Within resides the true soul, entering and exiting the land of blessings, circling the gate of life, chewing upon numinous mushrooms, rinsing with golden springs. Sweet dew flows like rivers, cascading into the cinnabar field. Purple auroras shine at dawn; the Three Qi condense into mist. Within the jade chamber, the immortal is transformed, seated serenely upon the golden lotus. The true form obscures the sun; dust-kalpas become years.

At that time, the assembled ministers, hearing the Perfected Ones of the cloud palaces chanting the numinous chapters and reciting the Dao-scriptures, each looked around to see the complexions of the crowd like clouds, their hearts illuminated, the affairs of the Three Times clearly and distinctly revealed. Their bodies transformed and ascended of their own accord, attaining fruition at will, without hindrance or obstruction.

The Perfected Youth asked the assembled ministers: "Having heard the Supreme Lord of the Upper Realms chanting the precious scripture, its numinous efficacy subtly felt and verified, merging with the Dao in an instant—is this not joyous? Those who study the Dao and attain the true fruit do not shift from their bodies. You, all of you, first made vast vows, entering the mountains to seek the Dao. The Supreme Perfected Emperor of the Upper Prime took pity on your earnestness, knowing you would not retreat, and has accomplished your bodies, enabling you to swiftly attain the Dao. You still have your original vows: you must dwell in the mountains and teach later learners."

At that time, the Perfected Emperor bestowed from afar upon the assembled ministers the titles of Perfected Ones. The Perfected Ones, though separated by thirty-six thousand dark heavens, through their attainment of communion, perceived it as if face-to-face. The Dao merged without words; no petition was heard.

Then the Perfected Ones all ascended into the void, mounting Kunlun at its central peak. In all four seasons and eight solar terms, they ascended to the Jade Purity and paid homage at the cloud palaces. The Supreme Great Dao sometimes tarries, descending once in ninety thousand great kalpas to wander the Four Heavens, delivering later learners. Appearing in forms suited to each, adopting their voices to expound the Dharma, all for their benefit—boundless and immeasurable, beyond conception.

As for later learners, those who do not cherish the mountains and waters, who lack lofty aspirations, who linger in the dust and filth, entangled in afflictions—even if they harbor a faint intention, they cannot achieve greatness. Without steadfast resolve, not meeting an enlightened teacher, not recognizing the true essentials, believing in perverse and inverted views, unable to distinguish precepts and prohibitions, intermingling the true and the false, the pure and the impure, they have not yet aligned with the causal ground. Deceiving themselves that they have attained fruition, their bodies not yet delivered, they expound the Dharma to deliver others. The Great Dao remains unheard; their perverse listening is in vain. The teacher is ignorant and dull; the disciples are likewise obstinate. Deceiving themselves and deceiving others, they vie with the worldly, scheming for worldly gain, sustaining their walking corpses. They dwell constantly in the realm of misfortune, unafraid of peril, advancing and retreating in self-aggrandizement, losing their lives across kalpas. The Dark Bureau records their transgressions; they are exiled in life and death to no avail, forever losing the human way. How lamentable!"

The Dao speaks: In times past, on the southern slopes of Yuntai in the lower realms, there were five men who formed a fellowship to study the Dao. They journeyed south into Danhuo Mountain, descended to seek the earthly path, and emerged at Fulong Mountain, exiting through the southern cave of Xiao’e to the mountain’s sunny side. Dwelling together for several years, they consumed pine resin and herbs, yet did not comprehend the precepts and methods, nor had they beheld the true scriptures. Through years of toil and hardship, their hearts never wavered or grew weary. They shunned worldly dust, sought no worldly gain, and wore only garments of grass. Six times daily, they paid homage to Heaven above, praying for deliverance and eternal life without death.

Thus they persisted for forty-six years, until the Supreme Mystery took pity on their solitary devotion. The Divine Youth of the Solar Palace was sent to test the five men. The first trial took the form of a beautiful woman who sought lodging with them. During a bitter snowstorm, she stayed nine days, sharing their bed. The five men gathered herbs to sustain her, kindled fires to warm her, and cared for her as if she were their parents, their hearts filled with compassion. The Divine Youth, perceiving their intent, briefly withdrew.

Nine days later, he suddenly transformed into a great rhinoceros that gored and killed a deer. The deer, too, was a phantom, dying beside their hut. The five men went to see it, weeping in sorrow, and buried it. The rhinoceros, knowing their intent, departed.

Seven days passed, and as the five entered the mountains to gather herbs and food, they suddenly encountered a treasure trove—gold and silver beyond measure. Yet their eyes did not linger upon it.

Another seven days later, the Divine Youth appeared as a destitute, ailing beggar seeking alms. The five men tended to him, providing food and care for a full thousand days before he departed.

Nine days thereafter, the Divine Youth manifested as over thirty ferocious tigers, followed by ten giant serpents. The tigers’ tails hooked together, the serpents’ bodies intertwined, encircling the five men. With gaping jaws and lolling tongues, they seemed poised to devour them. Yet the five remained fearless, their countenances serene, their qi calm, their bodies at ease, as if nothing were amiss.

Then the Great Dao took pity, and the host of sages showed compassion. The sun and moon halted in the sky for fourteen days; in the depths of winter, ice melted, jade trees bloomed, thunder resounded with clarity, sweet dew descended from Heaven, divine incense wafted thickly, and a harmonious breeze arose. The Supreme Great Dao extended its hand from the void, filling the world. Celestial patterns shone brightly, auspicious signs gathered, unicorns danced, phoenixes sang, and all sounds harmonized in praise of the five men. Every being in the world—saints and mortals, creatures of every kind, earth and stone, grasses and trees—all intoned the subtle Dharma-sound, weaving the warp of Heaven and the weft of Earth, transforming the mundane into the sacred, all to be heard and heeded.

The five men absorbed these subtle sounds, their hearts softened, their virtue and power unmatched. Their joints grew strong, their six viscera harmonized, their ears and eyes keen, their spirit and consciousness profound. They did not defy the four seasons nor oppose the five phases, returning to the constant Dao and far from delusion. Skillfully employing harmony, they remained free of illness, malevolent forces vanished, and their true nature renewed daily.

The Divine Youth sighed, saying: "Though men may be wise, they cannot employ virtue. Clinging to heterodox views, they deny the eternal Dao, following the world to extinction, prematurely losing their true nature. They do not know that the Dao is never far from the body, yet their divided minds do not endure. Willingly they embrace annihilation, their wandering souls clinging to change, abandoning themselves to circumstance.

"Long ago, there were two brothers of the Feng clan, born of the same mother. The elder, named Yun, was sixteen; the younger, named Yu, was fourteen. Their mother sent them to study abroad, where they encountered two teachers: one poor and humble, yet rich in virtue and the Dao, dwelling in Changshan for nine hundred years; the other wealthy and esteemed, well-versed in worldly affairs. The brothers each followed one teacher. The elder served the mountain recluse to study the Dao; the younger, greedy for wealth, attended the worldly master. Clasping hands, they parted and went their separate ways.

"After sixty-seven years, amidst the vicissitudes of life, they chanced upon each other in Liyin. The elder recognized his brother, but the younger did not recognize him. Though aged, the elder’s complexion remained unlined, appearing younger than before. At their parting, the younger’s appearance had withered, his ears and eyes impaired, his gaze dim.

"For three days, the brothers remained together, yet the younger did not realize. He said to the elder, 'Are you not a demon?' Then, suddenly, he exclaimed, 'If you claim to be my brother, you must mean me harm!' He swiftly drew his sword and thrust at his brother—yet the blade passed through him as if striking empty space, leaving no wound. The younger brother trembled in fear, his limbs shaking, and cried out in a voice that startled birds and beasts. He collapsed to the ground in terror, seeking to slay his brother.

"Moved by compassion for his brother, the elder helped him rise, soothed him, and nursed him until he gradually revived, though he still dared not believe. The elder recounted to his brother their parents’ birthplace, their shared history, their village and homeland. Though the younger vaguely understood, he still suspected the elder might be a ghost or demon who had learned these things.

"After a long while, he said, 'If you are truly my brother, strike me with your sword. If you are not, the blade will find its mark.' Yet when he struck, he felt no wound—by this proof, he still could not believe.

"The elder said, 'I have heard that those who embody the Dao are reborn in every part of their being, their bodies free from the realm of death. Thus, blades cannot harm me—this is no ghost or demon. Do not doubt. We were born of the same parents, grew up together, yet our studies differed, one coarse and one refined, their worth and folly starkly divided. Had you not been deluded by greed and sought the Dao of life, you too could be as I am, no different.'

"Yet the younger brother’s heart remained doubtful, his faith not yet pure.

"Then the two brothers returned home together. Seeing their parents, they knelt and paid their respects. Their parents, beholding their sons, rejoiced beyond measure."

Though the younger son had not spoken, his parents already knew which of their sons’ studies had excelled and which had fallen short. At that time, their relatives and old acquaintances, hearing of their return, all came to inquire about the circumstances of their learning.

The elder brother then recounted to their kin the origins of his own studies, and in turn detailed the master his younger brother had followed, explaining each cause and condition in full. Gradually, the younger brother’s heart began to awaken, and he came to know that his elder brother’s words were true and without error. He bowed to his brother, knelt long in repentance, and deeply reproached himself, offering three months of atonement. Yet though he sought to make amends, his heart remained hesitant, and he did not ask his brother to transmit the supreme Dao.

After six months had passed, he again took leave of his parents and set out for distant lands to seek learning. By chance, in a foreign land, he encountered a heretical teacher in a destitute household, begging for clothing and food. He requested to serve and follow him as his master, and the heretic soon granted his wish. For six years he served diligently, until at last the heretic imparted to him the way of false teachings. He then bade his master farewell and returned to his homeland. Along the way, he endured hardship and toil, fell ill with exhaustion, and suffered injury to his sinews and bones. He collapsed by the roadside, his corpse left unclaimed, devoured by beasts. Thus he lost the Dao of life, and his soul endured bitter torment—how pitiable his fate.

Later reborn in a remote borderland, he misled the common folk, and in the nine hundred lives since, he has expounded false teachings, seeking worldly gain and sustenance for his body. Though he has achieved some merit, it is not enough to attain accomplishment; he will never in this lifetime attain the Dharma-body. Yet this heretic still wanders mountains and forests, carrying his begging bowl, entering villages to beg for food. With no fixed abode, he practices improperly, his deceptive words confusing the deaf and blind, luring the young and ignorant.

Heaven, for his grievous transgressions, commands lower spirits to harass him, disturbing his mind so that he clings to death and scorns the Dao of life, joining with demonic forces as his companions. Such heretics will persist until the later kalpas, when the world grows corrupt and shallow, and the Dharma spreads across two realms while the great Dao declines. At that time, the blessings of beings will be exhausted, and heaven will send omens of disaster. The harvests will dwindle, the people starve, and the water kalpa will alter the course of fate, sweeping all away in a great flood.

Then, by the wind of destiny, the supreme Dao will be bestowed upon his parents. They will cultivate it with devotion for a thousand days, and though aged, they will be restored to youth. Later, following their son, they will enter the Azure Wheel’s vale, drink the golden essence, and chew the jade fungus. Their bodies will emanate purple qi, their eyes shine with flowing light, their bones grow light and buoyant, enabling them to fly. Before long, the three will ascend into the formless realm, enduring eternally, where eons pass like moments, and the longer they abide, the more they renew.

Such is the fortune of those who encounter and ride the rising tide of destiny. Though of one origin, they diverged midway, drifting apart. Once separated, they were estranged for countless kalpas. Without a true teacher, this was his fate. Let later learners take heed from this scripture: the human birth is hard to attain—do not squander life.

Then the Perfected Youth warned those of future generations who seek the true Dao, those whose aspirations lie beyond the worldly, who cast off worldly ties and wish to dwell in mountains and forests, secluding themselves in empty cliffs to study and savor the supreme Dao, seeking liberation and ascension. The essential requirement is purity—without it, there is no hope.

Diligently seek the supreme scriptures, clearly observe the precepts and methods of cultivation. With a mind of kindness and compliance, resonance comes easily. Keep the chamber of the spirit pure, remaining awake day and night. Polish the bright mirror to a diameter of nine inches, free of blemishes, and hang it before you to discern spirits and demons, distinguishing false from true.

Open the Hall of Light to summon afar the Two Radiant Ones. Morning and evening, chew the essence of the dawn and dusk. In your secluded chamber, sit or lie as you find comfortable—there is no need for uniformity. Consume the subtle and wondrous, regulate your breath to a state of harmony—neither too slow nor too swift, neither too coarse nor too fine. Like an infant nursing at its mother’s breast, draw in the qi in a continuous, delicate thread, unbroken. Without strain or fatigue, like a hidden spring flowing silently, let inner and outer be still, all senses calm, all distractions forgotten.

In profound stillness, as if deaf and blind, do not rely on sight or hearing for perception. Then the turbid will settle, the Dao and virtue will become manifest, the spirit will be nurtured within, and harmonious qi will flow smoothly. Life and death, departure and abiding, will be governed by the mind’s command. Once the Dao of life is firmly established, even death cannot be attained if one wished it.

Those who seek the true must treasure and guard this scripture, never revealing it carelessly. To transmit it to the unworthy brings nine generations of retribution, and one will not attain the Dao. Keep it deeply concealed, never exposing it. Practice it diligently, and great peace will be secured. To lose it is to perish; to preserve it is to flourish. Conceal it, and the true will descend; reveal it, and calamity will come.

At that time, the Divine Youth addressed those of later generations who aspired to learn the Dao, their resolve set far from the worldly realm, severed from all worldly defilements. They wished to dwell in blessed lands, enter renowned mountains, seek the true scriptures, and gather and consume the numinous lingzhi. For a thousand years, ten thousand ages, they would remain unharmed by malevolent forces.

These lands abounded with benevolent spirits; their earthly qi was harmonious and refined, their waters and herbs suited to human needs. In the four directions of Kunlun, beyond the southeast, lay the Jade Grotto south of Wangwu Mountain, corresponding above to the celestial realms. The sun, moon, and stars were as they were in the heavens above, no different. The earthly paths were tenfold open, with a thousand trails and myriad routes where true immortals came and went. There were also palaces, and the celestial scriptures were fully present, no less than in the heavens above.

Within these grotto-heavens dwelled many divine beings, who from time to time ascended the mountains to gaze upon those who followed in their footsteps. The land teemed with yellow essence, white wood, and lingzhi of the upper, middle, and lower grades. Sweet springs and jade nectar, when drunk, staved off decline. Perpetual divine incense suffused the bells and chimes, and celestial music resounded endlessly in the void, while divine voices chanted the celestial scriptures. Those who dwelt in these mountains found the true Dao easily attained.

Next was the mountain of Wutai, beneath which lay a grotto connected to Wangwu. Above and below the mountain dwelled divine immortals, who from ancient times to the present had never ceased their presence among humankind. Next was Changshan, beneath which lay a grotto linked to the ten directions, also abounding in divine herbs. Then came Taibai and Zhongnan.

Following these were the Five Marchmounts, Fanghu, Fulong, Tiantai, Danhuo, Zengcheng, Luofu, the grotto-heavens of Jiangyuan, Damei, and the blessed land of Wuling. These places were rich in the five metals, cinnabar, realgar, elixir waters, golden essence, jade marrow, and divine lingzhi. Consuming them prevented decline and even restored youth. Studying and reciting the celestial patterns, one could repent of sins and redress transgressions.

The incense smoke ascends, bearing the offerings of the heart. When merit is profound and conduct perfected, one’s achievements resound to the August Heaven. The Great Dao, moved by compassion, welcomes such a one with wheels of flame, and the body ascends to the Grand Void to receive the title of Perfected One.

The divine youth further spoke: The borderlands’ many mountains abound in noxious vapors, where cold and heat are unbalanced, and the earth’s qi harms mortals. They teem with malevolent spirits. Later students, unprepared for hardship, have yet to spread their true qi or dispel defilements. Lacking a worthy master and true scriptures, their earnest aspirations are thwarted by the remoteness of the mountains. Women and the infirm, without a teacher to rely upon, cannot journey far.

Yet those of steadfast resolve may instead seek level ground, build walls within walls, and sever all worldly ties. Following the precepts and rituals, they shall commit no transgressions. Within a secluded chamber, they burn incense and make vows, practicing the Dao in all six periods of day and night. They voice their heartfelt wishes, repenting their faults—pleading for the Nine Ancestors above and themselves below—that all offenses be pardoned by the Heavenly Courts, and the Four Offices and Five Emperors wash away their transgressions. Let their breath be soft and voices low, their devotion complete.

At first, when lighting the incense and making their petitions, they must not glance about or entertain stray thoughts. If their hearts are not sincere, demonic qi will respond. To slight the Most Sacred is to have one’s pleas unheard, laboring in vain, reaping nothing but exhaustion. Disturbing the common folk, they deceive themselves with hollow cries. If the true Dao is not practiced, they sit awaiting annihilation. At the brink of death, they declare the Dao powerless.

Alas! These walking corpses, incapable of true faith, drown in the cycle of birth and death, never loathing their plight nor seeking liberation in this life. The Five Rebellions and Ten Evils blind their eyes and ears; the three poisons of worms and maggots fester in their viscera. Even if they encounter true scriptures, their hearts remain unconvinced. Hearing of others’ attainment, they claim mortal bodies cannot achieve sagehood—only after death might their souls find the Dao. This is perverse view, the practice of external and superficial methods.

Scholars of the higher learning, upon meeting such people, must not walk with them nor dwell beside them; they should keep far away. Such souls defile the good, peering and slandering, or mocking with jest. The true Dao abhors them—beware, do not associate with them.

Scholars of the higher learning vanish into forests and valleys, their traces lost in secluded mountains. They build huts by cliffs, forever leaving the world behind. They refine body and spirit, studying and savoring the supreme Dharma. Gathering and consuming fine medicines, when clothing and provisions are exhausted, they seek nothing from without—donning grass, absorbing qi, sustaining life.

These are no mere ascetics who scorn food and warmth, despising comfort and loathing the company of others, fearing their goodness may be corrupted. Thus they flee into the famous mountains to avoid harm.

In truth, the Great Dao is everywhere; yet the world’s trials make undivided focus impossible.

Time flows swiftly, life is hard to preserve—sudden impermanence arrives, and what use is regret?

The Perfected Youth further said: Long ago, on the southeast of Kunlun and the southern slopes of the Onion Range, there lived two men of like mind who, hearing of the Way of Life, desired to study it. For six years, they spoke of it constantly, expounding it to others. Yet in their village, they had previously worshipped evil spirits, and these spirits, resenting their change, waited for their moment of weakness. One night, they struck the two men dead, and the Way of Life was lost to them. Heaven, seeing their sincere intent, commanded the Four Offices to gather their souls and rebirth them among men, sparing them the trials of hell and swiftly restoring their human form. The two changed their surnames and were born into the Ji clan—one named Hongdao, the other Hongde. Through seven hundred rebirths, they have yet to meet a true master, drifting through the world of men, their original resolve forgotten, their hopes forever unfulfilled.

If you wish to study the Dao with sincerity, guard your words carefully. Do not let the vulgar know of it, lest evil men slander and envy you, and malevolent spirits bring harm. The Dao teaches: When one first begins to study the Way and the first signs of resonance appear, many celestial sages descend to their dwelling to instruct them. Heavenly spirits and divine attendants follow these sages as they journey among mortals. At such times, even lesser ghosts and gods are pressed into service. They also guard and protect the student of the Dao and their household, though their labors are arduous and they find no ease in it. Thus, when worldly men study the Dao, they fear the burdens of service and the loss of their freedom.

At that time, there was a student of the Dao in the Wudang Mountains named Zhu Yuan, who, with thirteen companions of like mind, dwelt in Wudang for three hundred and sixty-two years. They gathered and consumed pine and cypress, and their forms showed no sign of decay. Later, they entered Luhun and wandered to Mount Taishi, where they gathered and consumed secret stone mushrooms and herbs. Lacking the true scriptures, they relied solely on medicinal diets, yet their hearing and vision remained sharp, and their speed matched that of a galloping horse. For over seven thousand years, they dwelt in seclusion among the mountains, occasionally entering grotto-heavens to pay homage to later sages, their resolve never wavering for a moment. Later, the Queen Mother bestowed upon them the Mystic Frost and Jade Elixir, and in an instant, they ascended to heaven. To this day, they reside in the Great Clarity Heaven. The Cloud Palace Heavenly Worthy, wishing to strengthen their resolve, commanded the Left Perfected Attendant Youth to bestow upon them the two-character *Cloud Scripture*, which they now consume, attaining the rank of Upper Perfected.

Yet worldly men are foolish and dull. Before even ten days of study have passed, their hearts grow slack and they retreat. How can such as these, mere walking corpses, hope to glimpse the supreme Dao? Though the resolve of these thirteen did not falter, and though they lived out their days in secluded mountains, their hearts held no aspiration, nor did they seek out enlightened masters to receive the true essentials. They merely withdrew from the world, avoiding the dust and filth, consuming fine medicines to sustain their bodies. They committed no defilements, yet practiced no other disciplines—thus, they could not attain the true Dao in this very body. Had they sought out enlightened masters and received the true essentials, their Way would have been perfected far more swiftly, without the need for so many years.

The Dao teaches: When a student of the Dao encounters an enlightened master and practices the true essentials, if their past merits are insufficient and their karmic destiny is to perish, or if, by the blessings of former lives, the True Emperor takes pity on them, they may attain the true Dao in but a few days. Long ago, during the Water Kalpa, west of Kunlun there lived a Qiang tribesman named Fuduoli, of the Poshejiā clan. Morning and evening, he would bow from afar toward Kunlun, vowing with great resolve to attain immortality and deliverance from the world. After more than forty years of such devotion, he was visited by the Female Perfected Wang Qinxin, who descended from the Great Clarity Heaven to wander Kunlun. She lingered in the Lang Garden for ninety thousand great kalpas, often speaking of this man: "In the southwest below, the earth’s qi is foul and turbid, and men know only killing. The Qiang tribes are fierce and treacherous, untouched by the supreme teachings. Yet this man alone desires to hear the Great Dao."

Then the Female Perfected spoke thus to the Perfected Officials. The officials replied: "This is but a wild tribesman—he eats no flesh but raw meat, drinks no water but blood, and wears the stinking hides of sheep. The supreme Great Dao is not for his ears. If he is sincere, wait until his death, then transform his soul and rebirth him in the Central Kingdom. Only then, in a later life, may he attain the Dao." The Female Perfected said: "The supreme Great Dao is like a great forge, melting and refining heaven and earth, transforming all beings—even earth, wood, metal, and stone—into ashes. If this man has a sincere heart, why should he not be delivered?" Thus, the Female Perfected pleaded earnestly, and the Male Perfected Lord of the Dao finally consented.

Overjoyed, on the night of the eighth day of the fourth month, she commanded the Central Perfected Attendant Maiden to gather his spirit while he slept and bring it to the Lang Palace. There, she taught him the Way of Life, bestowing upon him the Five-Stone Elixir of Mystic Nourishment and the method of consuming harmonized qi and divine water. When he awoke, he recorded and recited what he had learned, committing it to memory without error. With wholehearted devotion, he practiced for over three thousand days, and in time, he attained the Way of the Middle Immortal. He was appointed to oversee the lower offices, ruling over the various tribes of the western lands. Those among them who aspired to the Dao, he instructed. He dwelt in the center of Dragon Mountain, yet could fly at will, his body emitting radiant light. On the four seasons and eight solar terms, he ascended to the Great Clarity Heaven to pay homage to the Female Perfected. His attainment of the Dao was by her power. Now, ten thousand kalpas have passed, and he remains there still.

Thus concludes Scroll Eight of the *Supreme Dao Jade Clarity Scripture*.
Beginning of Scroll Nine of the *Supreme Dao Jade Clarity Scripture*.

**The Illustrious Might Perfected’s Subjugation of Evil, Chapter Nineteen**

The Supreme Dao Lord of the Purple Chamber of Radiant Clouds in the Jade Clarity Heaven, bearing the title **Illustrious Might Perfected**, embodies the Way of compassion and forbearance, responding to the cries of sentient beings. Through great mercy, he accomplishes salvation, delivering those in peril and distress.

Ever abiding in concentrated spirit, nine hundred million great kalpas pass for him in but a single instant. Descending in responsive transformation, he flows into the Two Realms, traversing the paths of darkness and light, the hearts of high, middle, and low. Each receives the true primordial qi, riding upon a single faith to guide their bodies. None fail to submit, for he allows their great return without deviating from the constant.

From ignorance to wisdom, all are forged in the great crucible; though their natures are left to follow their course, none can transgress its bounds—save those who transcend by the Great Dao alone.

The Illustrious Might Perfected, grieving that the world does not emerge from suffering, extends his compassion to shelter them, teaching the Way of riding and submission, gradually guiding them toward non-action. At that time, the later-learned sages of the ten directions, along with ordinary mortals, beasts, and all manner of ghosts and spirits—every being that turns toward the Dao—save those who have attained the correct path, must follow the Great Dao in accordance with their portion, riding and submitting to converge upon the One Way.

Those who study the sagely path ride the wondrous qi of the Dao. Those who study worldly affairs ride the norms of the world, submitting to its laws. Yet when the form decays and the bones rot, the wandering soul drifts without cease. Each steers their qi to a single direction, clinging to what they know, monopolizing the Dao and hoarding its power.

Thus, the paths of sentient beings diverge, and their encounters differ. Those who ride the wondrous qi of the Dao shall surely attain true perfection; those who submit to evil ways shall inevitably decay and rot. The Supreme Great Dao, mourning their premature demise, thus bestows the wondrous qi of the Way of Life to nourish all existence.

Thereupon, the Supreme August Perfected of Primordial Times universally dispensed the transformative power of the Dao, revealing methods to counter afflictions and skillfully resolve the ailments of all beings. He sustained and upheld the sentient, expounding the **Orthodox Unity** to convert the lofty; the **Oath and Might** rites to sever the roots of evil, gathering the auspicious qi of celestial clouds to compose the script of **Yin Generation**, raising the withered bones. He established the celestial offices of the Upper Bureau to govern the multitudes.

The **Perfected King of Grand Medicine** revives the dead, cures chronic illnesses, mends what is broken, fills what is lacking, circulates the warp and weft of life, enriches the blood and replenishes the brain, restores hearing and sight, making the dull bright and clear. Teeth regrow, forms rejuvenate, and the longer one endures, the more youthful they become.

The **Illustrious Might Great Perfected**’s divine power is unimpeded; the Way of provisional and true holds no distinction of superiority or inferiority. His true and responsive bodies pervade the dusty realms; the might and spirit of his virtue remain unchanged from beginning to end. The forms that arise in response adapt to each kind, their voices myriad, their preferences likewise varied.

Yet the world below fails to comprehend, severing itself from its source. Within a single body, discord suddenly arises, deluded thoughts breed afflictions, and the omens of demonic spirits appear. Not understanding the great crucible and vast norms of the beginning, from the Middle Antiquity onward, purity and simplicity gave way to turbulence and deceit. Falsehoods surged forth, and all swiftly declined. The multitudes, pursuing evil paths in search of what is most fitting, rush about in turmoil and strife, unable to escape the mire. Content with their lot, how pitiful it is!

At that time, the Radiant and Majestic Great Perfected, perceiving the unbegun origin of the myriad things and penetrating their ultimate end, established in reverse the forms of awe and dignity, manifesting the true and correct for those to come above, rejecting the heterodox paths in speech. Thus, those who cultivate and practice are given a guiding standard for the heart, a precise and veritable pointer to reality, enabling them to discern the true from the false.

The distinction between true and false is established and immediately tested. The way of testing lies in what is called "walking the upright conduct, living the upright life, and practicing the upright Dao." The upright Dao heals the heterodox; the upright body does not falter, the upright conduct does not waver, the upright life is not cut short. A life not cut short means a life without end; a body that does not falter means returning to infancy after dust-and-kalpas; unwavering conduct means walking the conduct of the unsurpassed Dao.

By cultivating the true and veritable Dao of the Great Sage, refining and transforming body and spirit, exiting the realm of being and entering the realm of non-being, one forever severs the cycle of birth and death, and the manifold afflictions do not continue. With this very body, one attains the Dharma-body. Freed from the sufferings of birth, aging, sickness, and death, this is called "forever severing the cycle of birth and death."

Those who practice heterodox paths readily reveal their nature. How is this known? By knowing that the cultivation of the heterodox does not lead to rebirth in the undetermined; those who practice it grow old and die, unable to transform, causing people to revert to infancy with bones decayed, skin wrinkled, teeth fallen, hair whitened, hearing lost, sight dimmed, and swiftly rotting away. Turning their backs on the Dao and corrupting virtue, they revolve in heterodox customs, unable to transcend duality, unable to cast off afflictions. Like silkworms, they consume and traverse the world, deluding and confusing the foolish below, their bodies and lives not upright.

They boldly claim that after the transformations of the spirit and the dissolution into ashes, form departs and consciousness scatters, yet they call this the attainment of the supreme fruit—this is heterodox doctrine and cannot be relied upon. If one encounters such a person, one should not abandon them but, with skillful means, expound the path of life and deliver them.

The unsurpassed Great Dao pities all those who stray into heterodoxy, thus manifesting radiant majesty to point the way for the drowning and lost. Those who cherish the true make vast vows to cultivate and practice, concealing their bodies in secrecy, unmoved by the currents of the world. They rectify their demeanor, purify their conduct, veil their brilliance, and obscure their keen perception. Clad in garments light and wondrous, fragrant within and without, they make no distinction between noble and base, nor discern beauty from ugliness. They regard wine, sensuality, and wealth as putrid and foul, and such foul thoughts do not arise in them—how much less would they lightly transgress?

With but a single touch of body or heart, the true qi departs far away; how much more so with constant intimacy? Those who seek the Dao through familiarity with such things invite demonic spirits to seize the opportunity, bringing misfortune and harm in their wake, toppling and collapsing in an instant.

The Radiant and Majestic Great Perfected, foreseeing the calamities of the latter kalpas, saw that in the age of perverse heterodoxy, yin qi would arise, and in the turbid and evil world, such ways would easily flourish. With the loss of pure simplicity, frivolity and competition would surge. In the four heavens below, beings would style themselves as divine kings—such demons are called "heavenly spirits." The turbid and evil world would spread across the lower realms.

Beneath the four heavens, the spirits of mountains, forests, and stones would attach themselves to living people, imitating one another, calling themselves "immortal kings," along with the lingering demons of the six heavens. Together they would form factions, branching and dispersing, assuming names according to the times. Those who turn their backs on the Dao would offer them food and pray for blessings, yet these beings gnaw at people’s essence and qi, consume their blood and vessels, and diminish their lifespans. Unaware, people allow them to enter their bodies, where they can also cause people to loathe life and love death.

Should such spirits enter your body, your descendants multiply, your essence and qi grow strong and unyielding, and they traffic with the living. Demon-women and spectral insects can also cause people to expound upon the emptiness of all things, fostering jealousy toward the Way of life. If men or women study and cultivate the Dao, these malevolent spirits will vie to assail them, desiring their death to seize their souls and spirits, making them companions. For this reason, they despise the Way of life.

Later learners who attain the Dao in body will find these wicked spirits and their factions serving and obeying them, yet they will not gain true freedom. Thus, those who study the Dao must clearly recognize heterodox afflictions and know in advance the methods of radiant might to dispel and sever curses, protecting their form and spirit.

If there are those in the world who serve heterodox ways with unwavering devotion, the virtuous should employ skillful means to instruct and summon them, but if they refuse, one must not draw near nor heed their words. Why? Beginners in the Dao possess but faint power and cannot yet subdue the myriad heterodox paths. Therefore, one ought to respect them from afar.

At the great assembly of return, the supreme Dao will descend to teach and transform the world, displaying its majestic power to subdue the strong and unyielding. At that great convergence, merits and transgressions, heterodoxy and orthodoxy, will be distinctly judged, with no power to alter or reverse them.

Later learners who delight in the true Dao should first seek a luminous teacher, exploring the profound and far-reaching. Those who can advance in cultivation should focus intently on the supreme Way, while also comprehending worldly classics, mastering the breadth of texts, and weaving the warp and weft of scriptures. With unwavering mastery of even one art, they may ascend to discern the celestial canons. Those who clarify the profound meanings of the Dao, resolve all doubts upon inquiry, and distinguish heterodoxy from orthodoxy—though dwelling in the mundane realm—may be called sagely teachers.

Second-tier teachers, however, are unversed in worldly affairs and do not comprehend the profound meanings of the great Dao, adhering only to a single method. Yet those capable of guiding the world observe purity with utmost devotion, their resolve unshaken. They concentrate their spirit, uphold precepts, and vow never to commit evil. Such teachers align with the Dao, their essence and qi undispersed, easily achieving resonance. Their form steadfast and spirit congealed, they cultivate inner harmony, and before long—even in an instant—they ascend, flesh and bone together, forever attaining the true Dao. Though ranked second, they do not lose the title of luminous teacher.

Third-tier teachers lack definitive practices but embody compassion and forbearance, steadfastly upholding non-killing. They guide households and transform the people, healing illnesses, understanding radiant might, and acting without deceit. They regard neither wealth nor poverty, beauty nor ugliness, nobility nor lowliness, freely bestowing wealth and food. They cultivate equanimity, seeing others’ kin as their own and others’ bodies as their own. When they witness peril or hardship, they employ skillful means to deliver and stabilize. Seeing others suffer, they share their pain, cherishing them with earnest compassion and never abandoning them. Extending great mercy, they bury the dead and inter bones, diminishing their own clothing and food to aid the destitute. They practice filial piety throughout life, commit no wrongdoing, and harbor no resentment toward foes. They firmly believe in the unseen and do not neglect the empty chamber. Their nature aligns with the Dao, and heterodox qi naturally distances itself. They do not seek the Dao, yet the Dao comes to them.

The Dao states: Later generations of ordinary people who study and attain the Dao through such deeds have no such path. Men and women of later times who seek the Dao should first establish the methods of merit, of which there are many kinds.

The first merit is to propagate the Dao and transform beings, assisting the Son of Heaven and honoring one’s parents.

The second merit is to propagate the Dao and eliminate harm, overturning heterodoxy and eradicating falsehood.

The third merit is to extend filial piety to all—from the chirping and creeping to the grasses and trees.

The fourth merit is to endure hardship in secluded cultivation, serve a teacher to seek the Dao, consume elixirs with single-minded devotion, and maintain inner and outer purity.

The fifth merit is to establish retreats and conduct rituals, guiding those with karmic affinity, inviting teachers to pray for blessings, repenting transgressions, and supplying the needs of secluded cultivators of the true Dao—clothing, resources, medicine, food, bedding, incense, candles, and all requisites—ensuring nothing is lacking.

The sixth merit is to ransom and liberate lives, regardless of status or size, tracing the origins of aquatic beings, channeling flowing waters, and if no outlet exists, returning them to deep waters to revive. For flying and walking creatures—whether hatched, born, or transformed—if their nests or burrows collapse and their young cannot fend for themselves, one should skillfully repair and restore them, preventing terror and ensuring their survival. Such people are called worldly Dharma-teachers, relieving distress and aligning with the Dao’s virtue. The great Dao befriends them, freeing them from the sufferings of birth, aging, sickness, and death, ensuring eternal continuity, forever severing toil and affliction, with no further calamities. Such people grasp the essentials of seeking the Dao and the mechanism of attaining it.

The Dao states: Good men and women who establish merit have yet another method—mastering radiant might, discerning heterodoxy from orthodoxy, severing spectral insects, and beheading deceitful spirits. They wish for all beings to be free of illness, to dwell and move in peace, and to abide in forbearance. Though lacking formal cultivation, each upholds their duty.

Those who establish merit cherish all beings with equanimity. If they encounter afflictions of bias or heterodoxy, they diligently and tirelessly resolve them. Seated in the Dao-field, their benefits are boundless. They first instruct suffering beings: those afflicted by heterodox maladies should bathe to cleanse dust and filth, vow to practice the true and great Dao, refrain from heterodox thoughts, revere the Dao-field, regard the teacher as a father, don fresh and splendid attire, maintain inner and outer purity, burn fine incense, and pay homage to the teacher according to ritual. The teacher then reveals their heart’s suffering, invoking the majestic power of the great Dao and the life-spirits of true might—countless myriads—to dispel heterodoxy and eradicate falsehood.

The teacher, for the sake of beings, fully receives all methods: internally to cultivate the body, externally to save the world. The internal methods of the Dao include the Three Clarities’ treasured texts, cloud-script divine chapters, dragon charts and phoenix seals, and the nine qi’s trailing radiance.

With wholehearted cultivation, one’s might subdues heaven and earth. Such precious scriptures total thirty-six thousand great treasuries, each treasury containing thirty-six thousand sections of scripture, and each section inscribed upon thirty-six thousand slips of yielding jade. Yet to obtain even one of these true scriptures is sufficient—there is no need to receive in full the Three Clarities’ treasured texts. One need only single-mindedly cultivate the Three Clarities’ singular method to attain the Dao, transcend the mortal form, and achieve liberation. The evidence is visible before one’s eyes, the verification immediate.

The methods for saving the common folk do not involve the inner scriptures of the Heavenly Treasures. Rather, one receives the Register of Luminous Might and Life-Spirits, the Nine Heavens’ True Talismans, the Nine Heavens’ Military Talismans, the Nine Heavens’ Community Decrees, the Nine Heavens’ Divine Phoenix, the Nine Palaces’ Divine Sword, the Nine Palaces’ Divine Talismans, and the Mysterious Hand True Techniques. These dispel heterodoxy and sweep away demons, drive away ghosts and command spirits, ascend the cosmic net and tread the celestial tracks, traverse the Seven Luminaries in flying steps, bind the fierce and unruly, overawe the perverse and wayward, reverse winds and halt rain, gather and disperse dark mists, arrest the dawn and detain the sunlight, inhale and exhale the divine qi, and transform misfortune into fortune. These methods are the natural Dao of the Nine Heavens’ true qi, bestowed by the great sages in their compassion to save the common folk. The Nine Talismans and Life-Spirits preside over the nurturing of all sentient beings, responding below to the multitudes. All men and women who reverently believe in the supreme great Dao are protected by its might and numen. This might and numen are formed from the qi of true orthodoxy, pervading the vastness of empty space. Those who believe in the Dao and invoke blessings to dispel calamity find the might and numen arriving in an instant, as swift as echo follows sound. Though this might and numen are qi ascending to heaven and spirits suffusing form and appearance, they are called the bestowal of the great Dao, filling the entire world.

The true qi of the great Dao transforms into wind and clouds; its wondrous qi congeals into sweet dew; its compassionate qi becomes nourishing rain. It may manifest as sweet springs, fine wells, mountains and peaks, headwaters and streams, deep abysses, lush forests, medicinal herbs, crops and grains, fragrant trees, or flowers and fruits—providing the world’s resources and bestowing boundless benefit. Yet the foolish people of the lower world attribute the three luminaries of heaven and earth, the winds and thunder, clouds and rain, frost and dew, and the myriad phenomena of the void to spontaneous generation, not to the great Dao. Those who harbor such thoughts are deluded by heterodoxy. Seeking the true Dao, they will never attain it. They forget their roots, betray kindness and duty, lack compassion and caution, and indulge in violence and arrogance. They defy heaven and rebel against earth. Though they may briefly live, they will not die a proper death, but perish in suffering, mired in hardship and misery. Neither humans nor spirits pity them; ghosts and demons afflict them alike. Cast into the paths of heterodoxy, they drown in the cycle of birth and death. Like rotten wood that cannot be made firm or a boulder fallen into a thousand-fathom ravine, they cannot climb back up.

The vulgar and perverse will never revere the upright Dao, much less seek its essentials or aspire to transcendence. Alas for the common folk, forever severed from the Dao! The moment they lose the true, their conduct deviates by a hair’s breadth. Gradually, the distance widens until it is beyond sight, and they forget their origins entirely. The initial estrangement from the Dao, though they dwell in the vast furnace of the cosmos, in the realm of vessels and images, is already a departure from true orthodoxy. Like a wicked person whose fleeting glance is perverse, whose heart is not upright, whose yin blood seethes in darkness, and whose wrathful qi takes form—such a one harms body and life, and the source of suffering arises. Though physicians apply remedies with double effort, they cannot cure the illness. How much less can one who sinks into heterodoxy for a lifetime, never beholding the luminous might of the true and orthodox Dao, hope to live?

The Dao speaks: In the distant past, at the beginning of the kalpa of fire, the essence of Mount Rong transformed into a human form, its body adorned with all marks, and went forth to teach the world. It gathered eighty thousand disciples and instructed them in the worship of fire and the observation of water for twelve years. It absorbed the people’s essence-qi, causing them to lose their orthodoxy, and their heterodox views took root. At that time, the people, united in their resolve to die, each entered withered grass, knelt with hands clasped, removed their clothes and untied their sashes, and turned to one another to ignite the fire. The withered grass blazed fiercely, burning over eighty thousand people at once. Their hair singed, their skin split, blisters burst and fluids oozed, their hands and feet cramped and curled, writhing on the ground in agony. Though they regretted and repented, they could not utter a sound. Then the mountain spirit snapped its fingers in praise and said: “All living beings ultimately return to annihilation; the body of affliction is a chamber of a hundred poisons. You should swiftly depart and seek early liberation. Destroy this body to attain the Dharma-body. If you find the fire’s venom too fierce, then cast yourselves into the deep abyss.” After the mountain spirit spoke these words, the eighty thousand people crawled into the water, where wind and waves tossed them, and river creatures devoured them. The river spirits seized their souls, and the watery palaces enslaved their essence-spirits, condemning them to toil in suffering for over seven thousand years—still unrelieved to this day. Once ensnared by heterodoxy, they are bound to the cycle of birth and death.

At that time, the essence of Mount Rong, having led the common folk to their deaths, knew it had committed a sin. Fearing the great might above, it hid deep within the stone. In spring, it encountered the Thunder God, who split the rock and dragged it forth, compelling it to serve the dragons day and night in toil, never free. To dispel such powerful spirits, one may command the Thunder Duke to sever and rend them—no need to trouble the celestial officials’ might and numen, nor expend the true and wondrous qi of the great Dao, nor invoke the might of the Dao’s life-spirits. The heterodox will vanish of their own accord.

At that time, there were also the island barbarians of Liaodong, among whom the essence of an iron bell transformed into a human form and went forth to teach the world. Its methods spread through eighty-one countries, causing people to weep at birth and sing at death. The elderly were called “ghostly simples” and abandoned in the wild grasslands to hasten their deaths. These barbarians have practiced such customs for over three thousand years. The abandoned elders starve to death in the desolate marshes, lying in wretched disarray. The Perfected of Luminous Might, moved by their suffering, dispatched five hundred million Vajra youths to dissolve the iron essence and all tree demons. They imposed the Way of filial piety and the method of nurturing the elderly to save the common folk.

At that time, the iron essence resumed its form, and the Vajra youths buried it deep in the earth, pressing it down with divine talismans of the Seven Treasures, where it remains to this day. Should later students of the Perfected seek to dispel this essence, they must summon the Vajra youths in their billions and myriads to annihilate the demonic essence, which will then dissolve and vanish of itself.

At that time, there also arose in the southwest a mountain spirit of the Iron Enclosure in the Metal Quarter, which took human form and went forth to teach the world. Its methods spread through the wild barbarian lands and a hundred countries, branching into over five hundred variations. These were called the Outer Ways. They worshipped all manner of images—Heaven and Earth, sun and moon, stars and constellations, wind and water, metal and wood, furnaces and fires, city walls and roads—and practiced various austerities, altering their garments and even their forms. They erected statues for worship, inscribed scriptures on leaves, mutilated their bodies, donned barbarian attire, and observed prohibitions and incantations. Entering towns to beg, each claimed their way led to the supreme fruit. They offered blood sacrifices and invoked the Heavenly Kings, or styled themselves as Brahmin masters, specializing in slaughter to present offerings to the celestial spirits, hoping to gain abundant blessings and worldly wealth. Each declared: "Whoever makes offerings to me shall receive boundless merit."

Such Outer Ways clung to human bodies, wailing and shrieking, tearing out their hair, leaping and flinging themselves about, seeking death to extinguish themselves. Some sat in silent darkness, gazing intently at luminous visions, claiming to behold great sages or witness all manner of karmic signs. When common folk heard of this, they competed to make offerings, surrendering treasures, wives, children, servants, horses, cities, fields, and dwellings—or even their own lives, heads, eyes, marrow, and brains—without the slightest reluctance. These Outer Ways taught their followers to love death, and whenever someone died, they would sing praises and hymns, abandoning the corpse in the wilderness, calling it "ascension to Heaven." Gathering in worship, they rejoiced and exclaimed: "Great beings and lofty souls, weary of the world and seeking deliverance, become like birds and beasts, their consciousness dissolving into Heaven. No more afflictions—how joyous indeed!"

Among the austerities of these Outer Ways was the Great Fire Heap, where they declared: "If any good man or woman enters the fire and burns their body, they are called the foremost great beings, freed from afflictions, attaining the supreme fruit, and reaching the realm of eternal bliss and purity, ascending to the unshakable abode of everlasting joy." These Outer Ways praised such great beings as heroic and unmatched in virtue and power, claiming they brought the greatest benefit to the world. Foolish people, seeing this, vied to burn themselves. At that time, the wandering spirits of the Outer Ways soared through the air, singing praises and performing all manner of music to delight their senses. Across a hundred barbarian domains, over decades, more than half were maimed or ruined by the deceptions of these Outer Ways.

Should later students wish to eradicate these heterodox paths, they must cultivate the method of Orthodox Unity, wielding great divine might to subdue them. With the wondrous qi of the Great Dao and the true power of the Life-Generating Spirit, they shall cast them out. The mortal forms of the Outer Ways will naturally submit, and their demonic essences will dissolve of themselves. Should later students seek to destroy this evil, they must skillfully employ the Way of the Fire Bell, and the evil will perish in an instant. Though these Outer Ways pursue the supreme fruit, they shall never attain it, for the path of self-destruction is not the true attainment. This is called the way of the walking corpse, the path of falsehood and deceit.

Within the teachings of the Great Dao, there are also such people—those whose hearts are restless, whose conduct is unrighteous, and whom wayward spirits possess. These too are called Outer Ways. Such people cannot distinguish truth from falsehood or purity from impurity; they are inherently drawn to demonic influences. With their hearts already biased, the Great Dao cannot flow through them. Instead, seductive spirits enter their minds, and they abhor the Way of Life. Later students must carefully discern this and purify all defilements with the qi of the Dao. They should invoke the Celestial Enforcers of Might, the Five Divisions of Divine Generals—each with fifty thousand multicolored soldiers—and five hundred million troops to widely establish Daoist altars, shattering the malevolent trials until they dissolve and vanish.

At that time, among the fifty-five barbarian states of the northern lands, a ten-thousand-year-old fox spirit transformed into a king, ruling east of Mount Kunlun. It seduced many women, fathering fox cubs, and its descendants flourished, filling all the lands. They bewitched and killed people, devoured livestock, and manifested all manner of strange lights and apparitions, gathering in powerful bands. The forms of their bewitchment included transforming into beautiful women or men to consort with humans, or even impersonating their relatives. At times, they would shave people’s heads, causing them to lose their minds, rave madly, and babble incoherently. They could also make people despise life and delight in killing, despise their own bodies, and suffer stabbing pains in their hearts and bellies, alternating between emaciation and swelling. Though clever and discerning by day, they would hide and roam at night, drawn to bright colors and preferring solitude.

Their transformations resembled those of tree spirits, flourishing in spring and autumn, fading in winter. Yet tree spirits are easily dispelled—simply have the Thunder God strike them with lightning, and they vanish of themselves. Later students must carefully discern fox spirits. To expel them, one should use a divine sword forged from western barbarian gold, secretly carried on the person, and swiftly employ the Way of the Fire Bell and the Shooting Star. Invoke the Life-Generating Spirit’s divine might, summoning billions of celestial cavalry to shatter the strong spirits and strike down the fox demons. At the sound, they will tremble and prostrate themselves, fleeing for ten thousand miles, their illusory arts naturally collapsing. For those pregnant with fox fetuses that have not yet dissolved, invoke the divine soldiers to heal them. Jade maidens bearing medicines of the Five Directions, along with needles, knives, fire, and moxa, shall enter their bodies, treating each ailment accordingly to swiftly cause the fetuses to crumble and fall.

Thus, the qi of the Dao flows freely, the primordial wind spreads, the demonic fetuses dissolve, and the Way of Life quietly prepares. When the Supreme Sages heal, the cure is instantaneous; when superior practitioners heal, it takes ten days to take effect. Such afflicted individuals have hollowed marrow and obstructed blood vessels. Teach them to calm their minds, uphold the scriptures and precepts, and they will gradually recover, freed from their bonds and at ease.

For those afflicted with grave illness, instruct them to devote themselves to the Dao. The master shall transmit the luminous might and demon-expelling methods, so that they may meditate morning and evening, offer incense and lamps, and uphold the master’s teachings as if standing before the imperial throne.

At that time, the Luminous Might Perfected, moved by great compassion, revealed this orthodox method and disseminated it throughout the mortal realm. Upon hearing of this, all stubborn spirits trembled in awe, their forms vanishing without trace, no longer daring to stir. In that moment, no need arose for striking or severing, for all demonic spirits willingly submitted, aiding and serving the true.

The Great Dao, in its boundless mercy, could not bear to annihilate them. Thus, it bestowed the method of luminous might, passing it down to later disciples to guard against all spectral and demonic beings. Should any transgress or offend the true and orthodox, later disciples must follow the correct method, severing and destroying them, eradicating the demonic and dissolving the malevolent spirits, so that those of true faith may find guidance in their hearts, and all beings rely upon this for peace and stability.

Wherever this scripture resides, it shall be cultivated by those of moral integrity, aiding the Dao in its flourishing and transformation, protecting and nurturing all beings without regard to rank or status, nor seeking recompense for their noble deeds. The Supreme Sages observe from afar, befriending the virtuous path, while the netherworld records their merits, ensuring their blessings are complete. The unsurpassed Great Dao sends forth divine beings to guard and protect them.

Wherever such a master dwells, all people and spirits shall revere them. None may slight, mock, curse, strike, or steal their possessions and sustenance, lest the celestial and terrestrial deities immediately impose punishment. Such a master, steadfast in mind and upright in conduct, aligns with the Dao as one. All people should bow in reverence, honoring them with utmost sincerity, as one would honor Heaven. Why is this so? Though such a master dwells temporarily in the world, their virtue merges with the celestial truth, and their might can command even Heaven, which itself holds them in awe. For this reason, all people should rise in reverence, esteeming their power. They govern Heaven and Earth, deliver boundless salvation, their merit equaling creation itself, their Daoist might beyond compare.

All men and women should cultivate a heart devoted to the Great Dao in the presence of such a master, aspiring that all people may study under them and attain the supreme Dao.

When the Luminous Might Perfected expounded this method, the demonic palaces trembled, spectral beings lost their essence, auspicious winds and felicitous clouds spread throughout the mortal realm, thunderous Dharma rains and Dharma storms moistened the four heavens, and medicinal herbs and trees bloomed in season. Deviant paths returned to orthodoxy, and the five demonic spirits vanished without trace.

At that time, the voice and radiance of the Luminous Might Perfected resounded far and wide, drawing the yearning gaze of all in the ten directions. Beneath the four heavens, men and women burned incense, prostrated themselves, and raised their aspirations to Heaven, praying for the Great Dao to descend into the mortal world, manifesting in form to fulfill their longing.

Then, the king of Da Qin, Yiqiruoti, beheld the true radiance and fixed his mind upon it, fasting for seven days without food, declaring: "If the Great Dao responds to me from afar, I shall renounce the burdens of my kingdom and leave the world to follow the Dao."

At that time, an outsider from Rinan named Fotuoli, leading six thousand disciples—shaven-headed and bare-bodied, bearing a single brazier of fire—entered the kingdom. The gatekeepers reported this to the king, who emerged to bow in reverence, mistaking him for a true master. He welcomed Fotuoli into the city, providing morning and evening offerings, neglecting the affairs of state. The king followed Fotuoli in leaving the world to seek the Dao, commanding him to bow morning and evening before the brazier. All men and women in the kingdom likewise worshipped the fire.
