The fire spirits flourished, gradually seizing the king’s heart. The king and his entire realm embraced death, each making vows to immolate their bodies in pursuit of the supreme Dao. The king and his ministers set the eighth day of the fourth month as the appointed time to gather firewood and burn themselves.

Moved by the king’s ignorance, the Luminous Might Perfected commanded the Dragon King of the Northern Sea and the Great General Xuanwu to ride the vast ocean waters to the southern lands. Six feet above the ground, they covered all of Da Qin, remaining for a full month. The outsider and the king had no chance of survival; fire vanished from the kingdom, and the people ate raw mutton. The fire spirits and their demonic essence naturally dissolved.

The king grew doubtful and addressed the outsider, saying: "Master, I have heard that in the northwest, there are masters and disciples who worship the water deity. Could this be a test sent by them?"

At that time, the outsider and his followers trembled in fear, unable to compose themselves, and replied: "Great King, you should know that there are over five hundred heterodox methods, each with its own fruition, ascending to the Brahma Heaven. Why should there be only one path to the Dao? Now, I and the king shall turn our hearts to serve the water."

Then, all men and women, young and old, in the kingdom wholeheartedly turned to revere the water. After another month, at the second watch of the night, a voice suddenly arose from the water, saying:

*"Though the Great Dao has no form,
It responds like an echo or shadow.
The void of space knows no bounds,
Yet perceptions arise from the mind’s eye.
Water and fire harm your life,
Trapping souls in dark abodes.
The cloud palaces’ carefree infants
Float aloft on the qi’s breeze.
Alas, those who follow deviant paths,
Lost in the dusty snares of delusion.
Grieve for the coming of old age and death,
Who shall reward your decay and ruin?
Why not seek longevity,
In an instant, traversing Heaven and Earth?
Form and spirit suddenly ascend,
Essence and qi forever radiant and vast."*

Upon hearing the true sound, the king and the outsider immediately delved into its meaning. After seven days, their minds suddenly awakened, their lifeless corpses transforming into fragrant remains. They listened to the true and correct teachings, perceiving the upper realms clearly, undeterred by the divine waters. They chanted the sublime sound, sat in silent emptiness, free from deviant thoughts, their minds fixed solely on the Great Dao. After a thousand days, the incense of their hearts ascended, and they sought the master’s guidance.

Then, the Luminous Might Perfected, moved by compassion, beheld their Dharma bodies and luminous forms, and expounded the teachings to the king. The king, Fotuoli, and nine hundred million followers and ministers all attained the Dao at once, ascending into the void, freed from the cycle of birth and death.

After the king of Da Qin attained the Dao, he earnestly entreated the Perfected to expound the method for later generations to dissolve the calamities of the five directions.

The Perfected One declared: The Dao’s method values only long life, aiding the nation and sustaining destiny, delivering the multitudes. To turn from the Dao is to lose life—self-wearied in joy and sorrow, unable to assist or protect all living beings. For this reason, the Supreme Great Dao brings forth the Way to purge the qi of death. Cultivate it with utmost sincerity, and your virtue will move Heaven and Earth. Yet if one merely practices superficial rituals without true devotion, nothing can be achieved, and the five kinds of calamities will not be dispelled.

Those who study the Dao must wholeheartedly aid the nation, performing fasts and rites to avert disasters, earnestly seeking divine response. The master should face the afflicted direction, take seven catties of fine realgar, seal it in a concealed vessel, and sink it into the depths of an abyss—let no one witness this. Inscribe the true scripture in gold upon jade tablets, and enshrine them in the five directions of the nation and within sacred mountains, in secluded cliffs and deep caves. Through fasting and prayer, invoke blessings for the Son of Heaven and all the people. If auspicious signs appear—divine incense wafting, winds stilling the branches, the four limits purified—then great fortune will respond, the nation’s destiny will endure, and the world will know peace.

At such times, the king should ascend the altar to petition Heaven, live in humble palaces and eat simple fare, let his grace flow throughout the land, show compassion to the aged and infirm, extend benevolence to all creatures, and refrain from harming any sentient being. Such a ruler rightfully occupies the throne of Heaven.

Those who study the Dao should follow this scripture, admonish the Son of Heaven, and may also provide abundant support, establishing long fasts in renowned mountains, secretly practicing the supreme method for the sake of the ruler and the people. This is called "hidden virtue," prized for its lack of ostentation. Practicing the supreme method while associating with the high and noble risks disturbing the mundane world; one may avoid transgressions and proceed smoothly.

Those who study the Dao must share virtue with the ruler, together serving all the people under Heaven. If their virtue differs, and they forcibly practice our Way, Heaven will not assist them, and their efforts will be in vain.

The Dao states: Those who study the Dao must possess ten virtues:
1. The first virtue: discerning truth from falsehood, not practicing blindly;
2. The second virtue: delving deeply into the supreme method, exhausting all wondrous gates;
3. The third virtue: steadfastly upholding precepts, the mind not wandering;
4. The fourth virtue: reciting sacred teachings, the mind free from doubt;
5. The fifth virtue: practicing kindness, filial piety, forbearance, and humility, not contending with others;
6. The sixth virtue: diligently performing rituals, the mind never lazy or negligent;
7. The seventh virtue: employing the Dao with gentleness, conducting oneself with subtlety;
8. The eighth virtue: courageously advancing in the Dao, undeterred by peril;
9. The ninth virtue: subduing external demons, liberating oneself from entanglements;
10. The tenth virtue: rescuing oneself from mortal peril, enduring eternally.

The Dao states: Those who study the Dao yet cannot escape mortal peril, who do not depart from deviant methods, have not attained the true Way. Though they may be called men of resolve, they possess no power of the Dao, cannot abide forever, and are swayed by external things. They are not called Daoists but heretics, no different from the common folk.

Those who vainly debate wisdom, forcefully expounding on emptiness without embodying the Dao’s essence, whose four great elements scatter, cannot preserve life. Their hun and shen drift and wander, meeting and relying on chance, drifting for countless kalpas, unable to attain the Dao. Pity the walking corpses of this world, mourning their loss of life—aging, dying, decaying, their spirits wearied in endless rebirth.

There are ten causes for losing the true Way:
1. Losing alignment with the correct path;
2. Deepening sin;
3. Inertia;
4. Deviance and perversity;
5. Arrogance and violence;
6. Heaviness and turbidity;
7. Restless competition;
8. Carelessness;
9. Cowardice;
10. Self-conceit.

These ten things can ruin the true Dao. They all stem from losing alignment with the correct path, branching into endless evils. Practicing the true method, however, branches into myriad transformations, wondrously hidden in the profound, also without end.

Those who study the Dao, establishing merit and building virtue, diligently cultivating the Way of life, distance themselves from mortal peril. On the day their practice is perfected, the true Dao will manifest, and they will be led to roam together.

The Supreme Great Dao cherishes life and abhors killing. Those who cherish life can attain our Dao; those who delight in killing lose our Dao. It is people who turn away, not the Dao that rejects them. The Great Dao is without intent, responding to those who can practice. Those who cannot practice the Dao, the Dao also responds to them—responding with the two paths of yin and yang, life and death. Prosperity and decay, success and failure, entry and exit, rise and fall differ; sorrow and joy oppose each other. Though the Dao constantly seeks to guide and receive, it cannot compel those who refuse. Alas, the common folk, perishing without return, pursue life as if pursuing death.

Heaven bestows cloud chariots to float through the void. If only they loved the Dao as they love wealth and sensual pleasures, Perfected Ones would be their companions, and all spirits their servants. If only they practiced gentleness as they practice harshness, even after dust kalpas as infants, they would never be harmed.

Those who study the true Way, chanting and cherishing this scripture, guarding themselves with precepts, will remain free from misfortune throughout their lives and surely ascend to transcendence.

The Dao states: Before ascending, those who study the Dao still dwell in the human world. They should pity all living beings, dispel their disasters, sustain their lives—this virtue is immense, the foremost merit.

When a region suffers calamity, the master should establish hundreds or thousands of Daoist sanctuaries, purifying the area with fragrant water, setting up altars and seats, placing scriptures and images, guiding the people to take refuge. They should burn incense, light lamps, and perform rites in the six periods, their hearts sincere and earnest, not relying on empty words. Speaking softly and humbly, they should not let the crowd hear.

The master should invoke the Great Dao, explaining the origins of the impending disaster. Then, summon the mighty deities of the five directions:
- In the East: the Nine Azure Dragon Generals, with eighty-one myriad followers;
- In the South: the Three Vermilion Bird Generals, with sixty-four myriad followers;
- In the West: the Seven White Tiger Generals, with thirty-six myriad followers;
- In the North: the Five Dark Warrior Generals, with twenty-five myriad followers.

In the Center: the Twelve Yellow Qilin Generals of Wu and Ji, with ninety thousand followers. Arraying the celestial instruments, they descend into the altar, moving their divine power to extinguish demons and revive the living. According to the source of the illness, the divine prescriptions counter it.

The master should make vows and recite prayers, pitying the sick as a mother loves her child, wishing them freedom from disease. He must strictly command the altar’s order, ensuring all matters are solemn and reverent. Avoid consuming pungent meats, fish, or flesh; male and female impurities; filthy or greasy clothing; discussing heterodox teachings; or acting with arrogance. If the heart is not sincere and reverent, the Dao of Heaven will not assist, evil spirits will not be vanquished, the illness will not be cured, and misfortune will instead befall.

Within the ritual space, fragrant water should be sprinkled every three to five days to purify the area. Those who have not bathed may not enter. Each altar remains active for several ten-day periods before being dissolved. The master does not compel attendance; those who come do so of their own will. For those too ill to perform the rites, they may remain in the world, and it is not strictly required that the sick person perform the rituals themselves. They may stand and observe, and as long as efficacy is achieved, conventional rules need not be rigidly followed.

The Dao states: The methods for healing demonic afflictions comprise three types:
1. Those whose aspiration is to leave the household life but who have not yet understood the precepts and rituals, their intentions biased and perverse, with demonic influences entering their hearts—these must be healed. Without healing, they will not recover. For such persons, sincerity of heart and fragrant water alone suffice. The poor may offer incense with a straightforward heart.
2. Those who devote themselves wholeheartedly to the Dao but have not yet received the Register of Life, practicing long-term abstinence and austerities, their merit and virtue not yet established, suddenly afflicted by misfortune and entering the ritual space—these require offerings of incense, lamps, rice, wood, herbs, and fruit, presented three times.
3. Those who feign devotion to the Dao but harbor heterodox intentions, their bodies stricken with illness and seeking healing, entering the ritual space—these must be assessed for sincerity and strictly follow the rules of the jiao rites. They must also offer silk as tribute, according to their wealth, to repay the grace of the Dao, providing the master with ritual implements, robes, and furnishings for his dwelling. They must further purchase medicine and food to offer to the poor and sick who cannot sustain themselves, ransom lives, and buy incense and oil for temple repairs. None of these may be used for secular purposes; violators will be afflicted with illness for ten days. After ten days, the benevolent spirits will depart, and their learning will not succeed.

If the sick person is not single-minded, their thoughts scattered, or if they violate purity taboos, fail to acknowledge their transgressions, or disobey the master’s teachings, their illness will not be cured. They will immediately face divine retribution, and no physician in the world can save them.

Those who study the Dao and establish merit and virtue, though not yet discerning in reclusive cultivation, must heal the sick in the world with caution and trepidation, as if dwelling in a famous mountain, their hearts no different in devotion. When summoned by others, they must not shirk labor or make excuses, such as claiming prior engagements, being called away after being summoned, or feigning absence. Those who feign illness, harbor suspicions, despise the poor or lowly, covet rewards, demand payment or offerings to sustain personal expenses, or refuse to aid the critically ill will be afflicted with illness for a hundred days. The benevolent spirits will depart, they will be tormented by evil forces, and no physician in the world can save them.

The Dao states: Among those who study the Dao, the Way may be shallow or deep, and virtue may be superior or inferior. If one encounters an enlightened master, they should submit humbly at their feet; or if they meet a perfected being descending to the world; or if the blessings of nine generations flow to them; or if in a past life they practiced the Dao but their merit was incomplete, briefly passing through the Great Yin to be reborn in a royal kingdom—taking advantage of this opportunity, they receive the precious scriptures in full, the royal qi pervading their body, divine might guarding their form. They will no longer undergo birth and death, attaining the perfection of the Dao.

Before ascending, they may wander the mortal realm, their disciples numerous but not yet pure and refined. If they suddenly become impure, purification is required. In such cases, their divine might is of no use; they need only chant the sacred verses to repel demons and recite the great history of the Supreme Sovereign. Their hearts soar with crimson qi, their eyes race like shooting stars. They wield the divine golden sword and illuminate with the round celestial mirror. Or they may sit in lofty stillness within an empty hall, guarding the truth with utmost sincerity. Internally, they visualize and petition without uttering a word. The Three Caverns generate the divine, weaving the warp and weft of concealment. Thus, the six evils are extinguished externally, the five poisons dissolved internally. The hearts of host and guest feel no fatigue, and whatever they undertake encounters no obstacles.

Such masters possess vast and mighty power, and all demonic spirits become their attendants and guards. If any disciples, male or female, have not yet dissolved their karmic obstructions, the supervisors of wrongdoing will censure them, and they may face divine retribution. The master, with compassion, intercedes on their behalf, pleading for the nine generations above and the individual below. If they wholeheartedly repent, there is nothing that cannot be resolved.

The Dao states: No transgression is greater than lewdness, killing one’s parents, or harming one’s master. These sins are extreme and cannot be repented or absolved. One will forever sink into the realms of suffering, with no hope of escape; never beholding the Dao, never hearing the Dharma—how then could one attain the Dao?

Those who study the Dao and all laypeople should cultivate right faith, compassion, filial piety, and obedience. They must not harbor perverse thoughts, turn their backs on the Dao, or forget righteousness. Whether advancing or retreating, they will face inconceivable punishment. If any worldly person or scripture claims that the sins of killing parents or one’s master can be repented, they are still fit for the Dao—this is the teaching of jealous ghosts and demons, the instruction of evil spirits, the words of the deranged. The Great Dao does not acknowledge this, Heaven and Earth do not pardon it. Evil ghosts will punish them with boiling cauldrons and burning coals, and they will forever lose the human realm.

Even the wanton killing of the smallest creatures possessing life and spirit is not pardoned by Heaven—how much less the deliberate, treacherous killing of one’s master? Those who study the Dao should proclaim these precious scriptures, opening the ears and eyes of the common people, making them universally known. The merit of this is incomparable and immeasurable.

The Dao states: At the beginning of the Dragon Han kalpa, during the kalpa of fire, there was a country called Liaoqiu in the midst of the sea, over seventy thousand li west of Huoqiu. There lived a Daoist named Qian Zhong, surnamed Wen, who at the age of twelve left home to seek the Dao. He observed the precept against killing, healed the sick, released living beings, was filial to his parents, and revered his masters and teachers.

Though he had not yet donned the talismans of immortality, by establishing merit and virtue with unwavering resolve, he had already attained his goal from beginning to end. After twenty-seven years, his merit moved the heavens, and within his oratory, perfected beings would often descend, altering their forms to appear as commoners. The spirits of earth and water served as his attendants, aiding in the preparation of rituals and bestowing upon him divine medicines to cure chronic ailments effortlessly. The efficacy of his touch was like hot water melting snow; cutting down demonic spirits required no exertion. He amassed great merit and virtue, taking pity on the poor and the sick.

The Heavenly Worthy of the Cloud Palace, moved by his diligence and knowing his resolve would not falter, on the seventh day of the first month commanded the Radiant Might Perfected to transmit to him the Dao of long life, enabling him to merge with the luminous and ascend to the void. He was conferred the title of Perfected and appointed to govern in the Thirty-Fourth Heaven, having already endured eight hundred million great kalpas. His form reverted to that of an infant, and he could extend his hand to traverse the entire world. The Great Dao, recognizing the vastness of his virtue, decreed that ten years hence, the Five Dragon Kings would elevate his dwelling. Ninety-seven individuals—men and women, high and low—were relocated to the Supreme Purity Heaven, all attaining deathlessness. His merit and virtue were immense, blessing his entire household.

For ordinary people who fail to liberate even themselves, how can their seven ancestors and parents rely on them to escape sin and be reborn among humans? Such a wonder is beyond comprehension.

The Dao states: Those who study the Dao and amass great merit and virtue move the Great Dao to compassion. Thus, their dwellings are raised aloft, and all their household possessions and livestock endure, spared from the calamities of death. This is not because there are no golden towers and jade chambers in the heavens above, but rather that the divine power is revealed through expedient means to ordinary people, urging them to distance themselves from heterodox paths, transcend the laws of decay, aging, and death, and escape the impermanent realms of the evil world—abodes of affliction—to attain the unchanging Dharma of eternal bliss.

Good men and good women, once their hearts embrace faith, across countless kalpas, there will be worthy ones in the world who study the supreme Dao, and their dwellings shall ascend to the void all at once. Good men and women, you should reflect upon this rare occurrence, turn your hearts toward faith, and know that all ordinary people can attain the Dao. Those who lose the true essentials in their study will fail to attain the Dao, but those who cultivate and grasp the truth—there has never been a single one who did not become a sage. The supreme Great Dao’s verification is immediate; why then the need for earnest exhortation?

*Thus concludes the ninth scroll of the Jade Purity Scripture of the Supreme Great Dao.*
*Here begins the tenth scroll of the Jade Purity Scripture of the Supreme Great Dao.*

**Chapter Twenty: The Dharma Seal**

At that time, in the Jade Palace of the Mystic Terrace, the True Person of Central Harmony addressed the later learners. On the seventh day of the seventh month, a grand assembly was held at the Wheel of Kunlun’s Jade Terrace, where they remained for three months. On the seventh day of the tenth month, another grand assembly convened upon the Golden Altar of Kunlun.

The essence of the Morning Star shone in the evening, its divine torch illuminating the radiance of yang’s brilliance, scattering its glow in lingering light. After another three months, on the seventh day of the first month, at the inception of the Supreme Mystery’s primordial origin, the qi of the Azure Heavens flowed into the myriad forms, marking the beginning of all transformations and the inception of Central Harmony’s flux. The True Person of Central Harmony, activating the Three Origins, initiated the first of the Three Assemblies. On this auspicious day, they paid homage to the Supreme Emperor.

At that time, the True Person of Central Harmony, along with a dharma assembly of thirty-six thousand exalted perfected beings, all rode upon the Wheel of the Orthodox Unity and Central Harmony. Their true essence and numinous authority led the way, with cloud-dragons guiding the path, celestial serpents flanking the procession, and the great demons of the Three Realms soaring through the air in chariots. The four divisions of numinous immortals bore aloft flying canopies. The incense officials wafted smoke, burning soul-reviving incense; dragons chanted and phoenixes sang, harmonizing with the celestial melody. A divine breeze gently stirred, circulating in perfect harmony. Fragrant flowers, banners, and canopies drifted upward in graceful ascent. The entire dharma assembly, with divine feet treading the void, moved without effort, as light and effortless as drifting clouds. In an instant, they ascended before the Dharma Gate of the Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy of the Jade Purity.

At that time, during the morning audience of the perfected beings of the upper realms, they paid homage to the Heavenly Worthy and then proceeded to the Right Cloud Palace of the Jade Purity to offer reverence to the Great Compassionate True Emperor. As time passed into the hour of *si*, the assembly of exalted immortals from the ten directions gathered to pay homage to the Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy. As time passed into midday, the lower immortals and celestial officials of the upper bureaus reviewed the registers of immortals. As time passed into the hour of *zi*, the officials of the Water and Fire Bureaus recorded the ledgers of life and death.

The Heavenly Worthy, for the sake of all sentient beings, also designated the three origin months, with the fifteenth day of each month as the time for the Three Bureaus to present their audience. For later learners offering homage, the seventh day of the first month of the Three Origins suffices, where morning and evening they may recite vows, repent transgressions, and seek blessings.

The Great Compassionate and Great Merciful Two August True Emperors are the ancestors of Heaven and Earth, the primordial root of all transformations. All later learners and sages trace their origin to the Dao of compassion. When paying homage and contemplating, one must first practice compassion. For this reason, throughout the ten directions of the cosmos, in the heavens above and the earth below, all beings—ordinary and sacred—speak of the Great Compassion and Great Mercy as the true teaching, the Dao of the Two Emperors’ compassion. Yet the worldly beings below grasp only its branches, rarely recognizing its root. If the officials of the Three Bureaus fail to pay homage to the Two August Ones during the four seasons and eight solar terms, they lose the Dao of compassion and cannot nurture the myriad beings.

Thus, Heaven covers and Earth bears all things without refusal. Above, the Dao of compassion of the Three August Ones and the titles of the Two August Ones are bestowed upon the ordinary folk of the lower realms—what is called "compassionate parent" is modeled upon this. All sentient beings who attain the Dao of compassion can nurture and raise the multitude of life. Though they may not universally attain the singular heart of the Great Dao, they can, like the Great Dao, nurture all that moves and grows. If all beings endowed with qi lacked compassion, they could not even sustain themselves—how then could they nurture the myriad things?

Therefore, those who study the higher teachings must first embody compassion, for then their cultivation becomes easily accomplished, and their words are heard on high. Even ordinary beings with sincere hearts may cultivate the supreme Dao in seclusion, and the Dao will respond to them. Thus, the four divisions of lower immortals do not waver in their resolve for the Dao. I perceive their aspiration and, through expedient means, guide them to ascend to the Jade Purity and pay homage to the True Emperor. Our assembly of perfected beings should spiritually commune, ever attending the Two August Ones as intimate companions. Though separated by thirty-six thousand heavens and earths, it is as if we dwell together in a single chamber, never feeling distant. Why is this so?

The ten directions and dust-like worlds share a single Dao-body. For this reason, in the ten directions of the cosmos, not a single thing or dharma can depart from the Dao-body; all sentient beings are the Dao-qi of the Two August Ones. Therefore, I lead the lower immortals to ascend to the upper realms, to pay homage and offer felicitations to the Two August Ones, to bow in reverence and inquire after their well-being, and to request the immortal seal, teaching and awakening later students.

At that time, the Perfected of Central Harmony, together with his attendants, prostrated at the cloud-gate, bowing for a long while. Burning incense and concentrating in mind, before any words took form, another long interval passed. Such a long while had elapsed that, in the lower worlds, ninety thousand great kalpas had already transpired.

Gazing upward into the cloud-palace, one saw emptiness and whiteness, clarity and vastness, solitude and brightness, purity and brilliance. Only nine-colored felicitous clouds draped and encircled it, their radiant hues intermingling in a display beyond compare. Within the void, true qi congealed into celestial scriptures, pervading the realm of the Dao. The characters were distinct and clear, easy to discern upon careful observation, yet those who recited them lightly could not comprehend their meaning.

The perfected immortals, concentrating in mind on the Greatly Compassionate Heavenly Worthy, wished to express their heart’s desire and spoke thus: “We pray for later students, that their doubts and entanglements be severed, and that the Heavenly Worthy bestow the Dharma-seal from his golden mouth.” Having spoken these words, they fell silent for a long while.

Suddenly, before the cloud-dragon throne of the Greatly Compassionate Heavenly Worthy, the incense smoke from the hundred-jeweled censer rose of its own accord, like the divine peaks exhaling great clouds—thick, luxuriant, and billowing, spreading throughout other realms. Heavenly flowers flew through the air, cloud-dragons danced in the void, sweet dew gently moistened all, the winds and dust stilled, phoenixes and simurghs sang in harmony, their sounds blending into sacred hymns that chanted the celestial scriptures. Though they moved through billions of kalpas, they never ceased. Those who listened forgot weariness, relinquished scattered thoughts, concentrated their minds in recollection, and all received benefit.

After such a long while, suddenly the Heavenly Worthy emerged from the void, his luminous qi and Dharma-body pervading all of empty space and existence. True qi spread afar, present everywhere—it was not only in the upper realms that the Heavenly Worthy dwelled, for in the ten directions of the cosmos, wherever one looked, he was there. The myriad phenomena were none other than his Dharma-body.

At that time, the four divisions of attendant immortals—eighty-four thousand cloud-canopy bearers and minor immortals—were not counted among the assembly. Witnessing the wondrous Dao-power of the Greatly Compassionate Heavenly Worthy, they all marveled in astonishment, exclaiming that they had never seen the like.

Then the Perfected of Central Harmony and the upper immortals, having already attained the six penetrations, remained silent, communing spiritually with the sand-like worlds without obstruction. Yet through expedient means, they wished to enable the lower immortals to see and hear the supreme Dao, to ascend to the upper realms, to pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy, and to request the Dharma-seal for later students. They did not act as teachers themselves, but the Dharma’s response was fittingly heard by the Greatly Compassionate True Emperor.

Thereupon, the Perfected of Central Harmony, on behalf of later students, addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: “The lower worlds are dusty and foul, with many paths of affliction. Having bathed in the mysterious grace for kalpas uncounted, we have constantly received the guiding hand of the Dharma, yet we foolish and deluded ones, adrift and wandering, have not attained perfection. The five emotions contend within, the six thieves rush outward. Later students, harboring divergent views, do not practice the great Dao, but stray into deviant currents, following the flow of suffering, subject to birth, aging, sickness, and death. For this reason, we cannot bear to see or hear of it.”

The Heavenly Worthy replied: “Excellent, excellent, good man! The later students of the lower worlds have shallow understanding of the Dao—how could they transcend the suffering flow of birth and death? Birth, aging, sickness, and death are the common lot of the world. Only those who possess the Dao can reverse the flow of suffering. Though in worldly teachings there are words of reversal, there is no true reversal in substance; though there is reversal in principle, there is none in practice. When principle is clear but practice is obstructed, this is not what the Dao esteems. When there are words but no substance, this too is not esteemed. Only when principle and practice are both clear, when words and substance are both realized—this is what my Dao accomplishes. The shallow, worldly, false, and defiled teachings of the lower realms are not worth inquiring about.”

Thereupon, the Perfected One bowed his head and received the command.

Then the eighty-four thousand direct messengers, canopy-bearing minor immortals, and the four divisions of numinous beings, who had not yet heard the supreme Dao and could not discern its profound meaning, were earnest in their questioning.

At that time, among the assembly, a minor immortal named Precious Appearance came forward, bowed, and addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: “Your servants are later students with shallow understanding of the Dao and do not comprehend its profound meaning. We have often heard in the records and transmissions of the ignorant and ordinary that our Dharma can transcend birth, aging, sickness, and death, can emerge from the flow of birth and death, attain the six penetrations, and achieve unimpeded wisdom. Yet we see that such people differ not at all from the ordinary—they are born, age, fall ill, and cannot escape death. We do not know whether these words are true or false. We only pray that the Heavenly Worthy, in his great compassion, will look upon our ignorance with mercy.”

Having spoken, he bowed his head and awaited the Heavenly Worthy’s merciful decree.

Then the Greatly Compassionate Heavenly Worthy, moved by compassion for the minor immortals, spoke to them: “Good men, you have attained the Dao and stand in the four divisions, having just entered the flow of the Dao, yet you have not escaped birth and death. It is only because you have received the blessings of past connections and encountered the assembly of heavenly perfected ones that your lives have been prolonged. Were it not so, you would long since have dissolved into ashes. What you have heard are the transmissions of worldly scriptures, which also say that our Dharma can transcend birth, aging, sickness, and death, and emerge from the flow of birth and death. Yet you see their bodies still subject to worldly arising and ceasing. This is the teaching of those who have entered principle—they speak of emptiness and attain unimpeded eloquence, but they cannot embody principle and attain true freedom. Their minds differ from the ordinary, yet birth, aging, sickness, and death remain unchanged. The suffering and afflictions of the world, the turning of the flow of birth and death—those who have entered principle, lacking the power of the Dao in their bodies, cannot reverse them. Only the great Dao can transcend them. The supreme Dharma of the Dao can transcend birth, aging, sickness, and death, and reverse the flow of suffering.

Good men, those who practice my Dharma, in their embodied existence, can attain long life, transform the ordinary into the sagely, and return to the formless. Harmonizing with luminous qi, they emerge from being and enter non-being, unimpeded in all things.”

“Good men, those who skillfully apply my Dharma to the principle of aging may reverse their forms to infancy and return to long life—this is called transcending old age. Those who apply my Daoist Dharma to the deluded and the afflicted with illness and suffering may free them from sickness, healing their afflictions—this is called transcending all who suffer from illness, rendering them free from disease. Those who apply my Daoist Dharma to the souls of the dead and the sinful may liberate them from suffering. For those who wish to be reborn, let their wishes be fulfilled; for those who do not wish to be reborn, let them attain non-rebirth—this is called transcending death.

Good men, the suffering currents of worldly Dharma arise from the root of greed and desire. Within the great Dao’s Dharma, there is the method of ‘removing the corpse and restraining the po’—those who cultivate and study this Dao will be free from desires. The currents of suffering also arise from the burdens of affection, worry, clothing, and food, yet within the great Dao there are the Eight Treasures of Heavenly Robes and garments of spontaneity, which adjust to one’s size and length. Within the great Dao’s Dharma, there is the qi of Supreme Harmony, the numinous talismans of Yin generation, and the divine waters and jade nectars that sate hunger and thirst, dispelling old age, death, afflictions, and illness—unlike the perilous and unstable provisions of the world. This is called the true Dharma of the great Dao, which reverses the currents of affliction and suffering and severs the cycle of birth and death forever.

The superficial worldly Dharmas claim to transcend birth, aging, sickness, and death, and to reverse the currents of worldly suffering. It is like a man afflicted with a hundred illnesses, impoverished and suffering, unable to obtain what he seeks, who then speaks falsehoods to deceive the ignorant, claiming, ‘I am a heavenly master, skilled in curing all diseases, versed in remedies, acupuncture, and moxibustion.’ The foolish hear this and rush to him, bearing offerings, relying on this deluded teacher and receiving his methods. Yet their illnesses do not heal, and their confusion only deepens. All their poverty and sickness come to resemble their teacher’s. The wise observe this, recognize its falsity, and abandon him to depart.

Thus, the wise choose their teachers carefully. Having met a true teacher, one who can truly heal illness, whose disciples are compassionate and kind, who pity the poor and sick and treat their afflictions—when such a teacher acts, it is like hot water melting snow. Yet these deluded teachers and their disciples, no different from the foolish, having received the true teacher’s Dharma, say: ‘If we follow this Dharma and gain sustenance, supporting our lives, what harm is there?’ The two groups—wise and foolish—stand in opposition. Then the disciples of the deluded teachers grow jealous of the true teacher, slandering him day and night. Yet the true teacher, morning and evening, advances the Dao, practicing great compassion, and does not contend with them.

Good men, the worldly Dharmas are like those foolish men, practicing deviant paths, while the true teacher’s Dharma is like my great Dao, the true teaching that can transcend old age and death, reverse the currents of affliction, and flow in harmony with the Dao.

The Heavenly Worthy further said: The worldly Dharmas do not attain the Six Penetrations or unimpeded wisdom—these are also false claims, unworthy of trust. Why? If the worldly Dharmas, when cultivated by people, could attain the Six Penetrations and resemble the Dao without distinction in superiority or inferiority, they should be able to reverse the currents of old age and death. Yet since they still age, fall ill, and ultimately perish, they are clearly without wisdom, definitively lacking the Six Penetrations and the power of the Dao.

Good men, use my Dharma-seal to seal all that is false and deviant, and you will naturally recognize that without cultivating the Dharma-seal, there is no way to discern falsehood.

Good men, there are those in the world who merely cultivate the principle of emptiness, doing nothing else, and verify it within themselves, claiming it is no different from the Dao. Such people only attain arrogance and the sin of boastfulness. For thousands upon thousands of lives, they will never attain the Dao. Why? Their arrogance prevents them from wishing to see the Dao, forever separating them from it, causing them to remain in the cycle of birth and death, flowing with the currents of suffering.

The Dao says: If there are those who seek the supreme blessing, not seeing any arising of existence, and say, ‘Originally I was unborn; this present body is like a dream or illusion,’ and wish to extinguish and transcend it to seek non-rebirth—good men, such people are tainted by deviant influences, speaking mad words without restraint. Why? To seek non-rebirth, one should cultivate the subtle and wondrous Dharma of the supreme Dao, using the power of the Dao to reverse old age and death, not flowing with worldly currents, and only then ascend into the formless, becoming neither born nor extinguished. It is not by extinguishing birth that one attains non-rebirth.

Good men, those without the Dao cannot preserve their forms—by this verification, it is clear they lack the power of the Dao. Lacking the power of the Dao, they cannot attain non-rebirth. Later disciples, hold my Dharma-seal and use it to seal all deviant paths. The Dharma will reveal itself, and without needing to attain the methods they cultivate, you will know them.

Good men, if there are those who study the wisdom of non-arising and say, ‘I study non-arising, yet cannot preserve my form; by this body, I attain the wondrous Dao, seeing the body ascend and transcend. Merely extinguishing this body, I return to the formless, and there will be no further arising’—if any being speaks thus, this is deviant speech, not the true teaching. Why? The Dao is not a Dharma of extinction. Seeking the Dao by extinguishing the body results in the Dao existing while the body perishes. Cultivating my Dharma-seal, preserving life to seek the Dao, results in both the Dao and the body existing, and only then can one empty the body and merge with the Dao. It is not by extinguishing birth that one merges with the Dao.

Then the Heavenly Worthy further addressed the immortals, saying: Though the Dao exists, it can be empty; though the body exists, it can be non-existent. Only when it can be empty and non-existent is it called the Dao.

Good men, that which can preserve but not extinguish is not the Dao; that which can extinguish but not preserve is also not the Dao. The supreme great Dao can both preserve and extinguish, and those who attain the Dao are likewise. All external paths can extinguish but cannot preserve.

Good men, you must now know: flowing toward death is easy, reversing it to avoid death is difficult. Good men, you must now know: those who flow toward death and are called ‘attainers of the Dao’—all corpses may also be called ‘attainers of the Dao.’”

If all corpses cannot be called "attainers of the Dao," then it is clear that the external paths’ destruction of form is not the attainment of the Dao. These external paths are called the path of entering death, not the path of ascending into formlessness and enduring eternally.

Good men, ascending into formlessness means cultivating the seal of my Dao, transforming the mundane into the sacred, refining the substance into subtlety, becoming indestructible and unchanging like empty space.

Good men, if there are beings who allow their bodies to arise and perish, unable to generate firmness, with the four great elements dispersing and their forms reduced to dung and dust, yet still hope for their souls and spirits to realize the supreme Dao—this is like a fool grasping at empty space to seek traces, and it shall never be attained. When the seal of my Dharma is applied to such fools, they are far from the Dao.

Good men, if among the masters, disciples, and followers of my Dharma, they transform beings through the path of conditioned arising—such as establishing pure halls, offering incense and lamps, providing expedient benefits to those who do not understand, showing kindness to all creatures, refraining from harming life, setting up vegetarian feasts to invoke blessings, and repenting for transgressions—they should not seize others’ treasures, grains, or silks, nor harm beings to sustain themselves, nor forsake righteousness and abandon great compassion. Such people are not my disciples but followers of heretical factions.

Those who do not harm beings and do not abandon great compassion are true disciples of the Dao. If my disciples, through the path of conditioned arising, transform those of lower roots and deluded beings who cling to self and others, indulging in filth, wine, and lust, accumulating without restraint, they should teach them the impermanence of life, the fragility of the body, and the precariousness of the four great elements. As for external wealth, they should employ expedient means to instruct without harming lives or property—such people are my true disciples.

If among the masters and disciples of my Dharma, they teach others to offer wealth, valuables, servants, livestock, houses, or fields, yet privately use them for personal gain without cultivating merit, these are called "thieves of the Dao." Those who do not sever ignorance and greed are unfit to transform others; they lead later learners to become worldly beings in future lives. If you encounter such thieves, be cautious and do not associate with them.

The Dao says: In later ages, foolish people will steal the essentials of my Dao and peddle them for profit, seeking wealth and indulging in wine and lust. Such transgressions are also called "thieves of the Dao." They are not my disciples but followers of external paths, heretical spirits, and accomplices of yin thieves. Those who uphold the seal of the great Dao should, upon seeing such people, keep their distance, avoid sharing the same village, and refrain from speaking with them.

The Dao says: These heretical masters and their disciples, driven by greed, exhort ordinary people to cultivate the path of causal conditions, urging them to make offerings and taking their grains and silks for private use. They claim to be great masters of the world, capable of increasing blessings and generating goodness for beings, asserting that those who offer to them will gain boundless merit. In later ages, those who study the truth and cultivate the seal of my Dharma will apply this seal to such fools, branding them as heretical thieves. Those who make offerings should not give to such people, for it will bring retribution in future lives, causing them to fall into the three evil destinies. Those who bestow alms should cultivate goodness, not evil. For this reason, they should not make offerings.

Disciples of the Dao who hold the seal of my Dharma must be cautious not to follow the ways of such heretical customs.

The Dao says: In a past kalpa, there was a heretical master named Seeking Fame. Lazy in clothing and food, he falsely claimed to have attained the Dao, hiding in a cold forest. He constantly proclaimed, "I have realized the Dao and deeply understand the characteristics of the Dharma." He walked while gazing at the ground, entered villages to teach, and after three years, the people outside the forest competed to make offerings to him, filling his store of wealth and food.

With these ill-gotten gains, he secretly provided for his wife and children, purchasing fish and meat to consume in seclusion, falsely claiming to eat only vegetarian fare. For eight years he continued thus. The celestial authorities executed him, and his soul was condemned to the filth-pit hell for eight hundred kalpas. Thereafter, he was reborn beneath the cold forest, taking form in a sheep’s womb. Thrice each year he was born anew, fully repaying his benefactors over five hundred lifetimes. Later, he entered a cow’s womb, again repaying human labor for another five hundred lives. Even now, he remains a servant, still unreleased. Though granted long life—living a hundred years without death—his sinews are feeble, his strength insufficient for labor, and he is constantly despised and scorned by the world. For eight years of deceit, falsely claiming to have attained the Dao, he suffers retribution across endless kalpas. How much worse for those who spend their entire lives in fraud, calling themselves masters, greedily seeking fame and profit, harming the lives and wealth of all beings? For countless kalpas they endure punishment, still unreleased, with no hope of entering the unborn—how could they ever attain liberation?

Men and women of later generations who hold my precious seal must be cautious never to deceive or accept offerings from others.

At that time, though the assembled immortals revered the Celestial Worthy’s golden-mouthed Dharma-seal, their minds remained clouded, unable to discern clearly. Together they bowed and respectfully petitioned the Celestial Worthy once more: "Previously, we received the golden-mouthed Dharma-seal of the Merciful One, which declared that those who practice our Dharma can transcend birth, old age, sickness, and death. Yet we remain uncertain—by what wondrous Dharma does the Merciful One deliver beings, enabling them to attain non-birth, non-aging, non-sickness, and non-death? Though we have received your compassion, we still perceive the sufferings of birth, old age, sickness, and death no differently than the world’s heretical customs. We beseech the Merciful One to explain further." Having spoken, they bowed their heads, weeping bitterly, prostrating themselves upon the ground, unwilling to rise, yearning for the descent of profound stillness.

Then the Greatly Compassionate Celestial Worthy addressed the divine assembly, saying: "Good sons, this Dao is most wondrous, its Dharma supremely spiritual, teaching all to attain perfection. It is not imparted to the vulgar or lesser immortals. You who now behold me are not far from the true. Moved by your sincerity, I shall not conceal it from you. Listen carefully, for I shall now explain."

In an instant, the Greatly Compassionate Celestial Worthy commanded the thirty-nine Perfected Ones attending at his side to strike the drums in the Great Compassion Palace of the Grand Void. Naturally, roots took form, and the void ordered the hun-souls. With wondrous harmony, they chanted the thirty-nine chapters of the Golden Phoenix Songs, regulating the thirty-nine qi, reciting their titles in a single moment.

At that time, jade-like branches unfurled, and gem-like blossoms bloomed. When the tuning was complete, the myriad transformations returned to their root. The thirty-nine Perfected Ones transformed into ethereal light, and the Golden Phoenixes altered their forms to become wondrous qi. Light and qi intermingled, shimmering like spring blossoms.

In an instant, they changed into immortal clouds, entering the palace, condensing upon the beams and rafters, still and unmoving. Within the Great Compassion Palace, roots took form anew, and the void ordered the hun-souls with wondrous chanting. The lyrics were as follows:

*"The Palace of Compassion illumines the true radiance,
Outshining the dawn’s first light.
The six directions open their gates,
The grand void reveals its windows.
Cloud-canopies array as light veils,
The nine qi transform into flying dragons.
With a single lift of divine feet, one roams,
Drifting without trace.
The Dao is named the Greatly Compassionate Worthy,
Whose divine power knows no equal.
The celestial scriptures array the myriad forms,
Chanting and sighing harmonize the heart and breast."*

Then the Celestial Worthy’s brows and divine hairs gleamed with radiance, brighter than the morning sun. The Dao-realm shone with penetrating brilliance, dispelling darkness to reveal dawn. The ten directions of the world all became clearly visible within the light.

At that time, the Treasure Forms and all the assembled multitudes beheld this true light. Their mind’s eyes became clear, and they saw all forms and images throughout the ten directions of the world, bright and unobstructed.

In an instant, the Greatly Compassionate Celestial Worthy filled the light entirely, expounding the Dharma everywhere. All forms and images could also speak, aiding in the recitation of the celestial scriptures. Those who listened well became worthy or sage, using this wondrous Dao to transcend the torrent of suffering. Those who ingested this wondrous qi immediately attained effortless attainment.

The dead who obtained it could receive new life;
The living who obtained it became free from illness;
The aged who obtained it reverted to infancy;
The sick who obtained it were instantly cured;
The Daoists who obtained it returned to their root and source;
The worldly who obtained it saw their wishes fulfilled;
The foolish who obtained it forever left blindness behind;
The heavens who obtained it saw the Three Luminaries steadfast and bright;
The great earth who obtained it never collapsed or sank;
The myriad things who obtained it could fulfill their lives;
The mute who obtained it could immediately speak;
The lame and infirm who obtained it could instantly fly.

The Heavenly Worthy addressed the numinous beings, saying: This Dharma-seal of mine is the Way for all later learners to preserve life and maintain bodily integrity, the Way of non-death. All sentient beings who lose this Way of mine will invariably suffer bodily ruin and the extinction of life, drifting with the current into death. Deprived of the power of the Way, they cannot attain non-death, nor can they escape death.

Men and women of later generations who study the truth and uphold this Dharma-seal of mine—let them deeply contemplate this Way, for it is the root and foundation of all later learners. If any sentient being departs from the subtle and wondrous Dharma of my great Way, there is no possibility of attaining the Way of bodily integrity and non-death. To lose my Way of life is like a bird losing its wings; it is also like one who would cross a river yet has lost their boat and raft—though the far shore may be seen in the distance, there is no means to reach it.

All the myriad things that lose the qi of my Way will never attain life. All sentient beings who claim they can attain the Way while departing from the great Way are like grasses and trees that, far removed from earth and water, assuredly cannot sprout and grow. All sentient beings who distance themselves from my Way will assuredly not attain the Way.

Good man, these matters may be understood by analogy, and the truth is clear and easily seen. That things are not used according to their kind—fools do not comprehend this; yet even when things are used according to their kind, people still fail to understand. Though the shallow and worldly may know what accords with kind and what does not, they cannot apply this knowledge with precision. When application is proper, one can preserve life; when improper, one harms their own form. Gain and loss stand in opposition, as do life and death.

The boundary between ascent and descent, deviation and correctness, life and death—this is naturally discerned, and there is no distance in it; yet once dualistic views arise, among ten thousand, not one can return. For these reasons, those who attain the Way are few, while those who lose it are many; those who are true and upright are few, while those who practice deviance are many.

The Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy says: All you assembled multitudes, merely recite the most true and wondrous invocations of the Great Compassion Palace, ingest and employ their numinous efficacy, and you shall skillfully emerge from the currents of birth and death, and deliver yourselves from the sufferings of birth, aging, sickness, and death.

The Heavenly Worthy further declares: These subtle words are no empty speech; their efficacy lies in ingestion and application. When word and deed are both enacted, numinous verification is immediate. Though one may recite the words countless times, they shall not touch old age and death. To practice without speech is to sever oneself from the dust. Child, if you can sever yourself from the dust, you shall dwell as a neighbor to the Dao. Dwelling as a neighbor to the Dao, things cannot resent you. When things cannot resent you, this is called returning to the root. With no form to inherit, preserving life enters into the formless—this is called non-birth.

Good son, one whose form is not whole cannot attain non-birth; one whose life is not whole is called entering death. Those who enter death are said to lack the power of the Dao. Without the power of the Dao, one cannot attain non-birth. To be born and enter death is no better than grasses and trees or insects and ants, which live but a morning and die by dusk. Though humans pass through a single lifetime claiming to study the Dao, if they only learn empty practices and hollow incantations, they shall not escape birth and death. Why is this? The practice of emptiness is possible for the highest sages, but for the learning ordinary person, it obstructs every encounter. Neglecting the tools of life, failing to gather form and spirit, life cannot be secured, and form and spirit scatter. Empty birth, empty death—such cannot attain the Dao.

Later, when the learning sage first stands upon the ground of study, they gather life and order its tools, diligent from dawn to dusk. Only after attaining the Dao can they then achieve emptiness—not that one practices empty methods while still in study. Good son, the deviant and false factions of the world’s vulgar currents, having heard peripherally of the subtle and wondrous dharma of the Great Dao that preserves form and life and enters non-birth, suppose that after the destruction of the body, the refined spirit and sinful ghosts may attain non-birth. These deviant and vulgar ones, practicing empty methods, claim their minds can act without obstruction, their power can overturn heaven and earth, reverse yin and yang, harmonize water and fire, and perceive no hindrance in the birth and death of heaven, earth, and the myriad things. Those who hold such views call themselves attainers of the Dao, deceiving the world to seek fame and profit. They disrespect their parents, or speak of non-birth while clinging to deluded thoughts. When the time of death arrives, they claim there is no death, no afflictions, no hunger, no cold, no sickness. All such views are but delusion.

When the vulgar and deviant hold such views, they call themselves attainers of the Dao. If one in my dharma, at the initial stage of learning, holds such views, this is called forgetting the taboo, rebelling against the Great Dao. The Dao does not darkly protect them; their bodies lack the power of the Dao. They live in darkness and die in darkness, unable to escape any karmic reckoning—how then could they realize the Dao? The officials of the nether bureaus still record their names in the black ledger for their hollow incantations, deceiving themselves and others. Such people mislead countless others, forever losing the path of life. Though they speak grand words, they do not practice the Great Dao. They are like the sick claiming to cure illness, or the lame selling medicine for swift travel. At first hearing, their words seem true, but the wise, upon examination, know their error.

At that time, Baoxiang and the assembled multitude bowed again and kowtowed, speaking thus: "Formerly, we received the Compassionate Venerable One’s discourse on the marvelous qi of the Dao, which those who ingest it need not await. We now humbly request its method to aid our bodily existence, that we may practice it lifelong without daring to carelessly divulge it."

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "The supreme and ultimate Dharma is bestowed upon those who can practice it. Since you have the heart for it, my Dao shall not be concealed. Listen carefully: the divine Dao of the utmost spirit admits no precedence."

Baoxiang and the assembled multitude prostrated themselves upon the ground, receiving the teaching with single-minded devotion.

The Heavenly Worthy declared: "The marvel of Dao-qi is of the most divine method. The ten thousand images of heaven and earth are born of primordial qi; there is not a single thing that does not attain freedom through primordial qi. Rising and sinking, flying and walking, they roam by riding qi. With qi, they exist; without qi, they perish. Those that exist cannot die; those that perish cannot live. Qi has purity and turbidity; affairs have adversity and prosperity. Ingesting pure qi enlivens; harnessing turbid qi kills. Pure qi ascends and floats; turbid qi descends and sinks. Pure qi forms heaven; turbid qi forms earth. True essence and marvelous qi are called pure qi; coagulation, filth, stagnation, and impurity are called turbid qi. The path of death is murky and turbid like muddy water; the path of life is limpid and clear like pure water. Humans are like fish; qi is like water. When water is turbid, fish grow emaciated; when qi is murky, people fall ill.

"Good man, the minds of sentient beings in the lower world are often rebellious and contrary, vexed and restless. They seek all manner of desires, their temperaments given to joy and anger, their natures fierce and violent—all these are death-qi. Benevolence, filial piety, composure, deliberation, harmony, and refined gentleness—these are life-qi. Forgetting the self and merging with the Dao, unaware of worldly burdens, myriad transformations pass unseen before the eyes, a thousand sounds go unheard by the ears. Movement is as if non-existent; stillness is as if emptiness. Constantly abiding in pure qi, let it flow into the twin palaces, dispersing and circulating through the meridians, suffusing the entire body like drifting clouds. At the celestial palace, exhale gently half the qi. With the mind focused on the remaining half, let it circulate through the twin palaces, preventing dissipation. At dawn, consume purple blossoms; at dusk, savor yellow coptis. This method is the ingestion of the morning qi of the sun, employing our morning qi to safeguard and witness great peace. Take enough to be satiated; there is no fixed limit. Thus, the meridians flow unimpeded, the hundred passages are harmonized and supple, complexion becomes radiant, hair turns black, and strength doubles. To preserve the body and perfect life, nothing surpasses this Dao. This Dao is the gateway and window of later sages, the pivot of true learning, the root of all myriad existences. Its circulation and coagulation form heaven and earth, sun and moon, stars and constellations, wind and qi, clouds and rain, frost and snow, mountains and rivers, soil and stone, plants and trees, water and fire, the wise and foolish, the ordinary and sacred, humans and non-humans—all are transformations of a single qi, riding its movements to attain life.

"Those who practice my Dao are called worthy; those who employ my Dao are called sages. Those who do not use this Dao are called walking corpses. Their forms disperse and scatter, their ethereal souls become sinful ghosts, sinking into the nine springs.

"At that time, when the Heavenly Worthy had finished expounding this Dharma, from his golden mouth issued forth thirty-six thousand rays of true, marvelous qi. All sounds harmonized in unison, celestial music flowed everywhere, and both the sentient and insentient spontaneously resonated. The assembled immortals below, having received the true qi of the Dao, together expressed their gratitude for this new life, rejoicing with boundless joy. Practicing this marvelous Dao, they all preserved their bodies and entered the path of non-birth. After attaining the Dao, they steadfastly cultivated without cessation.

"The Dao declared: 'Disciples of the Dao who have gained the power of the Dao are unknown to ordinary beings. Observing their forms, though not plump, their complexions are upright, their strength robust, their bodies light and marvelous, their skin and countenance moist and lustrous. Their hearing and perception are unobstructed, their gait is light and agile, they do not sleep at dawn or dusk, their bodies are free from blemishes and diseases, their appearance is fresh and pure, their voices clear and resonant. Such people are said to have gained the power of the Dao. Advancing in cultivation without retreat, they are certain to escape birth, old age, sickness, and death.'

"Good man, imprint these superior practitioners with the seal of my Dharma; verification is immediate, not awaiting attainment before knowing.

"The Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy further addressed the immortals: 'Do you wish to know the false Daoists? Observe their forms. If in the world there are those who claim to have attained the Dao, profoundly understanding its principles, or say they practice the Dao day and night without rest, or have done so for thirty or forty years—right and wrong can be discerned, gain and loss easily known.

"Good man, do you know the false Daoists? First, they consume blood-food; second, they indulge in lust; third, they suffer from grave illnesses. Their qi swells with sores and tumors, scabies and leprosy, jaundice and fistulas. Practicing heterodoxy, they lose their nature, suffering from watery distension and abdominal masses. Their complexions are scorched and dry, their ears and noses withered and parched. Everywhere they ache, their breath is labored, their fluids exhausted, lacking any moisture. They are slothful and wallow in filth, unable to forget life and death. Their appearance is grimy and greasy, their bodies foul-smelling wherever they go. They are quick to relieve themselves, fond of speaking ill, restless and competitive, insatiably acquisitive. Their flesh is ample but their bones small, their gaze shallow and near. Their natures lack benevolence, their hearts lack filial piety. Such people are certainly unable to attain the Dao. These are called leaky bodies, also named ruined bodies. Even if they possess some Dao-qi, they cannot save themselves, much less save others. Like those who cannot sustain themselves, how can they sustain others?

"Good man, when false Daoists perform their methods, men and women intermingle, doors are shut, and they bestow alms of wealth and food—but only to external paths, unable to universally bestow. This is called leaky practice and leaky almsgiving, not the true Dharma, not Dharma-giving. The supreme Great Dao is benevolent to all under heaven, dispersing primordial qi to nurture the ten thousand things, manifesting kindness while concealing its function. It does not rely on its merit, does not see what it bestows, does not see what it receives, much less seek recompense. The methods of external paths do not sever delusion and greed—these are called leaky and are certainly unable to attain the Dao.'"

"If my disciples perform such almsgiving, they align with those demonic deviants. My later disciples who hold my Dharma-seal—should they encounter such persons—must not walk with them, nor dwell together in Dharma. They ought to rebuke and admonish them with Dharma-teachings; if they refuse to comply, let Heaven condemn them. They must not take lives or strike with fists, for to commit such violent offenses incurs the sin of execution, and Heaven’s law grants no pardon."

The Heavenly Worthy said: "Later disciples who cultivate my Great Dao, while still in the stage of learning and before attaining realization, must embody compassion, forbearance, and humility, extending kindness to all sentient beings and fulfilling filial piety toward all. They should wear simple garments and eat plain, pure vegetarian fare, burn incense and offer vows, diligently practicing morning and evening. Their conduct must be meticulous, ever wary of evil; they should neither rush nor compete, dwelling in tranquil stillness. They chant the precious scriptures in soft voices with even breath, harmonizing body and mind, avoiding all stray thoughts. With single-minded devotion, they contemplate the Dao as if awaiting something. They ingest subtle qi, expelling the old and absorbing the new, consuming sacred mushrooms and divine herbs, along with spirit talismans and holy water. They retreat from the world, avoiding worldly affairs. Those who cultivate thus for less than a year will find divine attendants serving them, all poisons unable to harm them. Old illnesses vanish, their complexion reverts to youth, their strength becomes robust, and they naturally seek abundant blessings, their body and mind never sated. I seal such persons to surely attain the true Dao."

The Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy further addressed Baoxiang, saying: "In the lower world, foolish men who neither cultivate the Great Dao nor the supreme, ultimate Dharma yet claim: 'One must destroy this body to attain purity and meet the true essence.' This is like the southern slopes of Kunlun Mountain in the lower world, where long ago there lived a barbarian named Youposina. His nature was fierce and stubborn, and he kept many wives and children. His third wife was exceedingly ugly and bore him ten sons. The barbarian thought to himself, despising this wife..."

The wife again became pregnant. Thereupon, the barbarian thought only of his sons and, impatient to wait for the birth, poisoned the mother to death. After her life ended, he cut open her belly to remove the child, but the child was still unformed, only a congealed mass of flesh, which rotted along with the mother and could not be grasped. The barbarian, filled with self-loathing, later regretted his actions and said: "If only my wife’s body were like a mule’s—when pregnant, one could cut open her belly to take the child." Those who witnessed this told him: "Elder, you should know that when a mule is pregnant, one waits until the full term, knowing the mother is about to give birth, then cuts open her belly to save the child’s life. But your wife’s body differs from a mule’s. Moreover, she had only been pregnant for three months. Even if her term were full, you should not have killed her. How could cutting open her belly to take the child compare to nurturing the mother so she could raise her son? If the child had grown to maturity, the mother would have died of old age naturally. Why kill her in hopes that this child would carry on the family line? It is like cutting off the roots of a tree and expecting it to bear fruit—it can never come to pass."

"Good man, those who follow heretical customs and treat the body as a mere vessel are just the same. They do not cultivate the supreme principle yet seek to destroy the body, hoping their sinful souls will meet the true essence. This is no different from that barbarian who killed his wife to take her child—how stubborn and deluded! Alas, the ways of the world are so shallow and false—how can such people be fit to hear the Great Dao? Those who hold my Dharma seal must not act as he did."

"Good man, the path of cultivating causes still requires vows. One must vow to see the Dao and hear the Dharma in this life and the next—how much more so for those who seek liberation in this very body. Good man, as you study the Great Dao, preserve your form and life. The Dao of no-birth is like a boat or carriage: sturdy, light, and swift, its seams tightly sealed. On land, it bears its load; on water, it resists sinking. It safely reaches its destination without weariness or worry—is this not joyous?"

"Good man, there are foolish people in the world who, hearing of others attaining liberation, imitate them from the sidelines. But they lack wisdom and strength, their nature is lazy and careless, and they cannot even craft a proper carriage. They discard what others have broken, yet the boats and carriages they abandon could still ferry others through danger and drowning. Before reaching the halfway point, they capsize and perish, shattered and lost beyond measure."

"Good man, you must understand: a broken carriage or ruined boat cannot even sustain itself—how can it ferry others? Heretical customs are the same—they cannot save themselves, let alone others. Worldly fools who rely on external paths and heretical customs to deliver the living and the dead are like fools using broken boats and carriages—the disaster of destruction awaits them at once."

"Good man, if there were people who could cross the waters on a broken raft, then external paths would indeed lead to no-birth. But if a broken boat cannot cross, then external paths cannot lead to no-birth. Good man, men and women of later generations who wish to study the Dao should gather and recite the celestial scriptures and treasure texts. These texts are the warp of heaven and the weft of earth; north-south is the warp, east-west the weft. In the center, they become spirit; in things, they become qi; in humans, they become the numinous. Thus it is said: the warp of heaven and the weft of earth weave together the ordinary and the sage. All the myriad things, whether formless or formed, are woven by the true qi of the Great Dao."

The immortals asked: "We dare inquire of the Compassionate One: what is the method of this weaving?"

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "Heaven does not speak yet keeps faith, so it can be followed to perfect virtue. The Three Luminaries do not speak yet shine, so they can be emulated to perfect the body. Earth does not speak yet holds righteousness, so it can be modeled to nurture all things. The Dao does not speak yet is numinous, so it can give birth to heaven and earth. The ten thousand images of heaven and earth are also warp and weft, weaving the ordinary into sages."

The immortals asked: "We dare inquire: if the ten thousand images of heaven and earth are not the body of the Dao, how can they weave the ordinary into sages?"

The reply: "The Dao gives birth to primordial qi, primordial qi gives birth to the Supreme Ultimate, the Supreme Ultimate gives birth to heaven and earth, and heaven and earth give birth to the myriad things. Thus, the ten thousand images of heaven and earth are the descendants of the Dao—how could they not weave the ordinary into sages? The warp and weft of the Great Dao spread across heaven and earth, arraying the sun, moon, stars, wind, clouds, rain, dew, gold, jade, earth, stone, grasses, trees, and all kinds. All can be gathered and used to aid the learner, swiftly attaining sagehood. Once sagehood is attained, one can command heaven, earth, and the myriad things."

At that time, a lesser immortal named Zhengming, hearing the Heavenly Worthy’s words, was confused and failed to understand. He dared to ask further: "I do not yet grasp the meaning of the Dharma seal from the Compassionate One’s golden mouth—how can those who study the Dao gather and use the sun, moon, stars, wind, clouds, rain, dew, gold, jade, earth, stone, grasses, trees, and all kinds of things to aid their learning and swiftly attain sagehood? And once sagehood is attained, how can they command heaven, earth, and the myriad things? Your disciple is dull-witted and does not comprehend this profound principle. I only thought that using the Dao of heaven was inferior to heaven itself. I humbly beg the Compassionate One to clarify this distinction."

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "Those who study the Dao and use the Dao of heaven and the myriad images swiftly attain sagehood because the true essence and wondrous qi of the supreme Great Dao are hidden within heaven, earth, and the myriad things. When one skillfully employs the Dao of heaven and the myriad things, the Great Dao responds. It is like a filial son serving his parents: his heart holds no resistance, he attends to their warmth and coolness in all seasons, observes their countenance, and even when traveling far, his heart is filled with concern, remembering his parents as if they were before him. In waking and sleeping, his spirit does not leave them. Heaven protects him, and spirits guard him. If filial piety toward one’s parents can move heaven, then filial piety toward heaven should naturally move the Dao."

At that time, Dengming and all the later learners, hearing the Heavenly Worthy’s words, opened their minds and understood. They realized that heaven, earth, and the myriad things deeply benefit those who study the Dao, and they clearly saw that heaven, earth, and the myriad things are none other than the Dao. They sighed for the foolish who could not use them, saying: "Before our awakening, we were just the same."

The assembly bowed in unison to give thanks to the Heavenly Worthy for the grace of life.

Then the Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy spoke again to the immortals: "The virtue of heaven and earth is fully contained within the Dao. Though the myriad things possess virtue, none is complete in itself. Yet when one takes what is needed and harmonizes it for mutual benefit, its merit and power become one with the Dao. Those who know how to employ heaven, earth, and the myriad things to aid their bodies need not rely on the esoteric scriptures of the Three Clarities or the true methods of the Three Caverns. The esoteric scriptures of the Three Caverns are lofty in Dao and wondrous in method, yet difficult to receive or even witness.

"Those who study the Dao and seek the truth without ceasing—when their merit is complete and their conduct perfected—the Dao of itself will come to deliver them. These immortals, having deeply understood the meaning of the Dao and thoroughly grasped the Way of preserving form without birth, ascend through the three ranks of immortality, enter the land of no death, and all can rise into the formless, thereby proving that the unborn is not the extinction of life."

After Dengming, the True Person of Central Harmony, had requested the Dharma seal on behalf of the immortals, they all took leave of the Heavenly Worthy and lingered among the clouds for seven days and seven nights. The Heavenly Worthy then said: "Those who have attained the Dao can see afar and hear distantly; their bodies and minds are at ease, subtle and blissful, liberated and unobstructed. Though I am now separated from you by thirty-six thousand heavens and earths, it is as if we were on the palm of my hand, close before my eyes. How can there be any separation? This is unlike the walking corpses of the dusty world below, who stand face to face yet remain as distant as Hu and Yue.

"Return to the lower realm and exhort all beings, guiding them away from heterodox paths. Use gradual or sudden methods as appropriate to their capacities."

At that time, the immortals bowed their heads in reverence, received the Dharma seal, and ascended into the formless. The Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy multiplied his forms to gather the immortals and spread the transformation of the Dao.

When the immortals had descended to the lower realm, they halted in midair, ten thousand *ren* above the earth, seated upon auspicious clouds. Then the pillars of heaven trembled in the four directions, the great earth quaked, dragons and spirits rejoiced, and heaven and earth grew bright. Mist and fog rolled back, the three luminaries shone twice as brightly, fragrant winds spread far and wide, sweet dew poured down, the earth gushed forth milky springs, rivers and marshes became calm and clear. Auspicious qilin and phoenixes gathered in profusion, divine mushrooms and fine herbs spread their shade across the wilds.

The heavenly kings all declared it a blessing for the realm and hailed the ten thousand years. A great amnesty was proclaimed throughout the world; grain and silk were distributed from the treasuries to relieve the old and sick. All under heaven rejoiced, and ranks and emoluments were bestowed. The Son of Heaven, the various kings, and the multitude of dukes and ministers—too many to recount—ascended the altar to pay homage and give profound thanks for the grace bestowed. They offered vast treasures and established quiet offerings. All under heaven embraced the Dao, and the traces of demons and evil vanished. The myriad states enjoyed great peace; all under heaven prospered together, and the people lived in abundance, singing praises in verse.

For ninety thousand years, the sky bore no杂色 clouds, only purple mist; moisture flowed without separate streams, only sweet dew fell.
