The lesser immortals of the lower realm witnessed the power of the Dao’s compassion and knew it to be the might of the Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy. Then each immortal expressed their heartfelt wishes and bowed from afar toward the vast emptiness of the sky.

At that time, the Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy, together with the various highest perfected ones and the highest immortals, each extended their hands to fill the lower realm, expounding wondrous Dharma. They conferred upon the lesser immortals the first rank of the supreme Dao, instructing each to cultivate the highest methods and enter the Way of perfecting form without birth. Innumerable beings were delivered into the wondrous Dharma, attaining the fruit of non-retrogression.

The Hu, Yi, Man, and Liao peoples, along with all ghosts, spirits, and the suffering souls of hell, all received the mysterious transformation and gained its benefits. From this time onward, however, people grew increasingly shallow and contentious, filled with malice and harm. The great Dao was no longer practiced, and demonic influences began to arise.

Though many were not yet ready to receive deliverance, the Dao still extended its hand, bestowing the Dharma of great compassion. In later ages, men and women, lacking upright hearts, might only tentatively practice the Dao, yet the Dao would still grant its aid without reproach. Some would progress gradually, while others would retreat midway. Seeing their retreat, the Dao would not cling to them. Though the Dao is without intent, it constantly nurtures all things with compassion.

The great Dao is like water, quenching thirst and washing away filth. The Dao is like a fine medicine: if one diligently takes it, it will surely cure illness; but if one is sick and does not take it, recovery is rare. Men and women of later ages who diligently cultivate the Dao will surely escape death and calamity, preserve their bodies, and live on, entering the formless and becoming companions of the Dao. Those who turn their backs on the Dao will not have their names removed from the register of death, nor will they escape mortal calamity. Their forms will turn to ash and dust, their souls and consciousness will drift and wander, subject to karmic retribution. In life, they will lack the power of the Dao; in death, they will hope for the Dao’s rebirth, but it will never be attained.

From now on, yin qi will gradually grow stronger, and people will no longer fear death. They will study external methods and fail to attain the great Dao. Such people are often seized by demons and evil spirits, their souls and spirits captured, their bodies afflicted with illness, with no means of cure. After their lives end, they will follow the factions of evil and surely fail to attain the Dao. Though they may have minor good deeds, there will be no way for them to receive karmic reward, for they have lost the upright path and do not wish to practice the Dao, leaving them vulnerable to the encroachment of evil spirits.

Such people claim that the myriad things are empty, and their own bodies are also empty. If the realm of things is empty, what can encroach upon them? If their bodies are also empty, what can they receive? Their false notions of reception are ultimately empty and quiescent, utterly nonexistent. Yet foolish people, holding to such partial views, when they engage in this contemplation, find demonic spirits and spectral beings competing to harm them, with no fear or restraint.

Some, while still alive, are possessed by demons and follow evil spirits, departing in an instant—this is called "entering evil with the whole body," and they need not wait for death to have their souls and spirits taken. If a woman, while alive, harbors evil within, her complexion will wither and turn sallow, her body aching everywhere, constantly spitting phlegm and foam, or swelling severely. The noxious qi of water and earth will cause pain in all her joints; wind afflictions will enter her heart, leaving her confused and forgetful. How can she find time to seek the Dao while struggling to save her qi? Such is the sorrow of the degenerate world, where people bring about their own destruction.

Each body possesses its own Dao, yet they do not know how to employ it, though it is as near as a neighbor.

Those who refuse to analyze it merely draw near the mysterious stream yet lack the heart to cleanse their filth; though a divine physician stands at their side, they do not know how to cure their illness, willingly enduring suffering and embracing the pain of thorns. Such men are not far from the Dao, yet delusion clouds their hearts and veils their eyes, so they drift with the current and cannot swim against it.

The Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy expounds the Dharma-seal for all sentient beings, circulating and bestowing its offerings. Those of utmost sincerity treasure and practice it, while the perverse and vulgar raise slander on all sides.

Good man, you should now know that believing in and revering my Dao does not benefit me, just as slandering my Dao does not harm me. Good man, the perverse and vulgar are like hunting dogs feeding without a fixed master. For example, the eastern household cultivates goodness and observes long fasts, upholding the precepts and refraining from killing. The western household commits the ten evils, engaging solely in butchery, trade, fishing, and hunting, their home reeking with foulness. The scraps of their meals are discarded within their domain. The eastern household’s dog, drawn by the stench, goes to feed on the remnants and forgets to return. Now, the western household had no dog before; seeing this one, young and small, they delight in its presence and feed it even more of the rancid scraps. The dog’s original master, magnanimous in nature, does not call it back. As months and years pass, the dog grows large and no longer recognizes its former master. One day, the master happens to go out and briefly passes the western neighbor’s home, whereupon the dog barks in alarm. The former master, moved by compassion, does not take offense. Several days later, the household of the ten evils suddenly suffers heavenly calamity, and the entire family perishes. The remnants they had gathered, putrid and rotten, are also exhausted. The dog, now starving, howls all day. Hearing this, the former master’s household discusses: “When this dog was young, it loved to go to that house, feeding on foul and rotten scraps until its nature became corrupted. Even if we called it back now, it would not survive.” In an instant, the dog starves to death. The master sighs: “When this dog was with us, it often heard the Dharma. Though it did not awaken to it, its spirit was still nourished. I hoped that in its next life it might be born as a human. Yet for no reason, it went to that household of the ten evils, drinking blood and devouring fat, feeding on putrid scraps. Now it has starved to death without a single good affinity. This dog will certainly not be born into the human realm.”

Good man, I compare the perverse and vulgar who are jealous and forget their roots, slandering the Great Dao, to this dog—both pursue foulness and thus fail to recognize their former master. Those who study the Dao endure humiliation and bear slander, redoubling their diligence. In seeking the Supreme Dao, they must also reflect and observe: the perverse and vulgar cannot escape the suffering of birth, old age, sickness, and death; they cannot transcend the mire of entanglements, sinking into delusion, their bodies formed by the three poisons of ignorance, greed, and hatred. The ten evils and five rebellions are their companions; wealth and lust are their dwellings; malicious speech and venomous tongues are their songs; slander and jealousy are their hearts’ conduct. The perverse and vulgar do not see true scriptures, do not hear true teachings, and have no means to cease their evil—such are their calamities. Those who study later should distance themselves from such people, need not engage with them, nor contend with them in debate. They should seek their own ascent and deliverance, unwavering from dawn to dusk.

The perverse and vulgar follow teachings that rise and fall; their bodies are subject to aging and death. Before they even die, they are already afflicted by disasters—this is the sign that their perverse teachings are ineffective. Those who study the true Dao remain free from illness—this is the sign of their primal fortune and wholeness of life. They should rejoice in this, deeply avoid harm, uphold my Dharma-seal, and not accept perverse words.

Good man, at the beginning of the kalpa, there were people from Jianmu Village who entered the southern mountains to peddle true pearls. A merchant from the eastern mountains, named Poluoduo and called Manyuan, took out a hundred taels of gold, bought a pearl, round and luminous in his palm, an inch in diameter. He carried it in a pouch at his elbow, allowing no one to see it. Within several tens of days, a man from the southern mountains named Leijie came, falsely selling fish eyes. The western neighbor of Manyuan, a household named Shouliang, also took out a hundred taels of gold and bought a fish eye, likewise concealing it and allowing no one to see it. Six years later, both households fell gravely ill. They beseeched a skilled physician to come and treat their sickness, and in preparing the medicinal formula, a fine true pearl was required. At that time, the two men each brought out their pearls for the physician to examine. From afar, the physician knew that the latter had bought a fish eye. He immediately said, “This is not a true pearl.” Shouliang was suspicious, fearing the physician was deceiving him, and asked the physician to test it in water. After soaking it overnight, the container reeked of fishiness. When a true pearl is placed in water, its brilliance only increases. After nine days, it was taken out, now six inches long. Manyuan ingested it, and his suffering was immediately cured. Later, when he went to buy another pearl, he asked the physician to teach him how to soak it in water. After taking it, he became robust, and to this day, he has lived over ninety thousand years. His name is inscribed on the Jade Tablet of the Upper Sovereign as one who does not die, and all good spirits serve him in turn. This man also attained the Dao of my true qi and can ride the qi to travel, no longer subject to the peril of death.

The western neighbor’s entire household perished from that grave illness. Only a slave named Qinzi, young and thoughtful, often gazed at the sky and sighed, wishing to obtain the Heavenly Dao to save himself from suffering. I commanded the Perfected Immortal of Great Penetration to teach him to eat pine needles and pine nuts. To this day, he does not age, entering Mount Taibai and sometimes wandering to the Heavenly Mountains, ascending Kunlun. I have transmitted to him the method of the morning qi, and he is certain to escape death and attain the true Dao.

Good man, the true and the false Dao stand in opposition, with life and death as their counterparts—there is no equivalence. Upholding my Dharma-seal enables one to distinguish between the perverse and the upright. Those who study and cultivate should aspire to save themselves and deliver both the living and the dead, yet they must not act hastily, pursuing fame and profit while forgetting their great accomplishment.

In the realm of the utmost true Dharma, those who serve it can turn the Dao of heaven and earth and repel the four seasons, unchanging by day or night.

When heaven and earth collapse, the Dao can restore them;
when the cosmos is broken, the Dao can mend it;
when vital qi is deficient, the Dao can replenish it;
when the myriad things are unnurtured, the Dao can nourish them;
when the world remains untransformed, the Dao can transform it;
all that is fierce and evil, the Dao can alter;
all that is good, the Dao can bless;
those benighted in ignorance, the Dao grants them light;
the solitary and fearful, the Dao befriends;
hunger, cold, sickness, and distress, the Dao removes;
when treading through peril and hardship, the Dao brings peace;
when the blade presses upon the neck, the Dao delivers.

Good man, if you wish to study, do not within the supreme Great Dao’s utmost true Dharma give rise to improper conduct. In all your undertakings, maintain perfect uprightness. The profound protection of the Great Dao ensures that you need not fear perverse paths lacking true root-power or reliable support.

It is like one who has lost their way, advancing and retreating without direction, unaware of the essential path. From youth, they wander in confusion, their practice unsettled. Some speak of forgetting the mind, yet fail to perceive the body; if the mind has no arising, how can hearing be forgotten?

If the mind bears burdens, how can it be forgotten? When this body first returns to the four great elements, though the body may be temporarily forgotten, the four great elements remain. Even if the form is empty, observation cannot cease. One thing observed becomes two matters. The prior realm is not forgotten, and subsequent observation arises in succession. All causes and conditions arise from the four great elements; the body is born from their harmonious union. At the time of extinction, it returns to the four great elements. The followers of external paths are like grasses and trees: born from the four great elements, they perish by them. They cannot avoid arising, nor can they avoid ceasing. They cannot attain immediate arising, nor can they prevent arising. The followers of external paths are likewise bound within birth and death, enslaved by things, rising and perishing with conditions.

Good man, those who attain the Dao can forget both body and mind, perceiving neither ability nor forgetting. Both realm and wisdom are empty in substance; observation does not arise. The form I receive is born from the Dao. Now, forgetting this form, I return to the Dao, no longer held by the four great elements, no longer subject to the arising and ceasing of the four seasons, no longer bound by the fetters of affliction. The supreme Great Dao can preserve and extinguish: in extinction, it is without form; in preservation, it attains long life. Serene and profound, subtle and elusive, it cannot be known by wisdom, nor grasped by the mind. It responds to things with perfect completeness, its activity and function boundless.

Good man, the power of compassion of the supreme Great Dao is inconceivable. In later generations, men and women who uphold this Dharma-seal should reflect deeply and maintain right mindfulness. At that time, the Heavenly Worthy having expounded this scripture, the five hundred followers of external paths, including Ke Yewei and others, abandoned their heterodox teachings. Baring their shoulders in remorse, they entreated the Dao, seeking to leave home and attain deliverance. Beating their breasts in repentance, their bodies streamed with blood. They plucked out their hair and eyebrows like birds molting their feathers, leaping and flinging themselves down as if mountains were collapsing.

Then the Heavenly Worthy commanded the Perfected One of Central Harmony to initiate the followers of external paths, bestowing upon them the Dao of causes and conditions for rebirth. They were to contemplate impermanence with reverence, refrain from harm, sever delusion and greed, and avoid accumulation. The Perfected One of Central Harmony said: "You followers of external paths, from this day forward, take care not to exalt yourselves falsely as great teachers of heaven and humanity, harming others’ lives and property. The celestial registers of dark deeds record your transgressions; nine generations of ancestors suffer punishment, and you become rebellious ghosts. While you live now, wear simple clothing and eat plain food to sustain your bodies. Endure humiliation, cultivate diligently, and seek early transformation. In later lives, be born in the Central Kingdom, encounter the Dao, and hear the Dharma. With this impure and stagnant body, unfit to preserve its form, enter the Dao of non-arising."

At that time, the five hundred followers of external paths rejoiced, bowed in gratitude to the Perfected One of Central Harmony, took leave of the Heavenly Worthy, and returned to their dwellings. There they established pure abodes, practiced the Dao morning and evening, contemplated the impermanence of the body, and sought early extinction. Throughout the four heavens, humans and non-humans alike all took refuge in the true and correct Dao. Then the Heavenly Worthy, with the assembly of sagely hosts and true responsive bodies, pervaded the Dharma-realm. Thereupon, the assembly of divine immortals, eighty-four thousand in number, held the Dharma-seal, bowed in reverence, and received the teaching.

Thus concludes Scroll Ten of the *Supreme Great Dao Jade Clarity Scripture*.
